# Igros Kodesh

## Volume 22

In response to your letter, in which you write about your situation and the matters you are involved in:

It is well known that the primary vessel for receiving Hashem’s blessings—in all matters, and especially in those pertaining to one’s livelihood and success in one’s endeavors—is through the performance of mitzvos with hiddur (in a beautiful and meticulous manner). This is because the mitzvos are the channels through which the Ohr Ein Sof is drawn down into this world.

Furthermore, it is appropriate to strengthen one’s hiskashrus to the Rebbe, the Nasi of our generation, through the study of his sichos and maamarim, and by following his directives in one’s daily avodah. This creates a vessel for the blessings that the Rebbe bestows upon anash, and it brings success in both spiritual and material matters.

Regarding your question about the specific path you should take: one must always remember that a person’s success is not determined by their own cleverness or effort alone, but by the blessing of Hashem. Therefore, one should conduct oneself with bitul to Hashem’s will, and in all your ways acknowledge Him. When one acts with this mindset, Hashem directs one’s steps and grants success in all that one does.

May it be Hashem’s will that you receive good news regarding all the matters you mentioned, and may you be blessed with success in all your endeavors, both in your personal life and in your shlichus.

## 817

B"H, 7 Tishrei, 5722
Brooklyn

Greetings and Blessings!

We acknowledge receipt of your letter in which you write of your activities during the time since your arrival from... i.e., more than **half a year.** The hope—and surely for one such as yourself it is unnecessary to elaborate—is that the activities you describe are **perhaps** sufficient for a businessman, or generally for someone whose occupation is entirely in other matters, and who engages in the dissemination of Yiddishkeit or the support of institutions only during his free time. But this is not sufficient at all for one for whom this must be his occupation and his primary business. And the intent here is not merely because the salary comes from a public fund, and therefore the work must be done faithfully, etc.—rather, the main point is that a person must be concerned about the loss of his days, more and more. As is explained in Chassidus regarding the verse, "Days were fashioned, and for Him one of them," that the number of days corresponds to the necessary activities, and any day that is not full—and certainly if it is empty—of the necessary activities, then...

Indeed, to find a merit in the current case—[contrary to your letter, which suggests that because you did not have "bread in your basket" you were lacking in activity, whereas on the contrary]—it is because you *did* have "bread in your basket" that you did not pay attention to the words of our Sages, "Skin a carcass in the marketplace and do not say, 'I am a Kohen,'" to the point that before approaching any activity, you would conduct seven examinations to see if perhaps it is not in accordance with your dignity, etc., etc.

Our Sages have informed us that one does not cry over the past. And especially in the present case, for seemingly there is no practical difference whether it stems from a lack of desire or a lack of ability. The concept of shlichus is **specifically** that the shaliach should not wait for instructions for every single detail of an activity, nor should he wait for the days of Moshiach, when the spirit of impurity will pass from the earth and there will be no more concealment and hiddenness. On the contrary—one must spread light in a place of **darkness, concealment, and hiddenness** [and this concealment and hiddenness often includes the worry of parnassah. And regarding you, this was provided for, and nevertheless, etc.]. It is simple and understood that now, during the Aseres Yemei Teshuvah, one should not dwell on such matters, for the merits of each and every one of our brethren—may they live—must be emphasized more and more, and the reader will understand. In any event, from here on in, you should discuss matters with...

It is obvious that the above contains no element of harshness or the like, but only great pain that for strange reasons you have squandered your time, talents, and knowledge, without utilizing them at all as required for the dissemination of the wellsprings, within the framework of the dissemination of Yiddishkeit, and the reader will understand. Especially since you are situated among **tens of thousands**—may they live—of our brethren whose souls are hungry and thirsty for the word of Hashem [though a significant portion of them do not know the cause of their thirst and hunger, and fortunate is the portion of one who utilizes his talents to inform them of the aforementioned and to bring them under the wings of the Shechinah]. It appears that the saying, "Everything depends on mazal," applies here as well.

With the blessing of a *Chasimah V'Gmar Chasimah Tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 2220

B"H, 7 Tishrei, 5722
Brooklyn.

To the participants of the farbrengen on the auspicious day of Chai Elul,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received the news regarding your farbrengen on the auspicious day of Chai Elul, the birthday of the two great luminaries, the Baal Shem Tov and the Alter Rebbe.

Beyond the great importance of a farbrengen in general—as explained in the letter of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, printed in the Tehillim collection—this is all the more so when the farbrengen takes place on an auspicious day such as this. As is well known, every year the events repeat themselves and are reawakened anew.

May it be the will of Hashem that the light of these luminaries shine in their lives and in our lives, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, extending into thought, speech, and action.

And may we very soon merit the fulfillment of the promise, "May your wellsprings spread outward," and the coming of the Master, King Moshiach.

With respect and with a blessing for a *chasimah v'gmar chasimah tovah*.

**As is well known:** See also below, letter 582, and the references in the notes there.

## 2121

B"H, 8 Tishrei, 5722
Brooklyn.

To the students of Beis Rivkah in Kfar Chabad,
Founded and directed by my father-in-law, the Rebbe,
Grade 4, Group Gechaleh.
May Hashem grant them life.

Blessings and peace!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 3 Tishrei, in which you write about your activities in strengthening Yiddishkeit among the students of the school, and, together with this, your plan to connect with groups and classes from other places, etc.

Regarding matters such as these—the intention to connect with additional groups and classes—it is understood that caution and investigation are required beforehand regarding the groups and classes with whom you wish to meet, as well as the method of approach, etc.

Therefore, regarding the activities within the school—your own class and the other classes—the matter is correct, and your intention and your actions are good. However, regarding the second part of the plan, you should detail the matters before the administration of Beis Rivkah, and you should act according to the instruction of the administration, both in the general matter and regarding the details.

In keeping with the tone of your letter, it is my hope that you conduct yourselves in your daily lives in a manner befitting students of the school and with yiras shamayim, for each one of you is called a daughter of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah. May Hashem grant you success.

With the blessing of a *chasimah v’gmar chasimah tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 8282

B"H, 24 Tishrei, 5722
Brooklyn.

To the Vaad Nashi Kfar Chabad
Founded and directed by
My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory
May Hashem grant them life

Blessings and peace!

It was a pleasure to receive your letter from the eve of the festival of Sukkos, our time of rejoicing, bringing good news of your holy activities in spreading Yiddishkeit and its matters among the women and daughters of Yisrael, and regarding your good resolutions for the future.

The words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding material tzedakah are well-known, and from them we can also understand regarding spiritual tzedakah: that when one resolves to give tzedakah and assist one’s fellow generously—even if, on the face of it, it is beyond one’s current available means—at that very moment, a new source and channel are created from Above to provide everything necessary to fulfill that good resolution.

May it be Hashem’s will that you, too, in your avodah, will conduct yourselves in accordance with the above—that is, to resolve to work not only according to what is currently possible, but with an increase beyond that. Certainly, the words of the tzaddik of our generation, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, will be fulfilled, and you will be granted the full ability to bring your resolutions into actual practice.

And as is the custom among Chassidim, and especially among Chabad Chassidim, may all of the above be done with joy and a glad heart—true joy.

With blessings for success in your holy work and for good tidings.

#### ***8282***

**And it is well-known:** See also above, Vol. 21, letter 8119, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 8223

8223

B"H, 25 Tishrei, 5722
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, distinguished, and occupied with communal needs, R' Dov Aryeh, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

After a long interval, your letter from Erev Sukkos, the time of our rejoicing, was received.

Regarding what you write concerning my opinion on government support for yeshivos, yeshivos ketanos, and Talmud Torahs that are conducted in accordance with pure holiness:

I have already publicized the reasons—which were also printed in the journal *HaMaor*, which surely is in your possession—and the general point is founded upon the statement of Chazal: "Jerusalem was destroyed only because the children of the schoolhouse were neglected." Who is the person who would dare to prevent such support, when it is certain that because of this, **many** sons and daughters of Yisrael will be unable to be accepted into the aforementioned institutions? And if for the sake of building the Beis HaMikdash it is forbidden to neglect the children of the schoolhouse, how much more so [is this the case] when the reasons for doing so are based on imagined, or at the very least, remote concerns.

A conclusive proof of how the perspective of those who are *chareidim* to the word of Hashem should be regarding this question can be seen from the opposition itself: all those who years ago fought against parochial schools, all those who prevent the Federation of Charities from supporting *chareidi* institutions, and all those who fight against religious instruction for public school students, are fighting with all their might against the aforementioned support. And to the wise, a word is sufficient.

Surely, for one such as yourself, further elaboration on all this is unnecessary. My hope is strong that you will utilize all your influence, with the appropriate vigor, to assist the children of the schoolhouse—the education of the children of Yisrael upon the foundations of Torah, in our way, that is to say: the perspective of our Torah, the Torah of life, for eternity. And if one who saves a single soul of Yisrael is considered as if he has sustained an entire world, how much more so when the matter concerns tens, hundreds, and perhaps even thousands.

Surely it is known to you, also from the leaders of Agudas Yisrael, regarding the aforementioned, the heads of the yeshivos here, etc.

With respect and blessing for good tidings.

## 8224

8224

B"H, 26 Tishrei, 5722
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished, etc., R' Chaim Dov, may he live,
known as Dr. Mantel

Shalom u'Bracha!

It was a pleasure to receive your letter from the intermediate days of the festival, and especially the beginning of your letter, noting that you, your wife, and your son, may they live, visited Kfar Chabad, etc.

May it be the will of Hashem that your hand will write to bring good news regarding your personal matters, which will surely strengthen your peace of mind and your focus on the matters of spreading traditional Yiddishkeit wherever your reach extends. You are gifted with talent in this area and a special ability to utilize this talent among the youth—for any increase in them is multiplied many times over when they build a home in Yisrael, and this is simple to understand. Your efforts in this, carried out with joy and firm bitachon, as explained in the teachings of Chassidus, will add to your success.

We have just come from our "time of rejoicing" and Simchas Torah in particular, the purpose of which is to draw that joy into the entire year.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned, both in general and in detail, and with respect.

## 2205

## 6205

B"H, 29 Tishrei, 5722
Brooklyn

Mrs. G. Luzon, may she live and be well,

Blessings and peace!

In due time and with pleasure, I received the regards from you and your husband, may they live and be well, through the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing man, involved in communal needs, etc., Rabbi Yosef Weinberg, upon his return from his visit to your camp. I derived double satisfaction when he told me of the awakening, the willingness of heart, and the warmth shown by you and your husband toward uniting and drawing closer the Jewish families in your vicinity—and especially that your husband has taken it upon himself to teach the children. In our times, the education of Jewish children is of paramount importance, for through them, one influences the parents as well.

Surely it is known to you and your husband that which is fundamental to our faith in general, and emphasized particularly in the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov and the teachings of Chassidus—the concept of Hashgacha Pratis. Every matter, great or small, that occurs in the world—whether in the inanimate, vegetative, animal, or speaking realms—in all its details and the details of its details, is not, Heaven forbid, a coincidence. Rather, everything is by Hashgacha Pratis, with intent and purpose in the governance of the world. Needless to say, when a Jew finds himself in a remote corner of the world, far from his native land and generally distant from a Jewish community, this is certainly not a mere coincidence. He must view himself as a shaliach of the Makom, through whom the word of Hashem will reach even that corner, to increase justice and righteousness for each and every individual, and to disseminate Yiddishkeit and its mitzvos among the Jews there in particular.

In such matters, one should not look at the quantity, for our Sages, of blessed memory, have said that whoever sustains one soul in Yisrael is as if he sustained an entire world. If this is true at all times, how much more so in our era, after the destruction, may Hashem spare us, of such an important part of our people. Every Jew who has survived is a brand plucked from the fire and must fulfill not only his own role, but also fill the place of the holy ones who fell for Kiddush Hashem.

May it be Hashem’s will that you and your husband go from strength to strength in your efforts and your positive influence on your surroundings, and may you do so with joy and goodness of heart, in the spirit of "the time of our rejoicing" and Simchas Torah in particular, with which we conclude the month of Tishrei at the beginning of the year, in order to draw from this joy and enthusiasm throughout all the days of the year.

With regards to all our brethren, the Bnei Yisrael in your camp, may they live and be well, with honor and blessing.

In the secretariat, we write only in Lashon Kodesh, Yiddish, or English, and it would be good to inform us in which language to continue the correspondence from here on, as I hope there will be a continuation. However, from your side, you and your husband may write in French as well, as I read that language. The main thing is that you should be able to share good news.

#### ***6205***

**In your camp:** Madagascar.

**Our Sages have said:** Sanhedrin 37a.

**In order to draw:** See above, Letter 6204, and the references in the notes there.

## 827

B"H, 29 Tishrei, 5722
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., Moreinu Harav Betzalel, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding your note on the language of Sefer Yetzirah as it appears in the Tikkun Leil Shavuos (which contains only the beginning and end of the Sefer), in the Sefer Yetzirah printed separately and in its entirety, the language is: "Three good traits: a generous eye, humility, and a faithful eye. Three evil traits of the tongue: evil speech, the slanderer, and one who speaks with one thing in his mouth and another in his heart. Three good traits of the tongue: silence, guarding one's speech, and truthful speech."

And were I not hesitant, I would institute that it be recited this way in the Tikkun Leil Shavuos.

## 6228

6228

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Mar-Cheshvan, 5722

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

As we have just emerged from Shabbos Bereishis, and in accordance with the maamar of the Alter Rebbe that the light of Shabbos Bereishis illuminates all the Shabbosos of the year; and according to his teaching in the name of the Baal Shem Tov, which he received from his teacher the Baal Chai (who is Achiyah HaShiloni), that all the days of the year receive from Shabbos Bereishis:

May it be the will [of Hashem] that at the beginning and opening of the parsha of Bereishis—both of the Torah and of the world—there shall be light, including at the beginning of the matters of this "small world," the human being: both his matters that are in the category of "the heavens and their hosts" (spiritual matters), and his matters that are in the category of "the earth and its hosts" (physical matters).

Light in all its interpretations—light that is visible and revealed.

And the way to draw down all that has been mentioned here and now, below ten tefachim and in a revealed manner, is understood from the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov, that the aforementioned light (the light created on the first day) was hidden within the Torah.

And the quality of this light is that a person can see and gaze with it from one end of the world to the other.

[This implies] conduct according to the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of life—from one end of the "world" (the small world—the human being) to the other: "In all your ways, know Him."

With blessings for good tidings, generally and specifically,

**M. Schneerson**

## 229

B"H, 30 Tishrei, 5722
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, engaged in communal needs, etc., R' Yeruchem, may he live and be well.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your two letters from the first day of Chol Hamoed Sukkos, which were received in due time,

Many thanks for the good news... and may it be Hashem's will that the improvement continues to grow, and that from a place of peace of mind, you will be able to increase your involvement in your work—the work of Heaven—spreading traditional Judaism, and primarily, spreading the wellsprings through our institutions, and in general, through channels of *yiras shamayim* and *ahavas shamayim*, which is one and the same with *ahavas haTorah* and *ahavas Yisrael*.

My hope is strong that you did not content yourself with the *Simchas Beis HaShoeivah* that you wrote about, but that you also organized further celebrations throughout *Zman Simchaseinu*, and in this, of course—and most importantly—with the students, may they live, and the youth in general, with the highlight being the days of *Shemini Atzeres* and *Simchas Torah*. For these are general days for the entire year, and their purpose is to influence true joy—joy of Torah and joy of *mitzvah*—throughout all the days of the year in matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, in which one must include all of a person’s affairs, in accordance with the command, "In all your ways, know Him."

With blessings for good news.

## 8,131

8,131

B"H, 1st of Mar-Cheshvan, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter... It is my strong hope that you and your fellow bochurim, may they live, flee from any matter of machlokes, chas v'shalom, and from speaking lashon hara about anyone. Furthermore, you should influence others not to become involved in any matter of machlokes, and each and every one should occupy himself with the study of Torah and the performance of mitzvos as is incumbent upon him, and strive to increase in this.

If we have been given the severe warning of "love your fellow as yourself," then it is all the more so a complete prohibition from the Torah to seek out the faults of a fellow Jew. And if someone comes along and opens yet another place to teach Torah to the children of Israel, it is a definitive ruling in the Shulchan Aruch (Yoreh Deah, section 245, paragraph 22) that one cannot protest his actions. On the contrary, regarding this it is said, "Hashem desires, for the sake of His righteousness, to make the Torah great and glorious." It is surprising that he apparently does not pay attention to this ruling of our holy Torah, Toras Chaim; on the contrary, the language of the verse proves that one must assist the one doing this.

Our Sages have said that one does not cry out over the past, but I wish to hope that immediately upon receiving this letter of mine, he will look at the aforementioned ruling of the Shulchan Aruch and fulfill this ruling completely, especially since through this, peace will increase, and peace is the vessel that holds the blessing of the Ribono shel Olam. I will await good news regarding all of the above.

With blessings.

#### ***8,131***

**Our Sages have said:** See Berachos 54a.

**And peace:** See Uktzin at the end.

## 8132

B"H, 3rd of Mar-Cheshvan, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 1st of Cheshvan, in which you write regarding your spiritual state and therefore ask whether you should travel here, etc.

The astonishment and greatest wonder are understandable even regarding the initial thought, for as you wrote, you spent some time here, and whether by your own will or otherwise, you certainly absorbed several matters. However, as with all matters of Torah, one must ultimately bring them into action, in the style of our Sages: "Great is study, for it leads to action." 

Divine Providence has provided you with a relatively easy way to bring these matters into action: namely, through education on the purity of holiness in the institution of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisroel.

It is simple that one must engage in this with *mesiras nefesh*, with great joy, and with the utmost activity.

Especially since you are soon planning to build a home in Yisroel, an everlasting edifice, the aforementioned *avodah* is the conduit and vessel for your home to be built with success.

Yet, in exchange for all the above, ever since your return to Eretz Yisroel (may it be rebuilt and established), you have been contemplating ways to evade the aforementioned *avodah*, to the point that the *yetzer* wants to cloak this in the guise of *yiras shamayim*.

The conclusion from the above is that you should fulfill your aforementioned *shlichus* with joy and a glad heart in your current location, with *mesiras nefesh*, while of course also studying *nigleh* and Chassidus for yourself, as well as the specific *halachos* that are necessary. And since we are promised, "A person who sanctifies himself a little from below is sanctified much from above," you will succeed.

It is a great wonder that you do not write about your activities during the month of Tishrei, for this is a general month for the entire year. Surely you will fill this in at the next opportunity.

The date of the wedding — as is customary, as the two sides will discuss in a good and auspicious hour.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 8,233

8,233

B”H, 5 MarCheshvan, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

Your letter was received.

May it be the will of Hashem that in all your affairs you receive good news in the true sense of the word.

Regarding what was explained at the very beginning of this week’s parsha:

**Lech Lecha**: The general instruction is to go *lecha* — to your true reality and essence — the essence of every individual from the seed of Avraham Avinu.

This is achieved by leaving and departing:

**From your land (me’artzecha)**: The earthly and material matters; the coarseness of the *nefesh habehamis*.

**And from your birthplace (umimoladtecha)**: That which comes from habit; the character traits of the *nefesh habehamis*.

**And from your father’s house (umibeis avicha)**: The intellect of the *nefesh habehamis*.

This is the path by which one arrives:

**To the land (el ha’aretz)** — the higher land — **that I will show you (asher areka).**

As is known from the Baal Shem Tov in the name of Rav Saadia Gaon, the primary purpose of man’s creation in this world is to break his character traits, etc., and this is the meaning of "Lech Lecha," etc.

And on a higher level — the response of the Alter Rebbe to the Tzemach Tzedek: The entire concept of Chassidus is to change the nature of one’s character traits.

The command of Hashem through His servants, our Rebbes, also provides the strength to do so, provided that it is: specifically — you, through your own free choice.

I look forward to hearing good news regarding the above.

#### ***8,233***

A general letter, sent to several people on the dates of the 5th–10th of MarCheshvan. Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 2, p. 659. See also letter 8,543 below.

**Go to your true reality:** See *Kuntres* on the *maamar* "Lech" (I and II) in the *hemshech* of 5666; *Zohar* Vol. I, beginning of *Parshas Lech Lecha*.

**As is known from the Baal Shem Tov:** *Kesser Shem Tov* 3:3 [Kehot edition: 4:4–5:1].

**Response of the Alter Rebbe:** *Likkutei Dibburim* [Vol. 1], Simchas Torah 5694, sec. 6.

## 8131

B”H, 7 Cheshvan, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Rosh Chodesh Cheshvan, in which you write regarding a marriage proposal you received from someone who is over forty years of age.

As it appears from your letter, this is too large an age difference from your own. Furthermore, one must find out the reason why the person in question has not yet made a shidduch. Before taking any action in this matter, one must clearly know the reason, and also reflect upon the age difference, which carries significant weight. In the city where the person in question is located, you surely have friends who will hopefully be able to assist you in this.

Regarding what you write concerning parnassah—that you are running a business but are not entirely satisfied with it:

In general, in our times, it is not advisable to abandon a source of parnassah that is ongoing and has established practice, and where the business is already set, as long as one does not have a solid, firm alternative to replace it. Such things are not easy to find in our times, as many conditions change from day to day and from week to week.

Moreover, changing businesses is not an advantage for a shidduch, as people certainly investigate and inquire, and it makes a good impression when a business has been running for several years, rather than abandoning an old business to occupy oneself with something new.

And most importantly, according to the beginning of your letter, it is of the utmost importance that your daily conduct be in accordance with the instructions of our Torah, Toras Chaim, and the observance of its mitzvos, regarding which it is stated, "And you shall live by them." This is necessary at all times and in every place, and especially when one finds oneself in a situation where one is in need of a special blessing and success from Hashem Yisbarach to decide such a highly important matter as yours at this time.

It would be a proper thing for you to give a few coins to tzedakah every weekday morning—it is understood that this should be done *bli neder*.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

#### ***8131***

## 8135

B"H, 8th of Mar-Cheshvan, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I read with great astonishment the letter and telegram I received regarding your state of mind. This surprise is all the more understandable after you have witnessed open miracles and wonders in a way that is good, both visibly and revealed.

This surprise is further emphasized by the fact that the recent weeks have been under the impression of the month of Tishrei, whose conclusion and seal is Simchas Torah—a joy that breaks through every barrier of measurement and limitation. Furthermore, the halacha is established that the joy of Simchas Torah continues until the 7th of Cheshvan (see Shach, Choshen Mishpat, siman 43, subsection 47), and even after that, there is the **command** to draw from that joy and its matters for the entire year.

Regarding your own situation, it is explained in many places—and is also understood based on the above—that specifically strengthening one’s trust in Hashem, the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders, to the point of open joy in this regard, is the very channel and vessel for receiving Hashem’s blessing for great success in the medical treatment, leading to a swift and complete recovery. I look forward to hearing good news regarding all of the above, speedily in our time.

With blessings for proper health and good news.

#### ***8135***

**The halacha is established:** See also below, letter 8540.

**The command:** See also above, letter 8224, and the references in the notes there.

## 6130

[8 Cheshvan, 5722]

After a long interval, I received your letter from the 8th of Menachem Av, in which you write about the matters you have been engaged in regarding your livelihood, and you write that it is difficult to find suitable work.

The wonder of this is understood, for our Sages have said, "He who gives life gives sustenance," and it is explained in *Kuntres U'Ma'ayan* that this must come about through work and labor, as it is written, "And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you **do**." From this, it is understood that there is certainly suitable work available for you; it is just that, like all matters of this world, it is perhaps connected to toil and *hishtadlus*. Since this is the way of the world, it is understood that one should not be discouraged by this. It has already been said, "Man is born to toil," and the verse states, "When you eat the **toil** of your hands, you are fortunate, etc."

It is my hope that immediately upon receiving this letter of mine, you will consult with your friends among *anash* who are in your location. Before them, you should detail the matters you have dealt with until now, and whether you have engaged in them with the necessary *hishtadlus* but simply did not find [work], or if you have not yet exerted yourself as required. It has already been said, "And salvation comes through many counselors."

## 6,337

[9 Menachem Av, 5722]

...Regarding what you wrote about a name: It is brought in the early and later poskim that a person is the master of his own name, and if he changes it—even assuming that it is a change—it becomes his name for all intents and purposes.

I read your articles (in the Toronto newspaper) regarding the mitzvos, and you use the term "must" many times there in relation to Hashem. Although this terminology and similar expressions such as "nature," etc., are common in many places—even in Kabbalistic texts (see Pardes, end of Shaar Beis; Etz Chaim, Shaar Alef at the beginning; Shomer Emunim, Vikuach Alef, section 41 and onwards, and Vikuach Beis, section 19 and onwards, and see there; and in many other places)—it is understood that there must be some explanation for this, since there is no necessity above, chas v’shalom, for He is the "Impossibility of Impossibilities" (see Responsa of the Rashba, 1:413, and this is the conclusion of Toras HaChassidus).

The point is this: **We see** that Hashem **willed** that creation should function according to specific laws and a specific order (and it is within His power, **even now**, to will otherwise). And according to this order, the formation of the Sefiros is "necessary" (because one of the laws is that that which emanates from the Simple One is also simple), and so on and so forth.

***

6,337

Part of this was printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 7, p. 308; part in Vol. 17, p. 572; and it was completed according to the secretariat's copy.

**Regarding the name:** See also Iggeres 6,336 below.

Must = מוכרח (necessary/compelled).

**The point is this:** See also Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 30, p. 3, and the references there.

## 8238

B"H, 9 Marcheshvan, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Eliezer, may he live and be well,

Shalom u’Bracha!

It was with pleasure that I received the news that the tenth volume of your book series, *Be’er HaChassidus*, has been published. You have sent it to me, and it will surely arrive in the coming days; thank you for your thoughtfulness in sending it.

I was also very pleased to learn that a committee has been formed to hold a gathering in your honor in connection with the publication of these books, which shows that your work is appreciated. It is my hope that this gathering will also reveal an appreciation and admiration for the essence of Chassidus, the depth and preciousness of its Torah, and specifically its way of life. For the core of the Torah of Chassidus and its emphasis is the "therefore" (*uvchein*), which finds expression in a way of life that aligns with its conclusions and ultimate purpose—to make for Him, may He be blessed, a dwelling place in the lower worlds specifically. As the Baal HaTanya emphasizes, the intent is this physical and material world, lower than which there is no other, which is called the world of Asiyah. Therefore, its rectification is also through action, as our Sages of blessed memory stated: "Action is the essential thing," and "Great is study that leads to action." In these days, in particular, the need for this emphasis cannot be overstated, as the Alter Rebbe explains at length in *Tanya*, chapters 36 and 37.

It is worth noting in particular the holy letter (printed in the *Iggeres HaKodesh* section of *Tanya*, Epistle 20, beginning with the words *Ayhu v’chayohi chad, ayhu v’garmohi chad*), which our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe wrote "in the days before his passing in the village of Piena" (the language of his grandson and successor, the Tzemach Tzedek, and in the words of one of the Alter Rebbe’s greatest disciples, R. Aharon of Strashelye, "which he wrote before his passing, may his soul rest in Eden, in *Or HaChayim*"). Its core point is to explain the greatness of the practical mitzvos, which are the purpose of the descent of the souls into this physical world.

May it be the will of Hashem that you see good fruit from your aforementioned labor. That is to say, that the reading and study of your books will have a noticeable effect on the readers in their intellect, and from the Chochma, Binah, and Da’as in the mind—to the emotions and *midos* in the heart, for "the heart divides to all the limbs," so that all the limbs will conduct themselves in the manner of our Sages of blessed memory mentioned above: to be a dwelling place for Him, may He be blessed, to do His will and desire with a whole heart. Through *Be’er HaChassidus*, may they come to hew out for themselves cisterns that will contain the "water" that comes from the Source of Living Waters. And the merit of the many depends upon you.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 6239

B"H, 9 Menachem Av, 5722
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R' Tzvi Hirsch, may he live, Hakohen

Greetings and blessings!

After the longest of intervals, your letter of 6 Cheshvan was received, in which you write regarding the Bar Mitzvah of your son, may he live, which falls on Erev Shabbos, and you ask when the Bar Mitzvah should be celebrated.

Regarding the matter at hand: **On the day** he completes thirteen years, you should hold a farbrengen with at least ten Jews, and the Bar Mitzvah boy should speak words of Torah, both Nigleh and Chassidus, for regarding this day it is said, "Today I have begotten you" (Zohar Vol. II, 98a; see also Zohar Chadash, Parshas Bereishis [10], 3; 15b). It is understood that in addition to the above, he must be called to the Torah on the nearest day of Torah reading, which in your case is the following Shabbos. As for other gatherings—that depends on how you wish to arrange them in accordance with the timing of the city and the location.

It is a great wonder that you do not mention anything regarding your activities in spreading the wellsprings. Even though you have conducted yourself this way for many years, "once he has repeated it, it becomes permitted"—this only functions as a comparison, and especially in light of what has been said, that from day to day we are drawing closer to the true and complete Geulah, the necessity for effort and toil in spreading the wellsprings grows greater from time to time. As is well known from the holy letter of the Baal Shem Tov.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 6240

B"H, 18 Iyar, 5722
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, a man of stature, learned and G-d-fearing, R' Nasan Menachem, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Wednesday, and in due course your book, *Ra'ayonos Nasan* on the Torah, was received. Many thanks.

As is my custom in such matters, I have copied two or three notes in the margins—due to the fact that time does not permit more.

May it be the will of the Ribono shel Olam that you utilize your talents and potential in matters of Torah and mitzvos, for it is in accordance with the statement of Chazal: "Great is study, for it leads to action," and the action is the essential thing.

May this be done with joy and a good heart, for this, too, is a command of our Torah, the Torah of life (see Rambam, end of Hilchos Lulav).

With respect and blessing for good tidings.

***

It is a well-known principle that one does not respond to a *drash* (*Shaar HaPesukim*, Shemos 14:1) — nevertheless, etc.

**Regarding the Introduction.** Seemingly, the style requires correction, at the very least—for it is obvious that regarding the practical application of all that is discussed concerning the *bracha* of the Torah when writing words of Torah, this applies only to one who writes **before** reciting the *bracha* of the Torah that is part of *Birchos HaShachar*.

**At the beginning of the book, page 19.** Why did the Torah begin with the letter *Beis* and not *Alef*, etc.? It is difficult, as many words begin with *Beis* and their content is the opposite of a *bracha*, etc. One could say that the difficulty—that it should have begun with the verse "These are the generations of the heavens," etc.—is addressed in *Tanna D'bei Eliyahu Zuta*, Chapter 1: "And what is different about the *Beis*... that it is said *Bereishis bara Elokim*... and yet, is it not fitting to say only *Elokim bara bereishis*... at the beginning with a *Beis*, which is a language of *bracha*... but you might say, is it not written with a *Beis*, *Bocheh tivkeh* (you shall surely weep), etc.?" And see *Zohar Chadash* (85b): "With the letter *Beis*, which is a sign of *bracha*... *Alef*... the world was not created with it... so as not to give a place to the *Sitra Achra*, which is called *Arur* (cursed), etc."

**Ibid.** Regarding the antiquity of the *nekudos* (vowel points). The *Pardes*, *Shaar* 28, at the beginning, states: "It is famous among all the sages of Israel, a tradition passed down from mouth to mouth from Ezra the Scribe, who received it from mouth to mouth until Moshe Rabbeinu from Sinai, from the mouth of the Almighty, that the *nekudos* and their types are twelve, etc." End quote. The books he cites as evidence—their words have already been refuted long ago. And see how great was the distress felt by the author of the *Sdei Chemed* for having cited their opinion, even though it was only to **decisively** reject it. See regarding this in his *Maamar Pekuos Sadeh* at the end of the *Sdei Chemed*—at length.

**At the end of the book, page 274.** The connection of the end of the Torah to its beginning in the name of a great figure. The language requires correction, as his intent is apparently the well-known explanation that the greatness of the miracle of Moshe Rabbeinu over subsequent miracles—**even though they were in the same matter itself** (such as the splitting of the sea and the splitting of the Ginnai river for him—see *Chullin* 7a)—is because the miracle of Moshe was *Bereishis*—the first. The foundation for this explanation is the interpretation of the Baal Shem Tov on the saying of Chazal, "The entire world is sustained **because of** (for he opened and made) Chanina my son" (see *Sefer Toldos Yaakov Yosef*, beginning of *Parshas Kedoshim*. And see also what our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe wrote in *Likutei Torah*, end of *Parshas Tazria*).

— Regarding the aforementioned connection, it can be explained based on the question of Chazal (*Nedarim* 39b): "But is it not written, 'There is nothing new under the sun'?" And this is the continuation of the verses: "For all the signs and wonders, etc., which He did, etc. (and this is not new, but rather) *Bereishis bara*, etc.," for the Holy One, Blessed be He, made a condition with all the works of creation at the time of the creation regarding miracles (as per Chazal, *Bereishis Rabbah* 5:5; *Zohar* Vol. II, 198b; *Peirush HaMishnayos* and *Tosafos Yom Tov*, *Avos* 5:6).

## 8,141

B"H, 10 MarCheshvan, 5722
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished Rabbi Yeshaya Aryeh, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 7 MarCheshvan, in which you write regarding the idea of publishing the "content of prayer" in the form of a "Baal Shem Tov Siddur," etc., and ask for my opinion on this.

Regarding the above, there are two separate matters: a *Siddur*—meaning a *nusach* of prayer—and the "content of prayer," which can also be interpreted in two ways: the explanation of the words according to the Baal Shem Tov, or the general concept of prayer and its essence.

Now, regarding a "Baal Shem Tov Siddur," it is known that he prayed using the *Siddur* of the Arizal, and in fact, there already exists a "Baal Shem Tov Siddur" ; see *Shaar Siddur HaArizal* by Rabbi Shabtai of Rashkov.

Explanations of the words according to the *Chassidus* of the Baal Shem Tov are scattered throughout the books of the Baal Shem Tov’s students. Even though it is explicitly mentioned in only some of them that they are from the Baal Shem Tov, it is evident that most of them are, at the very least, founded upon the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, and the part testifies to the whole.

As for the content of the concept of prayer according to the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, it has been collected from many different books and has also been printed—in the book *HaBaal Shem Tov Al HaTorah* by Rabbi Shimon Menachem Mendel, *shochet u’vodek*, in *Parshas Noach*.

And since everything is by *hashgacha pratis*, it is my duty (and privilege) to urge you regarding the necessity of establishing set times for the study of *pnimiyus haTorah*—which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of *Chassidus*—on a daily basis, with an increase on the day of *Shabbos*, which is holy to Hashem.

With blessings for good tidings.

[P.S.] The places where the Baal Shem Tov is mentioned in *Tanya*, *Torah Or*, and *Likutei Torah* are noted in the indices at the end of the books.

***

**Rabbi Yeshaya Aryeh:** Dvorkes, Montreal.

## 8242

B"H, 20 Marcheshvan, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter requesting a blessing and a *pidyon nefesh*.

At a time of favor, I will mention once again all those you wrote about at the holy gravesite of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding what you wrote about the well-known matter, and that you recite *Tehillim* before going to sleep:

I believe I have already written to you that the advised approach in such a situation is *hesach hada'as* (distraction). *Hesach hada'as* is not a matter of battling the negative thought, but rather of diverting one's attention from it and occupying the mind with something else—and what could be better than the letters of Torah and *tefillah*? For if a little light pushes away much darkness, how much more so does a great deal of light. Therefore, the aforementioned practice—that you recite *Tehillim*—is the opposite of *hesach hada'as*, and this is easy to understand.

Furthermore, it should be noted that it is the custom of *anash* not to recite *Tehillim* at night before *chatzos* (midnight), except for *Rosh Hashanah* and *Yom Kippur*.

With the blessing that you fulfill the statement of our Sages: "You have labored" (**labor** in the study of Torah and diligence in the performance of *mitzvos*, and the promise of our Sages will be fulfilled in you) "and you have found."

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

#### ***8242***

**That it is the custom:** See also *Sefer HaMinhagim*, p. 20; *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 18, p. 435; below, letter 8285.

**Statement of our Sages:** *Megillah* 6, beginning of side b.

## 8247

B"H, 27 MarCheshvan, 5722
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, Rabbi Nissan [Nemnov], may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 24 MarCheshvan, in which you write regarding the situation in the Yeshiva.

While it is explained in many places and in Chassidic discourse that quantity is not the primary factor—as it is written, "Abraham was one, and he inherited the land"—at the same time, it is also explained in many places regarding the well-known statement of our Sages, "A thousand enter for Scripture... one emerges for instruction." The point of the explanation is that the quantity of a thousand entering for Scripture is necessary in order that there be one for instruction. This is understood with greater emphasis based on what is explained (in *Likutei Torah*, *Gimmel Parshiyos*, 3a) that the "thousand" is in the world of Asiyah, and upon this depends the "one" for instruction in the world of Atzilus. See the wonderful things discussed there.

It is understood that I am not writing this as a sermon, but rather regarding the quantity of students in the Yeshiva, which is alarming.

What is no less concerning is that over the last few years, [the numbers] have been steadily decreasing... Reports have reached here that in many circles of our Jewish brethren in France, and especially in Paris, they are preparing in the field of education for the immigration of Jews from Algeria to France, which has already begun and is growing from time to time. Yet in your letter, there is no sign of any echo of this information or of actions taken regarding the aforementioned...

Regarding your writing about students from here—it is understood that first and foremost you must turn to the administration of the Yeshiva here, and also explain how it is possible to arrange this in the middle of the school year, both here and in France [...] and above all, how the aforementioned will be effective, given that the students here speak Yiddish or English, while the Jewish brethren from Algeria and the like need to be spoken to in French, or at the very least in Lashon HaKodesh.

And since we are standing on the eve of the new month of Kislev, the month of miracles, may it be His will that a miracle occur in all the aforementioned matters, and that there be an increase and a steady growth in the number of students, the blessed seed of Hashem, who study Nigleh and Chassidus.

## 248

B"H, 27 Menachem Av, 5722
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and industrious in communal affairs, R' Tuvia, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

...Regarding your question about the customs of anash in the education of young children: You should clarify this with the elders of anash in your vicinity, as I have not heard anything specific on this matter (beyond what is mentioned in various places in printed works).

You will surely inform me of the progress regarding the matters of the yeshiva erev, the bochurim who traveled to Lod, the Chabad shul in Shikun Pagi, etc. Thank you in advance.

I have read several of the articles by R' Betzalel Landau in *Machanayim* and enjoyed them. Likewise, his book on the Baal Shem Tov (though it is a pity that it lacks source citations!!) is worthy of encouragement and praise.

The wedding of the Rebbe (the Rashab), may his soul rest in Eden, took place, as is the custom in Israel, at the home of the bride’s parents in Ovruch. Whether the bride’s grandfather, the holy Rabbi, etc., R' Yisroel Yitzchak of Cherkas, participated in it—I have not heard regarding this.

Treatment with "radium" rays regarding children in particular, and especially at a very young age, requires extreme caution. If there is a doctor who is concerned, it should not be done. May the Healer of all flesh send his healing in the best, revealed, and manifest way.

At a time of favor, may you mention all those you write about at the Tziyun of the Rebbe, may his merit protect us.

## 6,249

B"H, 27 MarCheshvan, 5722
Brooklyn

To the members of Moshav Bar Giora, in our Holy Land—
May it be built and established speedily in our days by Moshiach Tzidkeinu—
May Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter dated the 22nd of MarCheshvan, signed by several residents of your camp, bringing good news regarding the farbrengen held on that day, the delivery of the regards from here, and so on.

Certainly, as is the custom of the Children of Israel when they gather together in a group of ten or more—as our Sages have informed us that where ten are gathered, the Shechinah rests—and as Rabbeinu HaZaken (the author of the Tanya—the arbiter of the hidden aspects of Torah—and the Shulchan Aruch—the arbiter of the revealed aspects of Torah) explained, having heard it from his masters (the great Maggid of Mezritch and his master, the Baal Shem Tov, may the memory of the righteous be for a blessing in the World to Come):

This is true even if they are not speaking words of Torah. The resting of the Shechinah is to such an extent that if an angel were to stand there, he would be overcome with boundless and infinite awe and fear from the Shechinah resting upon them, to the point that he would be completely nullified from his existence (see Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 23).

How much more so, then, am I certain that at the aforementioned farbrengen, you spoke words of Torah and aroused one another toward the performance of mitzvos.

May it be the will of Hashem that the influence of this farbrengen be drawn down upon the days, weeks, and months that lie ahead for you and for us for the good, to increase in the study of Torah and the performance of mitzvos, with health, livelihood, joy, and a glad heart.

May it be His will that I receive good news regarding all of the above, especially as we stand on the eve of the month of Kislev, the month of miracles and redemption.

With respect and blessing for good tidings.

## 8250

B"H, 28 Mar-Cheshvan, 5722
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 27 Cheshvan, in which you write regarding influencing P.

In general, it is visibly evident that when one exerts influence through friends and acquaintances, one succeeds to a much greater degree than through direct influence by those closest to the person. However, one should speak once, twice, or more, and not be discouraged if there are no immediate visible results.

Regarding your writing as to whether you should reside in a certain city due to a rumor you heard:

In general, we are not responsible for baseless rumors. Furthermore, and most importantly, it is stated in the Torah, "You shall be wholehearted with Hashem your G-d."

Since everything is by Divine Providence, it is my duty (and privilege) to awaken you to the necessity and personal obligation to set times for the study of the inner dimension of the Torah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus—a fixed time every day, with an increase on Shabbos, which is holy to Hashem.

It is also appropriate to have your tefillin checked, and surely you should set aside money for tzedakah every day in the morning before davening.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

**P.S.** You also mention a rumor in your letter in the name of a certain person, as if he said that regarding the Thirteen Principles of Faith, anyone who lacks belief in them, even inadvertently, is considered an apikores. According to the explanation added by the aforementioned person, this applies even if one is completely coerced, like a child captured among the gentiles, or even at a higher level, as he interprets the statements of Chazal in a different way.

See Rambam, Hilchos Teshuvah, Chapter 3, Halachah 7, and the Ra'avad's gloss—it is proven to the contrary.

A clearer proof is what is visibly evident regarding the first three principles, as everyone—without exception—lacks knowledge of their interpretation and their true content (see Chovos HaLevavos at the beginning of Shaar HaYichud, and many other places), especially according to what is explained at length and clearly in the books of Kabbalah and Chassidus.

And this is understood.

## 8,155

## 850

B"H, 2 Kislev, 5722
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch
in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established,
May they live,

Peace and Blessing!

It is a source of great wonder that for a long time now, there has been **no** information regarding what is happening in the Reshet. I believe this period has lasted for half a year **or more**, during which only the most minimal and fragmented reports have been received. Even these were only provided when necessary for a specific question or issue. It seems that several of the Reshet school principals hold the simple view that it is the responsibility of the Reshet administration to provide reports, and consequently, they themselves provide no information at all.

It is obvious that the intention here is not to complain about the past, but rather to address the future. May it be His will that this leads to action regarding the immediate future, with the necessary level of detail.

I am writing now regarding the matters of the month of Kislev of every year. The point is that, seemingly, the themes of the month of Kislev are not being utilized in the Reshet schools in general, and specifically regarding the inner point of *hafatzas hamaayanos*—the teachings of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs [adapted to the age, level of knowledge, and character of the students]. The intention here is not only regarding the days of the 10th and 19th of Kislev, but also regarding the days of Chanukah. Even if one were to say that not everyone will grasp the explanation of the connection between the days of Chanukah and *hafatzas hamaayanos* specifically [for the miracle was with oil, the *raza d'razin* of Torah—the spring that is the source of the well from which the river is drawn—and the mitzvah is to illuminate the entrance of one's house from the outside, which is *hafatzas hamaayanos chutzah*], surely they will accept the explanation that Chanukah signifies the spreading of the light of Torah with *mesiras nefesh*, without regard for any obstacles or hindrances, whether from within (the conduct of the home, the parents) or from without, as emphasized in the text of *Al Hanissim*, etc.

And even if one were to say that part of the days of Chanukah are vacation days in the aforementioned schools—as I am not aware of the schedules in the schools in the Holy Land regarding those days—surely they speak about the matters of Chanukah beforehand.

It is appropriate that immediately upon receiving this letter, you should consult regarding all of the above so that the preparations are made in good time and in a planned manner.

May it be His will that all of the above be with great success, and may you bring good and detailed reports.

With blessings for success in your holy work, with joy and goodness of heart.

## 8258

B"H, 12 Kislev, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs, Rabbi Meir Aryeh, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 9 Kislev, in which you write regarding a certain mitzvah, noting that it is clear (even from your letter) that there is a dispute as to whether it is a Torah-level obligation or a Rabbinic one, etc. However, what is **clear** and agreed upon by all opinions is that the mitzvah of "Love your neighbor as yourself" is a great principle of the Torah.

Similarly, another great principle of the Torah—and this, too, is a general matter rather than a specific mitzvah—is that whoever has the ability to protest [against wrongdoing] and does not protest, etc. (*Shabbos* 54b). Since Chazal knew that the *yetzer* might come to confuse and entice one into thinking that a protest would be futile, because even if one were to protest, they would not listen, they informed us that in such matters, "Only to the Ribono shel Olam is it revealed, and to human beings, who is it revealed?" (*Shabbos* 55a). The discussion there concerns those who, Heaven forbid, worshipped idols during the time of the Beis Hamikdash and for many years thereafter; yet, Chazal said what they said, and they did not settle for the aforementioned excuse. They taught us clearly that the protest—"You shall surely rebuke your neighbor"—is an obligation (**and according to all** opinions, this is a Torah-level obligation), extending even to striking, cursing, and rebuking. And what kind of striking is meant? This, too, is **explicit**: it is the type of striking where "Saul cast the spear at him to strike him" (see carefully *Arachin* 16b). And can one truly say to himself, with a whole heart, that he is of the category regarding whom Chazal said that it is revealed before Him whether the rebuke will be effective, and that he has already rebuked to the point of at least cursing and rebuking? [Even this is not enough, and it must reach the point of striking—as per the ruling in the aforementioned (according to the Rambam; and see the *Acharonim* on *Shulchan Aruch*, *Orach Chayim*, beginning of section 608)].

May it be the will [of Hashem] that, out of joy and goodness of heart, you utilize all the talents and abilities with which you have been gifted by Divine Providence in your current location, which has a *chazakah* and a **clear ruling** in the *Shulchan Aruch*—"The poor of your city take precedence," and this, too, is **according to all** opinions a Torah-level obligation.

Regarding what you wrote in your letter about "transgressing my words," etc.: Who am I and what am I to speak on such matters? **I have merely transcribed** clear legal rulings **from the holy Torah**, which was given to every single Jew at the standing at Har Sinai and [which remains] until this very day—as is known regarding the precision in the Ten Commandments, "I am Hashem your G-d," which is in the singular form specifically.

I have also noted the sources above. You can examine them yourself and clarify the matter.

With blessings for the utilization of your talents in the place that is best for you and in the manner that is best for you, and in accordance with the instruction of the days of Chanukah (that the *halachah* follows Beis Hillel): "Increasing and going forward, increasing and adding light."

**M. Schneerson**

## 8,550

[12 Kislev, 5722]

In response to your letter of 10/12,

It is surprising that it lacks the essential point—I am referring to the teaching of Chazal regarding the ultimate purpose of man’s creation, which is to serve his Creator (Maseches Kiddushin, at the end) through the study of Torah and the fulfillment of His mitzvos in daily life. Although you begin your letter by introducing yourself, you write nothing about your *kevius itim*—your fixed times for study—in our Torah, the Torah of life, nor regarding the fulfillment of His mitzvos, of which it is said, "and he shall live by them." I am certain you will complete this in your next correspondence.

It is my hope that it is unnecessary to add that one of the mitzvos is "love your fellow as yourself," which means to also influence your friends—may they live and be well—and your surroundings, so that they, too, conduct themselves in the aforementioned manner. And there is nothing that can stand in the way of willpower.

## 6,263

B"H, 18 Kislev, 5722
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Avraham, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 5 Kislev, in which you write the main points of your life story and conclude with a proposal you received regarding a rabbinical position in the country of Guatemala, and what is even more significant, activities in education on the purity of holiness. You have already agreed to this, tickets for the journey have been purchased, and an apartment has been prepared for you, and you ask: should you go?

Based on the ruling of our holy Torah, the Torah of life, that whoever sustains one soul of Israel is considered as if he had sustained an entire world—which applies to the sustenance of the life of this world, and certainly to the sustenance of the life of the World to Come as well—and considering the additional point that the aforementioned is in the category of "the poor of your city," since you originate from a South American country and know the language, etc.:

The proposal is correct and good with true goodness, in the sense of the interpretation of Chazal: "good for Heaven, good for people, and good for the one who produces fruit." You should travel to the aforementioned country and work there with *mesiras nefesh* in upholding and disseminating traditional Judaism. The merit of the many will assist you, and the immense value of this matter cannot be sufficiently described.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that you carry out the aforementioned with joy and a glad heart, and may you be successful.

Surely you are aware of the significance of the day of the tidings, the day of redemption, 19 Kislev—the redemption of the inner dimension of Torah that was revealed in the teachings of Chassidus, which emphasizes how love of a fellow Jew, love of Torah, and love of Hashem are one. This adds even more pleasantness to the aforementioned.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 6754

B"H, 18 Kislev, 5722
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 11 Kislev, in which you write of the difficulties in your current location and the idea of moving away, etc.,

Although for understandable reasons I did not want to mention what is written below, since you have brought it up in your letter, I have no choice but to take a position on the matter, namely:

**Even** if it were a straightforward matter to move from your current location, it is not appropriate to settle in the city you mention. For the sake of strengthening *shalom bayis* in all respects, one should live with one’s husband and child—may they live—not near or in the same city as the parents—may they live. This is seen in practice in the vast majority of cases, that this is not desirable. For many reasons, which are not dependent on you, in your case this is true in an even stronger form.

Regarding the core issue—that you are experiencing difficulties in your current location—taking into account that the *mosad* is still relatively new, it is no wonder that one encounters difficulties, and consequently, this affects the conveniences needed by those in the *mosad*. However, there is no doubt that when you and [your] husband—may he live—look at the *mosad* and your work within it not as a forced or imposed task, and not as something done for the benefit of the *mosad* or other such reasons, but rather that this is for your own benefit as well, you will be able to reach an understanding with those who have a connection to the *mosad* much more quickly and easily, and be able to organize matters more readily.

Furthermore, and this is the main point: when you look at the *mosad* as mentioned above, there is no doubt that this will provide the opportunity to grow both *b'gashmius* and *b'ruchnius*, which in another place would hardly offer similar possibilities. One of the reasons is, as mentioned earlier, that the *mosad* is still new in the city, and the city has **many** possibilities in various areas. With the proper energy, and with *simcha* and a good heart, you will have *hatzlacha muflaga* both *b'gashmius* and *b'ruchnius*, both for the benefit of the individual—for yourselves—and for the benefit of the *klal*.

What is written above is based on similar experiences that have occurred in other cities, and the result was as stated above. Therefore, perhaps according to your perspective, and that of others who do not know of these other experiences or only have a superficial knowledge, the matter is not so clear, but the fact is as stated above.

Everything written until now is only from the standpoint of *sechel* and calculations *al pi teva*.

However, no less important—and perhaps even more so—is to reflect on the truth that this is work in a *mosad* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *Nasi Yisrael*, by whose name it is called. When the work is done with *mesiras nefesh*, dedication, and a good heart, this will add to the *hisorerus rachamim rabim* from the *baal hatziyon hakadosh*, where you will be mentioned for an increase in blessing and success in all your matters, both *klali* and *prati*.

With blessings for good news regarding all that has been said, and we are, after all, on the eve of 19 Kislev—also for good news regarding 19 Kislev and the upcoming Chanukah.

## 8,105

B"H, 18 Kislev, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from Wednesday, in which you write regarding your *kvius itim l’Torah*—the study sessions you have set for yourself, as well as your *limud b’rabim* (public teaching), etc.—and you conclude by mentioning the difficulty you are encountering in studying Tanya.

The wonder and surprise are understandable: given that you are capable of studying the *shiurim* you mention in your letter, it is puzzling that you encounter the aforementioned difficulty in studying Tanya. It can only be that the order of study—what comes first and what comes later—is not being done in the appropriate manner.

In this case, the correct approach is to first study Part III of Tanya, *Iggeret HaTeshuvah*, then the second part, *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah*, and only afterwards Part I of Tanya.

It is also good, at the beginning of your study, to have a set time to study the *Kuntres Uma'ayon* (by the Rebbe Rashab, *n.e.*), which surely can be found among *anash* in your camp.

We are currently in an *eis segulah* for these matters, as we find ourselves on the eve of the 19th of Kislev, the *Yom HaBesorah* and *Chag HaGeulah*.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all the above, and with blessings for *Chag HaGeulah*.

***

Regarding the explanation in Rashi at the beginning of *Parshas Toldos*: "And these are the generations of Isaac"—"Jacob and Esau, who are mentioned in the *parshah*." The question is: what is this teaching us? The explanation given is that the "generations of Isaac" prove that (as the verse continues) "Abraham begot Isaac," for a *mamzer* does not beget.

This explanation requires further study (*tzarich iyun gadol*), for according to this, Rashi’s words are entirely superfluous.

According to the *peshat*, it can be explained that the entire Rashi at the beginning of the aforementioned *parshah* is one continuous thought: "And these are the generations of Isaac"—(meaning) Jacob and Esau, who are mentioned in the *parshah*. (If so, the continuation of the verse poses a difficulty): "Abraham begot Isaac" (which has no connection to the story of Jacob and Esau). The resolution is: "Because he wrote..." etc., and the matter is understood.

***

**The correct approach:** See also above, Vol. 21, Letter 6,170, and the references in the notes there. See below, Letter 6,511.

**For a *mamzer* does not beget:** See *Baal HaTurim*, *Ki Seitzei* 23:2.

## 6870

B"H, 18 Kislev, 5722

As we stand between redemption and redemption, and in the time connecting redemption to redemption—which, although as explained in other places, differ in their nature, the common denominator between them is that both are redemptions that are visible and revealed even to physical eyes. Moreover, they arrive with the full consent of the "other side" [ha'le'umaz], which had been concealing, hiding, and opposing prior to the redemption.

As King David said in the verse of redemption: "He has redeemed my soul in peace... for there were many with me".

May it be His will that this be the case in all the matters about which you write, and as mentioned, that even that which had been concealing and hiding until now will be transformed into an assistant and a redeemer.

## 6,767

[18 Kislev, 5722]

...And as we stand between one Geulah and another—and as is explained in other places, the distinction between them—at the same time, the common denominator is that they are a Geulah that is visible and revealed to the physical eye. Furthermore, this occurs with the full agreement of the "other side" [ha'le'umaz], which had been concealing and hiding things prior to the Geulah.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that this be the case in all the matters about which you write, and as stated, that the details which have until now been hidden and concealed will be transformed into assistants and agents of redemption.

And in accordance with the saying of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, that when the Ribono shel Olam gives Bnei Yisrael the ability and the possibility, Bnei Yisrael will show how they fulfill through this the concept of "In all your ways know Him."

This is the inner point of the teachings of Chassidus and its guidance: to serve Hashem in all matters, down to their smallest details.

And at an even deeper inner point: to show the world that Hashem is the Elokim and there is nothing else besides Him.

May the avodah in this be without concealments or hiddenness, and with joy and a glad heart.

With blessings for good tidings and with the blessing of the Chag HaGeulah.

## 8170

B"H, 21 Kislev, 5722
Brooklyn.

To the avreichim participating in the regular study of Nigleh and Chassidus, and in the manner of achieving a special kavanah to maintain knowledge and connection with one another — in the city of Montreal,
May Hashem keep them alive.

Peace and blessing!

With pleasure, I received your letter from the night of the Chag HaGeulah, 19 Kislev, along with your names.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires for the good, regarding what was mentioned and what is contained in your letter.

May it be the will of Hashem that all of this be in a manner of "increasing and continuing," which is also one of the instructions of the upcoming days of Chanukah: to increase in light from day to day.

There is a further allusion in this, that the source of the light and its increase is from *shemen* (oil), the "secrets of secrets of the Torah." Through the study of the teachings of Chassidus—which reveals even the "secrets of secrets," to the point of actual understanding and comprehension—this will permeate all matters. In the language of the verse, "In all your ways [until you reach the goal] know Him" (*Mishlei 3:6*); "Know the G-d of your father, etc." (*Divrei Hayamim I 28:9*). This leads to a "perfect heart," a *mitzvah ramah* (high commandment) and exalted, and on the contrary, it surpasses them all (see *Kuntres Acharon 156b*).

With blessings for good tidings in all that was mentioned, and for a Chanukah appropriate to the above.

## 6171

B"H, 22 Kislev, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Following the interval, I received your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, in which you write regarding your state of mind, which is not as it should be.

It is surprising, for surely you know that one of the foundations of our faith and our Torah is the simple belief in the matter of Hashgacha Pratis, especially according to what is explained clearly in the teachings of Chassidus: that this applies to every detail and the minute details of the entire creation, and all the more so regarding Bnei Yisrael.

Since the Ribono shel Olam watches over you within the entirety of Klal Yisrael down to the smallest details, it is understood by logic—and it is an explicit verse in Scripture—"Hashem is for me, I will not fear," and "Hashem is my shepherd, I shall not lack." There is no need to elaborate on a matter that is understood even with slight hisbonenus.

Sometimes, one of the reasons for a state of mind that is not as it should be is a general weakness in health. Therefore, you should also consult a doctor and follow his instructions, for the Torah has given the physician permission to heal.

I trust you are keeping up with the three daily shiurim of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, as is well known. It is also appropriate that you have your tefillin checked, if this has not been done within the last twelve months.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

#### ***6171***

**It is surprising:** See also below, Igros 6194, 6217.

## 8173

In response to his letters from the day of the tidings, 19 Kislev (and those preceding it), the day of our redemption and the liberation of our souls, in which he writes regarding his holy work in chinuch al taharas hakodesh, which draws the hearts of the children of Bnei Yisrael to our Father in Heaven... and his letter was indeed written on that day of tidings, the Rosh Hashanah for the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus.

**The davening of the female students:** In his letter: "I wanted to know whether girls are obligated in the entire davening like boys, or only parts of it."
