In our school, too, such an organization exists... and I saw that girls also serve in the role of policewomen; I did not find this to be appropriate."

## 874

874

B”H, the first night of Chanukah, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the congregation of Yeshurun, lovers and cherishers of Torah and mitzvos, may they live,

Peace and blessing!

As we enter the luminous days of Chanukah, it is an appropriate time to reflect on where we stand regarding the dissemination of the light of **ner mitzvah v’Torah ohr** in our daily lives—both **al pesach beiso**, within one’s own home, and **mibachutz**, in the outside world. This is, in essence, the "practical" significance of Chanukah and the **ner Chanukah**.

Even if one can be satisfied in many respects with the achievements of the past days and years, it is certainly not enough. For the **ner Chanukah** teaches that there must be **mosif v’holech, mosif v’ohr**—that all matters of Torah and holiness must be spread and strengthened in an **increasing measure**, just as we light the Chanukah candles in a constantly growing number each night of Chanukah.

And even if there are difficulties, Chanukah demands **mesiras nefesh** from a Yid. Although the mesiras nefesh required today in a country like America is quite far from the mesiras nefesh that was demanded of Mattisyahu and his sons, and quite far even from the mesiras nefesh that Yidden demonstrate today in certain countries where Yidden and Yiddishkeit are persecuted and oppressed, *rachmana litzlan*—this does not mean that the danger of **l’hashkicham Torasecha** is smaller or less relevant in free countries than in enslaved ones. The danger of "peaceful assimilation" is in many respects even more serious than the danger of "forced assimilation."

The means to halt and remove this danger is to increase and spread **yeshiva chinuch**, education **al taharas hakodesh**—"Chinuch-Hashem."

This is not merely a question of bringing more Yiddishe children into the yeshivos, although every Yiddishe child is an **olam malei**, an entire world unto himself. It also means that each one of them must be a shining light, to spread and illuminate the entire surroundings with Torah-Yiddishkeit. The candles and the wicks are, B”H, present; one only needs to add a spark.

And this has always been the primary mission of the students of the Lubavitcher yeshivos—**neros l’ha’ir**, luminous candles, lights that shine and illuminate and ignite new candles constantly.

At the same time, the *baalei-batim* must, for their part—the **tomchei-temimim**, the supporters and friends of Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch—provide and generate the necessary financial assistance in an increasing measure.

The annual campaign of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch provides an opportunity to realize the content of Chanukah in a practical way. This opportunity signifies a duty and responsibility that must not be missed.

Participation in the work of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch throughout the entire year, and especially on the occasion of the annual campaign, in an increased and growing measure—in accordance with the content of Chanukah—will certainly bring to each and every one of the participants the Ribono shel Olam’s blessings, also in an increased and growing measure, in both material and spiritual matters, for themselves and their families, *shichyu*.

With respect and blessing, and with a blessing for Chanukah,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8175

By the Grace of G-d
25 Kislev, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Rabbi Shimon Yisrael, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

Based on my recollection that we have met in the past, and now that the Siddur of the Arizal by R. Sh. of Rashkov—which, as noted in the introduction, you have prepared for publication—has been brought to me, I feel it is my duty to express my strong hope, based on the promise of Chazal that "one mitzvah leads to another," that the action mentioned regarding the dissemination of the wellsprings—the wellsprings of the wisdom of truth—in print, meaning that it reaches the "outside" as well, will have a continuation. My intention is the study of this wisdom, the wisdom of Kabbalah, the *pnimiyus haTorah* that in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus, and all the more so, *kal v’chomer*.

Regarding the *kavanos* of *tefillah*, you have done [the work], etc., but "not every mind and heart can bear this." For this, one requires both the mind and the heart. Furthermore, it is self-evident that regarding the *kavanos* of *tefillah*, one must study the subjects, whereas the opposite is true: one can study the *pnimiyus haTorah*, the wisdom of Kabbalah, and (in the language of the *Rishonim*) "pray to understand this" (see *Shu"t HaRivash*, responsum 157).

If, regarding the performance of *mitzvos*, there must first be study that leads to action, then all the more so regarding the *kavanah* of *tefillah*, which requires much caution, as is explained in many places.

It is understood that the study of Kabbalah is not sufficient for this; the study of Chassidus is essential, as it explains the concepts of Kabbalah and strips them of their materiality. Without this abstraction, in the words of the Tzemach Tzedek, "The Baal Shem Tov commanded not to study books of Kabbalah (because without this knowledge) to strip the matters of their materiality, one becomes very materialized through this study, etc. And even though the words of the Arizal are faithful and true, and when they called the *Shechinah* by the name *Malchus*, etc." (see *Shoresh Mitzvas HaTefillah* by the Tzemach Tzedek, end of chapter 2 and chapter 8 there).

Since you have influence over many, the merit of the public surely depends on you—to disseminate the study of the teachings of Chassidus, as the instruction of the days of Chanukah teaches: to increase and continue in light—*Torah Ohr* and the light within the Torah.

As a token of my appreciation for receiving the aforementioned Siddur, I have noted a few points, albeit in haste. Since you are engaged in preparing it for print, they are enclosed herewith.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

**Regarding the Siddur of the Arizal – R. Sh. of Rashkov. Brooklyn, 5721.**

R. Sh. of Rashkov – In the *Shem HaGedolim HeChadash*, it is written that he was a student of the Maggid (and not a student of the Baal Shem Tov). This requires clarification.

At the beginning: **2a** "The general nature of the *tikkun*, etc.": See regarding this: *Shaar HaKavanos*, *Tefillas HaShachar*, *drush* 2-3. *Peri Etz Chaim*, *Shaar HaTefillah*, chapters 1, 5, 7. *Olas Tamid*, page 6, 8 (Jerusalem edition, 5667). *Nehar Shalom*, 48a, 54a and onwards (also printed at the end of *Etz Chaim*, Warsaw edition). *Shemen Sasson* on *Shaar HaKavanos* there.

There, Part 4, *Seder Tefillas Shacharis*, item 6.

The line beginning "The general nature of the *chitzonim*" should read: "the *chitzoniyus*."

The line beginning "When he turns, *tzitzis*, *tefillin*" – note *Berachos* 15a, *Zohar* Vol. 3, 120b, *Bach* to *Tur Orach Chaim*, end of section 2.

The line beginning "For in *Asiyah*, in *Asiyah*, etc., good and evil are mixed, etc., in *Yetzirah* they are not mixed" – this requires study, as (almost) everywhere it is explained that in *Yetzirah*, good and evil are mixed (*Etz Chaim*, *Shaar Maz*, chapter 4; *Shaar Maamarei Rashbi*, chapter 3; *Maamarei Rashbi*, *Maseches Heichalos HaKlipos*, chapter 4; and in many other places). It is only in *Etz Chaim*, *Shaar 39*, end of the introduction to the *drush*, that it is written that in *Yetzirah* they are not mixed.

See also *Shaar HaLikutim* on the verse "And Avimelech looked out."

In the book *Toamei Chaim Zochu* on *Etz Chaim*, *Shaar 37*, chapter 4, he distinguishes between when it is a time of *pegam* (flaw) and when it is a time of merit. This requires further study.

Indeed, even in the book *Saraf Peri Etz Chaim* (by R. Moshe of Dolina, one of the students of the Baal Shem Tov), *Shaar 1*, chapter 2, in the explanation of "when he turns, etc.," he writes that "in *Yetzirah* they are not mixed."

However, in *Shaar HaKavanos* (the aforementioned, page 6), he writes in his explanation of this very subject: "For in *Asiyah* and *Yetzirah* there is a mixture of good and evil." This is also the case in *Peri Etz Chaim* there, chapters 5 and 7, and in *Olas Tamid* there.

At the end: *Seder HaAvilus*. "A *shita* from his mouth, one should not go, etc." This is the case in *Maamarei Rashbi*, *Maseches Gemilus Chasadim*, end of chapter 2.

It is a *shita*. When it is prominent in *Horayos* 13b – it is written plainly, but it is explained as such in *Taamei HaMitzvos* by R. Chaim Vital, end of *Parshas Vayechi*. And so it is written in *Maamarei Rashbi* there.

Based on the words of Chazal regarding the importance of "ears to the basket," it is appropriate: a) To compile an index. The more detailed the index, the more praiseworthy it is. b) To note all the pages and also the sides (this is missing at the beginning of Part 2, at the end of Part 3, etc.). c) This notation should be done in one sweep—from the beginning of the section until its **end**. And not that Part 2 and Part 3 should begin again from **1**.

## 8170

8170

B"H, Sunday, the first night of Chanukah, 5722

1) Since it appears that P. (according to the attached sheet) is distancing himself from time to time from the source from which he draws, and is not utilizing his talents as he ought (both in quantity and quality), in accordance with the statement of our Sages (Kesuvos 67a) regarding the great necessity that it be specifically "as he ought,"

And especially in light of the words that hew flames of fire in Tanya, Chapter 30, regarding what is explained there as to how laziness and sluggishness affect the entirety of a person’s avodah—there is no **ganze** (complete) standing—and also in the details of his avodah (Chapter 26).

And on the other hand—the greatness of the virtue of alacrity, etc., which is stated and repeated in the words of our Sages (Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 21).

Since my actions in this regard, to improve the aforementioned, have not yet been effective at all,

Behold, even though perhaps according to the halachic ruling, I could say that I am not in a position to protest, and the proof is that my words are not being heard (except by the external ear—in which case the choice is not in my hands, as explained in Nedarim 32b, and consequently, at times, I have also received an answer—a pretext from the lips **and outward**).

And what is the demand upon me—for surely P. can justify his conduct—since I do not see who will "gain" from the answer and the order that will result from this answer—I will try once more—in a manner different from that which has been done until now, and perhaps, etc.,

And it is this: at the end of every week—that is, on Erev Shabbos—they shall ask P. in my name, from the secretariat, about what has been done during the week to improve the aforementioned (naturally—**in detail**), and the answer shall be delivered to me in writing so that it may endure for many days, and after a few weeks, and no later than the 10th of Shevat, G-d willing—the situation will surely be clarified.

And may it be the will of Hashem that it be in a manner of "increasing and adding light."

## 8,167

B"H, 26 Kislev, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 1 Kislev, in which you ask for advice regarding the fact that your husband, may he live and be well, wishes to move from your current apartment, while you are opposed to this for various reasons, etc.

In my opinion, once you have already told your husband, may he live and be well, your reasons for not wanting to move, you should not involve yourself in this any further. Most importantly, do not take it to heart, regardless of how it proceeds or how it turns out. After all, a person does not truly know what is better, and once you have done what depends on you, you must rely on Hashem Yisbarach that it will be for the good, for Hashem, may He be blessed, watches over everyone in accordance with what they need.

And just as in the past things have turned out better than one could have imagined in many matters, may it be so in this as well.

With blessings for a happy Chanukah and for good tidings.

#### ***8,167***

## 8,178

8,178

B”H, 26 Kislev, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 23 Kislev.

At an opportune time, I will mention you at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the contents of your letter.

It gave me pleasure to read in your letter about your holy work in disseminating traditional Judaism among those who fear the word of Hashem, especially the youth.

I have strong hope that you also utilize your influence to encourage assistance for the activities of Beis Lubavitch in your camp, for our Sages have taught us that "one mitzvah leads to another," and there is nothing that can stand before the will.

Regarding what you wrote about the *nusach* (prayer rite) — the ruling in the *shailos u’teshuvos* of the later authorities is well known: it is permissible to change from *Nusach Ashkenaz* to *Nusach Sefard*, and from *Nusach Sefard* to *Nusach Ari* (but not the reverse). This is especially true since, as you write, you pray in a synagogue where the *nusach* is not *Nusach Ashkenaz*.

Regarding what you wrote about the manner of *davening* — in general, even when one *davens* with eyes closed, it is proper to have the *Siddur* open to the place where one is *davening*. This is helpful against distracting thoughts, as is evident in practice.

The overall *davening*, whether with eyes closed or from the *Siddur* — and this is, of course, excluding the first verse of *Krias Shema*, which must be recited with eyes closed.

In general, no two people are the same in this regard. Furthermore, even for the same person, it varies from time to time as to which method makes it easier to strive for *kavanah*. A person knows his own soul and must decide for himself.

Regarding what you wrote about the well-known matter — in general, the advice for this is to increase the letters of Torah and *tefillah*, and likewise to increase in *tzedakah*. Among the auspicious times for this is every weekday morning, before *davening* the morning prayers, to set aside a few coins for *tzedakah*.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all that was mentioned.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

**P.S.** I trust you participated in the *farbrengen* of the Day of the Announcement, the Festival of Redemption, 19 Kislev.

## 8179

B"H, 26 Kislev, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 4 Kislev, which reached me in due time.

At an opportune moment, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter.

It is understood, and indeed simple, that conducting one’s daily life in accordance with the instructions of our Torah—the Torah of life—and through the fulfillment of its mitzvos, of which it is said, "that he may live by them," serves as the channel and vessel for receiving the blessings of Hashem for all that a person and his household require.

Regarding the matter of financial hardship, the advice offered by our Sages is well-known: to increase in tzedakah and to distribute it in many small portions. One of the auspicious times for this is every weekday morning before davening, by setting aside a few coins for tzedakah.

As for what you wrote regarding your peace of mind—you must contemplate the foundation of our faith and our Torah: that Hashem, may He be blessed and exalted, oversees every individual with Divine providence, and that He is the essence of good, and it is the nature of the Good to bestow good. However, one must be a prepared vessel for this—meaning, living according to the will of Hashem as He has revealed it to us in our Torah, the Torah of life. When this matter is engraved in your mind, there is no room to say that when you remember that Hashem is observing your actions **now**, you would do something that has no place in your intellect.

Regarding your writing that you do not find meaning in your work: since the salary you receive provides you with the possibility to support your family—may they live—and surely also to set aside tzedakah from time to time, and in your spare time to also learn, this is the strongest and most pleasant meaning a person can find in his life.

As for your writing that you do not have much spare time for Torah study: in your situation, it is not required of you to learn for many hours. Rather, you should begin (but—immediately!) with a small amount of time each day at first. After not too long a time, add a few more moments to this small amount. You will certainly discover that you have **much** spare time for Torah study. In the phrasing of our Sages, "the more one expands, the more one finds." In such a case, the practice is that, first and foremost, one learns the halachos necessary for daily life, to know the actions one is required to perform and the things one is forbidden to do.

We are currently in the days of Chanukah, the essence of which is to increase in light from day to day—to go and increase. May it be His will that this be the case in all your affairs.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

***

**8179**

**The advice offered by our Sages is well-known:** See also above, Vol. 21, Letter 8182; Vol. 17, Letter 6335. Below, Letter 8343; Letter 8376; Letter 8467.

**In the phrasing of our Sages:** Eruvin 82b, and elsewhere.

## 880

B"H, 27 Kislev, 5722
Brooklyn.

To the avreich, Zecharyah, may he live,
Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 25 Kislev, the first night of Chanukah, in which you ask:

1) Regarding the phrase in Kaddish, "before their Father in Heaven," which is in the third person—seemingly, the chazzan excludes himself and the congregation from this.

The word "their Father" follows the preceding phrase, "for all the House of Israel," which includes the congregants and the chazzan as well. Similarly, the phrase in Kaddish D'Rabbanan, "from before their Father in Heaven," follows the beginning of the passage, "upon Israel." Generally, this phrasing was chosen (as written in the Sefer Abudraham) because it is the language used by our Sages (in the Mishnah, Rosh Hashanah, end of chapter 3, in various places).

2) According to the opinion that twin sisters were born with the tribes, why does the Torah not mention them as it mentions Dinah?

In our Torah, only that which is relevant to our knowledge is written. As for Dinah, there is a lengthy account in our Torah regarding her.

3) Why did Yehudah not marry the twin sister of one of the tribes, instead marrying a Canaanite woman?

Rashi has already explained that "Canaanite" here means a merchant, based on the statement of the Gemara in Pesachim (50a).

It is surprising that you write questions from across the sea, when you are studying in a yeshivah and should be turning to your teachers and mentors with these questions, and they will answer you.

Since every matter is by Divine Providence, it is my hope that this letter will inspire you to increase your diligence and perseverance in the study of Torah, and also to set fixed times for the study of Chassidus. The Tzeirei Chabad in your camp and in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, can generally advise you on the appropriate order and method of study for you.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

880
Yehudah... Canaanite: See also Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 5, p. 263, note 34.

## 8181

B"H, 27 Kislev, 5722
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent in communal affairs, R' Dovid, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

After a very long hiatus, your letter of 23 Kislev was received. Even in it, you write nothing regarding the general matters of Chabad, and first and foremost, the Reshet, nor do you confirm receipt of previous letters, even though there is a *chazakah* that a messenger—the postal service—performs his mission.

You write regarding the construction of the mikveh in Petach Tikvah, concerning the plan to have one mikveh above another, and the benefits of this arrangement.

Since the esteemed Rabbi, etc., R' Y. Landau of Bnei Brak has spoken about this (and apparently on several occasions) with the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory, it is appropriate that you contact him and clarify the details with him, as I have no knowledge of this beyond the list that was published (in the sefer *Taharas HaMayim* by R' N. Telushkin).

Although time does not permit me to examine this and write at the necessary length, it seems simple that the greatest benefit of the aforementioned method of construction is that the immersion takes place in the *otzar* itself, with the floor merely dividing it into two parts, and the floor is nullified in its function due to the holes within it; the benefits of immersing in the *otzar* itself are many.

Regarding what you wrote—that there are those who say it is difficult to dry off—this is not understood at all. On the contrary, drying off is easier, since the water is not only drawn by a pump from above, but the remnants flow down into the *otzar* beneath the floor.

If you believe it is appropriate that I write regarding the above to the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent in communal affairs, R' Yisroel Eidelman, please inform me and I will write to him, as we are in correspondence.

In general, for many reasons, it is correct that the mikveh be on the ground level and not on the second floor. Seemingly, even from the architect's perspective, there should be a desire for this, and the construction costs would also be lower.

Regarding women, one must minimize their exertion in this regard **as much as possible**, including the exertion of climbing stairs, among several other reasons—some of which are even mentioned in *Bais HaLevi*—that it is better for a women's mikveh to be arranged in a way that they do not need to walk extensively within the building.

As per your request, the letter is being sent without waiting for its turn.

With blessings for good tidings.

***

**8181**

**R' Dovid, may he live:** Chanzin, Petach Tikvah. Additional letters to him: see above, Vol. 20, 7880, and the references in the footnotes there.

**Chazakah:** Eruvin 31b, and references there.

**Mikveh above a mikveh:** See also above, Vol. 20, letter 7818 (p. 82), and the references in the footnotes there.

## 8,282

B”H, 27 Kislev, 5722
Brooklyn.

Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be built and established,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the printed report of the national farbrengen, etc.

Since thirty days have passed since the resolutions were adopted, I must point out that it is most appropriate to conduct a review and summary of what has been accomplished during these first thirty days.

For even if we assume that everything required by the aforementioned resolutions has been carried out, a periodic accounting and summary will certainly increase energy, etc. And this is all the more so if there is anyone who is lacking in the fulfillment of these resolutions. A word to the wise is sufficient.

May it be the will of Hashem that the conduct regarding these resolutions will be in accordance with the adage and instruction of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi of Yisrael (also transcribed in the aforementioned report): speak less, think more, and do even more.

It is certain that the instruction to "speak less" refers primarily to the necessity of action that follows.

Regarding the section discussing the study of a unified *hemshech* of *maamarim* of *Chassidus*:

For the time being, only a question has been received, not a proposal. Naturally, it must be a *hemshech* that can be obtained in the Holy Land—printed, or at the very least, mimeographed—and it must also be something that the vast majority of *anash* desire. Based on these points, they should reach a decision among themselves.

I await good news regarding all of the above, and may it be the will of Hashem that it comes with true tranquility, joy, and a good heart.

It is worth noting the Gemara in *Makkos* (3b) that thirty days are considered as a year (even regarding a matter that has no connection at all to the concept of a year).

An explanation for this may be that a month in relation to the moon is the concept of a year in relation to the sun.

## 8,183

8,183

B"H, 27 Kislev, 5722
Brooklyn.

To the Committee of Kfar Chabad, founded and directed by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi of Yisrael in our Holy Land—may it be built and established by Mashiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days—
May Hashem grant them life.

Peace and Blessing!

Following a delay, your letter from the end of Cheshvan was received; it, too, took longer than usual to arrive.

You write regarding the addition of housing units in Kfar Chabad: whether to build them on the plots remaining within the village, or on plots that one hopes to be able to annex to the existing village area through effort, etc.

First and foremost, it must be clarified whether there are indeed plots available within the village. My intention is to take into account general matters necessary for the development of the village in its current state—and all the more so for when it expands—such as public facilities, park areas, and the like. Naturally, these do not belong on additional plots at the edge of the village, but rather within it; this is not the case for housing units.

If, even after the aforementioned calculation, there are vacant plots, then naturally the housing units should be built on those plots. This is because now is the opportune time to receive appropriate assistance from various government offices, which may not be the case later on. Furthermore, and most importantly, there are many families of Anash who are looking for suitable housing.

2) Regarding the establishment of a "silo" warehouse: In general, the matter is correct, as it will suffice and serve as a warehouse for the settlements surrounding Kfar Chabad as well. Through this, the influence of Kfar Chabad will increase, in addition to the aspect of livelihood involved in the matter.

In terms of details, it is of course necessary to clarify with experts in the field, and it would be best to consult those who know (at least by estimation) the plans of the relevant government offices regarding the development of the poultry industry in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established.

3) Regarding the method of developing industry in Kfar Chabad: As past experience has shown, it is worthwhile to focus on methods of production that engage and employ a few families. My intention is to rule out the two extremes: neither that of a single family, nor that of dozens of families together, as the latter makes coordination, cooperation, etc., extremely difficult.

Among the branches of industry, one must rule out—as I have written previously—matters that are dependent on kashrus, which ultimately leads to leniencies and even greater leniencies, and the wise will understand.

4) An exception to the above (from section 3) is regarding the baking of Shmurah [Matzah]. I have been—and still am—astonished by the negligence regarding this, at a time when, for several reasons, it would have been possible to develop the baking of Shmurah with the utmost hiddur in Kfar Chabad on a **significant** scale. There is no concern here for leniencies or the like, since the unique aspect of this would be the second line: *mehadrin min hamehadrin*.

It is obvious that my intention here is not to diminish the portion of those who have been involved in this in past years, and certainly not to deprive them of their share. It is understood that they have priority in the aforementioned, but...

#### ***8,183***

**For the baking of Shmurah:** See also below, letter 8,191.

## 6105

B"H, 29 Kislev, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Rabbi, G-d-fearing, distinguished, etc., Meir, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the publication containing your article, which was printed in connection with the day of good tidings, 19 Kislev. Thank you for your thoughtfulness in sending it to me.

May it be the will of Hashem that, as a continuation of the victory of the Baal Shem Tov’s Torah in those days at this time, the light should go on spreading, increasing, and shining ever brighter. This is in line with the concept of these days of Chanukah, where the miracle occurred with the oil of the "secrets of secrets" (*razin d'razin*). From this, the commandment for all generations was derived: that the candles should burn at the entrance of one's house **on the outside**, so that the wellsprings will spread outward until they reach even the "outside"—even that place which the Torah of kindness testifies is "outside"—and that they should reach there specifically through the *razin d'razin* of the Torah. For it is specifically that which is higher that reaches lower (as explained in *Shaarei Orah* in various places, as noted in the index).

And from one matter to another, may the prophecy be fulfilled that "the Master is coming, this is King Moshiach."

It is also worth noting the statement of Rabbi Pinchas ben Yair: "Chassidus leads to... Eliyahu the Prophet," who is the herald of the Redemption.

With respect and blessing,

## 8780

B”H, 29 Kislev, 5722
Brooklyn

The Rabbinical Committee of East Flatbush
May Hashem protect them and grant them life,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Following the long silence regarding your activities in the holy work of the purity of a holy people—the construction of the mikveh in your neighborhood—I was pleased to receive your notification regarding the second candle, that the construction is progressing.

May it be Hashem’s will that, in accordance with the instruction of these days in which your letter and my response were written, the progress will continue to increase from day to day, and all those who merited to begin this great mitzvah will also merit to see it to its completion.

May it be His will that this happens very soon, in our immediate future.

There is also a connection to the content of the days of Chanukah, for the war was fought because they wanted to force them to abandon the laws of Your will—specifically the *chukim* (statutes). This is also the matter of *tumah* and *taharah*, for it is a clear and revealed matter that the laws of *tumah* and *taharah* are *gezeiras hakasuv* (divine decrees), and they are among the *chukim*. The same applies to *tevilah* (Rambam, end of Hilchos Mikvaos).

May it be His will that we see the fulfillment, in our immediate future, of the conclusion of those words of the Rambam: "I will sprinkle upon you pure water," which is followed by, "And I will take you from among the nations, and I will gather you from all the lands, and I will bring you to your own land," in the true and complete Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

And from one subject to another, on the same subject: The words of the Rambam there, although seemingly part of *aggadah*, teach us a great principle in the **halachos** of *taharah*. He writes: "It is a clear and revealed matter... there is an allusion in this: just as one who directs his heart to become pure, once he immerses, he is pure... so too, one who directs his heart to purify his soul... once he resolves in his heart to separate from those evil counsels and brings his soul into the 'waters of knowledge' (*mei hada'as*), he is pure."

This comes to teach us, and we find that we learn, that *tevilah* is not merely a matter of removing *tumah* (to separate from those evil counsels), but also an act of purification (bringing his soul into the "waters of knowledge") and an ongoing action (just as it is an act of bringing into the "waters of knowledge").

To clarify the inquiry of the Gaon Rogatchover on this (in *Sefer Tzafnas Paneach*, Hilchos Matnos Aniyim 7:4; and see *Sefer Mefaneach Tzufunos* by Rabbi Kasher, p. 122, where he quotes his words, etc.).

With respect and with a blessing for success in your holy work.

## 8787

B"H, Chanukah, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the G-d-fearing, industrious, and upright man, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Avraham Yitzchak, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

After a long interval, your letter from the 7th of Kislev was received.

As we stand in the days of Chanukah, may it be His will that everything in this regard be in a manner of "increasing and going forward, increasing in light," which is also one of the lessons of the days of Chanukah: that one increases in light from day to day.

There is a further allusion here: the source of this light and its increase is from the "oil"—the secrets of the secrets of the Torah. Through the study of Chassidus, which reveals even the secrets of secrets to the point of actual understanding and comprehension, one will infuse light into all matters. In the words of the verse, "In all your ways [until you reach the goal] know Him" (Mishlei 3:6)—know the G-d of your father, etc.—and this leads to a "perfect heart," a mitzvah that is exalted and lofty, and indeed, surpasses them all (see Kuntres Acharon, 156b).

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned, and for a Chanukah appropriate to the above.

## 8288

[Late Chanukah]

... Regarding the note at the end of the *Iggeres HaKodesh* of the Alter Rebbe, *d.h. Hocheiach Tochiach* — just as the external aspect of *Zachor* is hinted at within its internal aspect in the words "the *kavanah* **in the Shabbos tefillah**," so too is there **literally** room to hint at the external aspect of *Shamor* within its internal aspect through a slight modification of his holy language, namely: "The cessation from speech **regarding physical activities**." Furthermore, it seems that even without the aforementioned modification, this is the intended meaning, for what other interpretation could there be for the matter of "physical speech"? The continuation, "just as He rested, etc.," also proves this.

#### 8288

This letter is addressed to Rabbi Ephraim Eliezer Yalles, and was written on the margin of his letter dated Wednesday, the fourth night of Chanukah. Additional letters to him are found above in Vol. 21, 7963, and in the references noted there. See below 8321, 8454, 8418, 8437.

**Regarding the note:** In his letter: "And by the way, I will review the chapter (at the end of the *Kuntres Acharon*) that we mentioned in the holy sanctuary of our holy and pure Rebbe [the Rebbe Rayatz] *zy"a* and *v'ch"a*. Surely the Alter Rebbe did not come to innovate or even to explain the *halachos* of Shabbos and their sources, but rather to emphasize the gravity of the sin of idle chatter on *Shabbos Kodesh*. For this purpose, he explained what is known to those who fear Heaven, that in all *mitzvos* there is an internal and an external aspect, and this is true of Shabbos as well.

If so, seemingly it would have sufficed to mention the external aspect of Shabbos (in the category of *Shamor*) as in "just as He rested, etc.," and the internal aspect of the category of *Shamor* as in "just as He rested, etc." Yet, it appears from his holy and illuminating words that he also wished to mention the category of *Zachor*. If so, why did he not begin with the external aspect, as it is stated, "And He sanctified it and blessed it, etc.," and afterwards the internal aspect, as it is written, "A Shabbos to Hashem, etc."? Therefore, I suggested as a mere hypothesis that the Alter Rebbe, in his wisdom, included the external aspect of *Zachor* within the internal aspect of *Zachor* by stating: "the *kavanah* in the Shabbos *tefillah*." This is in contrast to *Shamor*, where the cessation from physical action is not included in the cessation from physical speech.

## 8,189

B"H, Zos Chanukah, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Yitzchak Koren

Shalom u’Bracha!

It is surprising that for a long time I have not heard from you, although, of course, I inquire about you and receive regards from time to time regarding how you are doing. I was especially pleased to hear that you participated in the Yud-Tes Kislev farbrengen in Kfar Chabad. Surely, among the things heard at that gathering—and perhaps even beforehand—you heard an explanation of why Yud-Tes Kislev is called the "Rosh Hashanah" for matters of Chassidus, especially since you originate from Bessarabia and Romania, where the movement was widespread.

It is my hope that you have utilized and are utilizing your influence and ability regarding the matters we discussed when we met here, and first and foremost regarding the yeshiva in Kiryat Gat. Regarding what you wrote to me previously, that matters did not develop as they should have because the funds were not readily available—it is surely unnecessary to explain to you that all the matters that have been accomplished in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) were done precisely in such a manner. And if you will, this is also the lesson of the days of Chanukah. For when there was oil for only one day, and eight days would pass until new oil could be prepared, according to human logic, why light and then stop? It would be better to wait until there was enough oil ready, etc. Nevertheless, they lit immediately, and behold, it is a wonder that it continued and shone, and in a manner of "increasing and brightening."

With respect and blessing.

## 290

B.H., Zos Chanukah, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants of the farbrengen of Yom HaBesorah, 19 Kislev, the redemption of Rabbeinu HaZaken, Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, and our own redemption and the deliverance of our souls in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established,
May they live.

Peace and blessing!

With pleasure, I received the news regarding your participation in the farbrengen of 19 Kislev, the day of the redemption of Rabbeinu HaZaken and our own redemption and the deliverance of our souls.

May it be the will of Hashem that the inspiration of this auspicious day be carried through all the days of the year, and lead to actual practice—which is the main thing: strengthening oneself in the study of Torah, both Nigleh and Chassidus, and in the performance of mitzvos with light and enthusiasm. And all of this in a manner of "ever-increasing."

According to the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov that from every matter one must learn a moral lesson for one’s avodah to one’s Creator, this is also true regarding the proximity of 19 Kislev to the days of Chanukah.

For it is known that the imprisonment of Rabbeinu HaZaken was due to his approach of disseminating the part of Torah that until then had been in the category of "secrets of Torah"—to disseminate it until it reached the "outside" with understanding and comprehension. His redemption—in the spiritual sense—is the agreement and the granting of strength from Above for this dissemination, in a manner of "ever-increasing, ever-brightening," like all parts of the Torah that we have been commanded to elevate in holiness.

And furthermore: even if in previous generations, when the early ones were like angels, there was no necessity for this dissemination, when hearts have diminished, the necessity is all the greater. As is known, the parable of Rabbeinu HaZaken: regarding a precious stone that was in the royal crown, which is a diadem and the essence of the glory. But when the king’s son fell ill, to the point of danger, the king **commanded** that the stone be removed from the crown and ground down very finely in water, in order to give it to the king’s son to drink—on the chance that perhaps one drop would reach his mouth and he would be healed.

It is similar with the Chanukah light: the miracle is connected to the lamps of the Menorah in the Beis HaMikdash. And in the Beis HaMikdash itself—not in the courtyards or the hall, but in the inner Sanctuary. However, in the wake of the war with the Greeks and the increase of darkness, the mitzvah of lighting candles was established for every single person in his own home, even in the Diaspora, and even in this present time. Furthermore, one must light them at the entrance of his house from the outside. And as the Midrash says, cited and explained by the Ramban—these candles specifically are never nullified.

"There is no light but Torah," as it is said, "For the mitzvah is a lamp and the Torah is light." When the darkness increases, then, on the contrary, we add light and are commanded to illuminate not only the house from within, but also at the entrance of the house from the outside.

May it be the will of Hashem that each and every one will do in this regard all that is incumbent upon him, going and adding in light—

Until they illuminate the darkness of the Golus and the darkness of the world, in a manner of the transformation of darkness into light,

And the prophecy will be fulfilled: "The sun shall no longer be your light by day... for Hashem shall be your everlasting light."

With respect and blessing.

## 8,291

[Beginning of Teves, 5722]

...Regarding the writing of the name Pinchas, whether it should be written *chaser* (defective) or *malei* (plene) — see Zohar Vol. 3 (113b, and there 57b) that the *yud* is added in it. However, according to our *masorah*, and as it is ruled *halachically* (in the laws of *gittin* in *Beis Shmuel*), it must be written *malei*. See also *Minchas Shai* at the beginning of *Parshas Pinchas*.

Notwithstanding this, the *Maharshal* testified that most people write it *chaser* (presumably referring to contexts that do not affect the *din*). This is also the case in *Shas* regarding names such as *Rebbi Pinchas ben Yair* and the like.

#### 8,291

The letter is addressed to R' Pinchas Aharon, *sheyichyeh*, Weberman, and was written in the margins of his letter from *Zos Chanukah*.

Additional letters to him — above, Vol. 20, 7,665; below, 8,334; 8,457; 8,494; 8,554.

**Regarding the writing of it:** In his letter: I noticed that in the letters of the Rebbe *shlita* to me, he writes my name "Pinchas Aharon" *chaser*, without a *yud*; yet in the Torah, and also in *Beis Shmuel* regarding the names of people, it is written *malei* with a *yud*.

**Pinchas... malei:** See also *Likkutei Sichos* Vol. 8, p. 355, note 32.

## 8292

8292

B"H, 3 Teves, 5722
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who engages in the needs of the community, etc., R' Chaim Zusia, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from 25 Kislev and the one that followed.

We are currently in the day of Zos Chanukah, which, as explained in Toras HaChassidus, contains two interpretations. And to explain them in terms of practical avodah:

a) To draw down from the deepest power of the soul (Atik sheb’nefesh), which is the power of taanug, until it influences actual deed in one’s daily conduct.

b) To bring down from the guiding power of the inner faculties (Arich sheb’nefesh, the power of ratzon sheb’nefesh), so that it permeates the entire person and all of his experiences.

In order to accomplish this until it reaches actual deed, which is inherently connected with difficulties, one must reach and draw out a deeper power of the neshamah Elokis. Conversely, to protect the person himself and his feelings, one does not require such a power as the one who must connect with the external world.

And according to the well-known dictum, "Everything that is higher, descends lower" (that which is higher can reach that which is lower).

As was discussed at the farbrengen of Shabbos Chanukah, in the summary of the maamar (Boruch She’asah Nissim, Chapter 4), only the first interpretation is brought, which emphasizes the essence and the goal.

For this is the purpose of a summary: that it brings only matters that are essential, and not elaborations or explanations.

May Hashem grant success, that everyone should carry out the directives of Zos Chanukah, according to the aforementioned explanation of Toras HaChassidus, throughout the entire coming year—may it come upon us for good—to bring light within oneself, at the entrance of one’s home, and also outside (to one’s household members, those close to one, and also in the external world).

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

## 893

B"H, 3 Teves, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...In accordance with what is explained in various places, it is appropriate that a certain sum be paid toward the burial expenses, etc., from the funds of her late husband. Since this is symbolic, the specific amount is not of great consequence. Regarding the remainder of the sum, you should speak with the relative—may he live—who for the time being provided the money for the aforementioned, that he should give her that amount in exchange for her husband’s belongings (the Sefer Torah and the like). Afterward, he should return the items to her as a gift, and she will then repay him with that money for what he lent for the burial expenses, etc.

The point in all this is understood: the burial must be in a "field that he purchased for full price," rather than one purchased by others. Since the relative merited this great mitzvah, the matter should be arranged so that he, too, has a share in it, but in a way that does not affect the matter of the "field that he purchased." This is achieved through the aforementioned arrangement. However, it is necessary that the parents—may they live and be well—of her husband agree to all of this.

It is understood that she may tell the relative that this is my suggestion.

We conclude with goodness as we stand in Zos Chanukah, and may it be the will of Hashem that from here on, He will illuminate her portion and her fortune in a manner of "increasing and brightening."

As requested, the letter is being sent without waiting for the regular turn.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 8294

B"H, 4 Teves, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Teves, in which you write of your worries, etc., and ask for advice regarding this.

The advice, which is also simple, is to strengthen your bitachon in Hashem Yisbarach—the Creator and Guide of the world, who oversees each and every person with hashgacha pratis—and to contemplate the words of the Sweet Singer of Israel, speaking on behalf of every member of Bnei Yisrael: "Hashem is my shepherd, I shall not lack; Hashem is with me, I shall not fear." Study this psalm (Tehillim 23) several times until you know its content well, and from time to time, contemplate it. Indeed, the "adversary" mentioned in this psalm also includes the yetzer hara and its matters, which are the internal adversaries of every Jewish man and woman.

This is especially understood according to what is explained in the teachings of Chassidus: that Hashem is the essence of good, it is the nature of the Good to do good, and He oversees each and every person with hashgacha pratis.

Regarding what you wrote about the past: there is nothing that can stand before teshuvah. However, teshuvah, too, must be rooted in strong bitachon in Hashem Yisbarach, and not, chas v'shalom, in despair.

I trust you are taking part in the activities of N'shei Chabad.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 6,790

6,790

B”H, 5 Teves, 5722
Brooklyn.

Blessings and peace!

I have received your letter, and I have cabled my opinion based on what I have seen in many similar cases: that it is worthwhile to try treatment with compresses. They are effective in softening matters such as those you describe, and often they even cause them to disappear entirely. Within a short time, one can already see results if the treatment is appropriate. Certainly, the doctor will also agree to the above, and you should decide accordingly based on the results.

May the Almighty, the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders, send His word and heal you through this treatment and this person.

It is surprising that you do not write regarding your activities in the dissemination of Yiddishkeit in general, and the dissemination of the wellsprings [of Chassidus] in particular. Surely, for someone like you, it is unnecessary to elaborate on the magnitude of this matter and its necessity.

With blessings for good tidings, in good health, and with joy and a glad heart.

## 8297

8297

B"H, 7 Teves, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 5 Teves, in which you ask whether there is a concept of not shaving the corners of the beard at all, neither with a razor nor with scissors.

It is surprising that you have a question or doubt about this, given that it is well known that many people practice exactly this way, because they follow the halachic ruling of the Tzemach Tzedek on this matter, as that is the halacha (see his Responsa to Yoreh Deah, section 93, at length). This is in addition to those who follow this practice because, in their view, this is the proper approach at least according to the paths of Chassidus (see the Tzemach Tzedek’s commentary on Tehillim on the verse "And He, being merciful, forgives iniquity," where it is noted; see also the books cited in *Darchei Teshuvah* to Yoreh Deah, section 181, subsection 17).

This is discussed at length in the book *Amudei Arazim* by Rabbi Margaliyos (Jerusalem).

2) Regarding your question about a study program in Chassidic texts — it is understood that this depends on the student’s knowledge, his talents, and the time he can dedicate to it, etc. Therefore, you should speak face-to-face with a mashpia of Chassidus in your area or at the Central Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim, and they will guide you.

With blessings for good news,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 898

B"H, Motzaei Shabbos, 9 Teves, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants of the Gemara study group at the Adas Yaakov Synagogue, Brooklyn,
May they live:

Greetings and blessings!

It was a pleasure to hear from the distinguished, G-d-fearing, and accomplished Rabbi Moshe Pinchas HaKohen, that on the upcoming Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Vayechi, your group will be concluding Maseches Taanis and beginning Maseches Rosh Hashanah.

In accordance with the Jewish custom that upon the completion of a tractate of Torah—at the *siyum*—one recites the *Hadran* and words of inspiration, I am writing these lines to participate in your joy upon the conclusion of Maseches Taanis.

The text states:
"The Sages taught: What did the beautiful among them say? 'Direct your eyes toward beauty, for a woman is only for beauty.' What did the well-born among them say? 'Direct your eyes toward family, for a woman is only for children.' What did the plain among them say? 'Take your acquisition for the sake of Heaven, provided that you adorn us with gold.'"

In general, these three groups correspond to the three statements taught by Rabbi Chiya: "A woman is only for beauty," "A woman is only for children," and "A woman is only for her jewelry" (meaning, "adorn us with gold"—as Rashi explains there: "give us jewelry").

Since the author of all three statements is the same, it is understood that there is no disagreement; rather, each statement speaks to a specific type of woman.

This can be explained in terms of the *avodah* of the souls of Israel toward Hashem.

(In the language of the verse), they are the "daughters of Tzion" who call out and seek King Shlomo—the King to whom peace belongs—that He should choose and select them at the Giving of the Torah, the day of His wedding.

Based on this, the continuation in the Mishnah at the end of Maseches Taanis, and the relevance of the matters therein, becomes understood and pleasant: "They would say, 'Go out and see, O daughters of Tzion...' on the day of His wedding—this is the Giving of the Torah..."

There are three types of souls and their *avodah*:

**"The beautiful among them"**—those who are beautiful, with no blemish in them or in their *avodah*. This is *avodah* not for the sake of receiving a reward, but true *avodah* from love, as it is written, "Forget your people and your father’s house," and (thereby) "The King will desire your beauty." Therefore, they **say** and request, **"Direct your eyes toward beauty, for a woman is only for beauty"**—the ultimate perfection, *avodah* from love, for its own sake.

**"The well-born among them"**—those who require merit and the inheritance of the Patriarchs. Yet, their ancestral merit is not exhausted; it is complete. Their *avodah* is not yet at the level of the love of Hashem of which it is said, "How beautiful you are... love in delights," but rather from the hidden love in the heart of all Israel, which is an inheritance from the Patriarchs. Through this, they fulfill all the *mitzvos* of the Torah. Therefore, they **say** and request, **"Direct your eyes toward family,"** the lineage of "Avraham, My beloved," **"for a woman is only for children"**—the essence of the "offspring of the righteous" (and "Your people are all righteous") are *mitzvos*. For the soul descended below only to refine the body, etc., through the fulfillment of *mitzvos*.

**"The plain among them"**—those whose very merit (from the word *zikuch*, refinement and clarification) of the Patriarchs seems exhausted, because the love of the ancestral inheritance is hidden and covered within them by the "sackcloth" of *kelipah*. **What did they say** and request? **"Take your acquisition for the sake of Heaven"**—"Do it for Your sake, if not for ours"—**"provided that you adorn us with gold."**

For the daughters of Israel are beautiful (they are believers, the children of believers, and they desire to cleave to Hashem and not be separated, Heaven forbid), but poverty (there is no "poor" except in knowledge; this covers their beauty and their true desire) makes them appear unseemly.

They request that wealth be bestowed upon them—an arousal of *teshuvah* from Above: "Return us, Hashem, to You, and we shall return."

In general, these are the three categories: *tzaddikim*, *beinonim*, and *resha'im*.

According to this explanation, the continuation in the Gemara following the aforementioned teaching of the Sages is understood and sweetened: "Ula said... In the future, the Holy One, blessed be He, will make a circle for the *tzaddikim* (and "Your people are all righteous")... and each one will point..."

For "no one shall be cast away from Him," and every type of Jew—Hashem fulfills their request and their declaration, "I am to my Beloved, and my Beloved is to me."

Based on the above, one can hint at and connect this conclusion to the beginning of Maseches Rosh Hashanah: **"There are four new years: on the first of Nissan is the new year for kings."**

This refers specifically to the King of Israel, whose "goal and thought is to **raise** the religion of truth (elevation and perfection), to fill the world with **justice** (Torah and *mitzvos*, the aforementioned 'children'), and to break the arm of the **wicked** (the 'plain')."

All of this comes about through the *avodah* and the ascent of man on the ladder set upon the earth, whose top reaches the heavens—a progression from the easy to the difficult, an ascent.

**"And for the festivals"**—this means (as the Gemara explains) that the order of the festivals was established: *Chag HaMatzos*—when they were naked and bare, sunk in the forty-nine gates of impurity, etc., and the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He, was revealed to them and redeemed them. *Chag HaShavuos*—the Giving of the Torah, because the Jewish people said, "Our children are our guarantors." *Chag HaSukkos*, the "Festival of Ingathering"—the ultimate joy and perfection, the first for the reckoning, the victory of Israel in all things.

With respect and blessing,

## 6,399

B"H, 11 Teves, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings,

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh, in which you ask when the study of Tanya should take place—whether before davening or before going to sleep:

In truth, in such a matter, it is necessary at both times. However, it is primarily in the morning before davening, since this study adds to the davening and its essence (see also Rambam, Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah, beginning of Chapter 2, and Rabbeinu HaZaken in the introduction to the Siddur, in the discourse entitled *HaKol Kol Yaakov*). Furthermore, davening provides vitality for the entire day—not only regarding mundane matters, etc., which through davening are performed in an entirely different manner, but also regarding the study of Torah, and as in the prayer of Abba Binyamin, "May my prayer be close to my lying down" (see Likutei Torah, Bracha 96b).

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 15 Teves, 5722

Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After a long interval, I received your letter dated Tuesday, the day on which it was doubled in goodness, in which you write regarding the state of your health and the various opinions of the doctors on the matter.

In general, it is not understood, for it is well-known in this country that regarding ulcers, a diet is effective, provided that one adheres to it precisely. The benefit is not only in quieting the pain, but also in healing the ulcer itself. The pills that are added in this process are to hasten the healing, strengthen one’s health, and replenish vitamins and the like that may be lacking due to the diet.

Since your letter does not indicate that this is the case, perhaps it would be worthwhile for you to clarify this and speak once more with your attending physician.

After all, a person must act according to the way of nature, and the Ribono shel Olam—the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders—will send His word and heal him through a specific person and a specific treatment.

Regarding the news you shared about your wife, may she live and be well:

May the Ribono shel Olam fulfill the days of her pregnancy properly and with ease, and may she give birth to a healthy child, in its time and season, properly and with ease.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all that has been mentioned.

## 865

865

B"H, 19 Teves, 5722
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the distinguished Chossid, man of energy and many accomplishments,
Rabbi Tzvi Hirsch, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your book, the second volume of the Ramban’s commentary on the Torah, and I thank you very much for your thoughtfulness in sending it to me.

As I mentioned in my previous letter, may it be the will of Hashem that you continue, in tranquility and with a good heart, to explain and interpret the words of the *Rishonim* who were like angels. This is especially true for those who began the revelation of the hidden aspects of Torah, foremost among them being the Ramban, of blessed memory—the last of the true Kabbalists, etc. (until the arrival of the Arizal, as noted below). The work he produced is true, firm, established, and enduring, etc., for from the time of the Ramban onwards, the path of this wisdom was hidden until the Arizal began to reveal this wisdom, etc. (see the introduction of R’ Chaim Vital to *Shaar HaHakdamos*).

Indeed, our generation—an orphaned generation, in a darkness doubled and redoubled—is in particular need of the revelation of this Torah light.

With respect and blessings,

In the copy of your book that I received, it seems the second half of my second letter is missing.

**P.S.** As is my custom, I have transcribed below a few notes regarding the second volume of your book. Our Sages of blessed memory have promised, "And Vahev in Suphah" (and everything is perfected at its end), and everything follows the conclusion and the end.

**At the beginning:** See *Vayeshev* 37:1: "And the intention is to state." One should note the *Bereishis Rabbah* (82:13): "Because of a promissory note, for 'your seed shall be a stranger,' etc." Regarding the general commentary of the Ramban here, it requires further study in light of his commentary above (36:6).

**At the end:** Page 513, *Shitah Sheini* 152b (as it should be written), and in the note there (from manuscript): "Those grave-diggers, etc."

Seemingly, this also refers to what is written there accordingly: "The Sages taught: And the spirit returns to G-d who gave it—give it back to Him as He gave it to you, and the soul of my lord shall be bound in the bundle of life." On the contrary, this is the main point.

Regarding "those grave-diggers," the body—as he senses it—is seen to have substance. One must conclude that the explanation is "body" in its literal sense (and not the "second garment" mentioned in the Ramban’s commentary here, as is proven by the question in the *Shas*: "For you are dust," and "anyone who does not have jealousy," etc.). If so, the vitality that was within it is as written there (272), that the vitality remains until the grave is sealed or the flesh decomposes—meaning that this is discussed regarding *every* person and is not a matter exclusive to *Tzaddikim*. However, Rabbeinu Bachya writes here that "those grave-diggers" refers to the "second body." I have not merited to understand this, for if so, what is his difficulty with the verse "For you are dust," etc.? Since it is fulfilled in the body buried in the earth. And the same applies to the other questions there.

Also there in the note (98): "At set times"—meaning from one Erev Shabbos to the next, or from one Yom Kippur to the next. This is from Rabbeinu Bachya. One needs to search for the source for "from one Yom Kippur to the next." Perhaps he interprets the *Beraisa* in *Kesuvos* (103a) as referring also to the twilight of Yom Kippur (since this, too, is familiar to all—as per Rashi there).

It requires further study, as it should have said "from Erev Yom Kippur to Erev Yom Kippur." Perhaps there is a printing error in Rabbeinu Bachya and it should say "from Yom Tov to Yom Tov," which, in addition to the fact that its twilight is also familiar, fits what is written in *Sefer Chassidim* regarding the incident in *Kesuvos* where he would come and sanctify for his household, that this is also relevant on Yom Tov (unlike Yom Kippur).

**There in note 100 (from manuscript):** "R’ Yosi HaGlili, who would come to his home every Erev Shabbos, etc." The source for this requires study. The manuscript requires study regarding the continuation of the language; perhaps it was written initially with the acronym "R.H.N." (referring to *Rabbenu HaKadosh* mentioned earlier there) and the copyist mistook it for "R.Y.G."

Regarding the "garment of the soul," etc., mentioned above, see the *Kuntres Ner Neshama* (in *Sefer Shaarei Zohar* by Rabbi Margaliyos), page 134, and the sources cited there.

**End of the supplements (at the beginning of the book):** Regarding the statement of our Sages of blessed memory (cited in Ramban, *Bereishis* 2:9): "Three said the truth and perished from the world." In many editions of the Ramban, the version is "And these are: the snake, the spies, and Doeg the Edomite the Be'erosi." In *Pirkei Rabbenu HaKadosh*, it lists "the spies, Doeg, and the sons of Rimmon the Be'erosi." The difficulties are: 1) One must say that the Ramban, who lists the snake, disagrees with our version in *Pirkei Rabbenu HaKadosh*. 2) What is "the Be'erosi" doing next to Doeg?

To my mind, there is a strong difficulty from all this against our version in *Pirkei Rabbenu HaKadosh*: 1) The sons of Rimmon the Be'erosi did not perish from the world (and specifically—from the World to Come) because of their statement (see *II Shmuel* 4). 2) If we count the sons of Rimmon, we must also count the one who told David, "Behold, Saul is dead," and on the contrary, it is a *kal v'chomer*—as David himself said regarding this (*II Shmuel* 4:10-11). One must conclude that the sons of Rimmon are not counted. It remains to be studied how this error crept in.

Perhaps one can say regarding all this that the aforementioned statement of our Sages emphasizes the baffling fact that speaking the truth caused them to perish from the world. To add to the wonder, he also copied the greatness of Doeg. The version should be: "The snake, the spies, and Doeg the Edomite, *Avi HaRochim*" (as the verse says, *I Shmuel* 21:8), or "Doeg the Edomite, the *Av Beis Din*" (as per our Sages).

The copyist, who had not served his masters sufficiently and did not understand the above, came and "corrected" it to "HaBe'erosi" (the letters are similar in manuscript). And the one who came after him searched and found that "HaBe'erosi" belongs to the sons of Rimmon, and added an "explanation," etc.

8007

B"H, Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Shemos, 23rd of Teves, 5722

#### ***8007***

General details. Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 11, p. 192, and completed based on a photocopy of the letter.

**And in the words of:** Printed in its entirety from the Rebbe’s holy handwriting at the end of *Piskei Dinim* by the Tzemach Tzedek, p. 73 [511] (published 5752).

See also *Igros Kodesh* of the Rebbe Maharash, Letter 1.

**Iggeres HaKodesh of the Alter Rebbe:** *Igros Kodesh* of the Alter Rebbe, Vol. 1, Letter 65.

**Dew of Torah:** See also above, Vol. 2, Letter 289, in the footnote.

**Hasten:** Perhaps it can be said that this also includes a request that they be on the level of "meriting," as our Sages of blessed memory stated: "If they merit, I will hasten it" (*Sanhedrin* 95a).

**And may those who dwell in the dust awaken and sing:** *Yeshayahu* 26:19.

**Those who dwell in the dust, and he in their midst:** Note the teaching of our Sages of blessed memory regarding "those who dwell in the dust"—that he became a neighbor to the dust during his lifetime (*Sotah* 5a; cited in *Shulchan Aruch HaRav*, *Seder Hachnasas Shabbos*, 3). And the *Iggeres HaKodesh* of the Alter Rebbe is well known, which he wrote close to the time of his *histalkus*: "A soul that is truly and genuinely lowly..."

**Wonders from the Torah of Hashem:** Note that in the aforementioned introduction, the text reads: "Wonders from His Torah, the Torah of Hashem."

**Restores the soul in the body:** See *Zohar*, Vol. 1 (184b, bottom of page) and *Zoharei Chama* there—cited in the Tzemach Tzedek’s *Tehillim* (19:8, section 5).

**Dew of Torah:** The language of the verse in *Yeshayahu* there: "Awaken... for the dew of lights is your dew." And in *Kesuvos* (111b), they expounded on this: "The light of Torah gives him life." However, in *Tanya*, end of Chapter 36, it says "Dew of Torah." This is also the version in *Yalkut Shimoni* to *Yeshayahu* there.

And in the *Yerushalmi*, *Berachos* (Chapter 5, Halacha 2): "The dead will only live through dews... for the dew of lights..." And see *Shabbos* 88b, and elsewhere. *Likkutei Torah*, *Haazinu* 73c. And in the *maamar* beginning "Samchuni" (5660), that the level of "Light of Torah" and "Dew of Torah" is the level of "mysteries" and "mysteries of mysteries."

## 868

B"H, Motzaei Shabbos Mevarchim Chodesh Shevat, Eve of 24 Teves, 5722

Day of the Hillula of Rabbeinu HaZaken, Brooklyn, N.Y.
To the Second Annual Gathering of the Ladies Auxiliary of Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim in Montreal,
May Hashem grant them life.

Blessings and Peace!

In response to the notification regarding the scheduling of the second annual gathering of your Ladies Auxiliary for Wednesday, the [day] of the coming month of Shevat.

May Hashem Yisbarach help that it should be with much success, both in quantity—a greater number of participants—and in quality—larger and more numerous contributions.

And surely, one will not be satisfied with this, but will add to it, time and again.

For if in every era and in every place, the directive of our holy Torah is to "ascend in holiness"—to rise in sanctity—then all the more so in our era, and in these lands, where the demand is very great.

And it is simple and understandable that when the necessity becomes greater, the strengths and possibilities are also increased, along with the assistance from Above, for Hashem is good and upright.

And we are, after all, only a few days removed from the Yahrtzeit-Hillula of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael, who sacrificed himself for the dissemination of Yiddishkeit, Torah, and mitzvos in general, and the teachings of Chassidus and its matters in particular. He serves as an inspiration to continue to draw down blessing and success in your work for the benefit of Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim.

May Hashem Yisbarach help that you should do this with true and inner joy and goodness of heart.

With blessings to all the participants in the gathering, may they and their families be blessed with life.

## 819

B"H, 24 Teves, 5722
Brooklyn.

To the Avreich, Yechiel Michel, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 18 Teves, in which you share the news that you have accepted a position as a shochet of poultry.

It is surely known to you from the halachic ruling (brought in the Shulchan Aruch of the Alter Rebbe and in the Responsa of the Tzemach Tzedek) that a shochet must be exceptionally G-d-fearing. May you strive with all your ability to fulfill this requirement, for one who comes to purify himself is assisted.

May it be the will of Hashem that this be in a good and successful hour. And moving from one matter to a related one: may you increase your strength in teaching Torah in public. This certainly includes teaching the Torah of Chassidus and its concepts in public—the spreading of the wellsprings—which should also be done with success and with increase from time to time, as is the command to ascend in holiness.

Today, the day on which this response is written, is the yahrtzeit of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe. The parable he told regarding the spreading of the wellsprings is well known—the parable of the precious stone from the King’s crown. This teaches us that the responsibility is even greater to utilize the precious stone from the King’s crown, now that the King has already placed it at the disposal of the Jewish people, and the wise will understand. May it be the will of Hashem that your words emerge from the heart, and consequently, they will enter the heart of the listener.

With blessings for good tidings in all general and specific matters.

## 818

B"H, 24 Teves, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Day of the Hillula of the Alter Rebbe,
Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch,

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and accomplished, a man of many deeds, possessing fine character traits, descendant of holy lineage, etc.,
Rabbi Y.T. shlita,

Greetings and blessings,

I hereby confirm receipt today of the three volumes of *Etz Chaim*, *Mavo Shearim*, and *Shaar HaHakdamos*, which Divine Providence has merited you to publish successfully. This is most appropriate given the great necessity and the demands of the time to reveal this wisdom, as per the well-known words of the Arizal the Chai, which are brought and explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh* by our Rebbe, the Baal HaTanya, and in the *Kuntres Etz Chaim* by the Rebbe (Rashab) n.e., father of my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

Many thanks for the shipment. I assume that future publications by the publisher through your good offices will also be sent here, and I thank you in advance.

Although I hesitate to do so, I cannot refrain from noting my great astonishment and wonder that the notes of the publisher do not mention or cite at all the works of our Rebbes, the leaders of the Chabad school of thought. This is surely despite the fact that it is known that they explained many of the writings of the Arizal in their works [at the very least, some of them—they are noted, and their locations are understood from the indices to *Torah Ohr* and *Likutei Torah* by the Alter Rebbe, *Shaarei Orah* by his son and successor the Mitteler Rebbe, and *Sefer HaMitzvos* by his grandson and successor, my father-in-law’s father-in-law, the Tzemach Tzedek].

And if our Sages have generally explained the great importance of "ears to the basket" (referencing sources), then how much more so when the discussion involves explanations of the content itself. This is doubly true regarding books of Kabbalah, and in accordance with the directive of the Baal Shem Tov regarding special caution in the study of the aforementioned (brought in *Shoresh Mitzvas HaTefillah*, end of Chapter 2, by the Tzemach Tzedek; see there).

It is understood that my intention is not to complain about the past, and certainly not as a grievance, but rather because the matter concerns the future, as the publisher’s introduction states that they are preparing further writings of the Arizal for print.

I must also add, in continuation of the concept of "ears to the basket," that it would be most appropriate to supplement the notes and cross-references to other writings of the Arizal and his kabbalistic commentators as much as possible. First and foremost, this should include the references cited in the annotations and explanations to *Etz Chaim*, Warsaw 5651 edition, and similarly in the writings of the Arizal printed in Jerusalem with the annotations of R. M.M. Halperin and the like. The great importance of comparing the concepts within the writings of the Arizal from one place to another is certainly understood and self-evident.

Citations and cross-references to the writings of the Arizal (based on the statement of our Sages that "words of Torah... and they are enriched in another place") are surely only of benefit and value (unlike explanations of the text itself).

I trust that, consistent with your correspondence from the past, you are also exerting yourself in spreading the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov in every possible way—in writing, in print, and orally. May it be the will of Hashem that you see good fruit from this labor. For the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, his students, and his students' students, etc., constitute the *amala d'oraysa* (labor of Torah) which, through *dchilu* and *rechimu* (awe and love), ascends and pierces the heavens and stands before Hashem, as brought in the holy *Tanya* (Chapter 40 and the *Kuntres Acharon* at its beginning).

With respect and blessing.

***

## 812

B"H, 24 Teves, 5722
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

After a long interval, your letter of 17 Teves has been received.

It is understood that I am interested in the details you write about, for a person and his life are composed of such details—even the most essential matters. Just as we are commanded regarding the concept of unity in its literal sense, so too must a person strive for all his affairs to be unified, to the point of complete oneness. In the style of our Sages (who encapsulated great principles in a brief adage: "Which is a small section upon which all the essentials of Torah depend?"), **"In all your ways, know Him"** (Berachos 63a). See the explanation of this in the Laws of Character Traits by the great teacher, the Rambam, and the ruling in Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim, siman 231.

Naturally, it gave me special pleasure to read in your letter of your good and firm desire to ascend the path that leads to the House of G-d—through the study of our holy Torah and conduct befitting it. We have been promised: "He who comes to purify himself is assisted."

In response to your questions, they are explained in the legal rulings found in the Shulchan Aruch.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 813

B"H, 25 Teves, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the President of the Kehillah in Barcelona, may he be well,

Peace and blessing!

Your letter dated 18 Kislev was received in due time. In the interim, the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing man, and communal activist, Rabbi Michael Lipsker, visited here, and we spoke with him regarding the contents of your letter. He has already returned to Europe, and after spending some time there, he will visit your camp on his way to Meknes; perhaps he will have already visited your camp by the time you receive this letter.

On this occasion, as we stand on the eve of Shabbos Rosh Chodesh Shevat, I cannot refrain from mentioning the Yahrtzeit of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, on the tenth of Shevat. Anyone familiar with a chapter of our people’s history in Russia—especially those who emigrated from there—knows that this day evokes memories and profound emotional experiences from the period of the struggle for the preservation of Torah, mitzvos, and religious institutions under the banner of the one whose Yahrtzeit we observe. He literally risked his life to safeguard the values of our people and our way of life, with actual mesiras nefesh, day after day. You are surely aware of this illustrious chapter, at least in its general outlines. The entire purpose of remembrance in Jewish life is that it should lead to an increase in action—in this case, an increase in action in accordance with the worldview and the aspirations of the one whose Yahrtzeit we observe.

With respect and blessing to all the members of his community, may they be well.

## 814
