## 581

B"H, 10 Adar Rishon, 5722
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and dedicated to the work of Heaven,
R' Yehuda Leib, may he live and be well,

Shalom u'Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

We are currently in the weeks of the parshiyos that recount the command to build the Mikdash (the Mishkan), and subsequently, its actual construction.

The command begins with the words, "And they shall make Me a sanctuary, and I will dwell among them." This verse also explains the ultimate purpose: "and I will dwell among them." As our Sages of blessed memory explain, it does not say "I will dwell within *it* (the sanctuary)," but rather "I will dwell among *them*" — within each and every Jew.

The manner in which this command is fulfilled is specifically through taking physical materials—gold, silver, etc., the thirteen or fifteen items mentioned in the parsha—but one must elevate them: "And they shall take for Me a contribution." This contribution must be made in a way that "his heart moves him," and "for Me"—for My sake.

Furthermore, a matter emphasized right at the beginning is that the construction commences with the command to make the Aron, in which the Luchos are placed, and, as our Sages of blessed memory say, the Sefer Torah as well.

Moreover, in the Mishkan itself, and similarly in the Mikdash, the Aron is found in the Holy of Holies, and one reaches it only after passing through the courtyard (the *azaros* and the *ulam*) and the *heichal*.

The explanation for this is the emphasis that the Torah is the essence of the world—the world in its literal sense, and the "small world," which is man and his affairs.

Certainly, for someone like yourself, it is unnecessary to elaborate on the lessons to be drawn from all these matters and their details regarding the activities of each and every one of us, may they live, in their respective places and times, for the Torah and its instructions are eternal. And this is clear.

May it be the will of Hashem that just as in the construction of the Mishkan then, everyone performed the tasks with a wondrous alacrity that demonstrated joy and the desire to fulfill the will of their Creator and to bring satisfaction to their Maker—and they did this in purity and holiness, for it was the day after Yom Kippur, when the Holy One, blessed be He, said, "I have forgiven, as you have spoken"—

So too may it be now regarding each and every one of us, in all the aforementioned details,

And may this be with a light, vitality, and enthusiasm that befits the instruction of the Alter Rebbe: one must **live** with the times—which are the instructions of the weekly parsha.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 860

B"H, 10 Adar, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, it was a pleasure to read about your setting aside of fixed times for the study of Chabad Chassidus. It is my firm hope that, in accordance with the teaching of Chazal that "great is study, for it leads to action," your conduct will likewise reflect the teachings and customs of Chassidus. There is nothing that can stand before the will, especially since we have been promised that "one who comes to purify himself is assisted".

Regarding your question concerning the offer of a prestigious position, which you write is not very religious, etc.: since there are several levels of interpretation for such an expression, you should present the situation in the necessary detail to your friends in the community, as is the custom in Yisrael, and in the manner described—for "in the multitude of counselors there is safety."

Regarding your question: since, as Chazal state, a person’s sustenance is allotted to him from Rosh Hashanah, what room is there for the advice brought in the Gemara and elsewhere regarding livelihood and wealth?

You should look into this in the Likutei Torah of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, at the end of Parshas Korach, and in greater detail in the Kuntres U'Maayan by the Rebbe (Rashab).

It is my hope that you are aware of, and also keeping, the three well-known daily study portions of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 8558

## 859

B”H, 12 Adar, 5722
Brooklyn.

They are satisfied with this change, even though the treatment takes longer. In any case, the main thing is that, in a pleasant manner, efforts should be made to ensure he is occupied with work or matters that do not place a heavy burden of responsibility upon him.

## 860

B"H, 12 Adar, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of February 15th, in which you write about your family, your background, and the fact that you are studying in a Chassidic yeshiva, and that the *tzelem Elokim* is visible on your face [and not like those who are ashamed of it, and seek various ways to remove and cast aside the *tzelem Elokim*], and you ask for my opinion regarding continuing your studies, etc., especially since some of your family members have complaints against you in this regard.

It is understandable that all these complaints come from the "old and foolish king," the *yetzer hara*, who wars against Hashem, His Torah, and His *mitzvos*. He wants to make a Jew into someone whose *nefesh habehamis* overcomes their *nefesh ha-Elokis*, and he makes the **nefesh habehamis** (just like those who have these complaints) so strong that he wants to convince him that this is how **a person** should be. This was his conduct immediately after *Matan Torah*, when the *yetzer hara* persuaded them to make **a calf**, and for them to shout, "These are your gods, O Israel," *rachmana litzlan*. His students exist in this generation as well.

From what has been said above, it is understandable how your conduct should be moving forward: just as you have conducted yourself until now, and not like your relatives whom you mentioned. Rather, conduct yourself according to the instructions of our Torah, *Toras Chaim*, and fulfill its *mitzvos*, regarding which it is written, "and live by them." This is the true path by which a Jew can be happy—not merely for a few minutes with a deluded happiness, but with a true happiness, both in *gashmius* and in *ruchnius*.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
**Secretary**

**P.S.** In order to make the above easier, especially regarding the *tzelem Elokim*, it is worthwhile that every day before *davening* you should give a few cents to *tzedakah*, and after *davening*—also on *Shabbos* and *Yom Tov*—you should be careful to recite the monthly *shiur* of *Tehillim*, as it is divided according to the days of the month.

## 8661

B"H, 14 Adar, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Rabbi, Chossid, G-d-fearing, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Alexander Sender, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter of the eleventh of Adar Rishon, with the good news that the first three shiurim in the Tanya Kadisha have taken place.

Three times constitutes a *chazakah* according to all opinions—a *chazakah* to strengthen and acquire the body and the *nefesh habehamis* through the "second soul" in a Jew, which is truly a part of Elokus from above. May they, too, become subservient to the authority of the *nefesh elokis*, becoming completely nullified to it and a chariot for it, until they are filled solely with the aspects and garments of the *nefesh elokis*, and "no stranger shall pass through them," G-d forbid (Tanya, Chapter 9). This is in accordance with the oath they adjure him, and so on, leading to *iskafya*, and from *iskafya* to *is'hapcha*—transforming darkness into light and bitterness into sweetness. This is the purpose and perfection of the creation of the world—this "small world," which is man, and the world in its literal sense. As our Sages of blessed memory said, the purpose of the creation of this world, which the Holy One, Blessed be He, desired to create, is for Him to have a dwelling place in the lower realms.

These days are days of *segulah*, the days of the month of Adar, whose essence is the days of Purim. Their theme is "and it was turned about," to the point that even the nations of the land become "Jewish," for the fear of the Jews fell upon them. As is known, the interpretation (Rema in *Mechir Yayin*) is that the same fear that the Jews possess—the fear of Hashem—fell upon the nations of the land as well. First and foremost, this applies to the body and the *nefesh habehamis* (see *Likutei Torah*, *d'h Tov Lachasos*), through which one fulfills what was already accepted, as explained at length in the *maamarim* of Purim.

With respect and regards to all the participants in the aforementioned study, which possesses two virtues: it is *Talmud Torah* of the masses, and it is in the part of Torah where there is no dispute, etc., but rather, on the contrary, unity, and even oneness, as per the well-known words of the *Ra'aya Mehemna* (Iggeres HaKodesh, Section 26).

With the blessing that in our near future we will merit the fulfillment of the promise that the first redeemer is the final redeemer—as the *Ra'aya Mehemna* states there, that in the future Israel will taste from the Tree of Life, and through it, they will emerge from exile with mercy, and so on.

Awaiting good news.

## 8662

B"H, 14 Adar, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

After the longest of intervals, your letter was received, and in response to your questions:

According to what is explained in several sefarim, one must be careful with the text inscribed on a tombstone (and in general, regarding anything concerning a soul that is already in the World of Truth) not to exaggerate, etc., and certainly regarding something that is not factual. I am referring to writing that one belongs to a certain lineage if that is not the case; from this it is also understood that if there is any doubt, why enter into such uncertainties?

Regarding what you wrote about studying in Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim — it is understood that there is no difference whether this was in Lubavitch or elsewhere; it is one and the same. Similarly, there is no difference in this regard concerning the length of time of study, whether a year or more, as per the well-known statement of Chazal regarding "a student of one day."

Regarding what you wrote about matters and the like pertaining to me, the question is surprising, for the address to which you send your letters is the same address for all other matters.

It is understood that it is most distressing what you wrote regarding the cessation of the study of Chassidus. For on the contrary, when a special situation arises that makes an undesirable impression on a person’s state of mind, it is simple that one must immediately increase the study of Chassidus, which is called in the Ra'aya Mehemna "the Tree of Life," where there are no matters of the "other side," chas v'shalom, but only life and the Life of Life. Surely there is no need for any further explanation regarding this.

Regarding your question about tzedakah — it seems you are referring to what was pledged during the time of illness, and because of the illness.

The statement of Chazal is well known: "A statement to the Almighty is like a delivery to a common person." That is to say, this has no connection to what the heirs do to merit and elevate the soul, or what they set aside from the estate for matters of tzedakah. Consequently, if the Yeshiva of Toras Emes approaches them regarding the estate and the inheritance, this has no connection to the tzedakah of the aforementioned pledge, and this is simple.

Regarding your conclusion with the request to perpetuate the name of your father-in-law, a"h — I will endeavor in this, as is understood and also simple.

And as we are in the months of Adar, whose essence is the days of which it is said, "And it was turned around," may it be the will that all undesirable matters be turned around from one extreme to the other, and like the advantage of light from darkness, may it be for each and every one, immediately and completely, with light, joy, gladness, and honor, both literally and in its deeper meaning.

With blessings and regards to the entire family, shlit"a.

## 8,363

8,363

B”H, Shushan Purim Katan, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

We are currently in the months of Adar, the essence of which is the days of Purim—a month of success for Jews in all their affairs.

It is worth noting that, as is well known from our Sages (Megillah 13b, and elsewhere), the miracle of Purim was dependent on the fact that Moshe Rabbeinu was born in Adar. Our Sages added the explanation that it was a leap year, and this occurred in Adar Rishon (Sotah 12b).

The interpretation of the Arizal on the verse is well known: "And these days are remembered" (and therefore they are also) "fulfilled."

With blessings for good tidings in matters of the collective and the individual,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8664

B"H, 16 Adar I, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Yeshivas Achei Temimim Lubavitch, Pittsburgh, PA.

Greetings and Blessings!

To the annual event, I send my heartfelt greeting and blessing to the esteemed askanim and friends of the Lubavitcher Yeshiva Achei Temimim in Pittsburgh, and I express my inner hope that the event will more than justify all expectations.

It is a well-known saying of the Alter Rebbe, Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, that "a Yid must live with the times"—that is, with the time and the spirit of the weekly parsha. The "timeliness" of this event is reflected in the sedros read during these weeks, which speak of the **Mishkan**. The intent of the Mishkan is expressed in the words, **"And they shall make Me a sanctuary, and I will dwell within them"**—to enable the Ribono shel Olam to cause His Shechinah to rest among all Yidden, and within every individual Yid in particular.

The Ribono shel Olam is everywhere (**"The whole earth is full of His glory"**) and does not need a Mishkan for Himself; and if the Ribono shel Olam had wanted a Mishkan, He could have established one without human assistance. However, the Ribono shel Olam wanted every Yid to have a share in the Mishkan by contributing gold, silver, and so on. The Yidden understood how to value the great zechus associated with this, and they responded with the greatest heart, to the point that it was necessary to proclaim, "Enough!"

Our Chachamim, of blessed memory, say that after the destruction of the Beis HaMikdash, the batei medrash and batei knesios, where Yidden learn and daven, are the "mikdash me'at." In these holy institutions, the Ribono shel Olam causes His Shechinah to rest; the askanim and supporters of the yeshivos are equal partners with the talmidim in spreading the Divine Shechinah among all Yidden.

Therefore, it is to be hoped that each and every one will respond with personal warmth and dedication for the benefit of the Lubavitcher Yeshiva, just as the Yidden, men and women, responded for the benefit of the Mishkan. Through this, one also creates the "keilim" to receive the Ribono shel Olam's blessings in everything one needs, for oneself and for the entire family, may they live, in both gashmius and ruchnius.

With honor and blessing.

#### ***8664***

**Chachamim.. say:** Megillah 29a.

## 865

B"H, 17 Adar, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 15th of Adar.

At an auspicious time, I will mention them at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the fulfillment of their heart's desires for the good regarding the matter about which you write.

Since we are speaking of a young man, it is tangibly evident that the words of peers his own age are far more influential than the requests, entreaties, and commands that come from adults, even when they explain and persuade, etc. Since this is the nature of youth in general, and certainly so if, as you write, the individual in question has a rebellious nature, you should certainly find several of his peers who will attempt to speak with him in the direction you describe, without him suspecting that they are doing so at your request or at the request of your wife, may she live.

The recommended advice in such a case is to endeavor to have him take upon himself the role of a spiritual leader for a religious group, or at least a part in the management of a religious group; in this way, he will be drawn to matters of religion without feeling that it is being done intentionally or for a specific purpose, etc.

Seemingly, the following point has no practical difference at this moment; nevertheless, through clarification, the situation will certainly become clearer. It is to clarify the nature of the parents of the individual in question, their conduct, and, most importantly, whether he was born in purity. The benefit in the present is that since matters of Torah and mitzvos influence even the past, a specific and concentrated effort now in that area which, G-d forbid, had an undesirable influence, may improve and rectify the situation.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

#### ***865***

**Whether he was born in purity:** See also above, Vol. 8, Letter 2,354; 2,424.

## 866

866

By the Grace of Hashem, 6th of Adar, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Ki Sisa, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Annual Banquet of the Ladies Auxiliary of Brownsville and East New York for the Lubavitcher Yeshivos "Tomchei Temimim"

Blessings and Peace!

In response to your notification regarding the annual banquet taking place this coming Sunday, G-d willing, I send my greetings and blessing to all the participants, and my heartfelt hope that the undertaking will meet with the success it deserves, both financially and spiritually.

Since it is a custom among Jews to connect all significant events with the weekly parsha, I would like to refer to the beginning of the parsha that is read this Shabbos, which speaks of the mitzvah of the *machatzis hashekel*.

The Midrash relates that Moshe Rabbeinu wondered how a silver coin that a Jew contributes to the *Mishkan* could possess such tremendous power that it is accepted as *kofer nefesh*—a ransom and atonement, just as if one had given their very life to the Ribono shel Olam. The Ribono shel Olam then showed Moshe Rabbeinu a coin of fire (**matbeah shel eish**) and said to him: "This is what they shall give" (**kazeh yitnu**).

The explanation for this is as follows:

Although money is a physical, material thing, when a Jew gives *tzedakah* for a holy purpose—such as a *Mishkan* or a yeshiva—and gives it as it ought to be given: in full measure, with their whole heart, with true joy, and with fervor—they connect it to the fire of their Divine *neshamah*. Thus, even such a simple and material thing as money becomes a fiery, holy thing and acquires the Divine power of *kofer nefesh*.

The work of the Ladies Auxiliary to help provide this "coin of fire" for *Tomchei Temimim* should be animated by the participation of Jewish women in the building of the *Mishkan*, when the Jewish women distinguished themselves in particular with their devotion and *mesiras nefesh*, serving as a living example for all.

May Hashem Yisbarach bless your work with great success, in both quantity and quality, and may He send His blessing to you and your families, as well as to all the participants and their families, in everything they need, both materially and spiritually alike.

With blessings for good tidings.

#### ***866***

Excerpted from *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 2, p. 677, and completed according to the secretariat's copy.

**The Midrash:** See *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 26, p. 229, note 2, and the references cited there.

## 8667

B"H, 22 Adar Rishon, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Tuesday, the day on which "it was good" was doubled, in which you write regarding the matter of growing a beard and how this might affect your livelihood when the time comes to settle into a regular profession.

Since **everyone** agrees that a grown beard is the matter of the *tzelem Elokim* (Divine image), and **everyone** agrees that it is far more praiseworthy than the **opposite** behavior—as is proven even by the words of those who do not say that growing a beard is required by Torah law, as explained in their books—it is **certain** that one who adds in holiness and whose *tzelem Elokim* is recognizable upon his face, adds to all of this in the blessing of Hashem, **He** who sustains the entire world in His goodness, with grace, kindness, and mercy, and upon Whom a person’s livelihood specifically depends. It is understood that fulfilling the desires of his heart to grow a beard adds to his livelihood in particular.

Especially according to the words of the holy Zohar, that a grown beard (in the language of the Zohar, it is called the "thirteen *tikkunei dikna*"—rectifications of the beard) of the person below draws down from the thirteen attributes of mercy from above, which are without limit. It is simple that this is the path for a person’s benefit and assists his livelihood. See the explanation of the Tzemach Tzedek in his commentary *Yahel Or* on Tehillim (p. 6) regarding this.

It is proper that you have your *tefillin* checked to ensure they are kosher according to law, and likewise, you should maintain the three daily study portions of *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya* as is known.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

***

**Growing a beard... livelihood:** See also above, Vol. 13, Letter 4474, and the references in the notes there.

**Since everyone agrees:** See also above, Vol. 8, Letter 2997, and the references in the notes there.

## 8771

B"H, 26 Adar, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 23 Adar, in which you write regarding your speech, etc.

Very often, this occurs due to an event that was associated with nerves and tension. Therefore, in addition to fulfilling the instructions of the doctors—whose advice you should seek—you should strengthen your trust in Hashem, who oversees each and every person with Divine Providence. For then it is said, "Hashem is with me, I will not fear." When the measure of fear diminishes, the stuttering will, in the natural course of events, also diminish.

Another piece of advice regarding this: when you encounter a word that you stutter on, do not insist on pronouncing that specific word. Rather, try to replace it with another word, and it is best to do so after a few seconds, once the tension has passed.

The main point in all of the above is that everything depends on the blessing of Hashem, the Creator of man and His guide. Therefore, conducting one’s daily life in accordance with the instructions of our Torah—Torah of life—and the fulfillment of its mitzvos, serves as a channel and vessel for receiving Hashem’s blessing in all that is needed. This is especially true since every daughter of Yisrael is called a daughter of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

#### ***8771***

**Regarding speech:** See also above, Vol. 18, Letter 6,773, and the references in the notes there.

## 872

B"H, Erev Shabbos, Parshas Vayakhel Moshe Es Kol Adas Bnei Yisrael,
5722. Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants in the ninth annual luncheon of
Agudas N'shei U'Bnos Chabad in Cleveland, Ohio
May Hashem grant them life

Blessings and peace!

It is a well-known teaching of the Alter Rebbe, the founder of the Chabad philosophy, that one must "live with the times." This means living with the weekly parsha and the matters it relates. One can and must derive lessons from them—regarding personal conduct and what one must do for oneself and for others.

In the current weekly parshiyos, it is related in detail (with all the particulars) how all Jews, men and women alike, were instructed to erect a Mishkan. At that time, the Ribono shel Olam said, there would be *V'shachanti b'socham*—"I will dwell and be among them, and **within them**."

One of the lessons from this for us at this time is:

Every Jewish home must be a reflection of the Mishkan, where the Shechinah dwells. *V'shachanti b'socham*—and regarding this, *kol adas bnei Yisrael* were instructed—all Jews, and every individual Jew in all generations.

This is the task and goal of Agudas N'shei U'Bnos Chabad: to bring into every Jewish home Jewish light and warmth, imbued with Chassidic feeling and vitality, so that one may rightfully say that this is a home where the Shechinah dwells.

I send my blessing and express my *tefillah* that Hashem Yisbarach grant you success in the aforementioned work.

And may you be blessed, together with your families *shlita*, with everything necessary, both *b'gashmi u'v'ruchani*—materially and spiritually.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 874

874

B”H, Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Shekalim, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants in the annual luncheon of the N.Y. Committee for the Seminar for Teachers and Vocational School for Girls in Kfar Chabad in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established,

Blessings and peace!

It is a well-known teaching of the Alter Rebbe, the founder of the Chabad philosophy, that one must "live with the times." This means living with the weekly parsha and the matters it recounts. One can and must derive lessons from them—regarding personal conduct and what one must do for oneself and for others.

In the parshiyos of these weeks, it is recounted how Jews, men and women alike, contributed with great enthusiasm, alacrity, and to the fullest extent toward the construction of the Mishkan, where the Shechinah of the Ribono shel Olam rested.

One of the lessons to be drawn from this is:

Every mitzvah and matter of Torah—which is, after all, a directive from the Ribono shel Olam—should and must elicit an immediate and warm response from each and every person. This is especially true when it is connected to the education of Jewish daughters in the true Jewish spirit—preparing them so that when the time comes, they will build their family lives and establish homes of which it can rightfully be said that they are homes where the Shechinah rests.

## 870

B"H, 29 Adar Rishon, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Thursday, and in addition to what I wrote in my letter to the students who traveled from here to there—the words are, of course, directed to each one of you—

Regarding what you write about rectifying the past:

It is a well-known instruction of our Rebbes, the Nesi’im, that for a yeshiva student, his primary focus is the study of Torah [and when speaking of a Chassidic yeshiva, founded and directed by our Rebbes, it is understood that this also refers to the study of Chassidus], the performance of mitzvos with *hiddur* (meticulous care), and the core of it all—the *avodah* of *tefillah*.

Regarding what you write about preparations for marriage: You should discuss this with the *mashpia* of Chassidus at Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim. Furthermore, you should find out how this was handled in Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim [from its time in Russia and subsequently in Poland]. In Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt speedily, there are several people who were involved in these matters firsthand.

Regarding what you write about conduct on *Yom Tov Sheni Shel Galuyos*: It is understood that in all matters of *hora’ah* and *piskei dinim*, you must turn to and consult a *moreh hora’ah* from *anash* on the spot. You can detail all the reasons you wrote, and he will instruct you.

Regarding what you write about how to organize yourself after the wedding: It is understood that now is not the time to be *b'pizur hanefesh* (distracted) about this already, as there is still some time until the wedding, etc.

May it be Hashem’s will that you share good news regarding all the above. We are currently in the months in which we are commanded to be in a state of *simcha*, which is not merely one of the *chukim* (statutes) of the Torah, but one of the mitzvos that also has a rational basis—namely, that there is a reason, and indeed a great one, that brings about an increase in *simcha*.

I await good news.

P.S. Your letter from 29 Adar Rishon was received (and it is surprising that you are so agitated, etc.). It is understood that your statement—that it is not appropriate for you to argue with so-and-so—is absolutely correct. Next time, say (simply, with politeness and respect, but in a clear tone) that you are staying in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt speedily, and are remaining there for the time being as a student **within** Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim. Just as in any yeshiva—and especially in Tomchei Temimim—your conduct, your daily schedule (including times free from the *seder* in the *zal*, etc., and including Shabbos and the month of Nissan), and certainly your studies, are dependent upon and must be in accordance with the instructions of the yeshiva administration. Therefore, there is no benefit in debating with you (especially since you wish to maintain your relationship with him)—he should direct all such matters solely to the yeshiva administration. Until you receive instructions from the administration, your conduct should be the same as all the other students of the yeshiva.

In response to your letter, in which you write that until now you have not succeeded in your work and in the matters you have attempted to engage in, and you ask for guidance in this.

However, first you must check your tefillin and know clearly that they are kosher.

I will await good news regarding the above. We are currently in the month of Adar, a month of success for Jews in all their matters, as it is written: "For the Jews there was light, and gladness, and joy, and honor" (Esther 8:16). See the commentary on this verse in Maseches Megillah, page 16b.

With blessings for good news in all the above,

## 8748

8748

B"H, 5 Adar II, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned, who engages in communal needs, etc.,
Mr. Yosef, known as Dr. Burg

Shalom u’Bracha!

I received your letter and the accompanying booklet in due time. Thank you very much for your attention to this, and I am certain you will continue to do so in the future.

It is my hope that you received the regards I sent via the travelers from here some time ago.

On this occasion, and as a word in its proper time, you surely recall that last year I urged that efforts be made so that students in schools—and my perspective is well-known, that I do not refer to any specific type of school, but to all schools, for every single Jewish boy and girl is a child of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov, and of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah—should fulfill the mitzvos of *mishloach manos* and *matanos la’evyonim*. Although our Sages of blessed memory said, "Do not sit and weigh the mitzvos of the Torah," this case is different, as the intention here is the principle of *mitzvah goreres mitzvah* (one mitzvah leads to another), since the aforementioned mitzvos are easy to fulfill. Furthermore, every mitzvah possesses a unique quality and property, and in the case of these mitzvos, it is the matter of unity among the Jewish people. Unfortunately, even though this is not an election season, there is still room to increase, again and again, in the drawing together of hearts and the unity of one nation, in the spirit of the prayer we recite on Rosh Hashanah, that it may be realized in practice throughout all the days of the year: "And may they all become one single bond to do Your will with a whole heart."

I am not deterred by those who might say that this is nothing more than a fantasy, for it is precisely in the life of the Jewish people in general, and regarding Eretz Yisrael and its affairs in particular, that we have seen that it is specifically those matters which appeared to be fantasies—without foundation in the way of nature or according to human calculations—that were realized. And this is all the more so during the days of Adar, which are days of success for the Jewish people.

The interpretation of our Sages of blessed memory is well-known: Why are they called *Yehudim*? Because they denied *avodah zarah* (idolatry)—all matters that are foreign to the spirit of the Torah and the service of Hashem, both in the line of "do good" and in the line of "turn away from evil," the positive mitzvos and the negative mitzvos, which are included in the utterances "I am" and "You shall have no other gods," and from there they are drawn down. See *Tanya*, beginning of Chapter 20. And furthermore, this should be done specifically as the teachings of Chassidus demand: with joy and a good heart.

With respect and blessing for joyful tidings, in accordance with these days, which are days of increasing joy.

Regarding the article in the booklet, "Expressions from the World of Kabbalah in Our Language," one should note (in haste)—that one must add: the world of *Ein Sof*, the world of *taanug* (*almin d’kisufin*), the world of *ratzon*, the world of *pirud*. **And more.** All of these have entered into literature, speeches, etc.—beginning from the world of *kedushah* down to the world of *kelipos* and *sitra achra*.

The quote from *Tanya*, Chapter 4, which you cite, does not refer to the worlds, but rather to the soul of man. The "world of *machshavah*," etc., is found in his *Sefer Torah Or* (75b) and in many other places.

## 8,179

B”H, 5 Adar II, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Moshe Meisels,

Shalom u’Bracha,

Your letter reached me after a long delay...

Since it has come into my hands, I will adopt the style of your letter and ask your forgiveness for what follows, which is this:

Based on what I heard about you when you lived in New York—regarding your talents, your ability, and your potential to influence your surroundings—I do not feel I have the right to refrain from noting and expressing my bewilderment, which I have held for some time: how is it that you are not utilizing your strengths as much as is possible and necessary? In our current era, when the creative forces within the Jewish people—the forces that are active and that activate others—have diminished, it is understood, and indeed simple, that the responsibility of each and every person who has been gifted with talent, potential, and the ability to act is many times greater.

I have written cautiously that you are "not utilizing them as much as is necessary," but on the face of it, the argument is much stronger than that.

I must also add that when you were living in New York, I asked how it is that people allow you to remain at rest—at least regarding activity in your environment—at a time when it is an absolute necessity of the hour to activate all positive forces, etc., etc. It was explained to me that it is the nature of your soul to be "hidden among the vessels," or at the very least to distance yourself from the *kosel hamizrach*, and that you are attached to the statement of the *Mishnah*: "I have found nothing better for the body than silence," etc., etc.

Now, without entering into a debate as to whether these excuses are justified or correct in this specific case, it is clear that the environment does not gain anything at all from the fact that a certain individual has a nice excuse.

I know that while you were here, you were an editor for *Der Tog*, and according to reports, in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), you hold a senior position at the Bialik Institute. But is it truly your own opinion that this is the "stone with which he struggles"? Our Sages of blessed memory spoke at length about how work must be done as it ought to be done, and with astonishing emphasis (see *Kesuvos 67a* at the beginning). And based on the promise that the measure of good is greater than the measure of retribution, the magnitude of the reward is understood when one utilizes their strengths as they ought to be utilized—if we were speaking of a man who is specifically driven by the pursuit of reward and compensation.

I was also told that in your lineage and your outlook, you are connected to Breslov and their worldview. I mention this specifically here, because one of the common excuses used to justify a lack of action is that there is no hope for success, "what good will it do," and "you are the fewest of all the peoples," etc., etc. Yet this is in complete contradiction to the slogan of Breslov: "Do not despair."

And as we are in the month of Adar, there is also a connection to the above in this as well, for the entire matter of the miracle of Purim is that, according to the way of nature, there appeared to be no possibility for salvation, and the miracle came about specifically in a manner of "it was turned around"—from one extreme to the other.

With respect and with a blessing to increase joy within the entirety of the Jewish people.

## 880

B"H, 5 Adar Sheni, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of the sixth grade, may you all be blessed,

Peace and blessing!

Your letter was received after a long delay, in which you write that you held a farbrengen regarding Chassidus Chabad in general and read a sicha on the weekly parsha, and you request a blessing for growth in the study of Torah and vitality in the fulfillment of mitzvos.

I have mentioned each and every one of you at the tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires for the good, and "he who comes to purify himself is assisted."

Regarding the theme of these days of Adar, the Midrash of our Sages, of blessed memory, is well known concerning the nullification of the decree of Haman the Agagite: that Mordechai the Tzaddik gathered 22,000 Jewish children and taught them Torah, specifically regarding matters connected to the Beis HaMikdash. These are not merely stories, but Torah—from the word *hora'ah* (instruction)—and the instruction is:

When Haman arises—literally in the physical sense, and even more so Haman in the spiritual sense, which is the yetzer hara—the advised counsel to thwart their schemes is to strengthen education in purity and holiness, to make for Him, may He be blessed, a dwelling place and a home in the lower worlds, in this physical world. This nullifies all the strength of the "other side" and brings about, as the Megillah describes, "For the Jews there was light, and gladness, and joy, and honor." As our Sages, of blessed memory, explained, "light" refers to Torah, etc., meaning that Torah and mitzvos are a lamp to one's feet and a light to one's path for each and every person in their daily life and conduct, so that their lives may be worthy of the name.

With blessings for good and joyful tidings, in accordance with these days in which we increase in joy.

## 8581

8581

B"H, 5 Adar II, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the President of the Barcelona Community,

Greetings and blessings!

Your letter regarding the visit of Rabbi Michael Lipsker shlita was received with some delay, and my response has been delayed as well, as I was awaiting a letter from Rabbi Lipsker to understand the prospects of fulfilling your requests.

Regrettably, as it appears from Rabbi Lipsker’s letter, he does not currently have a suitable avreich among his students who can fulfill all the necessary requirements. Nevertheless, I have asked him to continue his efforts in this matter. Certainly, you too will do everything within your power, as traditional education is a vital necessity, and the survival of the community depends upon it. It is my hope that through natural efforts and firm resolve, you will succeed in finding a person suitable for this mantle, and may the will of Hashem succeed in your hands.

With blessings for good news and a happy Purim.

## 882

B”H, 7 Adar II, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 21 Adar I.

As we stand in close proximity to the upcoming days of Purim, when the Jews “fulfilled and accepted” [the Torah]—meaning they fulfilled what they had already accepted, to nullify the great intimidation regarding the Torah—may it be Hashem’s will that each and every one increase their study of the revealed Torah and the study of Chassidus. Especially in those studies that are in the manner of *Torah she-b’rabim* (Torah study in public).

In particular, it can be said that the study of the inner dimension of the Torah is what sustains the study of the revealed Torah.

—This is analogous to the general nature of *avodah*, as explained at length in *Kuntres Eitz Chayim*, regarding how *avodah* in the manner of *yichuda ila’ah* (higher unity) sustains the *avodah* that is in the manner of *yichuda tata’ah* (lower unity)—

And then, this will be drawn down into the performance of *mitzvos* and their fulfillment—in accordance with the instruction of Chazal, “Great is study, for it leads to action”—because the concealments and obstructions will be nullified, since the study encompasses both the revealed and the inner dimensions together.

As is understood from the aforementioned *Kuntres*.

It can be said that this is also the path through which the performance of practical *mitzvos* and their fulfillment will be drawn into one’s *avodas Hashem* even within mundane matters, [fulfilling the directive] “In all your ways, know Him.”

Furthermore, it extends even to the *avodah* of refining the three *kelipos*, [achieving] the actual transformation of darkness into light (*atafcha chashucha mamash l’nehura*).

This is similar to the explanation of Chazal regarding “In all your ways, know Him”—even for a matter that is a transgression, if it is a necessity for a *mitzvah*, such as Eliyahu on Mount Carmel.

The superiority of this *avodah* is understood from what the Tzemach Tzedek wrote: that although in the place where *baalei teshuvah* stand, even perfect *tzaddikim* cannot stand, nevertheless, through the aforementioned *avodah*, one reaches a level even higher than that of *baalei teshuvah*.

However, all of this must be with joy and a glad heart specifically, in a way that is good, visible, and revealed.

For this is the superiority of Purim, which is the joy of the body and its affairs.

Thus, from all of the above, the practical *avodah* is surely understood.

With blessings for good tidings, a happy Purim, and great success in your holy work, with tranquility.

**M. Schneerson**

883

B"H, 8 Adar II, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished, G-d-fearing, and observant individual, engaged in communal affairs, a man of noble character, a scion of a distinguished family, etc., R’ Sh. Z. Shazar, may he live.

Shalom u’vracha,

Following up on the memorandum I sent you, which I am certain you received in due time—and I hope you are doing everything within your power regarding it—these days I have been in the company of Mr. Moshe Sharett, may he live. Naturally, I spoke with him as well regarding the point of the memorandum concerning the buildings used as internal facilities for absorbing immigrant youth: that the funding should come entirely from the housing budget and not from the education budget, as I explained in the memorandum. Mr. Sharett said that he sees the logic and the reasoning in the matter, and since there is a rational basis for it, he will bring the matter up for discussion at the first opportunity. It was also discussed that he would advocate in favor of it.

Needless to say, I also emphasized the point that no partisan matter or key should have any place in this question—where the buildings will be established, etc.—but rather that the sole approach should be that the parents’ wishes and the children’s background will be the deciding factors, without pressure, and a word to the wise is sufficient. Mr. Sharett promised this as well, adding that this is the case in any event.

It would be appropriate to elaborate on this vital matter, but you are surely among the diligent in such things, and may it be considered as if I had elaborated.

During our conversation, moving from one topic to another, I touched upon another point, which I have spoken about on various occasions with other public activists from Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established). It is a matter that truly touches upon and pertains to your field of operations, and I trust you will forgive me for expressing my opinion so decisively.

The matter concerns the emissaries of the Jewish Agency abroad regarding cultural affairs. In this field, there are two types: the general culture department and the Torah culture department.

We have seen tangibly that the propaganda of the general culture department has weakened in recent years, out of all proportion to what it was in the early years. There is a natural reason for this: in the early years, there was much novelty in this propaganda, and the impression was greater. There was also room to raise an outcry about the need to defend the borders, pioneering, and building, etc.—and as you know, I always emphasize the point of continuity regarding the youth. This is not the case in recent years, as the security situation, thank G-d, has improved, the spirit of pioneering has waned to a certain extent, and much of the novelty has lost its flavor. As a result of all this, the influence has weakened significantly. And this matter directly affects the assimilation, integration, and intermarriage among the youth, G-d forbid. This is not the case regarding the work of the emissaries of the Torah culture department, whose role—which they have had throughout all the years as a shield against the calamities of assimilation and integration—has not lost its flavor nor has its strength faded; on the contrary.

In light of the above, although I cannot express an opinion on the need to increase the number of Torah culture emissaries, as that is tied to the budget, I will offer a practical suggestion. As I suggested to Mr. Sharett, it would be appropriate to mandate that all emissaries, from whichever department they may be, emphasize Torah and its subjects. As our Sages of blessed memory said, "Great is study, for it leads to action." This applies even to those who do not yet intend to move to Eretz Yisrael or in whom the spirit of pioneering does not beat, but for whom there is a vital need to strengthen their standing and situation as Jews in the place where they reside, so as not to assimilate or integrate among the nations. This is not merely a theoretical matter; a Jew must be recognizable in his way of life as being distinct and different from the nations among whom he dwells. I do not mean that the emissaries themselves must be obligated to realize this perspective in their own conduct—for there is already a movement and demand in Eretz Yisrael to obligate them to conduct themselves according to Jewish tradition—but rather that this program should be incorporated into the scope of their work and propaganda.

I also added that after and in addition to all the aforementioned reasons, it is also a matter of "if one has two hundred, he has a hundred" (i.e., it includes the lesser within the greater). That is to say, by doing this, not only will the effectiveness of the emissaries’ influence—of whatever type they may be—not be diminished, but on the contrary, they are given an additional line and field of propaganda beyond their own, and this is well understood.

It is the way of a Jew to connect every matter with the weekly Torah portion or the time of year, as per the saying of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, "A Jew must live with the times." This is also the point of the days of Purim approaching us for good. Before the miracle, there was a distinction between those who enjoyed the feast of Achashverosh and those who stood with Mordechai. But when the pressure came from without—the decree of Haman the wicked to destroy **all** the Jews, from young to old, children and women, without any distinction or separation if they were only called by the name "Jew"—it immediately brought all the Jews to unity in a state of *mesiras nefesh*. As our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe states (Torah Or 97a), "It was *mesiras nefesh* for the sanctification of the Name, for if they had wanted to convert, Haman would have done nothing to them, as he only decreed against the Jews; rather, they surrendered themselves to death for the entire year, and no extraneous thought entered their minds, G-d forbid. And through the level of *mesiras nefesh*, they merited the level of complete acceptance, whereby the level of *Ohr Ein Sof* (the Infinite Light), blessed be He, was drawn into them and entered them." Thus far his holy words. May it be the will that we, too, merit this level, and to its light, joy, gladness, and honor.

With respect and blessing for good and joyful tidings, and a happy Purim,

**M. Schneerson**

Regarding what I emphasized above concerning the weakening of the propaganda in a natural way: I do not mind, and on the contrary, if they grasp the matter from a perspective that is beyond the natural way—only that we are approaching the end of the exile and the coming of Mashiach, our righteous redeemer, at which time the prophecy will be fulfilled, "The earth shall be full of the knowledge of Hashem," and consequently, one already begins to feel the footsteps of the Redemption, as I have heard this expression from you as well, even though the darkness of the exile still covers the earth.

And we conclude with good, that we may merit very soon that the darkness be turned into light through the revealed light of Hashem, for "Hashem shall be unto you an everlasting light," etc.

## 884

B"H, 9 Adar II, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After the longest of pauses, I received your letter from Sunday, in which you write regarding the offer you received for an administrative position in another country, etc., and you ask for my opinion on this.

It is understood that I was alarmed even at the mere thought of leaving, Heaven forbid, your current position and the institutions that you manage.

For, with your pardon, I am greatly surprised and astonished even by this thought. Surely you see the situation in your country now and in its surroundings, and how necessary the aforementioned institutions are. You are the one who manages them and **sustains them**, etc. There is no need to elaborate on such a simple matter. On the contrary, you should surely add strength to the management of these institutions to raise students—may they live and be well—who are imbued with yiras shamayim and a Torah-Chassidic worldview.

It is certainly unnecessary to elaborate on what is tangibly evident: that only the vitality, light, and hislahavus of Chassidus provide sufficient strength to stand before all the difficult trials that this orphaned generation experiences, without compromising on any matters of our Torah—Toras Chaim—and a word to the wise is sufficient.

I look forward to hearing good news regarding all of the above—including regarding the conclusion.

These days are the days of the month of Adar, when we must increase in simcha, and the ultimate goal is that there should be for the Jews "light"—this is Torah, etc., etc.

With respect and blessing.

## 858

B"H, Erev Purim, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Rabbi Shlomo Treshansky, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

It is with pleasure that I acknowledge receipt of the three volumes of *Sifrei Emek HaNetziv*, following our conversation. Many thanks for your thoughtfulness in sending them to me, and for the promptness in doing so.

It is my hope that our conversation will bring about tangible benefit in all the matters and areas we discussed, especially in the realm of Torah study—that "they upheld what they had already accepted"—and in a manner that "the Jews had light and gladness, and joy and honor," both in the literal sense and as interpreted by our Sages of blessed memory: "light" refers to Torah, etc.

With respect and with wishes for a happy Purim holiday.

As is the way of the Bnei Yisrael to express an opinion, allow me to offer a few comments regarding the aforementioned books:

It is surprising that no details were provided regarding the manuscript itself, such as whether it was preserved in its entirety, and the like. This is especially so since, in **Sifrei Devarim**, it appears the commentary is incomplete, starting from Parshas Teitzei. This is a matter of note, given that, as cited in the author’s introduction to his commentary on the *She'iltos* (Part 1, 17), his commentary on the *Sifrei* was already completed by him.

Furthermore, it is a pity that Part 3 lacks indices—"ears for the basket"—for even if one were to say that the indices for the two previous volumes were prepared by the author himself, and for some reason he did not prepare indices for the conclusion of the work, the task of creating indices could certainly be performed by others. I emphasize this point for two reasons: a) It is known from experience that when indices, references, and citations are missing, this deficiency—especially in our generation—deters one from studying, researching, and even reading the book. b) It is still possible to rectify this, at least in part, by printing the indices in a separate pamphlet and attaching it to Part 3.

Enclosed is a piece that was recently published, and I hope that you will find it of interest.

***

**As interpreted by our Sages:** *Megillah* 16b.

## 8,787

8,787

B.H., 16 Adar II, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Reuven Yelin, may he live.
Peace and blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter from the evening following Shabbos, 27 Adar I, in which you write of your impressions from the visit to Kfar Chabad, which you undertook with a group of friends and their families. It is understood that I was very happy to read of the impression the visit made upon you, and my hope is that all the visitors, and the youth in particular, were impressed to the same degree.

Since our nation, the people of Israel, is a practical one—and it is no wonder, for our Sages of blessed memory taught us in their Mishnah, "The deed is the essential thing"—my hope is strong that there will be tangible results in daily life. And surely you, as one of the organizers of the visit, will utilize all your influence in this direction.

If in all times and places there was a vital need to provide content to daily life—content according to the Torah and tradition—this is all the more true in our generation, in which many ideologies and ideals, from the extreme left to the extreme right, have resulted in disappointment. This situation is expressed primarily among the youth, who have not seen a life illuminated by the values of the eternal people of Israel. They feel they have been left in a void, devoid of any content, which leads to highly undesirable phenomena—when life enters a path of normalcy, what is called in worldly terms "gray life," and there is no special mission that provides an opportunity to reveal inner strengths, strengths of *gevurah* and *mesiras nefesh*, etc.

And with your forgiveness, it is the duty of the parents of this youth, doubled and redoubled, to fulfill what they have lacked in the education of their children until now. As our Sages of blessed memory phrased it, "If not now, when?" And what will they answer on the day of reckoning when the children demand to know why they were not given eternal and fundamental values that would provide content to their lives and encourage them in the difficult and gray struggle for existence?

Surely it is known to you that it is not the instruction of Chassidus to offer mere moral rebuke; in general, we strive to replace that with matters that encourage and elevate the soul. This is the point emphasized by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, founder of the Chabad Chassidic philosophy: that within every single Jew there is a soul called the *nefesh elokis*, a part of Hashem from above, literally. The emphasis of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe (in addition to the language of the verse) is the word **literally** (*mamash*). This means that every single one of the children of Israel possesses infinite strengths, if only they are willing to utilize them properly in a way of life worthy of the name. Then, the matters of nature, which are called by the world "laws of nature," not only do not prevent or hinder the aforementioned way of life, but, on the contrary, it is within a person's ability, duty, and privilege to elevate nature to a level above nature. As I have emphasized this point in several conversations with members of his party, the very character of this party facilitates and assists in accepting the aforementioned way of life, since one of its foundations is discipline—the acceptance of orders without questioning them, etc., etc.

With respect and blessing, and with regards to the visitors and their families, may they live.

It would certainly please me if you would convey the content of this letter to your fellow visitors and their families, and may these be words that come from the heart, which enter the hearts of those who hear them.

#### ***8,787***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 22, p. 433, and completed according to the secretariat's copy.

**That our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe emphasized:** *Tanya*, beginning of Chapter 2.

## 8,788

B"H, 16 Adar II, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Gideon Naor,

Shalom u’Bracha!

After a long interval, I was pleased to receive your letter of 25 Adar I. I thank you especially for your thoughtfulness in writing to me regarding the evening dedicated to the Chabad movement that took place in your city, Kiryat Gat, especially since, according to the reports I received, it was successful. Since our people, as a whole, are a people of action—and it is no wonder, for our Sages of blessed memory taught us in their Mishnah, "Action is the essential thing"—may it be G-d’s will that the aforementioned successful evening be extended into actual practice and into the daily lives of the residents of the city in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, so that they may correspond to the title known throughout the ends of the earth, and even among the nations of the world: the Holy Land.

Surely, in your respected position and with the talents with which you have been gifted, you can accomplish much in the direction mentioned, and I hope that you are utilizing your influence to its fullest.

As we stand on the day after Purim—when, in the language of the Megillah, "The Jews had light and gladness, and joy and honor," both in its literal sense and according to the exposition of our Sages of blessed memory: "Light—this is Torah"—this means that the lives of the Bnei Yisrael cannot be illuminated and illuminating except through their alignment with the instructions of the Torah, of which it is said, "For the Torah is a light." May it be G-d’s will that this be so in the lives of the residents of your city, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael.

With respect and blessing for good tidings.

It was with distress and great astonishment that I understood from your letter that the two Sifrei Torah that were sent some time ago have not yet been delivered; perhaps they were delayed by the offices. In any event, I have written immediately to our activists in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, with a request to clarify the matter and expedite it as much as possible.

## 892

B"H, 29 Adar Sheni, 5722
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, and diligent communal worker,
R' Yitzchak, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

...Your letter of 6 Adar Sheni has been received. In response to your questions:

1) Regarding your question as to what the decree was in Esther being taken to the King’s house, etc., given that they did not know she was Jewish—your intent is difficult to understand: Does the fact that Achashverosh did not know [her identity] mean that there was no decree of *galus* upon Esther? [Furthermore, the decree of "and they shall be gathered," etc., applied to the daughters of Yisrael as well.]

2) Regarding the matter of the fast of Esther’s maidens, who were not Jewish—

(Incidentally, in *Megillas Sesarim* it is explained that they were Yisraelis)—

And here, too, your intent is difficult to understand—for they are no worse than the cattle, the herds, and the flocks of Nineveh. Furthermore, they were her servants (the law of a Canaanite slave—who is obligated in several *mitzvos*, etc.).

3) Regarding the statement that the creation of the world was on the 25th (of Elul) and not on this [date]—this (the 25th) is merely a hint—

So it is written in *Likutei Torah*, *Maamar* "Sos Asis," Chapter 2.

4) Regarding the statement that the entire house was filled with light—[this refers to] *Memalei Kol Almin*, for a house is a *Makif*, but the light that **fills** the house is *Memalei*.

Your *Pidyon Nefesh* will be read at an auspicious time at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

***

892

**R' Yitzchak:** Dubov. Additional letters to him appear above in letter 828, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 8394

B"H, 4 Nissan, 5722
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, man of many accomplishments, R' Aharon Elimelech, may he live and be well.

Greetings and blessings!

After a very long hiatus, I received your letter of the 27th of Adar Sheni along with its enclosure. As per your request, I have responded without waiting for my turn, and for added measure, I am enclosing a copy of the response, in case it is needed for encouragement or further clarification; I rely on your understanding.

May it be the will of Hashem that our correspondence from here on out be solely regarding matters of goodness that is visible and revealed, and in the "true good" as explained by Chazal: good for Heaven, good for people, and good that produces fruit.

You have been privileged, and through Divine Providence, have succeeded in influencing broad circles within our camp, and according to reports, even in the expanses of Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established.

And according to the teaching of Chazal, "a woman while spinning also talks," it is understood that I will also mention your success in *hafatzas hama'ayanos*—a mention whose purpose is also to serve as a demand regarding the failure to utilize your talents for *hafatzas hama'ayanos* to the fullest extent possible. This is a necessity of the hour and a personal obligation, etc., etc., for one such as yourself, surely any elaboration on this is superfluous, even though, when compared to the importance and great value of the matter, no matter how much one writes about it, it is never enough.

My hope is that you will bring me good news at the conclusion of our correspondence, in addition to the good news at its beginning, and that you will see good fruit in your work to spread the Torah of Chassidus in a way that is "increasing and adding light," until the true freedom—freedom from the *yetzer hara*—when the King Moshiach comes through *hafatzas hama'ayanos*.

With respect and blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 895

B"H, 5 Nissan, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed avreichim, G-d-fearing and distinguished, graduates of the class completing the fifth cycle
at the Vocational School in Kfar Chabad
May they live.

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter with pleasure, along with the list of the graduating students, may they live, with a request for a blessing on the occasion of their completing their course of study at the Vocational School in Kfar Chabad.

It is superfluous to emphasize that the completion applies only to the school itself. Regarding the spirit of the school in which they were educated—and certainly regarding all matters of Torah and mitzvos illuminated by the teachings of Chassidus and its guidance—there is no such thing as a "completion," G-d forbid. On the contrary, one must always ascend in holiness. Surely you will continue to go from strength to strength in this, in your daily lives and in "in all your ways know Him," as well as in influencing others, each according to his ability. And this depends only on one's will.

At an auspicious time, I will mention all of you at the resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, the founder of the institution which is conducted in his spirit, that Hashem may fulfill the requests of your hearts for good and for blessing, and that you may succeed in both material and spiritual matters alike.

And in anticipation of the festival of Pesach, the time of our freedom, which is approaching for us and for all of Israel for good and for blessing, my blessing is sent to each and every one of you for a kosher and joyous Pesach, and for true freedom—freedom from all matters that distract from the service of Hashem with joy and a good heart.

With blessing.

## 8398

B"H, 9 Nissan, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings,

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from Wednesday, along with the enclosure regarding a mitzvah which, in your opinion, is—to use your words—"a burning question in the heart of every Jew faithful to Hashem and His Torah."

While I do not believe I know you personally, you are surely aware of the state of the place and the country in which you **are located**—regarding loyalty to Hashem and His Torah, where the abandonment is great, etc., etc. Is it truly your opinion that the mitzvah about which you write is the burning question in the place where the majority of our people, the Children of Israel, are found? And what of other places and countries, and even in our Holy Land—may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu? Are you aware of the percentage of intermarriage, *rachmana litzlan*? Are you aware of the situation regarding the education of Jewish boys and girls on the purity of holiness? The situation regarding the observance of Shabbos and its opposite in public, **etc.** **etc.**? [Not to mention matters that are not as public].

Seemingly, it is **simple** that every Jew who is wholehearted toward Hashem and His Torah should have **acted upon this**, in the style of Chazal as it ought to be (*Kesuvos* 67a), by rectifying all the matters listed above. These are—by **all** accounts—from the Torah, and by all accounts, they are **fundamental** to the religion and its foundations. By all accounts, the redemption of Israel from this bitter exile—a double and redoubled exile—depends upon them.

Chazal have said that the Yetzer Hara is an expert craftsman (*Shabbos* 105b). Therefore, he does not begin by telling someone, "Go worship idols." Rather, he tells him, "Do this"—and as my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisroel, said, his beginning is such—that he agrees with the person’s path so that he will listen to his enticement. Since the person in question is a student of Torah who wishes to be faithful to Hashem and His Torah, he tells him that he agrees with him on all the aforementioned, and he invents matters for him to occupy himself with according to his stated path, provided that he does not pay attention to the truly burning questions. And ultimately, as per the instructions of our holy Torah, the *Torah of Life*, in the beginning, "when fire breaks out and finds thorns" (it burns only the thorns, but afterwards, "the stack of grain or the standing grain is consumed"). One should not dwell on a matter that is distressing to the point of alarm.

It is clear that my intention in all the above is not to preach morality, but rather—perhaps, just perhaps—that these few lines of mine will awaken you to utilize all your possibilities, and to influence every place your hand can reach so that they, too, may utilize their own strengths to repair the breach of Israel, both in the Diaspora and in Eretz Yisroel, *tichyeh v'tizkeh*, regarding all the above and similar matters.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all that has been said, and for a kosher and happy Pesach.

Regarding the conclusion of your letter, that you intend to emigrate from these countries—the attitude toward the approach of "fleeing from the battlefield" (the battle for Yiddishkeit in the place where one lives) is well known, provided only that "I have saved my own soul."

But has he truly done and accomplished **everything** he could have done here to strengthen Yiddishkeit? And "the poor of your city take precedence"—by **all** accounts?!

Regarding the content enclosed with your letter: After asking your forgiveness, it contains a confusion of issues. For the debate is: Is there in our time a mitzvah (from the Torah) to move from the Diaspora to Eretz Yisroel? If not, or even more so, that there is also the prohibition from Chazal not to "go up by a wall," that one who moves from Bavel to Eretz Yisroel transgresses a positive commandment, etc.

This is unrelated to the matter of kissing its stones, the prohibition of *lo techaneim*, the prohibition for one who is in Eretz Yisroel not to leave for the Diaspora, etc., etc. The fact that it is simple that those in the Diaspora are forbidden from causing destruction in Eretz Yisroel even in our time—this is no proof **at all** that they are obligated to move to Eretz Yisroel.

***

**Regarding the mitzvah:** See also above, Letter 8258, and the references in the notes there.

**And as the Rebbe said:** See *Sefer HaMaamarim 5689*, p. 124; *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 18, p. 296; and references cited there.

**And the poor of your city take precedence:** *Bava Metzia* 71a.

**The debate:** See also *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 2, p. 619 and onwards; Vol. 18, p. 399 and onwards; and references cited there.

## 8399

8399

B"H, 11 Nissan, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Menachem Begin, may he live and be well,

Shalom and blessing!

I received your letters in due time, and I was even more pleased to receive your personal regards via Mr. Yaakov Meridor, may he live and be well, who surely conveyed my regards back to you if he has already arrived in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, as well as the content of our conversation regarding the specific matter and matters of the general public.

It is surely superfluous to add that I was pleased to make the acquaintance of Mr. Meridor, and I thank you for having brought this about.

My heart aches due to the propaganda being conducted recently against religion and religious people, in a manner and on a scale that—I hope—no one imagined could exist in Yisrael, in both senses of the term: among the people of Bnei Yisrael and in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established. It seems that our era is capable of all manner of innovations and discoveries, even to the point of surprise. And according to the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory, that the measure of goodness is greater than the measure of retribution, may it be His will that very soon we merit surprising news in matters of goodness and holiness, the eternal values of our people, Bnei Yisrael, from time immemorial. And according to the motto of the teachings of Chassidus, beginning with its founder, the Baal Shem Tov, one cannot imagine the treasures hidden in the soul of every single one of Bnei Yisrael, and fortunate is the portion of each person who reveals them and puts them into action.

As we stand before the Festival of Matzos, the time of our freedom, may it be His will that there be freedom in all areas and matters—freedom of both body and soul together. In truth, one is impossible without the other, and as mentioned above, fortunate is the portion of each person who merits and succeeds in contributing their appropriate share to true freedom—not only the freedom of the individual, but also the freedom of the collective. And if you will, in truth, even in this regard, one is impossible without the other.

With respect and blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## Ch'T

11 Nissan, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To our brethren, the Children of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

The Festival of Matzos, the time of our freedom—*der yom-tov fun undzer bafrayung*—is a part of Torah. And Torah, after all, means *hora'ah*—instruction, teaching, and guidance.

It teaches us and illuminates the true concept of freedom—a concept that is interpreted in many ways, some of which are quite strange.

The Yom Tov of Pesach is a reminder and an explanation of what **true** freedom means. It must be a complete and total liberation in all three realms of which a person and their life consist: a) the realm of the **neshamah**, b) the realm of the **guf**, and c) **the world** around them.

It must be in each of these realms, and in all three **together**.

This means that in every one of these areas, a Yid must be truly free, and this must be in a way that there is no conflict or fragmentation between them.

On the contrary, they should complement and perfect one another; only then is it **true cheirus**.

It goes without saying that it is impossible for this harmonious and full freedom to be achieved if the neshamah—the *chelek Eloka m'ma'al mamash* (the G-dly element within a person)—bows to the guf, and both the neshamah and the guf bow to the world. The highest cannot serve the lower and be satisfied with it. The highest element in human life, the neshamah, will never agree to lower itself to the guf. From this follows the clear conclusion that true freedom can be reached only when the lower components of human life—the guf and the surrounding world—are elevated to the highest possible level of closeness to the neshamah and its aspirations, and the neshamah, in turn, is freed from everything that hinders its elevation.

***

This is what we find in the Galus of Mitzrayim and the Yetzias Mitzrayim.

**Galus Mitzrayim** was a **complete** enslavement in all three of the aforementioned realms of human life: (a) the spiritual enslavement in a land—and to a land—of tumah and the lowest moral degradation, which is why Mitzrayim is called *ervas ha'aretz*; (b) the worst physical enslavement of *avodas parech*; and (c) the total robbery of their share in the world to which they were entitled as human beings in general, and as Yidden in particular.

**Yetzias Mitzrayim**, the liberation, was also in all three realms, and in the fullest and highest measure: (a) First and foremost—the complete liberation of the neshamah: "Draw out and take for yourselves sheep... and slaughter the Pesach offering"—not only to refrain from serving the idol of Mitzrayim, but to publicly demonstrate its worthlessness. (b) The complete liberation from the enslavement of the guf—they left Mitzrayim **b'yad ramah**, with heads held high, with song and parade. (c) And their share in the world—they left **birchush gadol**, with great wealth.

***

There are those who wish to settle for the liberation of the neshamah alone: they daven, they learn Torah, and so on. But when they sit down to eat and drink, they are enslaved to the *behemah* (animal soul) that is within the person.

There is a further level—one recognizes that the guf and its needs must also be liberated, and it must be evident that it is a Yid who is eating.

But when they leave the house and must act in the world and **accomplish** in the world, to acquire wealth—they become a servant (slave) to the land of Mitzrayim, because they have left the Torah, the Shulchan Aruch, and their own *Yetzias* Mitzrayim locked away at home.

And this is what we remind and demand of everyone: "Remember the day of your departure from the land of Mitzrayim all the days of your life"—every single day of their life, a Yid must remember Yetzias Mitzrayim:

Remember that you were **liberated**—a liberation of the neshamah, a liberation of the guf, and that the liberated neshamah and guf have taken the wealth of Mitzrayim and turned it into **their** *rechush gadol*, a **Yiddishe** *rechush gadol*.

***

"I do not ask except according to their strength"—the Ribono shel Olam, who is the Creator of man, says that what He asks of Yidden and demands of them is according to their strength and capability. There only needs to be a firm will to fulfill the Ribono shel Olam's request. And this is also the way—the only way—that leads to **cheirusenu**, to our true freedom: liberation from the internal galus, and then also from galus in the literal sense—through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 8404

8404

B"H, 18 Nissan, 5722
Brooklyn.

Mr. David, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter of 12 Nissan.

Many thanks for your blessings. As has been mentioned several times, there is a strong instruction in the Torah that whoever blesses a Jew is blessed by Hashem, as it is written, "I will bless those who bless you," and the blessing of the Ribono shel Olam is with an increase far greater than the original.

Regarding the content of your letter concerning the mitzvah of *aliyah l'regel* (pilgrimage to Jerusalem):

I wish to be very hopeful, since you write in this manner regarding a mitzvah which—for Jews who were in the Diaspora while the Beis Hamikdash was standing, and certainly since the destruction of the Beis Hamikdash, for all Jews—is surely not a mitzvah *d'oraysa*. Therefore, it is *kal v'chomer* that from now on you will do **everything** that depends on you to fulfill the mitzvah of "Love your fellow as yourself." As our Sages explain, this includes the idea that just as one wishes to act for oneself—to conduct one's daily life according to the instructions of our holy Torah, *Toras Chaim*, and through the fulfillment of its mitzvos, of which it is said, "you shall live by them"—one must do the same for others. In ways of pleasantness, you should ensure that **all** those around you fulfill all the mitzvos that are certainly *d'oraysa*, all the mitzvos that are *d'rabanan*, and subsequently, also strive for *hiddur mitzvah*, and so on. We have been assured that "words that come from the heart enter the heart."

And according to what I have heard, there is much to be done in Passaic regarding *chinuch al taharas hakodesh*, as many children currently do not have such an education, as well as other matters of *al taharas hakodesh*. I hope that, as mentioned, you will act in this with great energy, and may the Ribono shel Olam grant you success.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

Due to the holiness of the *moed*, the Rebbe did not sign personally, and I sign on his behalf,

The Secretary

**P.S.** Understandably, it will be pleasing for me to hear of your success in all that was mentioned above.
