## 8,707

B"H, 30 Nissan, 1st day of Rosh Chodesh Iyar, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the annual dinner of Yeshivas Achi-Temimim Lubavitch in Newark,
May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom and Blessing!

I have received with pleasure the news regarding your upcoming annual event on the 23rd of Iyar, may it come upon us for good.

As we emerge from the auspicious month of Nissan and enter the auspicious month of Iyar, I send my blessing that Hashem Yisbarach should grant success to your endeavor in both respects—materially and spiritually—which, among Yidden, are bound and united together.

The month of Iyar is distinguished by the fact that every day of the month is blessed with a special mitzvah, the mitzvah of **Sefiras HaOmer**. It was also in this month that the construction of the first **Beis HaMikdash** began.

As is known, the yeshiva and the shul, where Yidden study Torah and engage in tefillah, occupy the place of the Beis HaMikdash today and are called a "Beis Mikdash Me'at." Their task is the same as the task of the Beis HaMikdash: to maintain the connection of Yidden with their Father in Heaven through Torah and mitzvos in daily life—the constant, uninterrupted Jewish way of life.

All of you who have a share in this, through your assistance to the yeshiva, are investing in immediate and eternal values and benefits.

I hope that you will do this with a generous hand, and this will stand by you to be blessed by the Almighty from His full and generous hand, in all your needs, both materially and spiritually.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 810

810

B"H, 2 Iyar, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Gershon David, may he live, known as Dr. Cohen,

Shalom u’vracha!

I received your letter in due time, as well as the reprints and the book. Thank you for the gift, although my many preoccupations have delayed this response, for which I ask your forgiveness.

As is the way of a Jew to add a touch of his own, I would like to offer a comment regarding the reprint of your article on the subject of the "Four Captives," which I read through in haste, and as a continuation of our conversation on this matter. On one hand, one must begin with praise regarding the discovery and the arguments you express there concerning the source of the narrative and the tradition of the Four Captives and the details thereof. Yet, after asking your forgiveness, I must say that the matter in its entirety does not sit well with me. This is based on a story told about a great figure in Israel: in a conversation with him, someone said that the Rambam writes such-and-such. He replied, "It is not so," and added that this was not because he was an expert in every corner of the Rambam and that no mystery was hidden from him, but rather because since the matter is entirely inconsistent with the entire system of the Rambam, it is impossible that such a thing could be written by him.

Similarly, in the present case, regarding the explanation you propose in your article—that the Ra’avad, author of *Sefer HaKabbalah*, invented the argument that there were captives, R’ Chanoch, etc., and that they were captured and arrived at a certain place at the same time, etc.—from a psychological perspective [and allow me to express my opinion more sharply, without a preconceived approach that one must invent something new], this argument is not at all intellectually acceptable. The reason is simple: there is no doubt that the Ra’avad was a keeper of Torah and mitzvos and knew the commandment, "Distance yourself from a false matter." Furthermore, he lived in a time and place that was **not** at a vast distance in time and space from the era of the Four Captives. Therefore, the mind cannot tolerate the idea that the Ra’avad invented the story of the Four Captives in order to strengthen his arguments and his system—and furthermore, that the overwhelming majority of his contemporaries accepted his innovation without any doubt!

It is understood that the challenges regarding the author of *Sefer HaKabbalah* concerning dates and the like have not escaped me. But this is along the lines of what I believe I mentioned in our conversation: it is possible that he was not as precise as required regarding sources, transmitters of tradition, etc. It is also possible to err, or perhaps to adjust in a certain direction regarding the date of an event that spanned a period of time, from its beginning to its end. As I mentioned in our conversation, for example, regarding the completion of the Talmud or the completion of the Mishnah—all of this is not a matter of contradicting the commandment to "distance yourself from a false matter." Rather, one might interpret the completion of the Talmud as the end of the days of Rav Ashi, while another might connect it to the Ravanan Savorai, since their statements are brought in the Shas. Similarly, one could conclude that the Talmud was completed in the middle of the days of Rav Ashi, and so on. But this is not at all comparable to the innovation and invention of a matter from its very foundation, as you propose in your article, which does not befit a Torah-observant Jew. Especially since, as mentioned, the Ra’avad lived approximately two hundred years after this, and there were certainly traditions, and even written records, regarding the details of the event, and the grandchildren and descendants of the Four Captives were still alive, etc.

To return to the content of our conversation regarding the actual dissemination of Yiddishkeit: action is the essential thing. The expression we mentioned in our conversation regarding the *etzem* (essence)—that the essence is unchanging and is the opposite of the "accidental" in the language of the Jewish philosophers—is my hope that this will continue in actual practice. Especially since you have been gifted with influence over a certain circle, an important part of which consists of youth and young people, for any good influence upon them shapes their form, leading even to the building of a home in Israel, etc.

With respect and blessing.

P.S. It is my hope that you will continue to send me your publications, and thank you in advance.

I would also like to note regarding the check you sent in your letter: even though when a Jew gives tzedakah through me, it is understood that I am happy to be a *shaliach* for any matter of a mitzvah—especially in the matter of tzedakah, which is equivalent to all the mitzvos—I must note immediately that in matters of tzedakah, the demand is to solicit from the one who is most wealthy in that area. Regarding you, whatever your situation may be in terms of tangible assets, you are certainly wealthier in spiritual values. Therefore, my hope is strong that you will bestow from these assets in the field of your activities as mentioned above, in appropriate content and in an appropriate form, and with words that come from the heart—the essence of the heart—which also does not change. This is as our Sages of blessed memory interpreted the verse, "I sleep, but my heart is awake"—I am asleep in *galus*, but my heart is awake to Hashem, to His Torah, and to His mitzvos.

#### ***810***

**Tzedakah:** Bava Basra 9a.

**As our Sages interpreted:** Zohar Vol. III, 95a.

## 6,812

B"H, 2 Iyar, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write regarding your health and the main points of your ailment over the past few years, along with the treatments, etc., that you have undergone.

It is not clear from your letter—though I am certain that this is the case—whether you are consulting with leading physicians in the field. There are several such doctors in Europe, and for an ailment such as the one you describe, especially given the uncertainty surrounding it, it is certainly worth the effort to connect specifically with a top specialist.

On the other hand, it is difficult to understand how, until now, they have not clearly determined the nature of the ailment and the method of treatment, especially since, as it appears from your letter, this has been going on for several years and you have surely had several X-rays taken.

Naturally, I am not writing to ask questions, but rather to prompt you, at the very least regarding the present, that it would be worthwhile to investigate who is the most expert specialist in this field, to send him the letters from the doctors who have treated you and all the information that needs to be known, and to ask for his general advice and whether it is advisable to visit him.

May it be the will of Hashem, the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders, that your complete recovery should come about through a suitable doctor and an appropriate treatment, and from Him—the Almighty—everything is wondrous.

And may the merit of the chinuch you provide for your children, shichyeh—chinuch based on the purity of holiness—stand by you in the aforementioned matters, and in all your affairs.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all the above, and likewise regarding your activities for the dissemination of traditional Judaism.

## 815

## 8416

8416

B"H, 17th of Iyar, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the National Convention of Yeshiva Administrators, 20-23 Iyar
Ferndale, N.Y.
May Hashem grant them life

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your notification regarding your convention, may it be Hashem’s will that it be met with overwhelming success and tangible results—a convention through which the Name of Hashem is sanctified, both by the gathering itself and by each individual participant, with added blessing and success in their holy work.

I wish to take this opportunity to bring to the attention of the convention and its attendees a fundamental point concerning the foundations of *chinuch* on the basis of *taharas hakodesh*. It is a point that requires swift and complete rectification, and it is surprising that it has not yet been addressed:

For various reasons, in the vast majority of yeshivos in this country, the students study both *limudei kodesh* and—to distinguish between the holy and the mundane—*limudei chol* within the walls of the yeshiva, at least until a certain age. Without entering into the merits of this situation, it is a reality that cannot be ignored.

Considering that students are at an age where they are influenced by every detail—not only directly, but also indirectly, and sometimes the indirect influence is even more powerful—it is impossible for the student not to be impressed by the attitude they perceive toward these two domains. Therefore, it is imperative that the student see, with absolute clarity, that even though both are studied within the walls of the yeshiva, the primary focus is the study of our holy Torah, the *Toras Chaim*, and that *limudei chol* are merely secondary, and incomparable to the primary.

The tragedy is that, unfortunately, in a significant portion of yeshivos—and perhaps in the majority—the emphasis, indirectly and sometimes even directly, is the opposite. That is to say, not only are they treated as equal in value, but greater importance is attributed to *limudei chol*. This greater "importance" is expressed in many ways: in the studies themselves—the insistence on progress, homework, frequent examinations, etc.; and the success in these examinations is lauded with all manner of praise, prizes, awards, and the like. This is true even within the walls of the yeshiva, to say nothing of the home. It is also expressed in external matters—the format of the textbooks, the classrooms, the facilities, and so on. Furthermore, it is evident in the personal attitude toward the teachers of *limudei kodesh* versus those who teach *limudei chol*, where a disparity is noticeable in favor of the latter in several areas, including salary and the like.

If this attitude came only from the laypeople or the parents, I would remain silent—and all the more so since, at times, this attitude is also evident on the part of the administration and the directors.

I have already written at length during the past Purim regarding the great damage caused by this excessive emphasis on *limudei chol*. For it is simple and understood that the primary goal of the yeshiva, whether it is called a *yeshiva ketana* or simply a yeshiva, is the study of our holy Torah. Even if one can find reasons or perhaps even "justifications" for certain details of the aforementioned attitude, it is easy for a person of understanding to see that this attitude undermines the foundations of *chinuch*, and the harm resulting from this cannot be overstated.

Therefore, I come to urge the convention to discuss this consequential problem with the utmost seriousness, in order to implement immediate improvement and rectification, and the merit of the many will assist you.

With respect and blessings for success,

## 817

817

B"H, Lag B'Omer, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the members of Agudas N'shei U'Bnos Chabad everywhere, and to the participants in the seventh annual convention in particular,
May Hashem grant you life!

Blessings and peace!

The annual convention is taking place this year immediately after **Shabbos Chazak**, the conclusion of Sefer **Vayikra**, which is called **Toras Kohanim** and **Sefer HaKorbanos**. I hope that this will set the proper "tone" for the convention.

The idea behind this is as follows:

Jews in general, and every Jew in particular, must be similar to a *kohen*, as Hashem has commanded: **"And you shall be to Me a kingdom of kohanim"** (you will be a kingdom of *kohanim* to Me). Just as a *kohen* was chosen to occupy himself with the holy *avodah*, not only for himself but also for his brothers, the entire Jewish people, so too is every Jew chosen to serve Hashem and bears a responsibility toward those around them.

**Avodas Hashem**—serving Hashem—does not mean isolating oneself or withdrawing from the world; it means serving Hashem **in** the world and **with** the world—starting from one’s own home, which should be conducted in such a way that the *Shechinah* rests there, as the verse says: "And they shall make Me a sanctuary, and I will dwell among them."

This is achieved through conduct similar to **korbanos**.

The concept of **korbanos** was: one would take items from their own possessions—a sheep, flour, oil, wine, salt, etc.—and from them create a *korban*: a *korban olah*, entirely for G-d; or a *korban shelamim*, where after a portion was offered upon the *mizbeach*, the *kohen* and the Jew who brought the *korban* would eat, eating in a state of *taharah*.

In this way, a Jewish home must be conducted in all its details; then the *Shechinah* rests there, and it is a home blessed in both *gashmius* and *ruchnius*.

Realizing this in life depends to the greatest extent upon—and this is the primary task of—the Jewish woman, the **akeres habayis**: to bring the *Shechinah* into the home and into family life, and to educate the children in this spirit.

May Hashem help you to carry out your task to the fullest extent, and with Chassidic warmth and vitality.

And in this way, also hasten the time when the *Beis HaMikdash* will be rebuilt and the *avodah* will be restored, when the *Geulah HaAmitis VeHaShleimah* will come through *Moshiach Tzidkeinu*, speedily in our days.

With a wish and blessing that the convention and all the members in general shall fulfill all of the above with success, in joy and with a good heart.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 819

B"H, 24 Iyar, 5722
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of the Reshet Yeshivos HaErev,
May Hashem keep them alive.

Peace and Blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 17 Iyar, along with the enclosure.

As we stand in the days between Lag B'Omer—the threshold of Atzeres—and Atzeres itself, the time of the giving of our Torah, may it be Hashem’s will that the interpretation of Chazal regarding the verse "How good and how pleasant it is for brothers to dwell together" be fulfilled in us. This refers to those who engage in the *shakla v'tarya* and the "war of Torah," and who subsequently return to one another in brotherly love. This is in addition to the literal meaning: the drawing together of hearts in a manner of *shabbos* (a term denoting settling and tranquility) *gam yachad* (together), until reaching complete unity.

This is also the preparation and the vessel for receiving the Torah, as in the account in *Tanchuma*: when the Holy One, Blessed be He, saw that Yisrael was *vayichan*—in the singular—encamped against the mountain, only then did He give the Torah.

This applies to both the revealed and the inner dimensions of Torah.

May it be so regarding all that was mentioned in your letter. May blessing and success rest upon your holy work, and through this, upon all your affairs, both general and specific. As the conclusion states: "For there Hashem commanded the blessing, life forevermore."

With blessings for success in your holy work and for good tidings in all that was mentioned.

## 820

B"H, 27 Iyar, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 21 Iyar.

At a time of favor, I mentioned [you] at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter.

Certainly, for someone like you, it is unnecessary to mention the instruction of Chazal: "A person should never despair," etc. This is especially true in light of what is explained regarding this in the teachings of Chassidus, the immediate conclusion of which is not to slacken in exerting appropriate influence on the aforementioned person in the appropriate direction. I believe I have already written to you regarding this, noting what is seen tangibly in similar cases: that indirect influence has better prospects than direct influence.

Furthermore, regarding your note that the person is under the care of a doctor who deals with mental health—while it is not entirely clear which doctor you mean—generally, in our generation, there is a specific type of such practitioners who begin treatment by speaking about Hashem, the honor of Heaven, and the honor of father and mother, etc. It is worth investigating and clarifying the great reward in this, and even if he [the patient] is skeptical, one must consider whether he is not losing out in the long run.

It is simple fact that many such doctors have been effective and have healed through upright methods, especially since one professor found the courage to declare and announce that—contrary to the theory of the founder of this treatment—faith in Hashem and religious inclination in general, which brings content to life, etc., are among the most effective paths to healing. Nevertheless, for several reasons, this approach has not yet penetrated wide circles of such doctors, and therefore, there is room for clarification.

I was pleased to read in your letter that you are acting for the benefit of the people of Kfar Chabad, though it is surprising that you limit your efforts by adding the word "materially."

With respect and blessings for good tidings in all the above.

#### ***820***

**Instruction of Chazal:** Berachos 10a.

## 821

821

*[Iyar, 5722]*

(Regarding all these matters, the subject under discussion is **not** Shabbos, but rather: [the phrase] *az alt* [old], *aliyas ruach* [ascent of spirit], *amo* [with him], and also *choshech* [darkness], etc.)

The connection of the concepts (at least according to the simple meaning): The general theme of the chapter is how one should contemplate and arrive at a state where his soul becomes inflamed, etc., to cleave, etc., and to be included in His light, etc. (this is [the movement] from below to above). But how does this inclusion occur? The text states: "upon your heart, and you shall speak of them," etc. (**from above to below**!). (However, this is not difficult), as is written in *Etz Chaim* that the essence is the **contemplation** (*iyun*). "And you shall speak" is merely the revelation of the aforementioned. (And one must still examine: what is the necessity for the revelation, and what is its connection to the aforementioned—to be included, etc.? And it explains:) For by every **"motza pi Hashem"**—which is the Torah—man shall live (even without the speech of man). Nevertheless, one does not fulfill his obligation, etc.—(and therefore, the revelation through the **speech of man** is necessary) down to the *nefesh ha'chiyunis*, etc.

(And this, too, is connected to the contemplation, etc., for the purpose is) in order to **elevate** them all, etc., and to **include them**, etc.

And to note, at least according to the simple meaning: 1) Perhaps it also emphasizes the term **"motza"** (source/outlet) of the mouth of Hashem—meaning the **source** (see *Drushei Masei*), which is the opposite of revelation. 2) Even though it cites the **language** of the verse, it omits the word **"kol"** (all) (from *kol motza pi Hashem*). And according to the above, it is explained—for the verse speaks of the *nefesh ha'elokis* and also of the *nefesh ha'chiyunis* and the body.

***

The letter is addressed to R' Eliyahu Nachum Sklar and was written on the margin of his letter. Another letter to him—see above, Vol. 1, 54.

**Regarding all these:** In his letter, he asks why the *Mafteach Inyanim* (Index of Topics) for *Tanya*, under the entry "Shabbos," cites the Rebbe: "*avad gi...*": But surely there is [the phrase] *az alt amo*.

**The connection of the concepts:** In his letter: "In the *Tanya* *shiurim* last week, at the end of Chapter 49, I cannot understand the point after 'the aspect of speech in words of Torah.' For surely this is not the conclusion of the matter. And furthermore, it is not understood because the *Tanya* *shiur* ends there, and in general, the connection of the concepts in these lines is not understood."

See also *Shiurim B'Sefer HaTanya* there.

## 8423

8423

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, [Chaim Mordechai HaKohen]

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated the 25th of Iyar.

...Regarding the matter of the mikvaos — in general, your suggestion is good. However, in the place where you suggest (for a certain reason) constructing a *bor* to render the mikveh kosher on the side, it has recently become common practice to construct **two** *boros* to render it kosher (on two sides): one by way of *zriah* (seeding) and the second by way of *hashakah* (contact). This is highly appropriate. And this is simple to understand.

#### ***8423***

Published in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 17, p. 476, and completed based on a photocopy of the letter.

**R' Chaim Mordechai:** Perlov, Melbourne. Additional letters to him appear above, Vol. 18, 6786, and in the references noted there. See below, 8448.

**Regarding the matter of the mikvaos:** In his letter: "My opinion is that the mikveh should be constructed according to the view of the Rebbe Rashab, *ztzvkllh"h zy"a v'achi"a*—a mikveh atop a mikveh, where the *hashakah* is at the bottom... It is understood that they [the city rabbis] agree to this, but they say that an additional *bor* of rainwater must be made above, into which the regular water will fall and also become kosher through *zriah* (and this is, of course, in addition to the *bor* of rainwater that must be ready at all times to replace the *hashakah* water below, as well as the *zriah* water mentioned above)...

But even if we say that it is not strictly necessary, it is, in any event, a form of *hiddur* (beautification of the mitzvah)."

In continuation of this — see below, letter 8448. See also above, Vol. 14, letter 5140, and the references noted there.

## 824

824

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the annual dinner of the educational institution
Oholei Torah
May Hashem keep them alive

Shalom u’vracha!

I was pleased to receive the news regarding your annual event.

May Hashem Yisbarach help that the event be successful, both materially and spiritually.

Since this event is taking place a few days after Shavuos, *Zman Matan Toraseinu*, I hope that all the participants and *askanim* will bring with them to the dinner the impression and spirit of the Yom Tov of *Kabbalas HaTorah*, especially the point that connects this Yom Tov with *chinuch al taharas hakodesh*. By this, I refer to what our Sages, of blessed memory, said: that the holy Torah was not given until the Jews provided their children as *arvus* (guarantee) that the Torah would be upheld and preserved — **"Our children are our guarantors."**

Since the Jewish people undertook this guarantee, and the Ribono shel Olam accepted this guarantee, it is clear that the guarantee is a tangible reality and can, and must, be fulfilled. In other words: Jews have the **full** and **certain** ability to carry out the obligation of "our children are our guarantors" in practice — through Torah-education *al taharas hakodesh*; one only needs to truly desire it.

Therefore, I hope that all the esteemed *askanim*, supporters, and friends of the educational institution **Oholei Torah** will — in the spirit of the Yom Tov of *Kabbalas HaTorah* — utilize the opportunity of this annual event to provide the necessary help, not only to support but also to expand the educational institution Oholei Torah. In the merit of this, Hashem Yisbarach will also expand His help to each and every one, together with their families *shichyu*, in everything they need, both materially and spiritually, as it is assured in the Torah — "It is a tree of life to those who grasp it, and those who support it are made happy."

With respect and with a blessing for success, and in the language of the Rebbe — my father-in-law, the Rebbe — for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness,

**Menachem Schneerson**

***

**Our children are our guarantors:** Shir HaShirim Rabbah on the verse "Draw me, we will run after you." Midrash Tehillim on the verse "Out of the mouths of babes and sucklings You have founded strength" (with slight variations in wording).

**A tree of life... are made happy:** See also Zohar Vol. III (53b) and the teachings of the Alter Rebbe on this, cited and explained in the *maamar* entitled *Etz Chaim* — Simchas Torah 5739 [Sefer HaMaamarim 5739, p. 68] — by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

## 8205

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Women’s Association of Brownsville and East New York,
May Hashem grant you life,

Blessings and peace!

I was pleased to receive the news regarding the annual luncheon and "closing meeting" that will take place, G-d willing, tomorrow, following Isru Chag of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah.

In matters of holiness, Torah, and mitzvos, it is self-evident that a "closing" in the conventional sense of the word is not applicable. One can only speak of a pause, but even this pause is not an end in itself; rather, it is a means to renew all matters of holiness, Torah, and mitzvos—which is the purpose of the Women’s Association—with increased strength.

This true intent behind the pause or "closing meeting" should be evident in the manner in which the conclusion or pause is carried out.

And this is, in fact, the concept of the Yom Tov of Shavuos and Kabbalas HaTorah.

For it is self-evident that the giving of the Torah and the receiving of the Torah occur every single day of the year; it is just that on the Yom Tov of the giving of the Torah, all matters connected with Torah and mitzvos—which includes the support of Torah study and Torah institutions established in purity—are refreshed and renewed.

May Hashem Yisbarach help that your undertaking be successful, both materially and spiritually, and that it bring encouragement to all the members and friends, so that this "closing meeting" may be a true preparation for the "opening meeting," with refreshed, renewed, and doubled strength, with Chassidic warmth and vitality, in good health, both physically and spiritually.

With blessings for success and good tidings, generally and specifically, and to receive the Torah with joy and inwardness.

A receipt from the *Lishkas HaTzedakah* is enclosed, and may the merit stand for all the members and their households, may they live.

#### ***8205***

**The giving of the Torah... every day:** See also *Sefer HaSichos 5751*, Vol. 2, p. 584, and the references noted there.

## 8,727

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Blessings and peace!

...In matters of holiness, Torah, and mitzvos, it is self-evident that there is no such thing as a "conclusion" in the conventional sense of the word. One can only speak of an *hefsek* (a pause or intermission). But even this *hefsek* is not an end in itself; rather, it is a means to renew all matters of holiness, Torah, and mitzvos.

This true intent of the *hefsek* must be evident in the manner in which the conclusion or pause is carried out.

And this is, in essence, the concept of the Yom Tov of Shavuos and Kabbalas HaTorah.

For it is self-evident that Matan Torah and Kabbalas HaTorah occur every single day of the year; however, on the Yom Tov of Matan Torah, all matters connected with Torah and mitzvos are refreshed and renewed.

Since this undertaking is taking place a few days after Shavuos, the *Zman Matan Toraseinu*, I hope that all participants and *askanim* will bring with them the impression and spirit of the Yom Tov of Kabbalas HaTorah, especially the point that connects this Yom Tov with *chinuch al taharas hakodesh*. By this, I mean what our Sages, of blessed memory, said: that the holy Torah was not given until the Jews provided their children as *arvus* (a guarantee) that the Torah would be upheld and guarded — **"Our children are our guarantors."**

Since the Jews undertook this guarantee, and the Ribono shel Olam accepted this guarantee, it is clear that this guarantee is substantial and can—and must—be fulfilled. In other words: Jews have the **full** and **certain** ability to carry out in practice the obligation of "our children are our guarantors" through Torah *chinuch al taharas hakodesh*; one only needs to truly want to...

With blessings for success and good tidings in general and in particular, and to receive the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 8,429

B"H, Erev Chag HaShavuos, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, etc.,
R' Shneur Zalman Shragai, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

Approaching Chag HaShavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah, which is arriving for us and for all of Yisrael for good and for blessing, I hereby wish you and all who are yours a joyous holiday, and in the traditional phrasing we received from my father-in-law, the Rebbe — that you may receive the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

As is the way of a Jew to connect the matters of day-to-day life with the matters of the Yom Tov, there is a connection between the content of our correspondence and the time of the giving of the Torah, based on the story of our Sages, of blessed memory, that the Torah was not given until we promised that our children would be our guarantors. It is understood that this promise and guarantee, which was given at Har Sinai, testifies that the matter depends on us—that is to say, a promise to strive that the children walk in the path of Torah and mitzvos, even to the point of actual mesiras nefesh. This is also proven by the beginning of the giving of the Torah and the Ten Commandments: "I am" and "You shall have no other gods," which are among the three mitzvos of "be killed and do not transgress."

Furthermore, it is emphasized in this that if one wishes to ensure that a child will not transgress "You shall not murder," "You shall not steal," and "You shall not covet," it is imperative that his entire education be founded upon faith in "I am" and the negation of all matters that fall under the category of "You shall have no other gods." To our sorrow, we have seen in our days and in our generation that the very nation that championed all sorts of philosophies and ideals, etc., ended up with nothing but the realization of "there is no fear of Elokus in this place, and they will kill me." This is in contrast to Torah, the Torah of life, which guarantees not only eternal life in the World to Come, but also a life worthy of the name in this world.

With respect and holiday blessings.

## 8331

B"H, Erev Shavuos, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Menachem Begin, may he live and be well,

Shalom and Bracha,

In connection with the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah, which is approaching for us and for all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby wish you and all that is yours a joyous holiday, and in the traditional phrasing we received from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: that you may receive the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

On this occasion, I acknowledge receipt of your letter in due time, dated the 12th of Iyar. It is surprising that you attribute the negative sentiments and the wave of hatred—referred to in polite terms as a *kultur kampf* (culture war)—on the part of the Left to a specific phenomenon. In truth, anyone who observes human nature, and these circles in particular, sees clearly that in this matter, it is not the intellect that dictates the will (in this case, the will for the aforementioned hatred); rather, the opposite is true: the will causes the intellect to devise clever justifications to validate that will. To draw a distinction, as we see among non-Jews, the true reason for their hatred of a particular people is that their laws are different from those of every other people. Yet, they attribute it to various other causes: where the Jews are wealthy, they blame their wealth; where they are poor, they blame their poverty, and so on.

Therefore, it is a great wonder that, seemingly, no one is addressing **the cause**—that is, the aforementioned hatred—and they are only seeking solutions for the effects by using superficial arguments to justify the hatred.

It is possible that the above contains sharp expressions, but considering the gravity of the matter and the situation—which I have not seen the likes of since I left the Soviet Union—even sharper expressions would be disproportionately mild. It is also understood and simple that I did not come, G-d forbid, to speak disparagingly of any member of the Jewish people. The instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, is well known: that between one Jew and another, whoever they may be, one should not say "to distinguish" (i.e., to separate oneself). Rather, as the saying goes, when it hurts, one cries out. My hope is strong that you will utilize your full influence, in your customary energetic and devoted manner, to stem these aforementioned waves.

With respect and holiday blessings, and with thanks for your faithful wishes.

***

**Mr. Menachem Begin:** Additional letters to him: see above, 8399, and the references in the notes there.

**It is surprising:** See also above, ibid.

**The instruction is well known:** See also above, Vol. 18, letter 6959; Vol. 15, letter 5483; Vol. 10, letter 3229.

Since this matter is for their own benefit and the benefit of their families, the mitzvah of "Love your fellow as yourself"—which is a great principle of the Torah—obligates you to endeavor to influence them to continue their studies in the yeshiva. And words that come from the heart enter the heart.

These days, the days of completion for the time of the giving of our Torah, are days of special spiritual potential. It is my hope that you celebrated the festival of the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness, and that you will carry this joy with you throughout the entire year, until the words of Torah are as new in your eyes each and every day—as per the command of our Sages, of blessed memory—just as they were at the hour the Torah was given by Moshe Rabbeinu at the standing at Har Sinai.

I look forward to hearing good news regarding all of the above.

## 8,434

B"H, 12 Sivan, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Aryeh Zweig, Principal
Mamlachti Dati School, Mevaseret
Jerusalem, Doar Na, Harei Yehuda

Greetings and Blessings,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 21 Iyar regarding the enrollment of graduates from your school in Kfar Chabad.

It is understood that this matter falls under the jurisdiction of the school administration in Kfar Chabad, as I am not privy to the details here. You may contact them directly, "based on my suggestion from here," and they are surely trustworthy to do everything possible to integrate these youths into a framework of education based on the purity of holiness.

Since every matter is governed by Divine Providence, I have the duty and the privilege to take this opportunity of your writing to me to express my hope—based on the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory, that "one only urges those who are already diligent"—that you are certainly striving to instill in the students of the school under your leadership a pure fear of Heaven to the greatest possible extent. And, of course, this must be in a practical manner; I mean that their feeling of *yiras shamayim* should be expressed in their daily conduct and in actual practice. Considering that in our current era, many undesirable and unusual winds are blowing outside, and the influence of the street often undermines the foundations of Torah and tradition—in addition to the usual challenges in the life path of youth—if one wishes for the graduating student to maintain a certain level regarding Torah and *mitzvos*, it is the primary duty of the school to provide the student, while they are still within the school walls, with a greater and more abundant measure, so that even after the influence of the street and the outside world, there will remain within them at least the minimal measure of matters of holiness and goodness in the spirit of their lives.

Indeed, this is one of the differences in our current era compared to the days of our grandparents and ancestors, when conduct according to Torah and tradition was a simple matter, and the primary role of the *cheder* and *yeshiva* was to add to the student’s knowledge of Torah and its matters. This is not the case now, where in most instances, the school must educate the student in the matters of our religion and our eternal Torah, starting from the A-B-C’s of appropriate conduct, etc.

Surely, for one such as yourself, further elaboration is unnecessary.

I would be pleased to receive good news regarding all the above.

With respect and blessing,

#### ***8,434***

**Statement of our Sages:** Makkos 23a.
**Certainly striving:** See also the subsequent letter.
**One of the differences in our current era:** See also the subsequent letter. Below, 8,436; 8,664.

## 8,335

B”H, 12 Sivan, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter, along with the report from the girls’ school. Due to various preoccupations, this acknowledgment has been delayed until now.

It is surely unnecessary to emphasize to someone like yourself the magnitude of the responsibility placed upon an educator in general, and upon the director of an educational institution in particular, to utilize all of one’s talents to instill in the students a pure yiras shamayim to the greatest possible degree. This must, of course, be done in a practical manner; I mean that the feeling of yiras shamayim should be expressed in daily conduct and in actual practice.

Taking into account that in our current era, many undesirable and unusual winds are blowing outside, and the influence of the street generally undermines the foundations of Torah and mesorah—in addition to the standard challenges in the path of life for youth—it follows that if one wishes for the student to maintain a certain level in the path of Torah and mitzvos, it is essential to provide them, while they are still within the walls of the school, with a measure that is greater and more abundant. This is so that after the influence of the street and the outside world, there will remain with them, at the very least, the minimal measure of holiness and goodness in their way of life.

Indeed, this is one of the differences between our current era and the days of our ancestors. In their time, conduct according to Torah and mesorah was a simple matter, and the primary task of the cheder and yeshivah was to add knowledge in Torah and its subjects. This is not the case now, where in most instances the school must educate the student in the matters of our religion and our eternal Torah, starting from the aleph-beis of appropriate conduct, and so on.

As we come from the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah, this responsibility is emphasized by the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory, that the Torah was not given until our children became our guarantors, and the matter is understood.

With blessings for success in your holy work.

## 8339

B"H, 16 Sivan, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you ask why even a fleeting thought regarding mundane matters is often realized in a person’s dreams—as a result of the musings of his heart—whereas thoughts of Torah, mitzvos, and fear of Heaven are not, even when one studies with deep concentration.

The explanation for this is understood from what is explained in the holy Tanya, Chapter 29 (37a), and it is noted there that this is based on the holy Zohar; see there.

Regarding your second question, as to why your peers ascend to great heights in Torah and fear of Heaven with ease, while you do not, and you connect this to what is written in Tanya, Chapter 41, regarding Torah study—that one must prepare oneself before studying and at all times thereafter; see there.

In all such matters, we have been given the assurance: "If a person sanctifies himself a little from below, they sanctify him much from above." Certainly, when you exert effort in this, you will succeed, for this is what our Sages have promised us.

It is well known that this is not the way—to seek out difficulties and questions, except on rare occasions. The main thing is to study our holy Torah—the Torah of life, both the revealed aspects and Chassidus—with consistency and diligence, in a relaxed manner. See the details regarding this in the Laws of Torah Study by the Alter Rebbe.

I trust you are keeping up with the established cycle of daily study: Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

***

8339

We have been given the assurance: Yoma 39a.

## 8440

B"H, 18 Sivan, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, and involved in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi A., shlita,

Peace and blessing!

Following our conversation, and in response to your question regarding the methods and manners of influencing the students, may they live, of the yeshiva under your administration, I would like to emphasize a point among the other points we touched upon. It is a primary point with far-reaching consequences, and a word spoken in its time:

Considering the alarming phenomenon of the cessation of studies during the summer months for a duration of more than two months—in the vast majority of yeshivos in this country—this break brings about a severance of the connection between the students and the yeshiva, and a lack of its influence on one hand, while on the other hand, there is the opposing influence of the city, especially during the summer days, and "idleness leads to..." etc., etc.

It is worthwhile and very appropriate to encourage the yeshiva teachers to volunteer to arrange meetings, at least once a week or every two weeks, with those students of the yeshiva who remain in the city during the summer, especially with the students of the higher grades.

The purpose of the meetings is to maintain the connection between the students and the teachers, may they live, throughout the summer months—through friendly farbrengens, which are opportune times for discussions on topics that will interest the students and which have the benefit of uplifting their spirits and strengthening their path and conduct, improving character traits, and the like. And in an appropriate manner, these meetings can be utilized to encourage the students to set times for Torah study even during the summer, to be meticulous in davening with a minyan, and to strengthen within them the sense of responsibility placed upon yeshiva students to serve as an example to others. And "one mitzvah leads to another"—to utilize various opportunities for educational activity in their surroundings to fulfill the great principle in the Torah, "Love your fellow as yourself."

There are several great advantages to these meetings: the meetings themselves and the encouragement within them, the tightening of the bond between teachers and students, a shield against undesirable influence, the prevention of completely casting off the yoke of the yeshiva, etc., etc., the results of which will be evident upon the students' return to the yeshiva at the appropriate time, G-d willing.

It is understood that for the sake of the matter, it should be arranged that the students come to the meetings of their own free will. Even if at first the number of participants is not very large, it is to be hoped that if the meetings have appropriate and heart-attracting content, the word will spread and the number of participants will increase.

My hope is that you will set your heart to carry out this plan, and from you, other yeshiva administrators will see and learn, and the merit of the many will assist them.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***8440***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 13, p. 300, and completed according to a photocopy of the letter.

**The purpose of the meetings:** See also letter 8445 below.

## H'tama

B"H, 19 Sivan, 5722
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned, etc., R' Yaakov Meshulam Zalman, may he live:

...Regarding the note on the Tosafos d"h "Katan" (Bava Kamma 109b), which explains that the immersion of a minor convert without his father is a subject of dispute in Kesuvos (11a) — it is understood that the intention is to reject the explanation there, "Here, what are we dealing with, etc." And he holds that the primary words of Rav Huna are also rejected (as per the explanation of the Tur — Yoreh Deah 268 — regarding the opinion of the Bahag on this).

For if it were not so, what compels the Shas to the strained explanation that we are dealing with one who comes to convert with her father? 1) Who mentioned a father in the Mishnah? 2) Regarding a captive and a maidservant — everyone agrees there is no need for a father. If so, it must be that the first clause is taught as distinct cases!

#### ***H'tama***

**R' Yaakov Meshulam Zalman:** Groger, Lugano.

May Hashem grant them life.

Greetings and Blessings,

In connection with the Chag HaSiyum, I send my greetings and blessing to the students who are the *baalei simcha*, and to all the participants in this *simcha shel Torah*.

As I have emphasized on previous occasions, I hope that this Chag HaSiyum will serve as a preparation and a **beginning** for a higher level in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of mitzvos. This is the true content of a *siyum* in Torah in general, and in a yeshiva in particular.

The *sidra* of this week — *Beha'aloscha es haneros* — begins with the mitzvah of lighting the Menorah in the *Mishkan* and the *Beis HaMikdash*—until it would kindle of its own accord—which Moshe Rabbeinu was instructed to transmit to Aharon HaKohen.

The Torah is *nitzchiyus*, eternal, and all its directives are eternal and not limited by time or place. Therefore, it is clear that in a deeper sense, the instruction of *hadlakas haneros* pertains to every Jew, in all times and in all places.

Based on the *maamar* "Beha'aloscha es haneros" of the Alter Rebbe—the *Baal HaTanya* and *Shulchan Aruch* and founder of Chassidus Chabad—this is understood according to the *pasuk*, "**The candle of Hashem is the soul of man**." The *neshamah* of a Jew, which is a *chelek Elokah mima'al mamash*, is the Divine "light," and every Jew is a "Kohen" according to the name that Hashem gave the Jewish people: "**A kingdom of Kohanim**." It is therefore the duty and the privilege of every Jew to kindle **his light**, his *neshamah*, with the radiance of *ner mitzvah v'Torah ohr*. Furthermore, he must kindle the light—the *neshamos*—of **every** Jew whom he can reach, who for various reasons is still in the darkness, and whose *neshamah* does not yet shine or radiate as Jewish *neshamos* ought to shine and radiate.

As Lubavitcher students, I hope that you will always remember that you must be ***neros leha'ir***—radiant lights who must also kindle and illuminate other lights, spreading the radiance of Torah and mitzvos with *hislahavus* and vitality, as is required by the mitzvah of *v'ahavta l'rei'acha kamocha*.

May Hashem Yisbarach grant you success in this, and may this also bring you blessing and success in all your affairs.

With blessings for success in all that is mentioned.

## 8443

B"H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Beha'aloscha, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter,

...May it be the will of Hashem that, in accordance with the instruction of this week’s parsha: "Hashem spoke to Moshe, saying, 'Speak to Aharon... When you kindle the lamps,'"

Each and every one of us should do everything within our power to kindle the "lamp of Hashem, the soul of man,"

Both the soul within oneself and the souls of our fellow Jews in one's surroundings—both those nearby and those far away.

As is well known, the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov is that Ahavas Yisrael extends even to one who is at the ends of the earth and whom one has never seen.

One should strive in this kindling until it reaches the level of "Beha'aloscha"—that the flame rises of its own accord.

The knowledge that we are performing this task according to the word of Hashem—for the word of the Ribono shel Olam is considered an action—itself adds strength and vigor in the fulfillment of this mission. It is a fulfillment carried out with joy and a glad heart, for one is privileged to fulfill the command of Hashem, and this is well understood.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 845

B"H, 25 Sivan, 5722
Brooklyn.

Mrs. Chaya Basya, may she live,

Blessings and peace!

After a long interval, your letter of 10 Sivan was received, along with the enclosure, and I viewed the enclosed stamp with interest.

In general, the idea is correct for several reasons. However, the depiction of the Luchos is somewhat puzzling, as you surely know that they must be square at the top as well, and not semicircular. This is explained in the statements of Chazal in many places [among them Bava Basra 14a], and it is also well-known through the illustration on the *Sichos Lanoar*, etc. My intention in the above is not for the sake of idle criticism, but so that when these stamps are all used up, it should be corrected in the next printing, and similarly in other places where there is a depiction of the Luchos.

Although you do not mention it, I hope that you consulted with the other schools of the Reshet regarding the stamps, for in this matter, too, one should strive for a uniform standard across all the schools.

It is surprising that you do not mention matters concerning the school in general or in particular, and I am sure you will fill this in at the next opportunity.

Since you do not mention anything regarding your health, I hope this is a sign that all is well.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 8479

B.H., 25 Sivan, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, engaged in communal affairs, scion of a noble family, a man of refined character, etc., R’ Shazar, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

It is my hope that by the time you receive this letter, you have already returned from your travels. Surely, you will not withhold the kindness of informing me how you found your family members in particular, and the family in the broader sense—anash and our brethren the Children of Israel—in general. It is certainly unnecessary to emphasize that in such matters, the more one details, the more praiseworthy it is, and I thank you in advance.

Yesterday, I met with Mr. Shragai, may he live. It is understood that among the primary points of our conversation, the issue of the new immigrants took pride of place, specifically in connection with the memorandum sent from here some time ago. The proposal therein—that the provision of absorption facilities and buildings for young immigrants should be included in the housing budget and not at the expense of the education budget—was discussed, as explained in the aforementioned memorandum. To my surprise—a pleasant one, of course—I learned that at the meeting of the Jewish Agency, a special committee was chosen to discuss this question, and that you are the chairman of this committee. This means that in addition to your positive influence regarding the discussion and the decision of this committee, it is also within your power to expedite the implementation of this matter and to advance it as much as is necessary.

I believe I have already written to you in one of my letters regarding the great virtue of *zerizus* (alacrity), based on the emphasis of our Rebbe HaZaken in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Epistle 21, concerning the *Akeidas Yitzchak*, which is mentioned many times in the prayers of the Children of Israel and in the sermons of the *Maggidim* and preachers, etc. The holy words of the Rebbe HaZaken there are: "And the *zerizus* of Avraham Avinu, peace be upon him, is what stands for us and for our children forever, for the *Akeidah* itself is not considered such a great test in relation to the stature of Avraham Avinu, peace be upon him, etc." He adds an explanation that the matter of *zerizus* demonstrates joy and the desire to fulfill the will of one's Creator and to provide *nachas ruach* to one's Maker. In the present case, the continuation of the Rebbe HaZaken’s words in that same letter is also relevant, regarding the greatness of *zerizus*, particularly in the act of *tzedakah*, which surpasses all else, etc., that it is good for us even in this world to expedite it as much as possible. For the proper absorption of youth and young people is *tzedakah* in the most comprehensive and internal sense—a constant *tzedakah* in the life of this world and in the life of the World to Come.

And although all of the above is surely known to you, we have been commanded to "urge on those who are already eager."

In these days, news reached me that the activist Petchersky and his colleagues, may they live, have been released from imprisonment and returned to their homes, but to my regret, I have not yet received further confirmation of this rumor. May it be verified soon.

With respect and blessings for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8447

8447

B”H, 25 Sivan, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Honorable Rabbi, G-d-fearing and accomplished, engaged in communal affairs, etc.,
Rabbi Sha’ar Yashuv HaKohen, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

Although a long time has passed since I have received news from you, I shall assume that you remain in good health and spirits, in body and soul alike. This is especially true in light of the ruling of the great teacher, the Rambam (Hilchos De’os, beginning of Chapter 4), that the health and wholeness of the body are among the ways of Hashem—and this applies all the more so to the health of the soul and its matters. In this vein, I refer to your activities at the institute, which you have merited to lead successfully. Incidentally, if any additional books or publications have appeared, surely you will not withhold the good, but will send them here as has been your good custom in the past. Thank you in advance.

Regarding the present matter:

I have recently learned that the Minister of Justice has appointed a committee of legal experts tasked with proposing a series of laws to replace the existing civil laws—in the areas of contract law, commerce, rental, and the like—which currently remain in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) as remnants of previous regimes. I also understand that among the committee members there is a representative of the religious sector, Attorney Lipshitz, and furthermore, that the committee members are authorized to consult with whomever they deem necessary regarding all matters pertaining to this field.

I have also learned from experts in this field that in the area of contract law, negotiations, etc., it is particularly possible to effect improvements, given the current confusion and mixture of various laws. Moreover, and most importantly, the opposition from non-religious quarters to implementing the laws of the Torah in this specific section of Choshen Mishpat would be minimal. Naturally, however, one must extract and compile from Choshen Mishpat the laws pertaining to the aforementioned area and incorporate them into the aforementioned framework using appropriate phrasing. The phrasing is certainly significant and will influence the success of the endeavor to base civil laws on the foundation of our Torah, the Torah of life. It is understood and simple that if the aforementioned project succeeds, there will be solid prospects for facilitating the advocacy and action to transition, step by step, the other areas of the judicial system in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) to the laws of the Torah.

Since organizing a group of talmidei chachamim to occupy themselves with the above—for the time being, regarding the area of contracts, etc.—is a complicated matter for several reasons, both in terms of the substance of the matter and in terms of organization, expenses, etc., it occurred to me that the most direct path to actual implementation (as time is of the essence, and we must not delay) is that the members of the institute, who are already engaged in such matters—and surely some of them are specifically in the aforementioned field—can have those most capable for this specific work selected from among them. Since, according to reports, Attorney Lipshitz is a reasonable person, etc., and would be interested, even from a religious perspective, in realizing the above, it is possible that the matter could be resolved with great success.

I rely on your interest and your understanding, and I will not elaborate further on what has been said. It would be pleasant for me to hear of your reaction to all the above, and primarily of the actions taken to bring the matter to actual fruition, while simply maintaining the point that this Torah shall not be replaced—a strict adherence.

With respect and blessing, and regards to his father, the Rabbi, may he live and be well.

## 8,449

B"H, 26 Sivan, 5722

In response to your letter from Sunday, in which you write regarding the question of an apartment after the wedding, may it be in a good and auspicious hour.

This should be a fixed time every day, with an increase on Shabbos, which is holy to Hashem, as per the words of the Arizal who lives in this. If at all times and in all places this was a necessity, how much more so in our era and in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, of which it is written: "The eyes of Hashem your G-d are upon it from the beginning of the year to the end of the year."

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

## 8450

B"H, 27 Sivan, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 24 Sivan, in which you write regarding the state of *shalom bayis* of your son, *sheyichyeh*.

In general, it is not at all the custom to respond to such a matter to anyone other than the person directly involved, for only he can detail the matter as necessary, and in the style of *Chazal*, "No person knows what is in the heart of his fellow." 

Nevertheless, due to the importance and magnitude of the matter, and out of respect, I have come to express my opinion, based on the ruling of our Torah, *Toras Chaim*, that peace is great in general, and even more so the peace between a man and his wife. In instances of differences of opinion between them, there is also a detailed instruction (brought in *Hilchos Ona'ah* by our *Alter Rebbe*, author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*, at the end) regarding being very careful not to cause the wife distress, etc., and to be careful regarding her honor, etc. And as is understood from your letter, this is not at all a matter concerning *yiras shamayim*; on the contrary, she is *chareidi* and observes Torah and *mitzvos*, etc.

May it be the will of the *Ribono shel Olam* that His peace should dwell in the home of your son, *sheyichyeh*, and that there should be peace in abundance, for this leads to an abundance of blessing, etc. (see *Esther Rabbah* at its conclusion).

And since everything is by *hashgacha pratis*, and based on the statement of *Chazal*, "One only encourages those who are already diligent," surely, as you are involved in spreading the wellsprings of the teachings of *Chassidus* wherever your reach extends, and we have been promised that "He who comes to purify" (and the precision of our *Alter Rebbe*, author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*, to purify others as well, is well known) "is assisted," may you be successful.

With respect and blessing for good tidings in all the above.

#### ***8450***

**Statement of Chazal:** *Makkos* 23a.

**And we have been promised... precision:** *Yoma* 38b. And see *Likutei Torah*, *Drushim* for *Shemini Atzeres* 88b.

## 851

It is not entirely clear from your letter where the stone is located, as sometimes it can be reached with an appropriate instrument to break it up, which makes its passage much easier.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 8454

[Rosh Chodesh Tammuz 5722]

... Regarding what is written in *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah*, Chapter 7, that the sun is "approximately 167 times the size of the earth," this is based on the ruling of the Rambam in *Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah*, Chapter 3, Halacha 8 (and he is more precise in the introduction to his commentary on the Mishnah, stating "166 and 3/8 times").

It seems that a question was raised to your honor regarding the fact that modern astronomers have supposedly researched and found otherwise—that it is 4 to 5 million times larger, or more. As with other "scientific" difficulties of this type, the questioner is ignorant of science as well!

The figure stated in modern astronomy of 4 to 5 million and more refers to the volume, whereas the Rambam is speaking about the diameter. Now, the value of the aforementioned diameter as brought in modern astronomy books is approximately 110 (not 167). However, this measurement of the sun’s diameter takes into account certain layers of the sun and not all of them, because the outermost layers—according to the opinion of modern astronomers—change (through contraction and expansion) from time to time to a great degree. Not all of them are visible to the eye (one only "sees" their effects), and so on and so forth; therefore, it is also difficult to measure them. Furthermore, they do not take into account the *protuberances*. However, (at times, at least) they have observed and measured that these [layers] expanded to such an extent that the diameter of the sun was **then** more than 167 times the diameter of the earth, and it subsequently contracted, etc., and this is not the place to elaborate.

#### ***8454***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 10, p. 180. The letter is to Harav Ephraim Eliezer Yalles. Additional letters to him appear above—8288, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 849

B"H, 2 Tammuz, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., R' Shmuel, may he live:

Greetings and blessings,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your book, *Eved HaMelech*, on the Book of Tehillim.

May it be the will of the Ribono shel Olam that you increase the ranks of those devoted to the Torah, both in the Written Torah and the Oral Torah—and not only in their revealed aspects, but also in the inner dimension of the Torah, which in our generation has been revealed through the teachings of Chassidus.

For it is one Torah. On the contrary, according to what is explained in the holy Zohar (Parshas Beha'aloscha, 152a), the inner dimension of the Torah is the *neshamah* of the Torah for the body of the Torah—the revealed parts.

If this was necessary always and in every place, it is certainly so in our generation, the generation of the footsteps of Moshiach, and in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year. As is known from the *Iggeres HaKodesh* of the Baal Shem Tov, that when his fountains spread outward, the King, Moshiach, will come.

With respect and blessings,

**P.S.** I would like to note a few points in your aforementioned book, though briefly, as time does not permit otherwise:

At the beginning of the book (3b): "We were commanded regarding this, etc."

Seemingly, in such instances, this phrasing is not appropriate, because we learn of the matter *agav* (from the fact that it is written "Happy is the man who has not walked..."), but it is not that the verse comes to issue a command. Furthermore, it can be said that this is not in the category of a command *mi-atzmo* (in and of itself), but rather in the nature of "good advice," as it were. See Rambam, *Hilchos De'os*, beginning of Chapter 6: "Therefore, etc., and he should distance himself, etc., **in order to**..." and it says "Happy is the man, etc."—emphasizing "**in order to**," and not that the matter is forbidden *mi-atzmo*. According to the above, the statement of Chazal (Avodah Zarah 18b)—"And of them the verse says, 'Happy is the man, etc.'—for these things **bring** [one to...], etc."—is also understood simply: it is **not** a prohibition *mi-atzmo*.

There (4a): "We were commanded regarding this to be constant in study, etc., and not to nullify [the study of] Torah, etc.," and you cite the statement of Chazal in Avodah Zarah (ibid.), "Lest a person say, etc."

Seemingly, this is also not precise, for the statement of Chazal there continues: "Shall I go and engage in sleep? The verse teaches, 'And in His Torah he meditates day and night.'" The intention is not to negate *bitul Torah*—for it is obvious that it is a transgression, and regarding him it is said, "For he has despised the word of Hashem, etc." (Sanhedrin 99a)—but rather the matter of "engaging in sleep," meaning that one who sleeps does not incur the sin of *bitul Torah*. And this is well-understood.

Regarding your explanation there on the parameters of fulfilling the mitzvah of "it shall not depart, etc."—see *Ba'er Heitev* in *Hilchos Talmud Torah* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, Chapter 3.

At the end of the book (85b):

It is surprising that the verse "Let every soul praise, etc." was omitted, along with the interpretation of Chazal that for every single breath one must offer praise (Bereishis Rabbah, end of Chapter 14), and in *Devarim Rabbah*, end of Chapter 2: "**He is obligated** to offer praise, etc."

## 8557

8557

[3 Tammuz 5722]

...Regarding your writing about an *eruv* in the city, since there are many *halachos* involved in this, it should not be done without the participation of a *rov* who is **expert** in these *halachos* **specifically**.

Regarding the regulations of the *Chevra Kadisha*, etc. — you should contact the *Chevra Kadisha* of Agudas Chabad.

## 8,459

B"H, 7 Tammuz, 5722
Brooklyn.

The women should maintain the good custom of kosher Jewish women to set aside money for Tzedakah before lighting candles every Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov.

And since you are the one bringing this request and you are a bochur in yeshiva, it is understood that you must increase your diligence and perseverance in the study of Torah and in the beauty of performing mitzvos. Beyond the immense importance of this in and of itself, it also serves as a channel and a vessel to receive the blessings of Hashem for what you need, and for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires for the good, in all that has been mentioned.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 875

B"H, 10 Tammuz, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Moshe Sharett,

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to learn from the Kfar Chabad committee of your visit to the village, and I was also gratified to hear from our representative, Rabbi Binyamin Gorodetzky, about his conversation with you. Together with the impressions that remained with me from your visit here, all of this adds up to a significant basis for strengthening my confidence that your support for all areas of our activities in Eretz Yisrael—may it be built and established—and for Kfar Chabad in particular, as well as regarding the general issues we discussed during our conversation, has brought and will continue to bring tangible results.

We are accustomed to connecting good news with auspicious days, and these reports reached me in proximity to the Chag HaGeulah, 12-13 Tammuz. This year marks the 35th anniversary of the liberation of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, from his imprisonment—a story of those days that you are surely familiar with. As with all memorial days in the life of the individual and the collective, the purpose is that they be "remembered and acted upon," meaning that the memory should inspire actual deeds. The central point of this Chag HaGeulah is how great the power of a single Jew is; through firm resolve and true mesiras nefesh, he was not only able to stand his ground against a dictatorship and a massive, fierce regime, but he also emerged victorious in his battle—the battle of Hashem and His treasured people. This was not merely a personal victory, but a general one, the results of which are clearly evident. And although who is the one whose heart would prompt him to compare himself to the Rebbe, especially in the strength of his mesiras nefesh, on the other hand, the conditions in the free countries where we operate are incomparably easier. The lesson is understood through a kal v'chomer and an argument from a lesser to a greater case. May it be the will of the Almighty that each and every one of us fulfills the role that Divine Providence has placed upon us, along with the necessary strengths to do so.

With respect, blessing, and best wishes for the Chag HaGeulah.

## 8,466

10 Tammuz, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Reuven Avinoam
Greetings and Blessings,

I received your letter of 13 Iyar with some delay, in response to my letter regarding your book.

Regarding the point in your letter—that you agree with my statement that the matter of mourning must be limited in time so that it does not interfere with a person’s primary task of being active and energetic, etc., but that you wish to distinguish between "mourning" and "remembrance"—it is understood that changing the name here neither adds nor detracts. The essence is the results, and the test is this: whether the remembrance or the mourning brings an increase in holiness, justice, and integrity to the world, or the opposite.

As for your comment that there are departed souls who possess special virtues or a special merit connected to a specific action, and that for this reason their memory does not diminish the energy and vitality of the parents, etc.: in reality, we see the opposite. The love of parents for children who do not excel in special virtues is often deeper. As the Sages put it, "A love that depends on something, when that thing ceases, the love ceases." This proves that even before that thing ceased, the love was not as deep and true as a love that does not depend on anything—in the language of Chassidus, an "essential love"—because children are of the very essence and being of their parents. 

Admittedly, this reason does not yet fully explain why the love should be greater for children who do not excel in special virtues; it would suffice for it to be equal. However, since there is both an essential love and a love that depends on something, the latter weakens the former—that is to say, it covers over the essential love. To provide a clearer example: we have seen in our own time, and even more emphatically in past eras—the eras of the persecutions and the Crusades, may Hashem protect us—that it was precisely simple people who sacrificed their lives for our religion and faith more readily than those who possessed intellect, understanding, and attainment. Although both groups are "believers, the children of believers," and in both, the point of Yiddishkeit is the source of their mesiras nefesh, those with great intellect are accustomed to directing all their affairs according to logic. Habit becomes second nature, and they felt they needed to find a reason and rationale for this as well. This is not the case with simple people; when they are brought to a test of faith, their point of Yiddishkeit is awakened without any garments or limitations. 

It is the same in our current case: if the love is dependent on something—even if that thing is great and most exalted—that thing is nonetheless limited, and it limits the essential love as well, covering it over due to the habit of linking the love to that specific thing.

To conclude with a matter of the day, the eve of 12-13 Tammuz—the days of the redemption and victory of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in his battle to defend the sanctities of our people despite the dictatorship and the immense regime in his country at the time (of which I am sure you know the history)—the primary point of these days, in my opinion, is how great the power of a single Jew is if he only exercises a firm resolve and true mesiras nefesh. And while not every person attains this level, the conditions in the free countries in which we live are incomparably more favorable, and Hashem only demands according to the strength of each individual, provided that they utilize it to its fullest.

With respect and blessing,

## 8,467

*[11 Tammuz, 5722]*

...You write regarding the state of your wife’s health, may she live, and the doctor’s opinion (in connection with this) regarding pregnancy, etc.

In such matters, it is understood and simple that you should turn to a Rav who is a *moreh hora’ah* in your vicinity, and he will instruct you in the *da’as Torah*—our holy Torah, the *Toras Chaim*—regarding what has been said, for one does not make decisions in such matters based on one’s own opinion.

It is appropriate that you have your *tefillin* and the *mezuzos* in your home checked, to ensure they are all *kosher* according to the law. Your wife, may she live, should observe the good custom of *kosher* daughters of Israel: to set aside, *bli neder*, money for *tzedakah* before lighting the candles every *Erev Shabbos* and *Erev Yom Tov*.

Regarding the financial pressure, the advice given by our Sages of blessed memory is well known: to increase in *tzedakah* and to distribute it in many small portions (see *Iggeres HaKodesh*, section 21). Among the times *mesugal* for this is the morning of every weekday (see *Chassidus* on the verse, "Lavan arose early in the morning") before the morning *tefillah* (see the introduction to the *Siddur*)—to set aside a few coins for *tzedakah*.

#### ***8,467***

May this fulfill the inner goal of all these activities: "We are workers of the day"—to make things bright—to illuminate, until the light is drawn down below to be "visible light."

With respect and blessings.

## 8,473

B"H, 20 Tammuz, 5722
Brooklyn.

Mr. Reuven, shichyeh,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter in which you write regarding the reprinting of your ancestors’ seforim, and ask for advice on this matter:

Regarding the seforim themselves, since I have not seen them, and in general—one should consult with experts in such matters who are in your vicinity, so they may examine the seforim.

Regarding institutions that deal with such things, surely you are also aware that if the seforim and their author have a connection to the countries of Europe that suffered in the last war, there is room to inquire with the Committee for Restitution and Compensation. In certain cases, they participate in the costs of preparation for printing, etc. Likewise, in Eretz Yisrael, tichyeh v'tikonen, there are certain institutions that assist in the publication of seforim; you will certainly be able to clarify the details regarding this as well from rabbonim and roshei yeshivos, etc.

You are surely doing so also through natural means, for a person must do what is dependent upon him through natural means, and this is a vessel for the fulfillment of what is written: "And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you do."

And since everything is by *hashgacha pratis*, it is my duty (and privilege) to awaken you regarding the necessity and the personal obligation to set times for study, including the study of *pnimiyus haTorah*, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. This should be a fixed time every day, with an increase on Shabbos, which is holy to Hashem. If in all times and in all places this was a necessity, how much more so in our era, and in Eretz Yisrael, *tichyeh v'tikonen*, in particular, for as it is written: "The eyes of Hashem your G-d are upon it from the beginning of the year to the end of the year."

With blessings for good tidings in all that was mentioned,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary
