## 8,775

B”H, 23 Tammuz, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Moshe [Meisels]
Greetings and blessings!

I have just learned of the passing of your wife, a”h. Since, according to the information I received, the days of mourning have already passed, may it be the will of Hashem that the days of mourning and all matters of mourning—both for the individual and for the collective—come to an end. May you and all your household, shlita, find only good, and in the language of Chassidus, may it be good that is both visible and revealed, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

Chabad Chassidim relate that when the wife of the Tzemach Tzedek passed away, he mourned her deeply and refused to be comforted. One of his close associates entered and said, “But we have heard explicitly from the Rebbe the teaching of our Sages on the verse, ‘See life with the wife whom you love’—this refers to Torah.” The Tzemach Tzedek replied, “You have revived me,” and through this, a turning point occurred in his state of mind, etc.

On the face of it, this matter requires deep study. Surely, the Tzemach Tzedek was already well aware of this teaching, and surely, in connection with the days of mourning, it must have crossed his mind many times. How, then, did the associate achieve anything by mentioning the teaching, to the point of causing a turning point in the Tzemach Tzedek’s daily conduct? It must be that a matter as it exists in thought is not the same as when one brings it into the world of speech—even though, seemingly, they are one and the same. And the saying, “A prisoner cannot free himself from prison,” applies even to the greatest of the great.

With respect and blessings for good tidings.

**P.S.** I must add that before I wrote this letter, the proverb common here in the city I have come to—that is, in the United States—crossed my mind: “Mind your own business,” especially regarding a person who is in distress. But the answer comes from the very same place: precisely in matters of distress such as these, the formula is “among the other mourners of Tzion and Yerushalayim.” This means that it is not a private matter; all the mourners of Tzion and Yerushalayim are partners in it. The proof is that they are partners in the consolation.

While I am on the subject of this letter, there is another matter—though regarding your letter, I was in doubt whether to include it here. It is my response to your letter from the end of Nissan, which I have not yet answered. It seems you are firm in your opinion, especially regarding a matter that has already reached a decision—and in particular, if I may be forgiven for saying so, in the decision of “sit and do nothing” regarding everything outside your own four cubits and your surroundings in general. For a certain type of person, it is difficult to change this mindset; it is like backbreaking labor for them.

Nevertheless, I find it my duty to address the content of your letter. It is that, in general, disappointment that leads to a reduction in activity—even if one were to say that the disappointment is well-founded and the disappointed person is 100% correct—requires investigation and examination: Who is the one interested in and stirring up this disappointment? In the language of the Tanya: Does this state of mind stem “from the right chamber or from the left chamber”? Another test: Who stands to gain from the lack of action and from the validity of the disappointed person’s claim, etc., etc.? For ultimately, in the style of our Sages, we are “workers of the day,” and as the Tzemach Tzedek explained—to make things bright. And surely the term “workers” is precise; it does not mean to illuminate a place that is already lit, nor does it refer to easy work, but rather to actual labor, the reward (and manner) of which is in accordance with the goal to which one aspires.

I must add that I do not agree with several of your claims at all. But as mentioned above, in my opinion, this does not touch upon the core issue I wrote about in my first letter: that **every single person** must spread light—the true light of our Torah, the Torah of truth, and the light within it, which is the inner dimension of the Torah—until the Torah, as its name implies, becomes a *horah* (instruction) in daily life. And not only in thought, for “Hashem desires the heart,” but as mentioned above, in speech and in actual deed. And even if one is an *anus* (compelled) and the Merciful One exempts him, we do not say “it is as if he has done it” (even in the world of speech, and certainly it is not “done” in our world, the world of action).

To conclude, based on the conclusion of your aforementioned letter regarding a *dvar Torah* on the reason for *mishloach manos*: I heard a characteristic story about this from one of the rabbis in Russia in our generation. Once, he was overcome with tears on Shabbos itself. When asked the reason, he said that a question had just come before him from someone who is meticulous in matters of Torah and mitzvos, even to the slightest detail of the words of the Scribes: Is he permitted to make Kiddush on wine, since he did not stand up to the test and was forced to go to his job on the holy Shabbos, even though he did no work there other than “being seen arriving”? But in the eyes of the public, it was a public desecration of Shabbos, and he asked about his own status: is he permitted to make Kiddush on the wine he touches?

If you were to say so, one can find a connection here to what was said above: if even to the eyes of the observers a great emptiness reigns in the world—emptiness from within, and “nine measures were taken,” etc., as written in your letter—who is it that can decide and judge based on what appears to his eyes that reality is such, to the point of concluding that he should shut himself within his four cubits, etc.?

If I have written at too great a length, I ask for your forgiveness. I will not hide that my hope is that perhaps precisely through this, together with the dissatisfaction you express in your letter, you will step out of your frame and begin to act wherever your hand can reach. And if there is a need, it is in the hand of Hashem to extend the hand to a hundred cubits and to act in the aforementioned direction—in the actual fulfillment of mitzvos in daily life. And even if there is someone who does not agree with all the matters about which you write with a pained heart, at the very least, connect with him in order to elevate him, so that he will put on tefillin, eat kosher, keep Shabbos, etc.

## 8757

8757

B”H, 27 Tammuz, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter dated 11/6, which reached me after a long delay, as well as your previous letter.

It is understood and simple that you and your colleagues—may they live—must endeavor as much as possible to disseminate our Torah, the Torah of life—the study of the revealed Torah and the inner dimensions of the Torah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus—in every place your reach extends.

It is likewise understood and simple that this conduct must be carried out through ways of pleasantness and ways of peace, which are the ways of our holy Torah, the Torah of life.

And since we have been commanded regarding both matters together, surely, with appropriate conduct and effort, you will be able to fulfill both commandments; that is to say, to avoid matters of controversy and instead occupy yourselves with the aforementioned matters—the dissemination of Torah (both revealed and Chassidus) and mitzvos—and to do so with a good heart.

And if anyone should, Heaven forbid, dispute you, pay no heed to it, and do not enter into arguments with them. In the end, that which has been stated—the Torah of the Baal Shem Tov, his students, and his students’ students—will prevail.

My hope is strong that you and your colleagues—may they live—and first and foremost, the dear Chassid, Rabbi A. HaKohen Tawil—may he live—will bring good tidings regarding the above, as is necessary. May Hashem grant you success.

With blessings for mazal tov and good tidings in all the aforementioned, both in general matters and in personal ones.

## 8778

B"H, 27 Tammuz, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 22 Tammuz, in which you write of various possibilities regarding your plans for the immediate future and ask for my opinion on the matter.

My opinion is clear, based on what we see regarding human nature: specifically at your age, one must study with persistence and diligence in a yeshiva, in an environment saturated with yiras Hashem and ahavas Hashem. To use the phrasing of our Sages, "If not now, when?" As mentioned, we see tangibly that regarding the postponement, chas v'shalom, of the aforementioned for a year or even less, one must apply the statement of our Sages, "Do not say, 'When I am free I will study,' for perhaps you will never be free." In these days, when undesirable winds blow in the world and in the street, in most cases, that "perhaps" is close to a certainty. There is no need to elaborate on a distressing matter. My hope is strong that these few lines, small in quantity, will suffice to set you on the path of truth and what is good for you—to dedicate the coming months (and the more, the better) to the study of our Torah, the Torah of life, both the nigleh and the pnimiyus. We have been promised that "one who comes to purify himself is assisted." It will be a pleasure for me to hear good news regarding all of the above.

With blessings for good tidings.

**P.S.** Regarding what you wrote, that someone did not accept your entry into the yeshiva: we see tangibly that when one speaks words that come from the heart to explain the aforementioned decision, eventually the truth is accepted—that it is for his own good, both in gashmius and in ruchnius alike. In any case—see Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah, siman 240, at the end.

## 8,479

B"H, 27 Tammuz, 5722
Brooklyn.

Rabbi Yaakov Dov, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter, along with the sefer *Be'er Yaakov* on Maseches Yevamos and Kinnim, an interesting approach to explaining Torah concepts.

May it be the will of Hashem that for many years you increase your strength for the sake of Torah, to disseminate the study of Torah with explanation, understanding, and comprehension—both the revealed aspects of Torah and the inner dimensions of Torah, which in our generation have been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus.

This is also a directive for our generations: to study until one understands and comprehends, as is explained in many places. See also the *Hilchos Talmud Torah* of our Rebbe, the author of the Tanya and the Shulchan Aruch, at the end of Chapter 2, and there in Chapter 1, at the end of Section 4.

With respect and blessings.

**P.S.** As is my custom, I will offer a few comments:

Regarding the diagrams, one should strive, if at all possible, for there to be a connection between the symbol and the thing being symbolized. Based on this, seemingly, the symbol for a prohibition should be the opposite of the symbol for a bond (*zikah*).

Seemingly, the symbol for *yibum* and for a prohibition are the same in your sefer.

Regarding *chalitzah*, there should be a sense of a broken line, with interruptions, whereas in *yibum*, which is a connection, it should be a continuous line.

Based on the above, it is also understood that in marriage there is no place for a broken line.

And another point from a completely different area: it does not seem right to me to use a square for a symbol (male), for there is nothing square from the six days of Creation.

Enclosed is a *reshimah* that I hope will be of interest to you.

***

**Rabbi Yaakov Dov:** Kantor, Tel Aviv.

**Nothing square:** See also above, Vol. 2, Letter 360.

**Enclosed is a reshimah:** The *sicha* of Shabbos Parshas Chayei Sarah 5722 (printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 2, p. 599 and onwards).

8,480

In response to your letter of 23 Tammuz, in which you ask whether it is permitted to change to the Chabad *nusach* (*nusach* of the Arizal).

It is certainly permitted to change, provided that the decision to do so is permanent, since one should not change from the *nusach* of the Arizal to *nusach* Sefard or Ashkenaz, as explained by the later *poskim*.

I trust you are keeping up with the three daily *shiurim* of *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya* as is well known, in addition to the main thing—studying *nigleh* and *Chassidus* with *hasmadah* and *shekidah*.

Secretary

## 8781

B"H, 28 Tammuz, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the fourth of the month, in which you ask my opinion as to whether a certain individual is fit to serve as a Rav and Moreh Hora’ah in Yisrael.

It is understood that it is impossible to testify about anyone without knowing them as thoroughly as is required, especially when the matter concerns a Rav and Moreh Hora’ah in a holy community—for if ten Jews constitute a holy congregation, then certainly several tens, may they increase, do so all the more.

Regarding your question concerning the status of those who claim that there are matters in our holy Torah that are not from Hashem, Heaven forbid, or who nullify even one mitzvah from our Torah, the Torah of life:

It is astonishing that such a question should even be asked. The law is explained and made explicit in the *Yad Hachazakah* of our teacher, the Rambam, *Hilchos Teshuvah*, Chapter 3, Halacha 8, which states: "One who says that the Torah is not from Hashem, even [regarding] one verse or even one word, etc.; and likewise one who denies its interpretation, which is the Torah Sheba'al Peh, etc.; and one who says that the Creator has replaced this mitzvah with another mitzvah, and that this Torah has already been nullified, etc." (See there; it is based on explicit Gemara). The Rambam in his book, and the poskim of Yisrael in general, represent the standard and definition of a settled ruling, as is explained in the poskim. See also the *Hilchos Talmud Torah* of our teacher, the Alter Rebbe, author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*, at the beginning of the second chapter.

As we stand in the days of *Bein HaMetzarim*, may it be the will of Hashem, Giver of the Torah and Commander of the mitzvos, that He mend the breaches of His people Yisrael, both in spirituality and in physicality, and that the religion, the study of Torah, and the performance of mitzvos in practice and with *hiddur* be strengthened in all the dwellings of the children of Yisrael.

And may we merit, speedily in our days, the fulfillment of the prophecy that a King from the House of David will arise, who studies Torah and occupies himself with mitzvos, etc., and will compel all of Yisrael to walk in its ways and strengthen its breaches, and will fight the wars of Hashem—he is the Mashiach Tzidkeinu—and he will build the Beis Hamikdash and gather the dispersed of Yisrael, as per the final ruling of the Rambam (*Hilchos Melachim*, end of Chapter 11).

With respect and blessings.

#### ***8781***

**It is astonishing that such a question should even be asked:** See also below, letter 8707.

## 8482

B"H, 29 Tammuz, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter—as is your custom, without indicating the date—and I have mentioned you and all those you write about at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for each according to their needs. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding them, and, as is understood and simple, this includes you as well.

May it be His will that this also include a change in how you view the world: from a dim lens to a good and illuminating lens. Through even a slight amount of *hisbonenus*, one sees that to a most significant degree, this depends on the person who is seeing and contemplating, and not so much on the world outside them. There are many examples to be found among people, where in the environment of each person there are examples of both good and the opposite. From this, the conclusion [and according to the well-known adage that the mind rules the heart, and furthermore, as the Alter Rebbe says, by its nature and birth—meaning that one does not need *avodah* and toil for this, behold] is that even those who have become accustomed to a less-than-desirable lens have the ability—and consequently, the obligation and the privilege—to let the mind rule. The mind must be permeated with *bitachon* in Hashem, that He is the essence of good and it is the nature of the good to do good, and all occurrences are merely *nisyonos*. If the matter is not accomplished, it is close to saying that the cause is not a lack of ability, but a lack of *ratzon*.

May it be His will that, just as we have been promised that these days will be transformed into joy and gladness—and the preparation for the fulfillment of this prophecy is the *avodah* of man in the present—each person will transform their own "small world," and through this, their surroundings as well and every place their hand can reach, into an environment of joy and light. As mentioned, according to the well-known adage, the full ability exists, and the matter depends only on *ratzon*.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

***

**As the Alter Rebbe says:** *Tanya*, Chapter 12. See also below, Letter 8484.

**The well-known adage:** See also above, Vol. 20, Letter 7609, and in many places.

## 8,484

8,484

B”H, 1 Menachem Av, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 27th of Tammuz.

At an opportune time, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires for the good.

Since you are studying at the holy Yeshiva Tomchei Tmimim in Lod, it is surely unnecessary to elaborate that your study must be with persistence and diligence, both in *nigleh* and *Chassidus*. Beyond the essential fact that this is the commandment of Hashem, it is also a channel and vessel for receiving Hashem’s blessing in all that you require.

It is appropriate that you have your *tefillin* checked, as well as the *mezuzos* in the home of your parents, may they live long, to ensure they are all *kosher* according to the law.

Regarding what you wrote about self-control—the answer to this is understood from what is explained in the *Tanya Kadisha*. The point is that the brain rules over the heart. The word **rules** (*shalit*) implies two things: a) that it is possible for a person to be a ruler over his spirit, and b) that this is a matter of governance and necessity. In this, everyone is equal; it is not an *is’hapcha* (a total transformation). That is to say, from time to time, it is possible for the *yetzer* to renew the battle, but even then, the Holy One, blessed be He, helps him. See there in the *Tanya*.

At an opportune time, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

***

**Tanya Kadisha:** Chapter 12.

## 8,788

8,788

B”H, 5 Menachem Av, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Following the longest of interruptions, your letter of 2 Menachem Av was received. It still does not explain the reason for the silence, and it also lacks the most essential information: your fixed times for learning Nigleh and Chassidus in general, and what you and your wife, may she live and be well, are occupied with—especially now that these are the days of vacation, etc., and particularly since your trip to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, also involved the matter of shlichus.

Regarding what you wrote about the confusing thoughts that naturally affect your mood, etc.: the saying of the wise is well known, “There is no joy like the resolution of doubts.” From the positive, you hear the negative—that doubt naturally confuses a person. The way to minimize this confusion, and eventually remove it entirely, is to resolve the doubt. In your case and that of your wife, may she live and be well, there is no doubt, for you were blessed with the Name and Kingship in the Seven Blessings (the formula and institution of the Men of the Great Assembly, transmitted from one to another back to Moshe Rabbeinu), which is an eternal edifice, “as You gladdened Your creation in the Garden of Eden of old.” This also applies to the matter of traveling here. Therefore, I have said for some time that the sooner you make this trip, the greater your peace of mind will be, and consequently, your mood will improve as well, etc., etc.

As for the point at the end of your letter—whether the trip will be for a certain duration, how long it will be, and when the time for a visit to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, will be, etc.—why confuse your soul with questions that will only be relevant several months from now? Especially since Rosh Hashanah falls in between, when we are written and sealed for a good and sweet year, in goodness that is revealed and manifest, and Hashem is the One who knows.

As you requested, this letter is being sent out of turn, and I am certain that you, as well as your wife, may she live and be well, will answer the question posed at the beginning of the letter.

Enclosed is an excerpt from the sicha of the farbrengen of Chag HaGeulah, 12-13 Tammuz, the theme of which is to take the inspiration from it for the entire year. It is sent in English, as it has not yet been transcribed into any other language, but the content is the same.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all the above.

B"H, 5 Menachem-Av, the Hillula of the Arizal HaChai

## 8490

B"H, 5 Menachem Av, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 20 Tammuz and the one preceding it, in which you write regarding your livelihood situation and your thoughts concerning future parnassah, and ask for my opinion on the matter.

In general, one does not abandon a source of parnassah in business—especially when one is a family man—in order to experiment with new avenues of parnassah. This is especially true since you have been engaged in your current work for some time. Even though you write that the environment there is not suitable, you are currently living in a community of G-d-fearing people, and therefore, ultimately, the environment at your workplace will not have such an influence if you decide for yourself that you must conduct yourself in accordance with the instructions of our Torah, Toras Chaim, and in the fulfillment of its mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them." However, it goes without saying—and for several other reasons as well—that it is not at all worthwhile to enter into arguments with those at your current place of work. Rather, you should be a living example of the conduct of a son of Yisrael, each of whom is called a child of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov.

We see tangibly that one's attitude toward various matters and environments depends on one's approach. I mean to say that if you view your current place of parnassah with dissatisfaction, or perhaps even worse, it is liable to [...] those who are there. But if you view it as a place of parnassah that enables you to use that parnassah for matters of Torah and mitzvos, and for the education of your children in the way of Torah and mitzvos—as every matter of parnassah is bound up with difficulties, for that is the nature of any parnassah—then the confusing aspects of your parnassah will not be so difficult, and they will not influence you at all.

It was pleasant for me to read in your letter of your connection and closeness to the Anash of Chabad in your area, and it is my hope that this will continue in the future as well, for it has already been said, "and salvation comes with many counselors."

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 8,491

B"H, 8 Menachem Av, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of Tuesday, the day on which "it was good" was doubled.

At a time of favor, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the fulfillment of your heart's desires for the good.

It is certainly unnecessary to emphasize that an increase in matters of Torah and mitzvos brings about an increase in the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach, and no matter how good one may be in this, one can always add more.

Regarding your writing about adopting a Jewish child: this is only in very rare cases where it is known clearly that the parents were observant of Torah and mitzvos. In most cases, one is not certain of this. In such instances, it is more advantageous—and desirable—when the mother is not Jewish, as through converting the child, all doubts and problems are removed.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

**P.S.** You surely observe the good custom of Jewish daughters to give to tzedakah each time before lighting candles on Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov.

## 8492

8492

By the Grace of G-d,
Between the Straits, 5722

May they be turned into gladness and joy.
Mr. Moshe, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter and the enclosed material, in which you ask—in connection with the educational publications of Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch—whether it is advisable to educate and teach children to believe in miracles. You express your negative stance and ask whether you have the right to criticize those who do not agree with you on this matter.

First of all, I must say—and I hope you will forgive me for this—that it does not even cross my mind that you do not believe in miracles. For even if there were times when it was possible not to believe in miracles, in our current time, for a Jew to say that he does not believe in the supernatural is merely a self-delusion. Not only have Jews who survived the concentration camps clearly witnessed miracles, but anyone who understands what has happened and is happening—if he only keeps his eyes open and does not allow himself to be influenced by superstitions—does not need to "believe" in miracles at all. He sees them even with his physical eyes.

From this, the answer to your questions is self-evident.

Even regarding adults, who possess a critical intellect and approach, one must always proceed with truth in word and description. How much more so must one uphold the principle of "distance yourself from a false word" when it comes to children, who have complete trust in their parents and especially in their teachers. It is understood that no one has the right to criticize teachers and educators for this approach, for that would undermine the child's trust in his educator.

You ask: If one tells a child about a miracle, and the miracle he hoped for does not occur, is that not harmful to the child?

Firstly, according to what was said above, this is no justification for withholding the truth from a child. Secondly, your question is not at all grounded in the context of our discussion. For when one tells a child or a student about a miracle that happened in the past, or even a moment ago, and one does not hide it from him, this is not connected to a guarantee that the miracle will happen tomorrow as well. For example, when one says that when one prays to the Ribono shel Olam, the Ribono shel Olam can help in a supernatural way—and the proof is that the Ribono shel Olam has helped this person, that person, and many others—no one is saying that the Ribono shel Olam **must** answer a prayer in every instance and 100% of the time. One only says that there is a possibility, and the more heartfelt the prayer and the more meritorious the petitioner, the greater the possibility.

You begin your letter by mentioning that you were once a teacher in a Workmen's Circle school, apparently to justify your stance regarding belief in miracles. I do not believe this is a justification, for many educators and leaders of Workmen's Circle schools do believe in miracles, and to an extent that influences their daily lives. And surely you know of even more cases than I do.

In conclusion, I feel it is my duty, and also my privilege, to touch upon one more point in connection with your writing that you were a teacher, which proves that you possess capabilities in the field of education and influence. I would like to emphasize that every person who is gifted with certain capabilities also incurs a duty along with them; it obligates him to utilize his capabilities, not only for himself but for his entire surroundings, to the maximum degree. And taking into account that all parts of the world are closely connected and bound to one another, not utilizing these capabilities, or not utilizing them to the fullest extent, is not his "private business," as they say here; rather, it disrupts the progress of the entire world around him.

Following the custom of our Sages, of blessed memory, they have also encapsulated the above in a short sentence, as formulated by the great teacher, the Rambam (Hilchos Teshuvah, chapter 3, halacha 4): "Every person should see himself throughout the entire year as if he is half-innocent and half-guilty; and likewise, the entire world is half-innocent and half-guilty. If he commits one sin, he tips the scale for himself and for the entire world to the side of guilt and causes its destruction. If he performs one mitzvah, he tips the scale for himself and for the entire world to the side of merit and causes its salvation and rescue."

With respect and in hope of good tidings.

## 8499

B”H, 22 Menachem Av, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of Sunday, Parshas Re’eh—*Anochi nosein lifneichem hayom brachah* (I set before you today a blessing):

May Hashem Yisbarach draw down His blessings upon you and upon every member of your family, *sheyichyu*, with blessings that are good in a revealed and manifest way. Thus, with joy and a glad heart, and without any matters that cause confusion, may you act in accordance with the continuation of the verse: *tishme’u el mitzvos Hashem Elokeichem* (you shall listen to the commandments of Hashem your G-d)—a conduct in daily life according to the instructions of our Torah, *Toras Chaim*, and fulfilling its *mitzvos*, regarding which it is written: *v’chai bahem* (and he shall live by them).

Included in this—and it is one of the essentials—is that the teaching of students in *chinuch al taharas hakodesh* should be done with dedication and with joy.

For if "a little light pushes away much darkness" —referring to anything that holds a Yid back from serving Hashem together with his household, with joy and a glad heart—then how much more so when, instead of a little light, there is much light: *Torah Ohr*, and the *Maor ShebaTorah*, the *pnimiyus haTorah*, *Toras HaChassidus*, and conducting oneself in a *Chassidishe* manner by studying *Chassidus* oneself and with others.

And may the verse "Make us glad according to the days You have afflicted us" be fulfilled, so that from now on and moving forward, only goodness, kindness, and joy shall be with each of you and with everyone together.

Especially as we approach the month of Elul, the month of mercy, which, as our *Rabbeinu HaZaken* says, is when the *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* receives each and every person with a friendly countenance (Likutei Torah, *dih* Ani L’Dodi) and descends to below ten *tefachim*.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

**P.S.** Regarding your question about a specific *hanhagah*: One must keep the *shiurei Chitas* every day, and every weekday, before the morning *tefillah*—and likewise before the *Mincha tefillah*—one should set aside a few *prutos* for *tzedakah*. Furthermore, it is essential to be strong in *bitachon* in Hashem, who oversees each and every person with *hashgacha pratis*, for He is the essence of good, and it is the nature of the Good to bestow good, even to the point of good that is revealed and manifest.

***

 *Me'at ohr*: Tanya, Chapter 12.

## 8503

8503

B"H, 28 Menachem Av, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 24 Menachem Av, regarding the question concerning the Torah of the Children of Israel, its mitzvos, etc., and which path is preferable, etc.

Our Sages of blessed memory informed us in their Mishnah that "the deed is the essential thing." Even though it is simple that "the Merciful One desires the heart," nevertheless (in the style brought in the sefarim), one who intends the best of intentions but in practice does not give charity to a poor person has not fulfilled the mitzvah of tzedakah, and has transgressed the commandment "do not harden your heart," etc. This is unlike the opposite, which is called tzedakah not for its own sake (*shelo lishmah*), which nonetheless sustains the life of the poor person and his household.

And (by way of mussar) it is the same regarding all matters of Torah and mitzvos, whose content is to sustain the hungry and thirsty—this refers to the *neshamah elokis* within a Yid, which is hungry and thirsty to fulfill the mitzvos of its Creator.

My hope is strong that the aforementioned questions are theoretical, and that certainly your conduct in daily life conforms to the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of life, and to the fulfillment of its mitzvos, of which it is said, "and he shall live by them."

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

It is not at all possible that there could be, as written, a true "identification" with the Ribono shel Olam together with a rebellion against the commandment of the Ribono shel Olam?!

#### ***8503***

**Rachmana liba ba'i:** Sanhedrin 106b.

## 8105

8105

*[1st of Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5722]*

See *Etz Chaim*, Shaar 50, Chapter 4; *Likutei Torah*, Shir HaShirim 31a. Regarding the medical aspect: The right ventricle does not generate the blood (as it **arrives there** from the left ventricle, where it collects from the body), but rather, it is infused with the element of **air** that gives **life** to a person — oxygen.

See *Shem HaGedolim* by the Chida, *Chelek Sefarim*, end of letter *Gimel*.

This is the case in *Pesachim* 94a and there; *Likutei Torah*, *Emor* 34a.

#### ***8105***

A portion was printed in *Likutei Biurim* on *Tanya*, Part 1, p. 87, and it has been completed according to the Rebbe’s handwritten draft.

The letter is addressed to R' Mordechai Dov Altien, and it was written on the margin of his letter dated Thursday of Parshas Shoftim. Additional letters to him: above, Vol. 12, p. 40; Vol. 6, p. 1596.

**See:** In his letter: In *Tanya*, Chapter 9, it is written that the dwelling place of the *nefesh habehamis* is in the heart, in the left ventricle which is full of blood, and the dwelling place of the *nefesh elokis* is in the *mochin* in the brain, and from there it spreads to all the limbs, and also to the heart in the right ventricle, which contains no blood. Seemingly, I have a difficulty with this, for are there not blood vessels in all the chambers of the heart?

**See:** In his letter: When we say there are 53 *sedarim* of *Orayta*, which *sedra* is not counted in the total, for seemingly there are 54?

**Yes:** In his letter: Regarding what is written in the words of our Sages concerning the distance from the earth to the firmament being a journey of 500 years, and likewise between each firmament and the next, and the thickness of each firmament—is this a physical measurement? Surely the time and space of all the firmaments are not equal, so what is the calculation of 500?

## 8507

B"H, 3 Elul, 5722
Brooklyn.

To the distinguished, G-d-fearing, and learned, etc., R' Moshe, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

...In response to your question—the matter discussed at the farbrengen is that it must be "the labor of your hands" and not [the labor of] your head (and your heart). The emphasis is also on the word "labor" (yegiah); meaning, there are many matters of livelihood that require the utilization of one's intellect, focus, etc., but they should not require exertion (yegiah) in the sense of toil. See the sources marked regarding "the labor of your hands" (in the index to Likutei Torah). [See also] the mitzvah of the shaving of the metzora (in Sefer HaMitzvos of the Tzemach Tzedek) and the references there.

## 8,509

B"H, 4 Elul, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding your writing about scheduling a wedding in the month of Elul — according to the custom of Israel in many places (and the custom of Israel is Torah), Elul is especially auspicious for this, to the point that [weddings] are scheduled even in the second half of the month (see Sdei Chemed, Asifat Dinim, Ma'arechet Chatan V'Kallah, section 21). As for your note that this is a time of *talmud torah d'rabim* (public Torah study) — see Sdei Chemed there, where it can be argued that, on the contrary, this is precisely the reason, *milta b'ta'ama* (a matter with a rationale). And it is worth noting what is written in Birkei Yosef (cited in Mateh Ephraim, 581, in the *Elef LaMateh*, subsection 15) that, on the contrary, in the month of Elul one occupies oneself with *tefillah* and supplications, and sets aside some studies. And the main thing is the *ma'aseh* (custom) of the *Rav*, as mentioned above.

#### ***8,509***

Published in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 21, p. 462, and completed based on the secretariat's copy.

**In the month of Elul:** See also above, Vol. 20, letter 7,722.

## 8511

B"H, 6 Elul, 5722
Brooklyn.

Mr. Gershon, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 5 Elul, regarding your question about the order of study for *Pnimiyus HaTorah*, which has been revealed in our generation through the teachings of Chassidus.

If possible, it would be most appropriate for you to speak about this face-to-face with the *melamdim* and *mashpiim* of this study at Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Brooklyn. Until then, for your own situation, the appropriate order would be to begin with the third part of the *Tanya* by our Alter Rebbe, followed by *Kuntres Uma'ayan Mibeis Hashem*, then *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah* (the second part of the *Tanya*), and subsequently *Sefer HaMitzvos* by the Tzemach Tzedek, focusing on those *maamarim* there that you find more appealing, as indicated in the index printed there.

The main thing is that the study should be conducted as it is in all other parts of our holy Torah, with the premise of *naaseh* before *nishma*. *Naaseh* in the study itself means that you resolve to succeed in your learning without being discouraged by the fact that, as our Sages say, "all beginnings are difficult." Furthermore, our Sages have said, "If one says, 'I have labored but not found,' do not believe him; 'I have not labored but I have found,' do not believe him; 'I have labored and I have found,' believe him."

We are currently in the days of *ratzon*, the month of Elul, the month of mercy.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all the above, and for a *kesivah vachasimah tovah*.

#### ***8511***

**The appropriate order:** See also above, letter 8265, and the references in the notes there.

**As our Sages say:** *Mechilta* and Rashi on *Yisro* 19:5.

**Our Sages have said:** *Megillah* 6b.

## 8512

B"H, 7 Elul, 5722
Brooklyn

To the campers of Camp Gan Yisroel in Eretz Yisroel,
Our Holy Land,
May it be built and established speedily in our days by Moshiach Tzidkeinu,
May Hashem grant them life.

Blessings and peace!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter, along with your greetings and the map you created with your own hands.

I am confident that, as you wrote in your letter, you have been strengthened in the appropriate chinuch during your time at the aforementioned camp—a chinuch befitting every daughter of Yisroel, for each one of you is called a daughter of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah.

This is especially true in our Holy Land, of which it is said, "The eyes of Hashem your G-d are upon it from the beginning of the year to the end of the year."

Just as regarding physical health, the hope is that your stay at the camp will add to your physical well-being throughout the entire year, so too, and even more so, is the hope that the health of your neshamah will be strengthened by the aforementioned chinuch throughout the entire year.

This is especially relevant in light of the well-known, immense efforts of our teacher, the Baal Shem Tov—after whom the camp is named—and following him, our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, among them the Nasi who founded Kfar Chabad, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the chinuch of the children of Bnei Yisroel, through ahavas Yisroel, permeated with ahavas HaTorah and ahavas Hashem Yisbarach.

May it be the will of Hashem that following this healthy summer, the coming year will arrive for you, together with all of Klal Yisroel, healthy in both body and soul, and may each and every one of you be blessed with a good and sweet year.

With blessings for a kesivah v'chasimah tovah.

## 8513

8513

B.H., 11 Elul, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished, who occupies himself with communal affairs, a man of noble character, a scion of a noble lineage, etc., R. Shazar, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby confirm receipt of your two letters along with the enclosed review, as well as the personal regards conveyed through Rabbi Mordechai Kirshblum, may he live. Many thanks for all of this.

As is the way and custom of the Jewish people to offer comment on every matter—and all the more so regarding a matter such as this—I wish to express my strong hope that following the aforementioned review, immediate conclusions will be reached. At the very least, this concerns our brethren, the children of Israel, who are on the other side of the Iron Curtain, and first and foremost, our brethren who are in the Land upon which the eyes of Hashem are from the beginning of the year until the end of the year, and for which they yearn, as you mentioned when conveying their regards—our brethren behind the Curtain mention it at every opportunity and long for news of what is happening there, etc.

Based on what is emphasized in the review regarding the signs of our vitality with the eternal Jewish people and its existence—which are specifically the performance of practical mitzvos—beginning with a matter that transcends logic and intellect, namely the matter of Bris Milah, which is engraved and sealed in the flesh (and not in the soul alone), and in the flesh of a tender infant eight days old (and according to the explanation of the Midrash and the Rambam regarding this, in *Bereishis Rabbah* 46:6 and *Moreh Nevuchim* 3:49, there was room for this mitzvah even earlier, but the Torah said that the health of the tender infant being circumcised should be strengthened first)—

The essence of the immediate conclusion, to be of assistance to our brethren who are in distress and captivity—an assistance for which there is no barrier or boundary to impede—is the strengthening in the performance of practical mitzvos by each and every one of us who is on this side. It must be a performance in public and with pride, stemming from the recognition that "He chose us and sanctified us with His mitzvos," the opposite of the secrecy and pressure to the point of soul-crushing despair that is associated with the performance of mitzvos behind the Curtain.

It is simple to understand that this idea will not be the most "popular," especially in the recent climate of public opinion in the Holy Land, may it be built and established. But surely, a lack of popularity does not in the least detract from the truth of a matter, the strength of its reality, and the necessity of it.

I also know that there is room for the argument that the aforementioned is the responsibility of each and every person, as stated above, and not necessarily of a specific institution, a specific party, or a specific type of person, and this is a completely valid argument. But it is also obvious that in accordance with the magnitude of the ability and the possibilities at the disposal of each person (individual or institution), so too is the responsibility and the task incumbent upon them in fulfilling their role.

I once heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that "a Chassid is a clever person and does not put off until tomorrow what he can do today." In the present case, we have been promised that "no one shall be cast away from Him," and as the prophet Yechezkel says, "It shall not be... if not with a strong hand will I rule over you." [And incidentally, "in continuation" of the above, our brethren love novelty, and what is better than a surprising novelty? We see recently that several of the shluchim from the Holy Land, may it be built and established, to the Diaspora have been instructed to conduct themselves with the observance of Shabbos, kashrus, etc., since they are viewed as representatives of our Holy Land, and that when they return from the lands of the nations to the Holy Land, they are released from the aforementioned command and order!]

Surely you will not take offense at what is written above, and I will not elaborate further in a place where it would have been appropriate to elaborate much more, since for someone like you, there is no need for length.

It is most distressing that until now, nothing has been done in actual practice regarding the matter of the buildings, etc., even though a committee was chosen long ago and you are its chairman. However, you write reasons for this in your letter, and "one does not cry over the past." May it be the will that from this moment forward, the matter will progress at the fastest pace possible, in accordance with the necessity and the demand of the hour.

As we are in the days of the month of Elul, the month of mercy, may it be the will that you receive good news from your relatives, may they live, who are there—regarding whom you write in your letter of the 18th of Menachem Av—in a good and revealed manner.

With respect and with the blessing of *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah*,

**M. Schneerson**

My previous letter was surely received in its time and season.

## 8514

B"H, 13 Elul, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

As we stand at the beginning of the month of Elul—the month of mercy and favor—a month which, in the words of the Alter Rebbe, is:

Like a king who, before entering his city, is met by the townspeople who go out to greet him in the field. At that time, anyone who wishes to go out to greet him is permitted to do so, and he receives them all with a friendly countenance and shows a smiling face to everyone.

And as my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, explains—they are permitted and they are able.

May it be Hashem’s will that all of this be drawn down into matters of both body and soul alike, even into the affairs of our "everyday life."

This is understood from the analogy: since the King is in the field and receives the townspeople with a friendly countenance just as they are in the field, their surroundings are also matters of the field—many of which are in need of salvation, blessing, and success.

Especially in light of the well-known statement of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi of Israel:

May the Almighty grant Jews a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters, in general and in particular—if Jews will do what they can, the Almighty will see what Jews can do.

With blessings for a *ksivah v'chasimah tovah* and for good tidings, in general and in particular,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8518

B"H, 19 Elul, 5722
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter and the enclosed outline of your life’s history:

It is understood that there is no need for an apology, and you may continue to write whenever necessary in the future. May it be the will of Hashem—who is the essence of good and whose nature is to bestow good—that the content of your letters be joyful and positive, in a way that is good, visible, and revealed.

Regarding the content of your letter, and with the hope that by the time you receive this response your state of mind will have already improved:

Since a person must do what is within his power according to the natural order—and many similar cases have occurred, especially in our current times—you are surely consulting with an expert in the field and following their instructions. However, the primary thing is for you to contemplate the reality of the Creator and Conductor of the world. We see tangibly that the world is not ownerless; there is a Master of this palace. The order we find in the inanimate realm, etc.—which constitutes the vast majority of the world around us—compels us to conclude that there is certainly order in the smallest parts of it as well, all the way up to man. One cannot say that there is no order in man, or that the opposite of order prevails within him.

This is also the approach of science: that the same laws governing 99 percent of any phenomenon surely govern the one percent that has not yet been examined or is not yet visible, etc.

The immediate conclusion from this is that, ultimately, order and goodness prevail. This provides confidence and encouragement: even if, for the time being, the good is obscured by a certain phenomenon or a certain ailment, man has certainly been given the strength to overcome them, provided he truly desires to. It is simply the nature of creation that a change in state comes step by step, not all at once from one extreme to the other. Contemplating this—especially given what you wrote regarding your education and your work in the sciences—should lead to encouragement and an increase in self-confidence and general optimism. Through all this, your energy will increase and your situation will improve, albeit, as mentioned, step by step.

If we are always in need of the blessing of the Creator and Conductor of man—Hashem, may He be blessed and exalted—then certainly in a situation such as this, we are in need of an additional blessing and a special blessing. The conduit and vessel for this is conducting one’s daily life in accordance with the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of life, and through the fulfillment of its mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them." It makes no difference whether or not one understands the connection between the conduct and the blessing. This is similar to improving the state of the body through medicine; it does not make much difference if the weak person understands how the medicine heals, especially when the healing comes after some time, provided that he takes the medicine. Certainly, for someone like you, there is no need for an elaboration on this, and I look forward to hearing good news regarding all that has been mentioned.

These are days of favor, the days of the month of Elul, the month of mercy and favor.

With blessings for a *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah* and for good news.

## 519

By the Grace of G-d
25 Elul, 5722
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life,

Peace and Blessing!

The year 5722, which is soon drawing to a close, has been a year of serious events in the world at large, and in the Jewish world in particular:

The fear of the power of atomic weapons; the tension and instability in international relations; the global race for armaments, and so on.

Regarding the Jewish situation specifically—Jewish communities in certain parts of the world have been seriously shaken.

So too regarding the individual, even in his daily life: although there has been a noticeable *hisorerus* (awakening), a thirst and a turning back to our eternal sources of *emunah* united with *Torah* and *mitzvos*—nevertheless, unfortunately (and may it not be mentioned during the days of *Slichos*), this tremendous *sha'as hakosher* (opportune time) has not been utilized to the proper extent.

***

In view of the new year, which approaches us and all of Israel for good, every Jew must ask himself the question: What can I do to improve and secure the situation in the coming year? What can I do for the individual, for myself, for *Klal Yisrael*, and for the world at large?

And *Rosh Hashanah* provides the answer; it also provides the possibility:

*Rosh Hashanah*, the *yom hamishpat* (day of judgment) for the individual, for the collective, and for the entire world—is the gateway to the new year, and the *rosh* (head) of the coming year.

The point of *Rosh Hashanah* is *hachtarah*—to crown the *Ribono shel Olam* anew as **King**—through *malchuso* (His kingship) which they accept upon themselves willingly.

With great *simcha*, strong *bitul*, and great *yirah*, we crown and accept the *Ribono shel Olam* as King, and submit ourselves to His will.

Every Jew fulfills on the day of *Rosh Hashanah* the directive **"Make Me King over you"**—crown Me as King over you—a directive to each and every one of us.

From the *hachtarah* of the individuals, each of whom is a constituent part of *Klal Yisrael*, comes the *hachtarah* of the *Ribono shel Olam* as **King of Israel** and its Redeemer. The *kabbalas malchuso* (acceptance of His kingship) of the individual, within *Klal Yisrael*, influences the entire environment, the entire world, and the request is fulfilled: **"Reign over the entire world."**

**Acceptance of His kingship** is expressed in arranging one’s daily conduct in full accordance with the King’s will and His commandments, which were given to us by the *Ribono shel Olam*, the King who desires **"life"** (who wishes to give a true, authentic life) in the *Torah*, the *Toras Chaim*, and the *mitzvos* regarding which it is written, **"and live by them."**

Such conduct ensures a calm and happy life for the individual, for the collective, and for the entire world—happy both in *ruchniyus* and in *gashmiyus*.

For in truth, *ruchniyus* and *gashmiyus* are not two separate worlds.

*Shema Yisrael* (when a Jew understands and hears that) *Hashem* (is) *Elokeinu* (the G-d of the individual Jew and of *Klal Yisrael*). *Hashem* (is) *Echad* (One—unique everywhere and in every place—forever and ever)—he brings this oneness to be revealed in the entire world, and he sees that G-dliness and *ruchniyus* direct the *gashmiyus*, and an improvement in spiritual life brings an improvement in material life.

***

The improvement in spiritual life, in the fulfillment of the *mitzvos* of the King, must come in both areas: *mitzvos* that are **bein adam lamakom** (between man and G-d) and *mitzvos* that are **bein adam lachaveiro** (between man and his fellow), and this is emphasized in the cry of *Rosh Hashanah*: **"Teshuvah, tefillah, and tzedakah avert the evil of the decree."**

**Teshuvah,** the firm resolution to return to the King, with complete regret for the past and a *kabbalah tovah* (good resolution) for the future, both in **tefillah**, in the realm of *bein adam lamakom*, and in **tzedakah**, in the realm of *bein adam lachaveiro*.

All of this removes the evil of the decree,

And brings for the individual, for the collective, and for the entire world,

A *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in *gashmiyus* and *ruchniyus* together.

With the blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* in the good that is seen and revealed,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 8521

B"H, Erev Rosh Hashanah, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Mordechai Namir,
Mayor of Tel Aviv

Greetings and Blessings,

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I wish to extend to you and all those dear to you a blessing for the year—for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

On this occasion, albeit with much delay—for which I ask your forgiveness—I wish to acknowledge receipt of the album of the city that you were kind enough to send me through your friend, who is also my friend. I view this as a sign of appreciation for the Chabad program and its activities, which also strengthens my hope that you will be of assistance to Chabad’s activities in Tel Aviv and its surroundings, and throughout the entire country, as your influence is evident even outside your own city and in wider circles.

As we stand in these days of reckoning regarding the past and preparation for the New Year, I wish to express my hope that you will utilize your influence in your city—the most populous in the Holy Land—so that it may also be the greatest in matters of spirit, holiness, peace, and justice. And since our Torah, the Torah of life, is largely occupied with practical matters, may it be His will that your positive influence be continued in actual deeds, and not like the slogan "the Merciful One desires the heart" [as if that alone] suffices, but rather through action specifically. Especially, as mentioned above, since the city is the largest in the land which is called the Holy Land, and in the language of our Torah, the Torah of life, "a land which the L-rd your G-d cares for; the eyes of the L-rd your G-d are always upon it, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year," which also guarantees assistance from Above for blessing and success in both quantity and quality.

With respect, and with regards to the other members of the city council, and with a blessing for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah*.

It is understood and obvious that I am aware that you are a member of a political party, but it is also understood and obvious that this does not contradict what was written above. On the contrary, since it is the party that holds the majority in the Knesset and governs in many matters and enterprises; and there is one Torah for us all, for all the children of Israel, without any party distinction whatsoever.

## 8523

8523

*[5722]*

It is not **absolute** — for the Torah of **life** teaches that every single day, the Exodus from Egypt must be **possible**.

However, it is given specifically to Bnei Yisrael — a gift through which they resemble their Creator — the matter of choice. And the Holy One, Blessed be He, desired that this aforementioned Exodus from Egypt should also come about specifically through this gift — through the choice of man, as it is written: **"And you shall choose** life" (an instruction, and also the **bestowal of strength** and a promise). If so, as mentioned above, he will choose the true life (the exclusive life — regarding Bnei Yisrael), the life of Torah and mitzvos, and he will succeed more easily and to a greater degree than he imagines. And since a person is close to himself — he should detail his situation before the administration of Tomchei Temimim and act according to their instruction with joy and a good heart.

## 8524

8524

[5722]

Regarding what you hear from various people who say that when one gets married, several problems, difficulties, etc., arise—this is not because such cases are common, for on the contrary, they are a minority of a minority (which, even according to Rabbi Meir, we do not concern ourselves with)—rather, it is because all those who do not have problems, etc., do not speak about this **at all**, because **this** is considered a **normal** state.

That getting married is good (and also necessary) is explicitly stated in the verse (Bereishis 2:18). And we also see this tangibly, from the fact that people mock those who have not married (an old bachelor, an old bachelorette). When you contemplate your past, you will see how you were saved from **several** troubles, and almost in a manner beyond the way of nature. And on the contrary, this contemplation, if it is **genuine**, will strengthen your bitachon.

**Contrary** to your letter—until now you have not exerted yourself hard regarding shidduchim, but only to show (even to yourself) that you can make a good impression, etc. But when it came close to the actualization and a decision—you would evade it (in order to remain free, without responsibility).

***

 **To Rabbi Meir:** Yevamos 119a. And elsewhere.

## 8525

[1962]

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter:

a) Between now and the upcoming Rosh Hashanah, each of you should donate to a Talmud Torah or yeshiva (for boys or girls)—in addition to your regular contributions—approximately $2.40.

b) Over the next three years, [you should observe] 120 fasts of **four** hours each (not, Heaven forbid, full-day fasts).

Note: You should eat four hours after waking from your sleep.

c) The main thing is regret for the past and a firm resolution for the future to be careful from here on out.

d) Also essential is to have trust in Hashem that He has granted you atonement, and to be **joyful and of good cheer**.

e) Bring at least three couples closer to the observance of Taharas HaMishpacha.

f) Influence and bring at least three students to a Torah-true education.

May Hashem fulfill the pregnancy of the couple, may she give birth to a healthy child at a good and auspicious time, and may both of you be blessed with goodness that is revealed and apparent.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 8527

8527

*[Notes on the sefer Beis HaMikdash [Shefer]. Jerusalem, 5722]*

**At the beginning**: The layout of the Beis HaMikdash according to the Tiferes Yisrael. **16** The fifteen steps — they were like half a round threshing floor (Middos 2:5). **And not** as depicted in the commentary of the Tiferes Yisrael and copied in this book.

Page 13. The Har HaBayis was entirely roofed. Its length was 500 amos, etc.

A note and explanation are necessary regarding the Beis HaMikdash (which is also included in the area of the 500 amos). Especially since the words of the commentators **appear** to indicate that the entire Beis HaMikdash was not included in the aforementioned roofing. And it is obvious that several places within it were not roofed. See the commentators on Middos, beginning of chapter 2.

In all the diagrams of the Har HaBayis in the book — there is no mention or indication (as is customary in diagrams) of roofing!

**Ibid.** Gates... their height is 20 amos — this is the height of the interior space and the gate opening.

Page 44. The length of the aliyah — should be 61 amos, and not 60.

**At the end**, page 51. The place of the guard. The Kohanim — from the inside; the Leviim — from the outside.

The explanation is missing. See Raavad, Tamid, at the beginning. Minchas Chinuch, Mitzvah 388.

Page 52. The Ish Har HaBayis. One man, etc. — On the face of it, it is simple that he was a Kohen, since this is also part of the guarding, and furthermore, he was appointed over the Kohanim regarding their avodah. And it is not similar to "the openings are Mordechai's" regarding the acquisition (Shekalim, beginning of chapter 5). And for the time being, I have not found in the book where they discuss this.

#### ***8527***

Printed in Likutei Sichos, Vol. 21, p. 481, and edited according to the Rebbe's handwritten draft.

## 8529

B"H, Between Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Gideon Naor,
Head of the Local Council of Kiryat Gat

Greetings and Blessings,

Following the New Year’s blessing which you surely received in due time, I wish to express my heartfelt gratitude for the presentation of the key by my representative, through the guests from Kiryat Gat, which was delivered to me on your behalf and on behalf of the Council during the farbrengen on Erev Rosh Hashanah. I have also instructed the shaliach to personally convey my appreciation to you, along with a few points that were mentioned at that occasion regarding the presentation of the key, based on the well-known dictum of the Baal Shem Tov: that every matter and event in a person’s life contains a lesson and instruction for one’s avodah to their Creator. Briefly, it is as follows:

The function of a key is twofold: to open and to lock. This implies that there is a door and a gate that must sometimes be open and sometimes be closed. In a person’s life, these are the two pillars: the path of "turn away from evil," where one must lock the door against undesirable influences, and the path of "do good," where one must open the door to positive influences.

This matter applies to everyone, both the individual and the collective. For every person, even one whose status and position are most elevated, prays, "Do not bring me into the hands of a trial," so as to be wary of undesirable influence. On the other hand, goodness is limitless, for it is connected to the Essence of Good, Hashem, Who is infinite. One must always strive to increase in goodness, as our Sages have ruled: "We increase in holiness."

Since everyone’s responsibility is commensurate with the possibilities and strengths granted to them, may it be Hashem’s will that you, as Head of the Council, and all the members of the Council, utilize your strengths and possibilities to their fullest in the two aforementioned paths: to strive that the city be locked and sealed against undesirable influences, and open to absorbing matters of goodness to the greatest possible extent. And since the city is in the land which is called the Holy Land—and in the language of our Torah, the Torah of Life, "a land which Hashem your G-d seeks out; the eyes of Hashem your G-d are always upon it, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year"—there is added importance to what was stated above, and you are also assured of assistance from Above for blessing and success, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With respect and with blessings for a *chasimah v’gmar chasimah tovah* (a good sealing and final sealing).

## 8291

B"H, Between Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Rabbi Mordechai Kirshblum, shlita,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I trust you have received the New Year’s blessing I sent you. Your letter, along with the enclosure, has just arrived.

Thank you for the heartfelt words you wrote regarding our conversation. Since the purpose of all discussion is for it to be drawn down from the world of speech to the world of action—and as is well known, the gravity of idle talk is significant—my hope is strong that both my words and yours will lead each of us to increase our practical action in the area and direction we discussed. This is especially true regarding the field of chinuch, which has been a vital issue from time immemorial, particularly in our generation, and all the more so in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established.

I read with interest the copy of the letter enclosed with yours and noted the figures presented there. Surely, for someone like yourself, it is unnecessary to emphasize that they are completely disproportionate, not only to the demands of the situation but also to the necessities of the situation. Therefore, I am certain you will not mind if I emphasize once again my hope that you will utilize your influence to its fullest in this specific area, to mobilize all the individuals and organizations within your reach in the desired direction. I trust you will keep me informed of developments in this area, and I thank you in advance.

On this occasion, I am enclosing a copy of a sicha and a letter for Rosh Hashanah, which I hope you will find of interest; if you look closely, you will find they have relevance to the content of our discussion.

With respect and with blessings for a *chasima v’gmar chasima tova*.

It is my hope, even though you do not mention it specifically, that you have a fixed time each day for the study of our holy Torah—the Torah of life—which, in addition to being a commandment from the Creator, blessed be He, also draws down Hashem’s blessing in all that is needed for both the soul and the body alike.

I was pleased to read in your letter that you are participating in the work of rescuing Jewish children from foreign influences. It is my hope that you will increase your efforts and activities to disseminate traditional Judaism in your surroundings in general, and specifically among the immigrants from Persia—since, according to your letter, that is your place of origin—and in the style of our Sages, of blessed memory, "the poor of your city take precedence." And we are promised that "he who comes to purify himself is assisted."

This is especially true as we stand in these auspicious days, the Aseres Yemei Teshuvah, regarding which it is said, "Seek Hashem when He is found, call upon Him when He is near." These days are most auspicious for making good resolutions and undertaking good actions for the duration of the entire new year that is approaching us and all of Israel for good and for blessing. May it be the will of Hashem that you increase in all of the above, and as our Sages, of blessed memory, commanded, "we elevate in matters of holiness," and may the Almighty grant you success in your path.

Regarding your question as to whether it is worthwhile for you to travel abroad to receive a Master’s degree: since you are in your second year of studies, it is still too early, and when the time draws near, there will be opportunity to decide on this.

With blessings for a *chasimah v’gmar chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

Since you also understand English, I have enclosed material relevant to the days, which relates to what was mentioned above.

## 8734

B"H, 26 Tishrei, 5723
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of Sunday, in which you write regarding your worldview, etc., and ask about the future of a certain movement, etc.

Surely there is no need to explain that every single man and woman of the Jewish people, without exception, is a part of our eternal nation, of whom it is said, "For there is one nation in the land," or in other phrasing, "A nation that dwells alone." This is because every individual of this people has received one Torah from one Hashem. Just as Hashem and the Torah are eternal, so too is the recipient of the Torah eternal—to the point that all the nations of the earth feel this, even if not all of them admit it. [And it seems that this feeling is also the reason for their hatred toward our people, which is found in **all** movements, from the extreme right to the extreme left, even though, logically, they should have been bridging the gap between all peoples and nullifying the eternal hatred toward the eternal people, the Jewish people.]

The immediate conclusion from the above is that although, on the face of it, the choice is given to every Jew as to which worldview to choose, and how to conduct themselves in life in general and in daily life in particular, they will never find true peace of mind except on the path charted for our eternal people by our eternal Torah.

In simpler terms: Every Jew must conduct their daily life in a manner consistent with the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of life, and through the fulfillment of its mitzvos, of which it is said, "And he shall live by them."

For it is impossible for anything to change its **essence**, even though it can cover it up and, for a time, conceal it—even with garments that contradict the very essence and point of its existence.

From this it is understood that everyone must utilize all their ability to strengthen this conduct—of Torah and mitzvos—and to disseminate it in their home, in their surroundings, and in every place their reach extends. There is no distinction in this regarding which party one is officially affiliated with, or whether one claims to be mindful of circles that recognize Torah and mitzvos, or otherwise.

From all that has been said—in response to your question—it is not our role to guess what the future of this or that movement will be. The vital task of every man and woman is to strengthen and establish the situation of our people, who are surrounded by haters and enemies on every side, and likewise to establish their own situation as much as depends on them. This is achieved by grounding Judaism and its eternal values and disseminating them in a manner that is "ever-increasing." And we have been promised, "He who comes to purify himself is assisted."

I look forward to hearing good news regarding all of the above.

With blessings.

***

**And we have been promised:** Yoma 38b.
