## 8536

B"H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Bereishis — "For the sake of Torah and for the sake of Yisrael" — 5723. Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of Yeshivas Toras Emes in Jerusalem, the Holy City, may it be rebuilt and established,
May Hashem keep them alive,

Peace and blessing!

In response to the notification regarding the scheduling of the cornerstone-laying ceremony for the buildings of the holy Yeshiva, Toras Emes,

May it be the will of Hashem that the laying of the cornerstone be at a good and auspicious time in every detail—a great house of study in which the "Toras Emes" (Truth of Torah) will grow, both the revealed and the inner dimensions together, and in which *tefillah* will also grow.

For it is *tefillah* that ensures that one’s learning is true and enduring, and leads to action, for through it, the fear of Hashem becomes the treasure of the student.

Especially in our generation, the generation of the footsteps of Moshiach, where the role of the Yeshiva is not only the study of Torah, but—and this is primary—education based on the foundations of Torah and *mitzvos*; an inner and true education that will not be daunted by any "winds" in the world (a play on the word *helem* and *hester*—concealment), and will stand firm against all trials.

And if this is true in any place, how much more so in the land upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year, and especially in Jerusalem, the Holy City, where the name itself is significant: *Yireh Shalem*—the perfection of fear—as interpreted by our Rebbe, the author of the Tanya (the authority on the hidden dimensions of Torah) and the Shulchan Aruch (the authority on the revealed dimensions of Torah).

And surely, the instruction of our Torah, the Torah of life, also provides the strength and assistance from Above to fulfill this directive.

May it be the will of Hashem that the construction proceeds with the necessary alacrity until its actual completion, and most importantly—that the entire house be filled with this light, which is Torah, with attentive students who are in accordance with the will of our Rebbes, the *Nesi'im*, the founders of the Yeshiva, may the merit of their righteousness protect us.

And fortunate is the portion of each and every person who participates in this lofty endeavor, participating with their money and also with their person (by influencing friends to do the same).

According to what has been stated, this is a matter that encompasses all three pillars—Torah, *avodah* (tefillah), and *gemilus chasadim*—all together.

With respect and blessing to all those participating in the celebration, and to all those who assist this endeavor in the past, present, and future, may they live and be well.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 8737

B"H, 2 MarCheshvan, 5723
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 30 Tishrei.

I was pleased to read of your impressions of the Chassidim in Kfar Chabad, and the hope that this experience will also translate into practical action. I mean that you should endeavor to share these impressions with others. As per the well-known saying of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, the teachings of Chassidus are not, Heaven forbid, the property of any specific group, but rather the inheritance of every single Jew. He exerted himself—even to the point of mesiras nefesh—for its dissemination, as did the Nasi’im of Chabad throughout the generations who succeeded him, and they gave their blessings to all who strive in this, that they will ultimately succeed.

If this applies to every person, it applies all the more so to one who has the opportunity to influence the youth. Influencing them, even if it seems slight, can alter the character of their lives in general, and specifically when they eventually marry and build homes in Yisrael. Surely for someone like you, further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

Regarding your question about teaching a secular subject with one’s head uncovered, there is room to argue that this makes it easier to find common ground.

There are two points to consider:

a) Matters of Shulchan Aruch are not subject to "negotiation"—selling a minor transgression to acquire a major mitzvah (excluding, of course, the specific cases explicitly detailed in the Shulchan Aruch, where it is not a matter of negotiation, Heaven forbid, but a halachic ruling like any other).

b) And this is the main point: We see clearly, especially in relation to youth, that compromise—even slight—lowers the value of the Torah and mitzvos in their eyes. It destroys their trust in the one who compromises; if a compromise is possible in one area of the laws of Torah and mitzvos, it is proof that these matters are not absolutely true. For in **truth**, there is no room for compromise or even a hairbreadth of deviation. If there is room for compromise, then it is not the path of truth.

Although it is said that "Truth was cast to the ground," and "There is no righteous man on earth who does good and does not sin," the approach in Chabad is explained: one must draw everyone near, without exception, with the assurance that even one mitzvah can ultimately lead to all 613 mitzvos—and at the very least, nothing is lost [as the Alter Rebbe writes in the holy Tanya, Chapter 32]. Therefore, if nothing else is possible, one begins by speaking about one mitzvah. However, alongside this approach, one must never say, Heaven forbid, that this is the only mitzvah (that we are discussing) and that one is a **complete** tzaddik for fulfilling it. Rather, one must **emphasize**—albeit in pleasant and peaceful ways—that this is only one of the 613 mitzvos, but due to certain circumstances, the person is not yet ready to be spoken to or expected to observe the other mitzvos, and so one begins from the easier to the more difficult.

Now, all of the above concerns the demands made upon the students. But regarding the mashpia, it is understood that none of the aforementioned justifications apply. On the contrary, when he demands things of his students and they accept them, he must be a living example—not only of what he demands of them, but of the entire way of life he speaks about. In the phrasing of Chazal, he must be "moist enough to moisten others." The students will surely reason *kal v'chomer*: if it is permitted for their teacher to transgress a certain matter, then the student certainly has permission for many other matters, and the rest is obvious.

One could elaborate at length on all of this, but I hope that these lines—few in quantity relative to the importance of the subject of education—will suffice.

With respect and blessing.

## 8,538

B"H, 3 Cheshvan, 5723
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

This is in response to your letter from the 1st of Cheshvan, and regarding the conclusion of your letter concerning your son, may he live.

Certainly, once you write his address, we will try once more through the *anash* rabbis in Chicago, if he is still there.

And although *tefillah* and *bracha* are helpful, a Yid must also do that which depends on him *b'derech hateva*.

Since your letter was written the day after the month of Tishrei—the month that is "satisfied with all good"—and as my father-in-law, the Rebbe, said that this month is a general month for the entire year, this means that the "satisfied with all good" should be fulfilled in your affairs as well, throughout the entire year.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

**P.S.** Regarding your question as to what is meant by the writing of "unwanted thoughts which stem from *marah shechorah*":

The matter is simple, and it is connected to what my father-in-law, the Rebbe, wrote to you regarding the concept of "against your will you live." This refers to the general attitude of not being in a state of *b'simcha u'tuv levav*, despite the fact that every Yid begins the day with *Birchos Hashachar*, the beginning of which is *Modeh Ani Lefanecha*, and immediately afterward, many times, *Baruch Atah*—which shows that there should be blessing and that there is much to be thankful for. This applies especially to strengthening yourself in *bitachon* regarding your efforts with your son, may he live.

## 8,339

B"H, 7 Mar-Cheshvan, 5723
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and G-d-fearing man, whose work is the work of Heaven,
Rabbi Nachum Ze'ev, shlita,

Greetings and blessings!

With a significant delay, I received your letter, along with the copies of the letters of the esteemed Chossid, a man of many accomplishments and fine character, Rabbi Yitzchak HaLevi, a"h. Many thanks for your thoughtfulness in sending them to me; as our Sages have already stated, "A thing that is old is precious."

This has further confirmed for me what I had heard some time ago from several people: that his father, the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing man of many accomplishments and fine character, a"h, not only studied the teachings of Chabad with depth, but also disseminated them among his students (at least on some occasions, even by citing the sources).

It is puzzling that some of his students and those he influenced attempt to conceal this. There is no need to dwell on a matter that is both astonishing and distressing.

According to the words of our Sages in the Mishnah, that a father merits his son with wisdom and upright reasoning, my hope is strong that you, too, are doing the same—that is, studying the teachings of Chassidus with depth and disseminating them wherever your reach extends.

If, decades ago, they saw a necessity for this, how much more so in our generation, an orphaned generation where the darkness has grown and doubled, to the point of "rebuke" and action—to call darkness light and light darkness. This is the requirement and necessity of the hour, and fortunate is the portion of everyone who spreads these fountains until they reach even the "outside."

With respect and blessings, and a request for forgiveness for the delay in acknowledging and responding until now.

Regarding the reasoning concerning the printing of the letter about the concept of Tzimtzum: it was written briefly, etc., as per the limitations and style of writing a letter. The matter has already been explained well in several printed seforim, in accordance with the depth of the subject and the necessity for it—especially since some who are "wise in their own eyes" have erred in this (Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah by our Rebbe HaZaken, Chapter 7). Some of these places (though not all) are noted in the index at the end of Torah Or, Likutei Torah, and Derech Mitzvotecha.

## 8540

8540

B"H, 7 Mar-Cheshvan, 5723
Brooklyn

To those involved in the fundraising for "Machne Israel," both one-time and monthly, may Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter from the 28th of Tishrei, and subsequently the list of donors for the month of Tishrei, may it be a year of blessing.

At a time of favor, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

The magnitude of this matter—based on the magnitude of the activities of "Machne Israel"—certainly requires no explanation, and all the more so, no elaboration. For it was founded by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the Nasi of our generation, and is well-known and publicized in its general scope as well as in the details of its activities—in the plan that was publicized during his lifetime in this world, orally, in writing, and subsequently in print as well.

In your letter, you mention that at the beginning of these days, you proclaimed and continue to proclaim, "And Yaakov went on his way" (*Bereishis 32:2*). It is possible to say that "Yaakov" is "Machne Israel," in accordance with the explanation that he is alluded to in the verse by the title "Bnei Yisrael."

May it be the will [of Hashem] that the aforementioned [activity] be in a manner of "going," and as explained in the teachings of Chassidus regarding the true meaning of "going"—that it is in a manner of "from strength to strength" (*Tehillim 84:8*), and even beyond measurement and limitation.

And may this be "on his way," in both extremes: at the beginning, through an arousal from Above (*is'arusa d'leila*), which is the path upon which he was commanded to walk.

And through the avodah of an arousal from below (*is'arusa d'letata*), which is his own "way," whereby he becomes the master of the path and its affairs.

This is in accordance with what has been explained previously and in other places regarding the two interpretations of the conclusion of the verse, "And the angels of Elokim met him" (*Bereishis 32:2*), leading to the unification of the two extremes. This is as the verse there hints: "Machanayim" (two camps), that both are in one word. For through "Yaakov went on his way" during the weekdays throughout the entire year—we draw down from Rosh Hashanah, from the place of true choice, for it is precisely there that "He will choose our inheritance for us, the pride of Yaakov" (*Tehillim 47:5*).

With blessings for success in the aforementioned activity, and may it be with joy and a glad heart.

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***8540***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 18, p. 197, and completed according to a photocopy of the letter.

**7 Mar-Cheshvan:** The conclusion and seal of the festival (and the pilgrimage)—Shach, Choshen Mishpat, 667:47. And what is written there. And even though now, etc., [it is just] a manner of speaking, etc.—based on what the Alter Rebbe wrote in Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chayim, 217:1: And even, etc., **even today**, etc. It may be said that the difficulty of the Shach is resolved by this, and it is not merely a **manner of speaking**, etc., but the **substance** of being occupied with the matters of the festival.

**In accordance with what has been explained:** Torah Or, beginning of Parshas Shemos.

**The concept of "going":** Maamar "Im Bechukosai" 5710, Chapter 5.

**The path upon which he was commanded:** Note Torah Or and Ohr HaTorah, end of Parshas Vayeitzei.

**Which is his own "way":** Note Torah Or, end of Parshas Vayeitzei.

**The two interpretations:** See Zohar Vol. III, 154a; ibid., 155b.

**Machanayim:** Note Ramban (Vayeitzei 32:3) and Ohr HaChayim there: Yaakov, the chosen of Hashem.

## 8541

B"H, 8 MarCheshvan, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Rabbi Gedaliah Klaperman, shlita

Shalom u’Bracha!

I was pleased to receive your letter of Tuesday, 3 MarCheshvan, and I thank you as well for your books on the history of our people. In my spare time, I will certainly look through them, and as you suggested at the end of your letter, I will write to you with any comments I may have.

I read with interest your letter regarding your impressions of the Chassidic teachings you heard during your visit. This aligns with the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory, that "study is great because it leads to action," and furthermore, "it is not the study that is the main thing, but the action." It is my strong hope that you will translate these matters from the world of thought, speech, and emotion into the world of action, especially as you serve in an important community in Israel, which you are surely striving to make a community worthy of the name—a *kehillah kedishah*. We have been promised that "one who comes to purify [and according to the precision of the Alter Rebbe, author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*—not only to purify oneself, but also to purify others] is assisted."

With respect and blessing,

P.S. You were very generous with your praise in your letter, and surely, as mentioned above, the intention is toward the teachings of Chassidus and its matters. May it be the will of Hashem that each of us merits to be a sponge and a conduit for its teachings and directives, and that, together with this, the words should come from the heart, for then they enter the heart.

***

**Regarding the statement of our Sages:** *Kiddushin* 40b.

**And we have been promised... precision:** *Yoma* 38b; *Likutei Torah*, *Drushim* for *Shemini Atzeres* 88b.

## 8543

B"H, 12 MarCheshvan, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

May it be the will of Hashem that, in accordance with the well-known interpretation at the beginning of this week’s parsha—after which the entire parsha is named—the strength inherent in the general command "Lech Lecha" will be revealed within each and every one of us among the Jewish people. May each person fulfill this command with joy and a glad heart:

**Lech Lecha** (Go for yourself) **me'artzecha** (from your land—from your earthliness and materiality);

**U'mimoladtecha** (and from your birthplace—from the matters in which you were raised and to which you are accustomed);

**U'mibeis avicha** (and from your father’s house—the nature of your animal soul from birth);

**El ha'aretz asher areka** (to the land that I will show you)—specifically from Above, for "one cannot stand upon it, and one cannot know the power of that land, for it is deep and hidden."

And may all that is stated immediately thereafter be fulfilled in practice:

**Va'asecha** (And I will make you)... **v'hayei beracha** (and you shall be a blessing)—the ultimate elevation, until one becomes a blessing himself, a source of blessing, and one who blesses the Jewish people.

**V'nivrechu becha kol mishpechos ha'adamah** (And all the families of the earth shall be blessed through you)—that his portion in the world is also clarified and blessed, to the point that "strangers shall stand and pasture your flocks," which is their clarification and elevation, until they are blessed and included among the children of Israel.

With blessings for success in the holy work of chinuch,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8546

B"H, 22 MarCheshvan, 5723
Brooklyn.

To the avreich, Yechiel Yitzchak, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh, in which you ask regarding the matter of immersion in a mikveh.

The immense importance of this matter is explained in many places, particularly in connection with the avodah of tefillah. See Likutei Torah by our Rebbe, the author of the Tanya—the decisor in the hidden aspects of Torah—and the Shulchan Aruch—the decisor in the revealed aspects of Torah—in Parshas Tavo, 43b. Furthermore, it is explained in many seforim that the Baal Shem Tov merited the most sublime matters because of the matter of the mikveh. See also the discourses on mikveh by the Mitteler Rebbe, son of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe. Many sources regarding this matter have been collected in the sefer Taharas Yom Tov, Part Yod, page 365 and onwards.

I am sure you are aware of the three daily shiurim—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—which are well-known: 1) To study each day the portion of Chumash with Rashi’s commentary according to the weekly parsha (on Sunday, from the beginning of the parsha until the second aliyah; on Monday, from the second aliyah until the third, etc.); 2) To recite each day, after morning davening, the monthly shiur of Tehillim—as Tehillim is divided for the days of the month; 3) To study each day a shiur of Tanya, as Tanya is divided for the days of the year. In any event, you should keep them from here on in.

With blessings for good tidings in all that was mentioned.

***

**In many seforim:** See Kesser Shem Tov, section 219.

**In the discourses on mikveh by the Mitteler Rebbe:** In Siddur Im Dach, Part 2, 456a and onwards.

## 8547

8547

B"H, 24 Menachem Av, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter of 19 Cheshvan regarding your state of health and the opinion of the doctors.

In general, between the two methods you mention—surgery or radium/electricity (meaning radiation)—one should lean more toward the first option. This is understood to be with the consent of a Rav who is a *moreh hora'ah*. For with radiation, one cannot always predict the outcome, and one is not always certain that the desired result has been secured.

As is the practice in such cases, one must have the decision confirmed by two doctors who are specialists in this field, in addition to the agreement of the Rav, as mentioned above. May Hashem Yisbarach guide you in whatever is best for you in all respects.

Surely you observe the good custom of Jewish women to give to *tzedakah* each time before lighting candles on Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

#### ***8547***

**Your state of health:** Ailments during the menstrual cycle.

## 8,548

8,548

*[24 MarCheshvan, 5723]*

Following a long interval, I received your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, 20 MarCheshvan, the birthday of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe (Rashab), may his soul be in Eden.

For the Holy One, blessed be He, does not deal tyrannically with His creatures, especially according to the concept of Hashgacha Pratis as explained in the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, that it is down to the finest detail, and all the more so regarding matters of Torah and mitzvos. And this is simple to understand. Therefore, you should **increase** your efforts in order to assist the requesting institution as well.

**The Holy One, blessed be He, does not:** Avodah Zarah 3a.

## 8549

B"H, 25 Mar-Cheshvan, 5723
Brooklyn.

To the Avreich, Uri Tzvi, may he live.
Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of the 22nd of Cheshvan.

At an opportune time, I will mention you at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding all the matters you wrote about.

Regarding your question as to what is the way to alleviate the trials and confusions in the path of life of the Bnei Yisrael in this world of ours: it is by living according to our Torah, the Torah of life, and by fulfilling its mitzvos, of which it is said, "and he shall live by them."

Well-known in this regard are the words of our Rabbeinu HaZaken, author of the Tanya and the Shulchan Aruch, that this very fact should arouse one to additional courage to live life according to the instruction of the living G-d, without looking at the trial, difficulty, or suffering. This is achieved by contemplating that surely Hashem does not deal harshly with His creatures, and He only asks of them according to their strength. If a trial has been increased, it is most certainly the case that prior to this, He increased the inner strengths of the one undergoing the trial. However, just as in a victory in physical matters—if one is heavy-hearted, doubts his own strength, and is discouraged, he is liable to be defeated and fall, even if he is stronger than his opponent—therefore, it is emphasized everywhere that it is necessary to serve Hashem with joy and a good heart, and with a strong confidence in the victory of the good and the holy. And it is not always the time for making a cold and dry calculation [and especially a calculation according to the instruction of the nefesh habehamis].

Knowing your father, may he live, from previous letters, and now having met face-to-face, my hope is strong that these few lines will suffice. And in the style of the written word, "Give to the wise and he will become even wiser."

I would like to add one more point, based on what is emphasized everywhere regarding the army: that there must be an addition of holiness there, since one requires the written promise that "Hashem your G-d walks in the midst of your camp to save you, etc." (which is through) "and your camp shall be holy" (Devarim 23:15). Upon this depends the security of the entire group and platoon.

Based on the above, surely you will also have a daily shiur in the study of our holy Torah, with an addition on the day of Shabbos, which is holy to Hashem.

I am certain you will bring me good tidings regarding all the above, and may it be His will that this be very soon.

With blessings for good tidings.

**M. Schneerson**

## 8553

8553

B"H, Erev Shabbos Parshas Toldos, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

As we stand in the week of Parshas Toldos, and in accordance with the well-known dictum, "The deeds of the fathers are a sign for the children," there are many details in this Parsha that can be interpreted and applied as a hint to the life of every single Jew.

Every Jewish person, whether a tzaddik or a rasha, possesses two souls, which are two *nefashos*: one *nefesh* from the side of *kelipah* and *sitra achra*—Esav; and the second *nefesh* is a literal "part of Hashem from above"—Yaakov.

"The first came out, red"—this is Esav, the *nefesh habahamit* and the *yetzer hara*, which "precedes" in its coarseness, and he is a "man of the field," outside the city of our G-d and its sanctity.

And Yaakov, the *nefesh elokit* and the *yetzer hatov*, is a "wholesome man," for even at the time of sin, his faith remains with him. He is a "dweller of tents," as he was commanded not to leave it in a state of chaos, but rather "He created it to be inhabited." This is achieved through his dwelling in the tents—the tents of Shem and Eiver, the tents of the Written Torah and the Oral Torah—for through study, one comes to action, the performance of *mitzvos aseh* and *mitzvos lo taaseh*, which is the main thing, and which creates a dwelling place for Him, may He be blessed, in the lower worlds.

This is why the hand of Yaakov was "grasping the heel of Esav"—for the descent of the *nefesh elokit* below, and its enclothement in the body and the *nefesh habahamit* as mentioned above, is in order to refine them (by fulfilling the command, "Go out to the field and hunt game for me, and make me delicacies") and to make this lowest world, than which there is no lower, a dwelling place for Him, may He be blessed.

And the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov is well known: "When you see the donkey of your enemy... you shall surely help **with him**"—to refine the body and purify it, rather than breaking it through self-affliction.

And as a result of this, "May G-d give you of the dew of the heavens and the fatness of the earth and an abundance of grain and wine," which our Sages explain refers to *Mikra*, *Mishnah*, *Talmud*, *Aggadah*, etc., and according to its literal meaning: the dew of the heavens, the fatness of the earth, and an abundance of grain and wine, etc.

May it be His will that all of this be fulfilled in the life of each and every one even now,

And for the totality of Israel—with the coming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu, when Hashem will expand our borders, leading to the fulfillment of the promise, "And you shall spread out to the west, and to the east, and to the north, and to the south," and we shall be fruitful in the land.

With blessings for good tidings, in general and in particular.

**M. Schneerson**

## 8595

8595

*[8 Kislev 5723]*

...And since I have heard... that the matter is being discussed at a Torah gathering of many, and furthermore, that the time for it is the upcoming night of holy Shabbos, I have therefore, in accordance with the instruction in Shulchan Aruch, felt compelled to respond as soon as possible with what appears to me to be the explanation, albeit briefly, as time permits.

This concerns what I have asked before you from the Zohar (Vol. I, 53b): "‘And He drove out the man’ (Bereishis 3:24). Rabbi Elazar said: I do not know who performed the divorce upon whom... but the word is inverted, and it says ‘He drove out *es* (את) the man.’ *Es* refers precisely to the Shechinah... ‘The man’ certainly drove out *es*. And because of this, it is written, ‘And He sent him away’ from the Garden of Eden. Why ‘And He sent him away’? Because the man drove out *es*."

**There are several** points of precision in the above. The main one is the explanation of Rabbi Elazar’s words, "I do not know..."—for it is difficult to understand, as a verse does not depart from its plain meaning, especially since, according to his conclusion, the word must be inverted, which is not the order of the text.

Also, the doubling of the language in the Zohar, and more.

In brief, this can be understood based on two premises: 
1) In the Zohar, the inner dimension of Torah and the inner nature of matters are revealed, while the external dimension is hinted at. The reverse is true in the Shas, the revealed dimension of Torah. However, since all parts of the Torah are included within one another, one finds simple meanings and halachos in the Zohar, and hints and secrets in the Shas.

2) Regarding punishments (and similarly regarding rewards), there are those that are, in the language of the Jewish philosophers, "natural," or as the verse puts it, "Your wickedness shall discipline you." And there are those that are "segulic" (supernatural/decreed), meaning that it arose in the will of Hashem that for such-and-such a sin, such-and-such a punishment should occur, and it is not necessarily the case that this is a direct consequence or result of the sin. This is similar to the mitzvos categorized as *chukim* and the like.

This is the doubt of Rabbi Elazar: The plain meaning (of the matter and the verse) is certainly that the man was driven out. But regarding the inner dimension of the expulsion (the punishment for the sin of the Tree of Knowledge), "I do not know who performed the divorce upon whom." Is it *HaKadosh Baruch Hu* (that it arose in His will that for the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, *HaKadosh Baruch Hu* would perform the divorce upon man) or not (but rather that *Adam HaRishon himself* performed an act whose "natural" consequence was the expulsion)?

—And although **in general**, the attribute of the Holy One is "measure for measure," in the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, the warning in the verse was death, not expulsion.

The resolution of this doubt comes from the redundant language of the verse, which follows the previous verse: "And He sent him away from the Garden of Eden..." If so, here too it should have said: "And He drove him out and He placed..." The redundancy of the words "the man"—beyond the plain meaning—hints (by inverting the order) at the inner dimension of the matter: that the man drove out *es*. And because **of this** it is written, "And He sent him away..." [which seemingly is not understood at all, for who mentioned "sending away" in the warning of the sin? And if so, why "And He sent him away"? (Rather,)] because the man drove out (and the natural consequence, measure for measure, resulting from this, is—"And He sent him away"). I will not elaborate further.

* * *

Regarding the fact that "es" (את) indicates the Shechinah, and the explanation of the concept of Shechinah: "Es" indicates in every place something that is secondary.

Shechinah is called the level of Elokus that "dwells and is enclothed within all worlds to give them life and sustain them," from the expression "And I will dwell among them." Now, all the worlds together do not occupy any space at all in relation to Him, may He be blessed, for with the letter *Heh* (the final letter) this world was created, and with the *Yud* the World to Come was created. As is explained at length in Tanya. And this is not the essence of Elokus—that He creates worlds. Therefore, this level is called by the name "es."

And based on the above, that the parts of the Torah are included within one another, the matter mentioned above regarding the word "es" also contains a **hint**—that in this word all the letters are hinted at, from their beginning (*Aleph*) to their end (*Tav*). And in general, *es* is also from the word *os* (letter).

For "from my flesh I shall see Eloka": When a person wishes to reveal his will, his intellect, and the like, and to bring them to another, it is through his speech, which is organized and divided into letters (which is why it is said that *os* (letter) is from the expression *ata boker*—the morning comes/appears). And so it is, as it were, above: The creation was through the ten utterances, the revelation of His wisdom, and the will of Hashem—through the Ten Commandments, etc.—

This is the level called Shechinah.

## 8550

B"H, 8 Kislev, 5723

...Regarding your note on Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah, end of section 242, concerning the statement, "If you were like Moshe, Rabbi Akiva would flog you":

1) From Sanhedrin (31b), "He showed him what he had already answered"—this is not a difficulty, since the comparison is made only regarding a single matter or detail, and this is possible. And even on a higher level, etc., as in Menachos (29b), "And he did not know, etc." See also Sanhedrin (11a) and the references noted in the margins.

2) Regarding the expression found in many places, "Moshe, you have spoken well"—this is already resolved by Rashi in Shabbos (101b), who explains that he is "like Moshe in his generation." If so, on the contrary, this is one of the foundations of the Torah, as in Rosh Hashanah, end of chapter 2.

Based on the above, the statement of our Sages in Bereishis Rabbah (17:7), "There is no generation, etc., like Moshe," is also resolved.

However, a difficulty remains from the Tanchuma, end of Parshas Toldos: "And he took from Moshe"—which is stated without qualification, implying in all matters.

(See Rambam, Hilchos Teshuvah 9:2, and see Rosh Hashanah 21b regarding "the kings arose." See also Likutei Torah by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, Tzav 17a, and the end of Shir HaShirim, and the references there to the Arizal.)

#### ***8550***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 6, p. 255. The letter is to R' Yehuda Zarchia Mordechai Leib Chaim Segal.

Additional letters to him—above, Vol. 19, letter 7192, and the references noted in the footnotes there.

**And he took from Moshe:** See also above, Vol. 13, letter 4324; Vol. 4, 9823.

## 8557

8557

B"H, 10 Kislev, the Yom HaGeulah of the Mitteler Rebbe, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the congregation of Yeshurun, lovers and cherishers of Torah and mitzvos, may Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

In connection with the upcoming annual campaign of the Merkaz HaYeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch, on the 24th of Teves, I hope that lovers of Torah in general, and the activists of the yeshiva in particular, will utilize the few remaining weeks to ensure that this undertaking achieves the desired success.

The story is well-known that we heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the Mitteler Rebbe: how he used to be deeply immersed in his learning, and how, as a young man, he was once so absorbed that he did not hear his child fall out of the cradle that stood nearby and begin to cry bitterly. His father, the Alter Rebbe, who was in an upper room and was also immersed in his learning, heard the child’s cry, went downstairs, picked up the child, calmed him, and rocked him back to sleep. Afterward, the Alter Rebbe spoke to his son, explaining that no matter how deeply one is immersed in the highest matters, one must always hear the cry of a Yiddishe kinder.

Since this story was told to us, it is proof that it contains a specific directive for each and every one of us.

The directive is: Unfortunately, there are many Yiddishe kinder today who have fallen out of their "cradles" of Torah and Torah-education, whose souls are crying out and demanding that they be given an education in Torah and mitzvos *al taharas hakodesh*. No matter how busy and immersed each person may be in his own affairs, and no matter how high those matters may be, one must hear the cry and the demand of these children. One must interrupt and pause other things to occupy oneself with them, for there is no higher or more important matter than *chinuch al taharas hakodesh*.

The Lubavitcher yeshivos and educational institutions hear and perceive this call from the Yiddishe kinder, but unfortunately, due to a lack of funds, it is not possible to pick everyone up and bring them back into the cradles of Torah and mitzvos. It is the highest duty of every man and woman to help provide the necessary material assistance to expand the educational institutions. The upcoming annual campaign is the opportunity to do this; and may the Ribono shel Olam help that it be done with all one's heart, with a generous hand, and with joy. And the Ribono shel Olam will bless [the donors] *midah k'neged midah*, many times over, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With respect and blessings for success,

**M. Schneerson**

## 5858

B.H., 14 Kislev, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all the participants, men and women, of the Yud-Tes Kislev farbrengen,
The day of the liberation of our Rebbe, the Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, the festival which "redeemed our souls in peace," and through which the light and vitality of our souls was given to us in Kfar Chabad in our Holy Land—may it be rebuilt and established speedily by Moshiach Tzidkeinu—may Hashem grant them life.

Greetings and blessings!

Though distant in place, I am close in spirit, and I participate in your farbrengen—a farbrengen of words of Torah, words of hisorerus, and the raising of a cup for l’chaim, for life and for blessing.

As this year marks the one hundred and fiftieth anniversary of the histalkus of our Rebbe, I will participate in a special way by sharing a story from his life—a story that contains both conduct and instruction.

***

**The cry of a child.**

Our Rebbe—the Admur HaZaken—lived in a house together with his son (his successor), our Rebbe DovBer, the Mitteler Rebbe. The Mitteler Rebbe was distinguished by powers of concentration, depth, and dveikus like no other. When he was engaged in his studies or his davening, he would feel nothing of what was transpiring around him.

Once, while the Mitteler Rebbe was immersed in his studies, and in a corner of his room stood a cradle with an infant inside, the infant fell from the cradle and began to cry. But the Mitteler Rebbe did not notice a thing.

However, his father, the Admur HaZaken, even though his own apartment was on the upper floor and he too was immersed in his studies at that very moment, heard the child’s cry. He stopped his learning, went down, entered his son’s room, picked up the infant, cared for him, calmed him, and laid him back in the cradle, not moving from there until he saw that his grandson was at peace.

Yet, the Mitteler Rebbe still did not notice his father or his son. Later, at an opportune moment, the Admur HaZaken rebuked his son, explaining that this is not the way—to be so immersed in matters of study and the like, to the point that one does not hear the cry of a child.

***

This story has been passed down from generation to generation, and was transmitted to us in particular by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the Nasi of our generation. Certainly, this story contains practical instructions for these generations, and for us, within Klal Yisrael, in particular. One of the instructions is:

A person must not be so immersed in any matter whatsoever, even the most lofty matter, that he does not hear the cry of a child in his proximity, in his environment, or even at a distance. The cry of a child must reach every single person, and in such a way that the listener stops what he is doing, attends to the crying child, and does everything in his power to fulfill the child’s needs.

In our current era, in particular, there are many infants and children who, for whatever reason, have "fallen from their cradle." They have been disconnected (or were never in one to begin with) from a true Jewish "cradle," and they are crying—whether with a cry that is heard, or with an internal cry that is not heard—out of the distress of their souls. Their soul is a literal "part of Elokus from above," and it is hungry and thirsty for the word of Hashem, for His Torah and His mitzvos, and there is no one to attend to them and fill their lack with an education of pure holiness.

Likewise, there are many of our brothers, the Children of Israel, who, although they are grown in years, are still "small," or even infants, regarding the Torah which is our life and the fulfillment of His mitzvos. And if they do not see or discern this—their *mazal* sees it, and they cry out of a spiritual distress—sometimes they do not even know the source of it; they only feel the terrible emptiness in their lives, lives without any content or purpose worthy of the name.

It is forbidden to turn a deaf ear to the cry of these children of Israel, whether they are children in age or "children" in their knowledge of Torah and mitzvos. To each and every one of you, the instruction, the command, and the order is directed:

Do not sin against the child. Stop any other business of yours, attend to the child, and return him to his Father—our Father, the merciful Father. Let him learn the Torah of our Father and fulfill His mitzvos, and then he will live a life of eternity, a life that is full, complete, and good.

***

And what is the way to calm the child, to return him to his Father, and to fill his lack?

It is the path of the threefold love: Ahavas Yisrael, directed by Ahavas HaTorah, the foundation of both being Ahavas Hashem.

It is a path that leads to constant actions for the true benefit of the other—his benefit in the physical and his benefit in the spiritual.

And it reaches its ultimate goal—to set him on a path of true life, a life according to the Torah of life, illuminated by the light of the wellsprings of Chassidus and permeated with the enthusiasm that is within it.

***

May it be the will that from this farbrengen, and from the farbrengens of Yud-Tes Kislev in other places in the Holy Land and abroad, a call will go out to all our brothers, the Children of Israel—may they live and be well—whose hearts are sensitive to the cry of a child.

A call for vigorous action in spreading Torah in general, and spreading the wellsprings of Chassidus in particular—study and action together, and with enthusiasm, vitality, and light.

With respect and with a blessing for great success in all that has been mentioned—l’chaim, l’chaim and for blessing.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 8549

B"H, 15 Kislev, 5723
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Dovid Nosson, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge with thanks the receipt of the Chanukah candles, as is your good custom each and every year.

They were received in the days close to 19 Kislev, the Rosh Hashanah for the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus.

The common denominator between the two is that the inner dimension of the Torah in our generation has been revealed through the teachings of Chassidus—the *razin d'oraysa* (secrets of the Torah), the oil of the Torah—whose point is to spread the *ma'ayanos* (fountains) and to illuminate, until they shine even in the *reshus harabim* (public domain). This is analogous to the teaching of our Sages regarding the Beis Hamikdash, that its windows were specifically "wide on the inside and narrow on the outside," and this has been drawn down into the Chanukah candles, which must be lit specifically at the entrance of one's house, facing outward.

This order is likewise reflected in the inner dimension of the Torah: initially, it was for the select few, and subsequently, the matter became a *mitzvah* to reveal this wisdom, in accordance with the ways of the Arizal, the living [teachings], and as brought in the *Tanya Kaddisha* by our Rebbe, the author of the *Simcha* and the *Geulah* of 19 Kislev, extending to the spreading of the *ma'ayanos chutzah* (fountains outward), and this is well understood.

May it be the will that each and every one of us fulfills all three details: 1) in the manner of *hafatzah* (spreading), 2) the *ma'ayanos* (fountains), 3) until they reach—also—*chutzah* (outward), and all this with *simcha* (joy), *chayus* (vitality), and *hislahavus* (enthusiasm).

With blessings for a *Chag HaGeulah* and for illuminating Chanukah candles.

**P.S.** As I have spoken and as is based on the words of the Zohar, I have emphasized this in connection with the Chanukah candle.

## 8561

[22 Kislev 5723]

...As we stand in the days between 19 Kislev, the "Day of Good Tidings," and the days of Chanukah—

And especially in this year, where the beginning of the week, Sunday, is 19 Kislev, and its conclusion is the completion of the seven days of the **cycle**—Shabbos Chanukah—and the principle is known that (in holiness) "their end is embedded in their beginning, and their beginning in their end"—

We must explain the common denominator between the days of Chanukah and 19 Kislev.

The miracle of Chanukah occurred with oil—which alludes to the *pnimiyus haTorah* (the inner dimension of Torah)—for the lamps of the Sanctuary, which were located in the *Heichal*, a place not everyone could enter, and the time for their lighting was during the day.

In the days of Mattisyahu ben Yochanan Kohen Gadol and his sons, who displayed *mesiras nefesh* for the sanctification of Hashem’s name—the true *yichud*, as the Sages say, "With all your soul, even if He takes your soul"—the miracle occurred. Through this, they were commanded regarding the Chanukah lamps, whose *mitzvah* is to be lit by every single individual (*nefesh*), at the entrance of his house from the outside (*olam*), and specifically after the sun has set (*shanah*).

All these matters apply likewise to the study of *pnimiyus haTorah*—the "oil of Torah."

Initially, it was hidden and concealed from all but the most select few, and even then, it was studied privately, not in public. But in these latter generations, it is a *mitzvah* to reveal it—beginning in the days of the Arizal and so on—until the redemption of 19 Kislev, which marked the beginning of the essential work of spreading the wellsprings outward, until every person can understand and grasp how "He fills all worlds and He encompasses all worlds," and so on.

May it be the will of Hashem that each of us acts in this regard, in all three details: 1) in the manner of *hafatzah* (dissemination), 2) the wellsprings themselves, 3) until it reaches even the "outside,"

And may this be done with vitality and light, in a manner of "increasing and continuing to shine."

## 8562

B"H, 26 Kislev, 5723
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, engaged in communal needs, R' Moshe Zev שי', HaLevi.

Peace and blessing!

... Thank you, thank you for [visiting] the gravesite of the Gaon, the Yaavetz. See *Pri Etz Chaim*, *Shaar HaShabbos*, chapter 21, and in the *Siddur* of the Arizal regarding before *Mincha* of Shabbos, that this is how the **early authorities** (*ha-kadmonim*) were accustomed to act. And in *Taamei HaMitzvos*, *Va'eschanan*, it is stated that the Arizal would study six paths in *Halacha* corresponding to the six days of the week, and one [path] according to the *sod* (mystical) approach, corresponding to the day of Shabbos.

***

**R' Moshe Zev שי':** Gringlas, Montreal. Additional letters to him: see above, 8368, and the references in the footnotes there.

**On the gravesite of the Gaon, the Yaavetz:** In his letter: R' Yaakov Zilberman שי', a *Sofer STaM*, showed me what he recently found in the glosses and novellae on *Gittin* (in the large Shas editions, Vilna format) by the Gaon R' Yaakov Emden, of blessed memory, on page 60a, regarding Rabbi Yochanan and Reish Lakish studying the *Sefer D'Agadta*. His language there is as follows: "It seems to me that the book of *Etz Chaim* (or *Eitz HaDaas*?) and the wisdom of truth, which we call *Kabbalah*, were not studied on weekdays except for [matters of] laws and *halachos*, to know what one must do in Israel. On Shabbos, they would not occupy themselves with laws and *halachos*, as they are difficult to master—similar to what we say, 'One does not review [new material] on Shabbos'—because they are weighty. Instead, on Shabbos, they would study words of *Aggadah*, which draws the heart, because the *Oneg Shabbos* and the holiness of the day assist one in perceiving and understanding the hidden wisdom. It is holy of holies. And they said, 'Do you wish to know the One who spoke and the world came into being? Study *Aggadah*.' And this is not the *Aggadah* of mere stories, which is spelled with a *hei* (*Haggadah*)."

End quote. And seemingly, this is a proof for what is brought in the *Kuntres Etz Chaim*, that on holy Shabbos, the day is dedicated to the study of *Chassidus*.

## 8,563

[Kislev 5723]

...Regarding your observation on the Tosafos (s.v. *lemi'ut*, Chullin 140a) which raises a doubt regarding an animal from an *Ir HaNidachas* that one transgressed and consecrated and then offered as a sacrifice—whether it is a valid offering—the difficulty is that it must be referring to an animal belonging to *tzadikim*.

(For the animals of *resha'im* are disqualified in any event because of *Zivchay Resha'im To'evah* — Sanhedrin 112b. However, it could be said that Tosafos holds like the Ra'avad in *Hilchos Avodas Kochavim* 4:13, that the prohibition does not take effect.) And since he offered it—meaning it is in Jerusalem—the property of *tzadikim* that is outside the city is saved.

It may be suggested (and this also resolves the seemingly superfluous language in Tosafos) that they wrote and specified "**transgressed** (*avar*)" and consecrated it, meaning that the act of consecration occurred through a transgression, after the *gmar din* (final verdict) when the animal was within the city, and he offered it afterward in Jerusalem—for since the people who left the *Ir HaNidachas* are not saved by that, and it is said regarding them, "You shall surely strike" (Sifri, Re'eh 13:16), then all the more so for an animal. Another possibility is that since at the time he consecrated it he **transgressed**—it was already designated for burning at that time—consecration does not take effect on an animal [destined for] burning. Based on this, it requires further study whether this involves the prohibition of offering *chullin* in the *Azarah*, or whether it is not even considered *chullin*. Perhaps one could connect this to the clarification of what the prohibition actually is: offering *chullin* as implied by the word "yours" (*shelcha* — Kiddushin 57b) in the *Azarah*, or [is it prohibited because] it is not *hekdesh*? But this is not the place to elaborate.

## 8,464

By the grace of Hashem,
The Eve of the Ner Hashem of Chanukah, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal affairs, a man of noble character, a branch of a sturdy tree, etc., R’ Sh. Z. Shazar, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

After a very long hiatus, I received your letter from the eve of the auspicious day, 19 Kislev, the Rosh Hashanah of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus—

Which, according to my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, and in the words of his father, the Rebbe [Rashab], its purpose is "to draw down the inwardness of Torah and mitzvos, and the inwardness and essence of the Ein Sof, Baruch Hu, so that it should shine within the inwardness of the soul, until our entire existence is directed toward Him, Yisbarach, alone." And it is worth noting that anyone familiar with the spiritual path of the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory, knows that his entire being was immersed in inwardness and essence. Yet, when he mentions the "inwardness of the soul," he immediately adds the clarification, "until our entire **existence** [is directed toward Him]... meaning the essence **and the manifestation**," for the body in relation to the soul is like the manifestation to the essence.

Therefore, I have strong hope that by the time you receive this letter, your health will have improved, and you will share good news in this regard. This is especially so since you wrote your letter on the eve of that auspicious day, and this response is being written during the days of Chanukah. Both of these—the day and the festival—have the purpose of spreading the "lamp of the mitzvah and the light of Torah," in a manner of "increasing and continuing," adding light each and every day. An increase in spiritual light brings about an increase in physical matters, for Yisrael is one nation in the land that unites the spiritual and the physical. This includes the health of the body, as is known from the saying of the Maggid—whose yahrtzeit is 19 Kislev—that "a small hole in the body makes a large hole in the soul," and therefore, the health of the body is "among the ways of Hashem."

Regarding what you wrote, that you are considering publishing a collection in connection with the 150th anniversary of the passing of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe: you have correctly surmised that I would be pleased by this. In fact, it is more than just "pleased." I only hope and pray for all those participating in this collection that all the maamarim included will be entirely consistent with the teachings of the Alter Rebbe. His Torah is not merely theoretical; it is, primarily, a "Torah of life," providing guidance for daily life in actual practice. If that is the case, I will be able to express my satisfaction not only in a letter to you personally, but also publicly.

I was particularly pleased to read at the end of your letter that you are participating in the distribution of the Alter Rebbe’s books, both the Tanya and the Shulchan Aruch. According to what is explained in several places regarding the halachic ruling in such a case—even according to the perspective of the "world of the mitnagdim"—the one who participates is considered as if he himself had studied and completed all the books.

And last but not least, many thanks for the good news regarding the restoration of the resting places (tziyunim) in Haditch and Nizhyn.

Naturally, I look forward to the results of the conference’s efforts to arrange for the absorption of young religious immigrants—practical actions. May it be His will that in this, too, the approach will be according to the instruction of the Torah, that every single Jewish man and woman is a "believer, the child of believers." In the words of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, in Chapter 24 of the Tanya, even at the time of sin, they were **in faith** with Him. From this, it follows that **all** the children of Israel—and certainly the youth, who are included in this—are **religious**. Especially since they are immigrants, for an aliyah is surely "from below to above and from left to right," because the opposite direction is, G-d forbid, a descent.

With blessings for Chanukah—for an increase in light from day to day, in both the spiritual and the physical, and for good tidings in good health, with joy and a glad heart, and with appreciation.

You have surely received my letters over this time, along with the enclosures, even though you did not confirm receipt. Enclosed is what was recently sent to you.

## 8565

B"H, Chanukah, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the avreich engaged in labor, Mr. Avraham, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

It was a pleasure to learn of your meeting with the working youth—not only with their counselors, but also with the members themselves—and of your efforts to bring them closer to traditional Yiddishkeit.

It is well known how positively our holy Torah—called "Toras Chayim" because it provides instruction for daily life, for a life worthy of the name—views labor in general and the laborer in particular. Our Sages of blessed memory spoke at length on this, as is recounted regarding the first Jew, Avraham, who was one. When he would travel through various lands and see the local inhabitants eating, drinking, and acting frivolously, he would say, "May I have no portion in this land." But when he arrived in Eretz Yisrael and saw them busy weeding during the time of weeding and hoeing during the time of hoeing, he said, "May my portion be in this land." The Ribono shel Olam then said to him, "To your seed I will give this land" (Bereishis Rabbah, ch. 39:8).

This is especially true regarding Eretz Yisrael, the Holy Land, as our Sages of blessed memory expounded on the verse, "When you come to the land and you shall plant" (Vayikra 19:23). This teaches that one must first engage in the matter of labor and planting, so that through this, one becomes similar to the Ribono shel Olam, who was the first planter: "From the beginning of the creation of the world, the Ribono shel Olam occupied Himself only with planting first, as it is written, 'And Hashem planted a garden in Eden.' So too, when you enter the land, occupy yourselves only with planting first" (Vayikra Rabbah, Kedoshim, ch. 25:3). Everything here is precise: the essence of planting is that it is something that produces fruit, and the great value of labor lies in this—that it should produce fruit, and fruit that produces fruit.

In a general sense, this is the concept of **"In all your ways know Him"** (Mishlei 3:6)—that a Jew must sanctify all his affairs, including the matters of his work, and especially in the Holy Land. If this is the task of every individual, it is all the more so the task of the working youth, who are gifted with an extra measure of energy and are just entering the path of life.

May it be the will of Hashem that you and your colleagues, may they live, act in this regard according to the instruction of the days of Chanukah: "adding and increasing, adding and increasing in light."

With warm regards to all the aforementioned, may they live, and with blessings for success and good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8,566

B"H, Chanukah, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Yaakov Glis, may he live and be well,

Shalom and blessings!

Through the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing man, whose work is the work of Heaven, a man of energy and fine character, etc., R' Aharon Mordechai Zilberstrom, I received your book, "Neighborhoods in Jerusalem." Many thanks for your thoughtfulness.

As we find ourselves in the days of Chanukah, when the mitzvah is to kindle the lights at the entrance of one's home from the outside, and in a manner that "increases and adds," may it be the will of Hashem that each of us, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, do everything in our power to spread the true light—the "mitzvah is a candle and the Torah is light"—in a manner of "ascending in holiness." This is also the core point of the teachings of Chassidus, which is founded upon the three loves: love of Hashem, love of Torah, and love of Yisrael, and based on the motto of the famous letter of the Baal Shem Tov: "May your springs spread outward."

The precision and emphasis here are: 1) Spreading it in a place that the Torah testifies is still "outward" (chutza); 2) Spreading the **springs** specifically—the source of living waters in their purity; 3) And not merely by hint, or drop by drop, but in a manner of **spreading** and abundant flow. And since the Holy One, Blessed be He, does not act tyrannically with His creatures and only asks according to the strength of each individual, it follows that the demand of the Torah is within one's capacity; furthermore, the command of the Creator is also the provision of strength.

With respect and blessings,

***

## 8568

B”H, 3 Teves, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Shlomo Tal
Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established

Peace and Blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 27th of Kislev, as well as the previous one, along with the enclosures. It goes without saying that I am in complete agreement with you regarding the immense necessity to engage in education that is purely holy. If this was always the case, it is all the more so in our days, in which two primary differences have been added: on one hand, we must fill the deep void left after the decrees and the destruction of a third of our people, the Children of Israel; and on the other hand, we must take advantage of the spiritual awakening in general, and among the youth in particular—an awakening to search for and seek the truth, even if some of them do not yet know what they are seeking, while others already recognize the need to return to the sources.

Great is the one who acts and causes others to act in education specifically, as every positive change in the youth influences their entire life. In connection with this, I am enclosing a copy of a sicha regarding the obligation to listen to the voice of a crying child.

Regarding the content of your letter, it is understood that when our shluchim visit the countries you mention, they will endeavor to meet with those you write about, as is their custom to meet with local activists, even though until now these countries were not included in the itinerary due to the distance and other reasons.

Since we have just come from the days of Chanukah, I will express my blessing and hope that each and every one, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, will act and increase in the "mitzvah candle and Torah light," without compromises and by rejecting even the touch of a stranger. This is also a lesson from the days of Chanukah: when they came to light the Menorah, there was olive oil, but it was oil that had been touched by the hand of a stranger, and therefore it was impure for Jews. The analogy is understood, and unfortunately, it is also a matter of great relevance to our time.

With respect and blessing for good tidings.

#### ***8568***

**Copy of a sicha:** Regarding the voice of a crying child—see above, letter 8557, and the references in the notes there.

With respect and blessing.

## 5771

5771

B"H, 4 Teves, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Zalman Maschari
Kfar Azar

Shalom u’Bracha!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 3 Kislev, especially after several of anash told me of your assistance to Kfar Chabad since its founding and throughout the days of its development. For this reason, I was confident that you would continue along this path, and my confidence was strengthened upon receiving your letter.

It is my hope that, just as with all matters of goodness and holiness we are commanded to elevate in holiness and in a manner of "increasing and continuing," so too will the assistance to Kfar Chabad be, and the village, for its part, will continue to increase in the abundance of its light, in accordance with the inner point of Chabad’s activities in every place—and especially in our Holy Land, may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

I read with special interest your proposals regarding the development of the village, and primarily regarding the establishment of a second Kfar Chabad. I have been in negotiations regarding this matter for some time, and surely you are also aware of the matter, although, to my regret, **the majority** of it is delayed until now due to reasons beyond my control. Especially since, according to the plan I proposed more than two years ago, the time should have already arrived to be concerned about a third Kfar Chabad. And even with the consolation that everything is through Hashgacha Pratis, etc., I will admit—and I am not ashamed—that for me, this is less than "half a consolation," and I will not dwell on this distressing matter. But my hope in this has not yet been lost, **Chas V’Shalom**.

Based on what is known to you regarding the approach and conduct of the people of Chabad, my lines below will surely not surprise you. It is an expression of hope that you will utilize your influence within the Histadrut and wherever your reach extends to instill the eternal values of the Jewish people, which are written and transmitted in our holy Torah, both the Written and the Oral. And according to the instruction of our Sages, of blessed memory, "The study is not the essential thing, but the deed"—the fulfillment of the mitzvos of the Torah in actual practice in daily life. And we have been promised that words that come from the heart enter the heart and accomplish their effect.

With respect and blessing.

## 8572

B"H, 4 Teves, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Avraham Krinitzi
Shalom and Blessing!

I have been informed by Anash that you are celebrating your seventy-fifth birthday, may you have long days and good years. I would like to wish you all the best. As we have discussed, the concept of "good" is first and foremost manifest goodness, proper health, and so on. Yet, at the same time, the Jewish people are "one nation on earth" that unites physicality and spirituality as one, and "there is no good but Torah." May it be the will of Hashem that, from a state of proper health and with the appropriate energy, you utilize your influence to make your city a place of Torah in every detail and nuance.

To paraphrase the verse: "Avraham was one, and he inherited the city."

In closing, as in my opening, I wish you a year of success and productive avodah, along with my thanks for your assistance with the affairs of Chabad, in which you will surely continue to increase and grow.

With respect and blessing.

## 8595

B"H, 11 Teves, 5723
Brooklyn.

To the Avreich, Uri Tzvi, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from the second day of Chanukah, in which you write about the life in your current environment, the particular difficulties therein, etc.

It is surprising, as it seems you do not recognize at all the positive points within them. This is especially understood in light of the well-known saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that when the promise of the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu is fulfilled, people will "clutch their heads" (placing their hands on their heads with great feelings of sorrow and regret) over the days and the best period at the end of the time of Galus. These were times when they could have accomplished through Torah and mitzvos by overcoming all the concealments and hiddenness of that time—for then, the avodah is more pleasant and dear, both to the one performing the avodah and to the One who commanded the avodah, the Creator and Guide of the world. This is unlike the time when the spirit of impurity will pass from the earth and there will be no opposition, etc. The lesson from this for your situation is simple.

Another point regarding the above, and this too is fundamental, is what you mention in your letter: that you are in a setting where the only things that matter are "discipline, strength, and feet" (physical presence). Yet, this is one of the foundations of a person’s faith—simple faith, specifically—whose essence is the precedence of *naaseh* (action) to *nishma* (understanding/discipline). It is the absolute trust that the One who gives the mitzvah provides, from the outset, the **strength** and the possibility to fulfill the command, provided that one desires it and, in practice, **walks** in the path of Hashem, as per the testament of the first Hebrew, Avraham: "For I have known him, to the end that he may command his children... and they shall keep the way of Hashem, to do tzedakah and justice" (*Bereishis* 18:19).

Now, it is the nature of man—for "man is born a wild ass"—to conduct himself specifically according to his own nature: to fulfill his own desires, and even his own cravings. Furthermore, this desire biases his intellect and invents explanations, reasons, and justifications. The remedy for this is *kal v'chomer*: If regarding the commands of flesh and blood, one is compelled—as you write in your letter—to have discipline, strength, and physical presence, and moreover, the entire maintenance of the framework in which you are situated, and through this the existence of the entire army, the guarding of the borders, etc., etc., depends on it—meaning that it affects the fate of the entire population—how much more so is this true regarding the command of the "Supreme Commander," the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, for every single one of the Children of Israel is part of the "armies of Hashem."

And a third point, which is also fundamental—and perhaps the most important of all three—is that it is highly doubtful whether you would have the possibility to influence an environment in need of the knowledge of Hashem, Torah, and mitzvos, as you have now. After all, you are together throughout the entire day, and you are bound by a framework of discipline, etc., as mentioned above. When one speaks words that come from the heart, and the content of the speech is the Torah of truth and its mitzvos—eventually, "truth will sprout from the earth."

These few lines are written in proportion to the importance of the matter in general, and especially the importance that you **utilize** the possibility that Divine Providence has given you to return many of our brethren, the young men—who will soon be settling into family life—to the good and straight path, the path of Torah and mitzvos. The improvement of the situation of each one is multiplied in the future many times over, by the number of family members, their children, and their children's children until the end of all time. Along with the possibility and the command, the Holy One, Blessed be He—who does not deal tyrannically with His creatures—also grants the strength to fulfill the task. And if you will say—this is also the lesson of the days of Chanukah, for our Sages, of blessed memory, testify that they were weak and few against the strong and many, yet they decided with firmness and fought for purity, the mitzvos, and the engagement in Torah. Therefore, a great salvation and deliverance was wrought for them, in such a way that from then on, and every year, we light candles, specifically in a manner of "increasing and adding" from day to day amidst the darkness of the night that surrounds us.

With blessings for success in your holy work mentioned above, and with joy and a glad heart.

**M. Schneerson**

## 8576

B"H, 13 Teves, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. A. Friedman, may he live,
Chairman of the Religious Council, Be'er Sheva, may it be built and established,

Peace and blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter of 14 Kislev, and I enjoyed reading about the success of the Chabad Chassidus evening that was held in your city. And as with every matter of Torah, regarding which our Sages of blessed memory said, "The essential thing is not the study, but the deed," my hope is that the hisorerus that emerged from this Chabad evening will be tangible, leading to practical matters in accordance with the instruction of Chabad Torah and its approach, which demands "and therefore" (*uvchen*), purpose, and the drawing down of every good matter from the world of thought and speech to the world of action in actual reality.

Regarding your writing about the establishment of a vocational yeshiva in your city, it is understood that this is a matter for which you should turn to the *anash* activists in the Holy Land, may it be built and established, especially since, according to the information here, there are several yeshivos in Be'er Sheva, the City of the Patriarchs, and perhaps they are not of the type you are writing about.

Since I see that you are the Chairman of the Religious Council, and everything is through *hashgacha pratis*—and "the Holy One, Blessed be He, does not come with complaints against His creatures"—it follows that along with your appointment, you were certainly given the strengths and ability to fulfill your role as required. I express my hope that you will utilize them to their fullest in all religious matters in Be'er Sheva. We are promised that one who comes to purify himself (and according to the precision of the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch—on the 24th of this month, three jubilees will be completed since his passing-hillula—also to purify others) is assisted, in addition to the merit of the many which assists him.

With respect and blessing.

## 8577

B"H, 15 Teves, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of Wednesday, in which you ask regarding certain matters of Torah, mitzvos, yiras shamayim, etc., and the opinion of your parents (may they live and be well) regarding this.

It is to be hoped that your parents will not interfere in the matters mentioned above. As is well known, the din Torah regarding this is based on the explicit verse, "Every man shall fear his mother and his father, and you shall keep My Shabbos" (see Yevamos 5b and the poskim cited there).

2) Regarding your question on the interpretation of the holy Tanya, end of Chapter 11, "Therefore our Sages of blessed memory said, etc."

The continuation is that since even a *rasha v'ra lo* possesses good (it is just that his good stands in the category of *makif*), therefore, "when ten are gathered, the Shechinah rests among them" (see Tanya, end of Chapter 35, regarding the precision of the term **sharia**), even with ten Jews of any sort, even the lowest *rasha v'ra lo*.

It is to be hoped that you have a set time for the study of the inner dimension of Torah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus—a set time every day, with an increase on the day of Shabbos, which is holy to Hashem.

With blessings for good news in all the above.

## 8578

B"H, 15 Teves, 5723
Brooklyn.

And if everyone is obligated to do more and more in this, it is especially incumbent upon those whose lineage and the rock from which they were hewn obligate and privilege them to do so. Surely, further elaboration on this is unnecessary, and the merit of the many will assist you.

With respect and blessing.

## 8579

B"H, 15 Teves, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

As we stand in the parshiyos of the week, the conclusion of Sefer Bereishis—which is called *Sefer HaYashar* (the Book of the Upright), because the deeds of the upright, Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov, are written within it—

It is understood and simple that the intention is not merely a historical narrative, G-d forbid, regarding the deeds of the Patriarchs, but rather a lesson and instruction for each and every individual. As our Sages of blessed memory state, "The deeds of the Patriarchs are a sign for the children."

May it be the will that each and every one of us, within the collective of Klal Yisrael, acts according to the three lines of the three Patriarchs: the line of *gemilus chasadim* (acts of kindness), which is the *avodah* of Avraham Avinu; the line of *avodah* and *tefillah*, the *avodah* of Yitzchak Avinu; and the line of *Torah*, the *avodah* of Yaakov Avinu.

And this should be done with *taanug* and *chayus* specifically—despite the matters of the world (*olam*, related to *helem*—concealment) which limit, conceal, and constrict.

On the contrary, through the constriction itself, one should add *chayus*.

As it is at the beginning of this week’s parsha, "And Yaakov lived"—the synthesis of all the Patriarchs—in the land of Mitzrayim.

To do what is upright in the eyes of Hashem, and the reward of a *mitzvah* is a *mitzvah*—"The upright shall behold His countenance," the fulfillment of the promise that "eye to eye they shall see"—with the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**
