## 5181

By the Grace of Hashem, Wednesday, Parshas Vaeira, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the annual dinner of Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch,
May Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

The annual event of Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch takes place this year on the auspicious day of 24 Teves, the yahrtzeit-hilula of the Alter Rebbe, Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, the founder of the Chabad-Lubavitch movement, *shita*, and way of life.

Of special significance is the fact that this day marks 150 years since his passing, and that the *kevius* (the calendar configuration)—both regarding the day of the week and the weekly parsha—is exactly the same as it was on the day of his passing.

It is therefore certain to hope that all participants in this gathering will unite with the spirit of the *baal-hilula*. This will find expression in the appropriate response—from each one of them—to the call of the yeshiva, thereby achieving the maximum success for this endeavor, both in *ruchniyus* and in *gashmiyus* (financially).

* * *

One of the final writings that the Alter Rebbe wrote shortly before his passing, and possibly **the very last** (known by its opening words as *Nefesh HaShfelah*), contains the task and primary *avodah* of a Jew in these current generations: to learn and disseminate Torah, to engage in *gemilus chasadim* and *tzedakah* with *kiruv hadaas* (fostering closeness between Jews), and to accept everything *b'ahavah* and *l'shuv ad Hashem* (to return to Hashem).

These three things—learning and disseminating Torah, *gemilus chasadim*, and *l'shuv ad Hashem*—must be founded upon, and indeed reflect, the three loves: *ahavas Hashem*, *ahavas haTorah*, and *ahavas Yisrael*, which are the foundations of the education in the Lubavitcher yeshivos:

Learning Torah together with *hafatzas haTorah*: **"To learn and to teach... with love"**—to learn oneself and also to learn with others, and both **with love**.

*Gemilus chasadim* (*tzedakah*) of the students and those educated in the Lubavitcher yeshivos, which is expressed especially in their readiness and *mesiras nefesh* to strengthen and spread Yiddishkeit even to the most remote corners of the world.

*L'shuv ad Hashem*—the *avodah* of *tefillah*: showing how to daven and "learning" how to daven, revealing and strengthening the connection of a Jewish heart with the Ribono shel Olam.

* * *

The *askanim*, friends, and supporters of the Tomchei Temimim yeshivos—in addition to their personal obligations in these three areas—have the great *zechus* of acquiring a share in the accomplishments of the yeshivos through their efforts for the strengthening and expansion of the yeshivos—with their money, time, and effort to also draw their friends and acquaintances to all of this.

* * *

The Alter Rebbe, the *baal-hilula*, said: "Hashem gives us *gashmiyus*, so that we may make *ruchniyus* out of it."

May it be the will of Hashem that He, with His generous hand, give to everyone, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, everything they need, and may everyone make *ruchniyus* out of their *gashmiyus* through authentic Yiddishkeit, Torah and *mitzvos* in general, and through engaging in kosher *chinuch* in particular—by, as written above, helping the Lubavitcher yeshivos free themselves from the burden of debt and expand their work in accordance with the ever-growing need and demand for it.

With respect and with a blessing for success in all that has been mentioned,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 8582

B”H, 24 Teves, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

The day of the Hilula of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 12 Teves, along with the *pidyon nefesh* which will be read at a time of favor at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Generally, in matters such as these, every year the events return to their original state, just as they were the first time. This is all the more true when the calendar alignment corresponds to this, both regarding the days of the week and the *parsha* of the week.

According to the well-known directive of our Rebbe, the Baal HaHilula, one must “live with the *parsha* of the week and the *parsha* of the day.”

This is consistent with the words of his sons, of blessed memory, that at the time of his passing, “he was bound in a single knot with the Holy One, blessed be He.”

And it is a known legal ruling of our Torah that “the body follows the head.”

And although who is he, and where is he, whose heart would dare approach to grasp even one-thousandth of his level—and if in the laws of *Orach Chaim*, which are revealed to us and our children, his ways were as far above our ways as the Holy of Holies is above the mundane, then *kal v’chomer* regarding the “hidden things to Hashem our G-d,” which are the *dichilu* and *rechimu* (fear and love) of the mind and heart, etc.

Nevertheless, a small portion and a mere glimmer of his great goodness and light shines forth, for “when he departs, he is present even more than in his lifetime,” especially for all those who desire and resolve to walk in the straight path that he taught us.

May that “single knot” with which he is bound to the Holy One, blessed be He, influence the *avodah* of the mind and heart of each person—namely, in a general sense, the *avodah* of *tefillah*, and through this, the study of Torah and the fulfillment of *mitzvos*. For *tefillah* is like the spinal cord, which sustains and maintains all of these, as is explained at length in the teachings of the Baal HaHilula.

May all this be accompanied by that which is found “even more” in the blessing regarding worldly matters as well—amidst health, joy, and a good heart.

With blessings for good tidings in general and in particular,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8583

25 Teves, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of Yeshivas Kiryat Gat, affiliated with Yeshivas Tomchei-Temimim,
May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom u’Bracha,

Thank you for the news regarding the progress and development of the Yeshivah. It is my hope that, in accordance with the directive of our holy Torah to "ascend in matters of holiness," you will continue to add strength and vigor to increase the pace of its development. Great is the merit of each and every person who participates in supporting its growth, to be blessed measure for measure—and indeed, many times over—with the measure of the Ribono shel Olam, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

Since we are currently following the auspicious day of 24 Teves, the Hillula of Rabbeinu HaZaken, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch—who this year marks 150 years since his passing—I wish to emphasize on this occasion that Rabbeinu HaZaken was a living example, even in his private life (if one may say so), of everything he taught and contemplated in his Torah, even before he was revealed as a leader and Nasi in Yisrael. Regarding our current subject, three main points should be noted: the matter of helping others, which in its general sense is the pillar of tzedakah; the dissemination of Torah, both the revealed Torah and the inner dimensions of Torah; and the "central bolt" that connects these two matters, which is chinuch according to Torah on the foundation of purity. Through this, both the dissemination of Torah and the matter of tzedakah are achieved as one: spiritual tzedakah provided to the students, and tzedakah in its literal sense of *tomchin d’oraysa* (supporting those who study Torah).

In these fundamental matters, he was an extraordinary living example, as is known from the story of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, author of the Hillula on the upcoming 10th of Shevat, based on family tradition: that even before his marriage, Rabbeinu HaZaken stipulated that he would be able to use his dowry as he saw fit. Immediately after the wedding, he dedicated the dowry to a relief fund and gemach for Jews in matters of livelihood, particularly for those who, following his suggestion, began to engage in agricultural work and the like. This is tzedakah in its literal sense. Regarding the dissemination of Torah, his efforts in teaching Torah to the masses are well known, both to great Torah scholars and to simple people, and he concerned himself with the chinuch of the sons and daughters of Yisrael.

(It also appears that he intended to begin his book *Likutei Amarim*, the Tanya, with the section called "Chinuch Katan," but for hidden reasons, it was printed as the second part of his book.)

However, in truth, the greatness of his stature is known—who among us can compare to him? Yet, each person, according to his own capacity, must be stirred by the power of his deeds to follow in his footsteps with actual deeds, each to the greatest extent of his ability. The Yeshivah is a channel and a vessel to fulfill all of the above in actual practice. Through this, as Rabbeinu HaZaken writes in his book *Torah Or* at the beginning of Parshas Bereishis, "Tzedakah exalts a nation"—which refers to the totality of Hashem’s blessings in everything that is needed for each and every one of you and your families, may they live, from soul to body.

With respect and blessing for success and good news,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8586

With respect and blessing.

## 8587

B"H, 10th of Shevat, the day of the Hilula of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe.

Brooklyn, N.Y.

5723 — The 150th year of the Hilula of the Alter Rebbe.

Greetings and blessings!

As we stand on the day of the Hilula of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi of Israel, may it be the will [of Hashem] that this auspicious day influence each and every one to act in each of the three pillars — Torah, Avodah (tefillah), and Gemilas Chasadim — as instructed by the Baal HaHilula, with actions permeated by light, chayos, and Chassidishe hispaalus.

And it is understood that in these actions, the inner point is the dissemination of the wellsprings outward (hafatzas hamaayanos chutzah).

For this is the path to the fulfillment of the promise in the Iggeres HaKodesh of the Baal Shem Tov, that when his wellsprings spread outward, the Master, King Moshiach, will come.

May it be speedily in our days, amen.

With blessings for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***8587***

General details. Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 11, p. 233, and completed according to a photocopy of the letter.

**Letter:** Igros Kodesh of the Alter Rebbe, Vol. 1, Letter 38.

**In the letter:** Igros Kodesh of the Rebbe Rayatz, Vol. 4, Letter 890.

**Auspicious day:** See the letter of the Alter Rebbe upon his return from P.B. (as this year is the 150th year of his passing): "However, it is necessary to make known that on the day of the passing of our great master, the Maggid, the great Hilula, on that very day I was set free." See further at length in the letter of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe (Sefer HaMaamarim Kuntreisim, Vol. 2, p. 450 [403b]).

**Each and every one... of Torah:** See Hilchos Talmud Torah by the Alter Rebbe, end of Chapter 1; Hilchos Birchos HaShachar, end of Chapter 47.

**To act:** See the explanation of the Tzemach Tzedek: "We are workers of the day" — our work is to make things bright (Likkutei Dibburim, p. 520).

**Permeated by light:** See Tanya, Chapter 46, that even regarding light, it is possible for it to be "within it and within the depths of it." And in Kesuvos (111b): "The light of Torah gives it life."

**Chayos and hispaalus:** See Kuntres HaHispaalus by the Mitteler Rebbe (at the beginning): "Chayos, etc., and afterwards, etc., hispaalus, etc."

**Inner point... the wellsprings:** For they are the soul of Torah and mitzvos (Zohar Vol. 3, 152a).

## 8588

B"H, 11 Shevat, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Annual Banquet of the Ladies Auxiliary of Brownsville and East New York for the Lubavitcher Yeshivos "Tomchei Tmimim"

Shalom u’Bracha!

I was pleased to receive the news regarding the annual banquet on the 23rd of Shevat, and I wish all the active supporters and participants much success in this endeavor in every respect.

We have just passed the 13th yahrtzeit-hilula of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, who transplanted the Lubavitcher yeshivos to this country 23 years ago. The Lubavitcher yeshivos have, B"H, been successful, and the Ladies Auxiliary has played a most significant role in this.

This year, marking 150 years since the passing of the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch and founder of Chabad, is a special segulah-year for all supporters and participants in these holy institutions, which are conducted in his spirit and according to his instructions. The first sefer that the Alter Rebbe published was **Hilchos Talmud Torah**, thereby emphasizing that the primary obligation of a Jew is to study Torah, support Torah, and conduct one’s daily life according to Torah. The holy Torah is called **Toras-Emes** (Torah of Truth) and **Toras-Chaim** (Torah of Life), because it provides the true content of Jewish life and true happiness, both materially and spiritually.

May Hashem Yisbarach grant that you all continue your good work in an increased measure; as is required, that all matters of holiness and goodness should grow and spread. May the merit of this mitzvah bring you and your families, shichyu, the Almighty’s blessings in an ever-increasing measure, in all that you need, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for success and good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8,489

8,489

By the Grace of Hashem, 11 Shevat, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants in the annual dinner for Yeshivas Achei Temimim in Pittsburgh,
May Hashem sustain them,

Peace and Blessing!

Coming from the yahrtzeit-hilula of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, the founder of Yeshivas Achei Temimim in Pittsburgh, I hope that the dinner taking place in the coming days of this month will be imbued with the impressions of the memories of the life and work of the Baal HaHilula, and the inner awakening that this must evoke in everyone connected to the Rebbe and his institutions.

On this occasion, I wish to share a story that I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe—a matter that holds a lasting and ever-relevant significance for us all. Especially in this year, which marks 150 years since the histalkus of the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, the founder of Chabad.

The Mitteler Rebbe, the son of the Alter Rebbe, as is well known, possessed an extraordinary power of concentration. When he was focused on a subject, he would neither hear nor see what was happening around him.

Once, while the Mitteler Rebbe was deeply immersed in his thoughts, his child fell out of a nearby cradle and began to cry. The Mitteler Rebbe, however, did not notice it at all. At that same time, the Alter Rebbe was sitting in his own room on an upper floor, also deeply immersed in his studies. Yet, he did hear the child’s crying. The Alter Rebbe interrupted his learning, went downstairs, picked up the child, comforted him, and rocked him back into the cradle. The Mitteler Rebbe still had not heard or noticed a thing, so deeply absorbed was he. Later, his father spoke to him: "No matter how important the matter in which one is immersed may be, one must always hear the cry of a child!"

* * *

Since this story has been told to us, it is clear that it holds an important significance and practical instruction for each and every one of us. The yeshiva, where a Jewish child receives a Torah education, is that "cradle." We must ensure that not only do the children of the yeshiva not fall out of their cradle, Heaven forbid, but we must strive to bring as many children as possible into the yeshiva, for only in this way can we ensure them a life without tears—a truly happy life, both spiritually and materially.

It is therefore to be hoped that each and every one of the participants and friends of Yeshivas Achei Temimim in Pittsburgh will respond generously and warmly to strengthen and expand this vital "cradle" of Torah education that you have been privileged to have in your city.

The merit of the founder, and the merit of the mitzvah of tzedakah and supporting Torah, will surely assist you all, and your families, may they live, to be blessed by the Ribono shel Olam in everything you need, materially and spiritually, with much joy and true Yiddishe nachas.

With respect and blessing.

8590

## 8192

B"H, 17 Shevat, 5723
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 9 Shevat, which reached me in due course, in which you ask regarding the transfer [of the deceased] from Germany to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established.

It is a well-known general rule that in questions such as these, one must turn to a Rav who is a *moreh hora'ah*. It seems to me that the clear instruction in this matter is that the custom is to transfer [the deceased] to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, especially since in those years, Germany was viewed merely as a temporary place of transit.

We conclude with good tidings, with the strong hope that you are engaged in *hafatzas hamaayanos*, to the point that they reach even the "outermost regions" as much as possible and even more (for it is within the power of *Bnei Yisrael* to change reality, especially when it is in the mission of Torah and *mitzvos*). This is in accordance with the hope and instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, whose *histalkus* and *hillula* we recently commemorated on 10 Shevat. This year is a *shnas segulah* — the 150th year since the *histalkus* and *hillula* of the Alter Rebbe.

Regarding what you wrote about your son, may he live, traveling abroad to study: On the face of it, this is entirely incomprehensible, for there are *Tomchei Temimim* yeshivos in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, where the students are successful, etc. What is the point of uprooting someone from Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, to go abroad?

With blessings for good news regarding all of the above.

***

**8192**

**Regarding the transfer:** The transfer of the deceased.

**Especially since in those years:** This likely refers to the period following the Second World War, when Jews stayed in displaced persons camps for several years (see also *Toldos Chabad B'Russiah HaSovietit*, p. 486 and onwards).

**In the power... of reality:** See *Sefer HaSichos 5751*, Vol. 2, p. 692, note 96, and the sources cited there.

## 8593

8593

B"H, 17 Shevat, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Yosef Tzvi Steinhart, President of the Synagogue,
And Mr. Yehudah Eliezer Mishkin, Chairman of the Board,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and Blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter bringing the good news that this coming Sunday, the 23rd of Shevat, a public celebration will be held in connection with the presentation of a rabbinical contract—until 120 years—to your esteemed and distinguished Rabbi and spiritual leader, Rabbi Dovid Dov Hollander, shlita.

This news has given me special satisfaction. On one hand, Rabbi Hollander is truly worthy of all this honor and esteem; and on the other, it is a testament to the fact that Hashem has granted you the privilege of having a distinguished synagogue and the ability to lead an important, high-standing community along the waters of Torah and mitzvos, whose leaders and members know how to properly appreciate their Rabbi and spiritual guide, and recognize the success they have merited in having a Rabbi and leader such as him.

This is especially significant in our current era and in this country, where, to our great sorrow, there is a blurring of boundaries and values to the point where—in the words of the prophet—people call evil good and good evil, put darkness for light and light for darkness, and put bitter for sweet and sweet for bitter (Yeshayahu 5:20).

My father-in-law, the Rebbe, already sounded the alarm immediately upon his arrival in the United States against the widespread and false notion that America is different from all other lands and is not a place for Torah and mitzvos, etc.

On the contrary, he not only completely rejected this false assumption, but he pointed out several positive qualities that our brethren, the Children of Israel, possess in this land. He noted that the conditions of the place and the call of the hour are most suitable in many respects, and that they necessitate extensive work in the field of disseminating and strengthening Torah, mitzvos, and proper chinuch. The matter depends only on the will, the energy, and the cooperation between the Rabbis and spiritual leaders and the community activists and baalei-batim who are faithful to their mission and duty. The significant achievements over the last twenty years have proven that his motto was well-founded and has been validated.

My blessing is sent to your esteemed Rabbi, a man of energy and many accomplishments, Rabbi Dovid Dov Hollander, shlita, and to all the leaders of the synagogue and the members of their congregation, may they live: that you may work shoulder to shoulder on the path leading to the House of Hashem, to strengthen and establish your community so that it conforms in every detail to the traditional name of a community in Israel—a "Kehilla Kedosha." As our Rabbeinu HaZaken, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch—this year being the 150th year since his passing—emphasized, the Rabbi and the members of the community are like the head and the other parts of the body; it is understood that only when both are together are they a complete entity, a living, active, healthy, and whole body.

Based on the commandment "Love your fellow as yourself," which is a great principle in the Torah, my hope is strong that your community will serve as a living example and a source of positive influence for other synagogues, so that they may see and do likewise. May it be the will of Hashem that you go from strength to strength, with peace of mind, joy, and a good heart.

With honor and blessing to all the participants in the celebration, shlita.

***

**8593**

**Already sounded the alarm:** See also above, Vol. 1, Letter 157, and elsewhere.

**As our Rabbeinu HaZaken emphasized:** Tanya, Chapter 2.

## 8594

B"H, 19 Shevat, 5723
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, in which you write about the differences of opinion regarding your study schedule, etc., and also mention that some suspect your desire to change your study schedule is because you wish to study less, etc.

Since you are currently in the middle of the academic year—during which it is generally not customary to change one’s course of study for several reasons—and the question will be on the table at the beginning of the next academic year, it is appropriate that you increase your *hasmadah* and *shekidah* in the study of our holy Torah, the Torah of life. Continue according to the arrangements you have followed until now, but as mentioned, with an increase in the *chayus* you bring to your learning. When it becomes evident that your soul truly desires to study Torah without being distracted by other subjects, this itself will serve to diminish the complaints, etc.

The aforementioned intention regarding the increase in *chayus*, *hasmadah*, and *shekidah* is secondary to the primary reason: that study must be conducted in a manner of "ascending in holiness," as this is the will of Hashem. The root from which you were hewn assists you in this, beginning with our Alter Rebbe, who elaborated wondrously in many of his books and *maamarim* on the immense importance of *hasmadah* and *shekidah* in the study of Torah. It is surely superfluous to add that study must be, as per the instruction of Chazal, study that leads to action. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all of the above.

With blessings.

#### ***8594***

**As per the instruction of Chazal:** Kiddushin 40b.

## 8,795

B”H, 24 Shevat, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

The Administration of the Gemilas Chasadim Shomrei Shabbos Society
May Hashem preserve them and grant them life.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter at the beginning of the week, containing the report of your holy activities regarding tzedakah—the mitzvah of the Holy One, blessed be He—and the great virtue inherent within it, which is the matter of gemilas chasadim.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that, in accordance with the opening of Rabbeinu HaZaken in the sefer *Torah Or*: "Tzedakah elevates a nation" (*Tzedakah teromem goy*)—the raising and elevating of the *midos* (and in another place it is explained that this refers to the elevation of the levels of *Netzach, Hod, Yesod*, as well as the levels of the *mochin*),

May this be so in all matters concerning the participants in the society’s activities, and the administration at their head—shlita.

And a verse does not depart from its literal meaning: "elevates a nation"—"a single nation on earth," which refers to the Children of Israel.

For tzedakah brings about the personal geulah of the one who gives tzedakah, and draws closer the general geulah of all the Children of Israel.

The personal geulah, in its literal sense, is the nullification of all matters that distract from the avodah of Hashem with joy and a good heart.

This means that all the needs of every individual—in the three categories of children, life, and sustenance—should be met in their literal sense, as required, and even more—in completeness, and even more—in a manner of abundance.

And this is especially true regarding the matter of tzedakah, as it is stated regarding it: "Your mitzvah is exceedingly broad" (*rachavah mitzvosecha me’od*), according to the interpretation of Rabbeinu HaZaken.

And this year is a year of *segulah*, the one hundred and fiftieth year since his passing and hillula.

Enclosed is a contribution.

With blessings for success in your holy work, and in a manner—as per the instruction of Chazal—of gemilas chasadim for the wealthy, so that the prophecy may be fulfilled: "There shall be no needy among you, for Hashem will surely bless you"—and the Children of Israel will perform the will of the Makom.

**M. Schneerson**

Our Sages have already promised, "If you have labored and found," and "Whoever sanctifies himself a 'little' below, they sanctify him 'much' from above"—all the more so when one sanctifies himself more than a little.

With blessing.

#### ***8599***

## 6,300

B"H, 25 Shevat, 5723
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, Moreinu HaRav Tzvi Aryeh, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding your writing concerning a schedule for studies: Our Sages, of blessed memory, have already stated [that one should study] in the place where his heart desires.

The common denominator for everyone: a tractate of Shas (for *girsa*—fluent reading), and another tractate or *poskim* (for *iyun*—in-depth study).

The weekly *parsha* and the like—in *Torah Or* and *Likutei Torah* (for *girsa*), and additional study in *Chassidus* (for *iyun*). The studies for *girsa* should be done every day. For *iyun*—at the very least, three days should not pass without this study. See also the *sicha* of Chai Elul 5722.

## 8404

8404

B.H., 4 Adar, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants in the twelfth annual dinner
of the Lubavitcher Yeshiva in the Bronx,
May they live,

Shalom u’vracha!

I send my greetings and blessing to all the participants in the annual event of the Lubavitcher Yeshiva in the Bronx, with the inner hope that this event will fulfill all expectations, both financially and spiritually.

In this week’s parsha—the first in a series of parshiyos that discuss the building of the Mishkan—a general instruction is given immediately: **"From every man whose heart moves him to give"** (*m’eis kol ish asher yidvenu libo*)—to accept contributions from all Jews whose hearts are willing. **All** Jews were meant to have a share in the Mishkan, yet at the same time, the acceptance of contributions was limited to only those who would give with a full heart. On the surface, there appears to be a contradiction here. But in truth, there is no contradiction, for **all** Jews give tzedakah for holy causes with a warm heart; one simply needs to find the correct approach for every Jew. Then, every Jew gives according to his capabilities: one who can give **zahav** (gold) gives gold; one who can give **kesef** (silver) gives silver; and one who can give **nechoshes** (copper) gives copper. And when a Jew gives with a full heart, he certainly desires to give more than he is able, and the Ribono shel Olam counts this *nedavas libo* (willingness of his heart) as tzedakah as well, and grants the blessing of **"Aser bishvil shetisasher"** (tithe so that you may become wealthy). Thus, one who can currently only give copper is blessed so that he may be able to give silver; one who can give only silver is blessed to be able to give gold; and one who can give gold is blessed to be able to give *avnei shoham v’avnei milu’im* (precious stones).

Our Sages, of blessed memory, often emphasized that the concept of the Mishkan in our time has transitioned to the yeshivos, as Chazal say that after the destruction of the Beis Hamikdash, the Shechinah rests within the *daled amos* of halacha.

The saying of the Alter Rebbe—author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, the founder of Chabad, whose 150th yahrtzeit was on the 24th of Teves—is well known: "The Ribono shel Olam gives Jews gashmius, and Jews transform gashmius into ruchnius." The tzedakah that the supporters of the Bronx Lubavitcher Yeshiva give to sustain and strengthen the yeshiva is the highest form of transforming gashmius into ruchnius, and thereby they are also blessed with an increasing measure of gashmius—from copper to silver, from silver to gold, and so on—to be utilized for good, healthy, and happy things, in good health and with true Yiddishe nachas from their children, *sheyichyu*.

With respect and blessing for success and good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8475

B"H, 7 Adar, 5723
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who engages in communal affairs with great energy, etc.,
R' Shneur Zalman, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 2 Adar, in which you inquire regarding the concept that the redemption of Yaakov—and the principle that "the deeds of the fathers are a sign for the children"—implies that our own redemption is contingent upon the refinement of Esav, etc., you ask where the foundation of this idea lies.

It is founded upon the words of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe in his book *Torah Or*, Parshas Vayishlach; see there, where his primary explanation is in the style of the wisdom of Kabbalah. It is further explained regarding the *avodah* of man in the literal sense in the book of his son, the Mitteler Rebbe, *Toras Chaim* on the aforementioned parsha (and see there especially Chapter 8 and Chapter 11).

Incidentally, based on the above, several difficulties in the teachings of our Sages in the aforementioned parsha are resolved: from the beginning, Yaakov’s notification to Esav that he had observed the 613 *mitzvos*, etc., to the end, regarding the children—"This is Melech HaMashiach" (*Devarim Rabbah* 1:20)—and "And saviors shall ascend Mount Zion" (*Bereishis Rabbah*, end of Chapter 78).

In connection with the upcoming days of Purim, I am exerting effort again this year regarding *mishloach manos* and *matanos la'evyonim*. It is specifically in these *mitzvos* that there is great neglect, while on the other hand, they contain a particularly significant point of *chinuch* and guidance. Surely, in Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established) in general, and in the appropriate offices, they are doing so; however, I found it necessary to emphasize this point in this letter of mine, since in the instructions (a copy of which reached me) from the Ministry of Education, only the *mitzvah* of *mishloach manos* was mentioned! Would that we had already merited the promise, "There shall be no needy among you," and that Israel performs the will of the Omnipresent (*Sifrei* to *Devarim* 15:4).

With respect and blessing.

*[Secretariat Letter regarding Mishloach Manos and Matanos La'evyonim]*

B"H, 1 Adar, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To our esteemed friends, may they live,
In every place and location,

Greetings and blessings!

At the *farbrengen* of the Shabbos of the week of Adar this year, the Rebbe shlita saw fit to mention what he urged last year regarding the need to publicize to the masses that, aside from the obligation to fulfill on Purim the *mitzvah* of reading the *Megillah* and the other *mitzvos* of Purim (reciting *Al HaNissim* and more), everyone—men and women—is obligated to fulfill the two *mitzvos* of **mishloach manos and matanos la'evyonim**. Furthermore, that this obligation also applies to boys who have reached the age of thirteen and girls who have reached the age of twelve, and that there is a duty of *chinuch*—to accustom even young boys and girls who have not yet reached the age of Bar or Bas Mitzvah to this as well.

The Rebbe shlita also saw fit to emphasize how **easily** these *mitzvos* can be fulfilled. The *mitzvah* of **mishloach manos** can be fulfilled simply by sending even to just one person (a man to a man, and a woman to a woman) two types of food (one type of food together with some beverage). The *mitzvah* of **matanos la'evyonim** can be fulfilled by giving even just two *prutos* to two poor people—that is, one *prutah* to each of them (and it is self-understood that whoever increases in *tzedakah*, it is praiseworthy).

* * *

In accordance with the above, we wish to urge and request of each of our friends, may they live, to hasten and do everything possible, whether personally or through others, regarding the obligation to fulfill the *mitzvos* of *mishloach manos* and *matanos la'evyonim*—and how easily they can be fulfilled—and to publicize this through every means of publicity (letters, announcements, the press, radio, etc.), so that the information regarding the above and the *hisorerus* in this matter reaches every single man and woman of the Jewish people in every place and location, and to be among those who merit and bring merit to the masses.

We would be happy to hear about what is being done in this regard, and we thank you in advance.

With blessings for a happy Purim,
Secretariat of the Rebbe shlita

## 870

B.H., 7 Adar, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of the "Beis Rivkah" Seminary,
May Hashem grant you life,

Blessings and peace!

I was pleased to receive regards through the member of the administration regarding the progress of the seminary, and it is my hope that this progress will continue at an ever-increasing pace, in accordance with the directive of our Sages, of blessed memory: "We elevate in matters of holiness."

On this day, the birthday of Moshe Rabbeinu, it is certainly appropriate to contemplate that his birth, rescue, and upbringing were brought about through the dedication of two women in Israel, mother and daughter—Yocheved his mother and Miriam his sister. At a time when the decrees of Pharaoh reached the peak of the harshness of the bondage, to the point that they caused a collapse of spirit and withdrawal even among the "cedars of Lebanon" of that generation, these two women—the mother and the daughter, the "Hebrew midwives"—did not lose heart. On the contrary, they continued their work with true mesiras nefesh to **keep the children alive**, and in the intensity of the galus, they established the generation of the Geulah. They imparted their spirit and courage not only to the women, but also to the men, until they merited that through them would come the redeemer of Israel to lead the children of Israel out of bondage to Geulah.

This is the same matter in these final generations of this bitter galus, and especially in our own generation: the same role, the same responsibility, and the same privilege that fell to the lot of the women in the first galus are the inheritance of the women in this final galus, as my father-in-law, the Rebbe, emphasized frequently in writing and orally.

In this auspicious year, the year marking three jubilees since the passing of our Alter Rebbe—author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch and founder of the Chabad movement, its system, and way of life—one must remember and be impressed by the great influence of the mother of the one who is being honored this jubilee year, the Rebbetzin **Rivkah**, on the upbringing of the Alter Rebbe, as described at length in the *Sefer HaZichronos* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

In accordance with his teaching to be one who says and does, and that action is the essential thing, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, did not suffice with propaganda; he stood and founded a network of schools and "Beis Rivkah" seminaries in our Holy Land and in the Diaspora to educate the daughters of Israel in the spirit of Yocheved and Miriam.

Therefore, I hope from the depths of my heart that the students of the seminary will recognize the magnitude of their responsibility and privilege, and will utilize all their strength to absorb this spirit—the spirit of da'as and yiras Hashem—that the seminary seeks to instill in them. And since the students are destined to be teachers and guides in Israel, mothers of children, and the foundation of the home, every addition to their education and knowledge is multiplied many times over in the students and the homes they will establish for honor and glory; every effort and exertion in this direction is worthwhile.

May Hashem, blessed be He, send His blessing to each and every one of you to succeed in your studies with diligence and perseverance, and with appropriate conduct, and may the verse be fulfilled in each and every one of you: "Our sister, may you become thousands of myriads, etc."

With blessings for a happy Purim and to continue this hisorerus throughout all the days of the year—I await good news.

## 8707

B"H, 10 Adar, 5723
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 5 Adar, in which you ask "regarding a Reform house of worship, etc."

Surely you are referring to the Reform movement—that is, those who, G-d forbid, do not acknowledge the concept of *Torah min HaShamayim* (Torah from Heaven), etc. If that is the case, then the doubt is incomprehensible, and what is your question? This is especially so after the clear ruling in the *Sefer Mishneh Torah*, which is the *Yad HaChazakah* of the great teacher, the Rambam, *Hilchos Teshuvah*, Chapter 3, Halachah 8, regarding even one verse, etc. (see there carefully). You should certainly arrange the *kiddushin* **only** in a communal hall that is founded upon the thirteen *Ani Maamins* within the **totality of Torah and Mitzvos**, or at the very least in a neutral hall or even a private home.

May it be the will of Hashem that, in accordance with these days—as it was in those days, so may it be at this time—"the Jews had light"—this is Torah—(and connected to this) "joy"—this is *Yom Tov* (and the study of Torah which leads to action)—"and gladness and honor"—this is *tefillin*—for the entire Torah is compared to *tefillin*.

With respect and blessings for good tidings and a *Purim Sameach*.

8708

And given that the concept of "remembrance" is one that draws forth inspiration into all the powers of the soul, extending even to actual deed—and, on the contrary, the deed is the essential thing—

May it be the will [of Hashem] that this be the case regarding all four matters that were "in those days, at this time": light, gladness, joy, and honor, both in their literal sense and in their deeper meaning. "Light" refers to Torah, etc., and "honor" refers to tefillin, for the entire Torah (the mitzvos) is compared to tefillin, 

Until we merit to "connect redemption to redemption," from the redemption of "we are still servants of Achashverosh" to the true redemption, "as in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt," etc.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 8,419

B"H, 16 Adar, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, diligent in communal affairs, energetic, etc.,
Rabbi Yehuda Leib Rubenstein
Glasgow

Peace and Blessing!

Through the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing, energetic, etc., Rabbi Shlomo Zalman Hecht of Chicago, who visited our holy camp, I received your regards. He also wrote of how he was received with a friendly countenance by your community in general, and by yourself in particular. Although there is no place for expressions of gratitude in such matters—for the reward of a mitzvah is the mitzvah itself—I wish to express the satisfaction I derived from this. It is heartening to know that there are those who share the same view regarding the dissemination of traditional, authentic Judaism, without compromise, and in the style of the Baal Shem Tov: "spreading the wellsprings outward"—meaning, even among those who are still "outward."

This is especially relevant since, unfortunately, there are those who challenge this approach, not only from the left but also from the right. And although, of course, there is no room for such challenges—for our Sages, of blessed memory, spoke at length about the importance of "extracting the precious from the vile" —nevertheless, since there is opposition, any encouragement is most precious, especially encouragement that is accompanied by action.

With G-d’s help, I will fulfill your request through Rabbi Hecht. May it be His will that, in good health and with a glad heart, you utilize all your talents, as mentioned above, for the dissemination of traditional Judaism even "outward," and especially among the youth.

May it be His will, as we are coming from the days of Purim, that just as in those days, so too in this time, there will be for the Jews "light and gladness, and joy and honor" —in the literal sense, for "no verse departs from its literal meaning." And together with this, as per the exposition of our Sages, of blessed memory, in the Oral Torah—for we have one Torah, the Written and the Oral—"light" refers to Torah, and so on, until "honor" refers to tefillin. For all mitzvos were compared to the mitzvah of tefillin, and the one depends upon the other: that through "light"—which is Torah—it is guaranteed that there will be "light," etc., in the literal sense as well.

With respect and blessing for good tidings.

***

## 811

B"H, 25 Adar, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Eliyahu Amikam, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

For some time, I have wanted to write to you, but I did not know where you were located. Now, I have learned that you are already in Eretz Yisrael, and I have your address.

First of all, I wish to express my gratitude for the book. Since our library is for the benefit of the many, it is my hope that you will continue to do so in the future as well.

I hope that you also retain memories of our meeting and our conversation. Most importantly, I hope that the matters we discussed regarding communal affairs—including several of the most vital and serious issues—will bear fruit and bring benefit to the many.

We see this tangibly, especially in our generation, following the discovery of the most staggering energy contained within the smallest quantity. It is sometimes within the power of a single individual to bring about a fundamental change in the lives of the many, for it is not quantity that is decisive, but quality. If this is true regarding matter and inanimate substance, how much more so is it true regarding the substance and physicality of the Jewish body, and even more so regarding the spiritual life of our people, the children of Israel.

However, the individual must reveal all the energy within him, which is in truth infinite. To use the phrasing of our Rabbeinu HaZaken, the Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch—this year being the 150th anniversary of his passing—the second soul in a Jew is a **literal** part of Elokus from above. Since its source is in the Ein Sof, blessed be He, it and all its powers are infinite.

With respect and blessing for good tidings.

## 8,412

B"H, 25 Adar, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Eliezer Steinman,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Glitzenstein, I was especially pleased to receive regards from you through our friend, R’ Shazar, who, as he told me, saw you shortly before his departure from Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt and established—and will surely convey your regards upon his return. It is my hope that by the time you receive this letter, you will have already resumed your work at home. Engaging in this work with joy will add blessing and success, as is well known how much our Rebbes of blessed memory emphasized the importance of joy, particularly the joy of a mitzvah—and in this case, the dissemination of the teachings of Chabad.

Moving from one subject to a related one, I offer my warm and heartfelt thanks for the Bar Mitzvah book you sent me. It certainly requires no praise, as it is distinguished even by its external presentation [contrary to the opinion of those who mistakenly think this is unimportant; for while it is true that the inner essence is primary, our Sages of blessed memory have said, "Beautify yourself before Him in mitzvos"—a beautiful tallis, beautiful tzitzis, etc.].

I do not know if I am justified in offering an opinion in a field that is not my own, or if it is relevant to the current situation, but in my view, it would be desirable that the illustrations in a book intended for youth at the Bar Mitzvah age should not necessarily demonstrate a specific school of art, but rather **correspond** more (and how much better if they were) to their values and age. As mentioned, I ask your forgiveness, especially since one does not cry over the past, but since it has already "happened before" and you have succeeded in releasing subsequent editions, perhaps there is room for adjustment.

I was especially pleased to see that your book begins with the laying of tefillin and their blessings **in their simple, literal sense**, emphasizing that the act itself is the main thing. This serves to counter those who, unfortunately [and to use the expression—"may nothing be lacking"], wish to distort the concept of Bar Mitzvah, Heaven forbid.

With respect and a blessing for good health and success in the aforementioned matters and in all your affairs in general.

**M. Schneerson**

## 8414

B”H, 11 Nissan, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

Pesach, being the **first** day and the **first** Yom Tov for the Jewish people—the first in time and the first in stature and importance, for its content is the liberation of the Jews and the beginning of their existence as an independent nation with its own way of life according to the Torah, its own mitzvos, Yomim Tovim, and so on—possesses a unique importance for all Jews and for every individual Jew in all times and in every place. Therefore, the details of Pesach and Yetzias Mitzrayim also hold a special significance as a general directive and lesson in Jewish life, whether for the individual, for the group, or for the community at large.

***

One of the important details of Yetzias Mitzrayim is that it took place **"on this very day,"** which means, as our Sages of blessed memory explain, that at the moment the *Ketz* (the appointed time) arrived—the time of liberation—the Jews left Egypt without delaying even **"for the blink of an eye."** It is further added that had the Jews delayed that **moment**, they would have lost, Heaven forbid—they, and we, and our children, and our children’s children—the entire matter of the redemption from Egypt!

This is entirely incomprehensible: the ten plagues had already occurred, which had led the Egyptians to drive the Jews out of Egypt—so what was so critical about that "blink of an eye"? And how can it be understood that if one had delayed by a single moment, the entire redemption would have been lost?

Furthermore, the main question arises: what is the Torah—the *hora’ah* (instruction)—therein, for the sake of which the Torah tells us "on this very day"?

***

The explanation is as follows:

When the *Ketz* arrives—when the moment comes to put an end to things and emerge from the *tumah* of Egypt—one must not postpone the opportunity even for a blink of an eye.

The danger of missing that moment was not that the Egyptians would then have second thoughts, but that among the Jews themselves there would be those who would have second thoughts, who would not want to abandon the accustomed way of life in Egypt and go off into a desert to receive the Torah.

The instruction for every Jew—man or woman, young or old—is:

The meaning of "Yetzias Mitzrayim" in daily life is the liberation from the enslavement of a person to their body and *nefesh habehamis*, from the enslavement to physical demands and habits, as well as from the materialistic environment surrounding them. This liberation comes through listening to and fulfilling the constant call of the Almighty, the G-d of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov: "I will take you out from under the burdens... and I will be to you a G-d," which is expressed—just as it was then, at the time of leaving the land of Egypt—by accepting the Torah and fulfilling its mitzvos.

***

This call is constant; Yetzias Mitzrayim must take place *bekhol yom vayom*—every day is a *Ketz*, a *sha’as hakosher* (opportune moment) to fulfill the call.

However, there are those who "delay," who postpone the *sha’as hakosher* for the "three pious days of the year" (Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur), or at most, for Shabbos and Yom Tov. Even among those who recall and observe "Yetzias Mitzrayim" every day during davening, there are those who limit it only to davening and let the *sha’as hakosher* that exists throughout the day pass by.

And as it is in the life of the individual, so it is in the life of the group and the community; only here, the *sha’as hakosher* is, of course, far, far more important.

***

The extraordinary *sha’as hakosher* and opportunity that is "knocking at the door now" is the fact that among very broad circles, especially among the youth, there has been, for several years now, a strong movement to **return to our true sources**. And in many places and in many matters, even the non-Jews are "driving" the Jews away from the ideology of modern "Egyptian *tumah*."

A large portion of those circles that were alienated from Yiddishkeit are seeking the way back to Torah and mitzvos, and a large portion of Torah-observant circles are seeking to strengthen and deepen their connection and identification with them.

With the exception of those who have stopped thinking for years, this is now a time when everyone, and especially the youth, are not only ready to hear the full truth, but they **demand** that one tell them the full truth. Even those who are not yet ready to take upon themselves all the mitzvos at once and turn their lives upside down in one leap are mature enough and courageous enough to hear the pure truth, without compromises and not "tailored to order." Experience has shown that where the youth comes into contact with genuine Torah-and-mitzvos Yiddishkeit, they are drawn to it, and a very significant portion of them have begun to organize their daily lives in accordance with it, and with the decisiveness and vitality with which youth is gifted.

With sorrow, however, it must be said that although this awakening has been present for several years, the *sha’as hakosher* has not been utilized to the proper extent, and the sorrow is especially great seeing that it has been utilized almost not at all by those who should be the spiritual leaders.

***

May it be the will of the Almighty that just as our ancestors in Egypt did not delay their departure from Egypt even for a blink of an eye, and this led to the full redemption of the body and to the full redemption of the soul (through the acceptance of the Torah, which was the purpose and conclusion of Yetzias Mitzrayim)—

So too should every man and woman utilize to the fullest extent the extraordinary *sha’as hakosher* of the present moment, to help themselves and others, and the group and the community, to be liberated from all kinds of enslavement, and primarily from the heaviest of them all: the thought of "we shall be like all the nations," and return to Torah and mitzvos to the **fullest** extent. And may the promise and the ruling be fulfilled: "Israel performs *teshuvah*—and **immediately** they are redeemed," with the true and complete redemption through Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

With the blessing of a kosher and happy Pesach,

**Menachem Schneerson**

For the virtue of man is that he is a "walker" (in which he is superior even to the ministering angels, who are merely "standers"). This is also the concept of the exodus from Mitzrayim every day—to depart from the constraints and limitations and to ascend higher and higher, from one level of ascent to the next. And action is the essential thing, as is understood: the performance of practical mitzvos, in which—and especially in which—one must "ascend in holiness," including the mitzvah of "love your fellow as yourself," with emphasis on influencing others. My words have already been said, and I believe I also wrote to you in my previous letter, that the youth are ready and prepared to hear and accept much more than one might imagine. More on this subject can be found in my general letter regarding the matters of the day, which is enclosed.

## 8,718

B"H, 29 Nissan, 5723
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, occupied with communal needs,
R' Efraim Eliezer HaKohen, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

This morning, before my departure to the holy gravesite, I received your letter dated Monday, along with the enclosure. I mentioned you at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the contents of your letter.

Regarding your note at the end of the letter—concerning what is written in *Torah Or* (though I do not have it before me)—that seemingly, when Bnei Yisrael entered Eretz Yisrael, they were permitted to eat *chadash* during the seven years of conquest, for it is no more stringent than the "pig's ribs" [permitted during war], and the explanation given is that there was a prohibition of harvesting, and only what they found ready-made was permitted. You, in your own wisdom, offer a resolution to the difficulty raised against this explanation [that harvesting in Jericho was permitted (Rashi, *Pesachim* 55b, s.v. *v’kotzrin*), since the produce of Jericho was not fit for *menachos*], namely, that this only applies when they are settled in the land, where there is a place to bring from the choicest, and you conclude that the matter requires further study (*tzarich iyun*).

In my humble opinion, the following points should be noted regarding these three matters:

a) Regarding the difficulty: It seems simple that the permission for "pig's ribs" is connected to the war* (or at the very least, connected to the conquest**), whereas the prohibition of *chadash* was in effect immediately upon their entry into the land, before any war or conquest, as is explicitly stated in the verse.

b) The explanation that only ready-made food was permitted, but not that which required harvesting, is difficult to understand. For it is **explicit** in the verse, "vineyards and olive groves," and why should grain in the fields be any different? Perhaps the intention is that only the prohibition of eating was lifted, but not other prohibitions—as the verse concludes, "and you shall eat."

c) Regarding your own explanation, and your conclusion that it requires further study: It seems simple—since the *Omer* must come from the land, it is only possible to bring it from land that has already been conquered. At that time, Yisrael was only in the vicinity of Jericho. And it is no worse than "roofs or huts" (*Menachos* 64b), where, if it has not yet ripened, one brings it from **any** place.

With blessings for good tidings.

---

* See Rambam, *Hilchos Melachim* (8:1), "If he is hungry."
** See Rambam, *V'Eschanan* (6:10), "He permitted them the spoils."

## 8220

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Iyar, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, engaged in communal needs, R' Yehuda Leib, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

As we stand at the beginning of the month of Ziv—the month of Iyar, the second month to Nissan—a time which corresponds to the second [day of] the Festival of Matzos, it may be suggested that just as there are two aspects to matzah—the "food of faith" (*michla d'meheimenusa*) and the "food of healing" (*michla d'asvasa*)—so too here.

The teachings and explanations of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, regarding this are well-known: the Alter Rebbe—this year being the 150th anniversary of his histalkus and hillula—and his son, the Mitteler Rebbe, explain that the "food of faith" refers to one who is healthy from the outset, while the "food of healing" refers to one who became ill and was subsequently healed, and so on.

One may hint at this through the two ways of writing [the name] Iyar. [The spelling] *Aleph-Yud-Reish* (איר) is an acronym for "I am Hashem your Healer" (*Ani Hashem Rofecha*). [The spelling] *Aleph-Yud-Yud-Reish* (אייר) is an acronym for "Avraham, Yitzchak, Yaakov, Rachel" (*Avraham Yitzchak Yaakov Rachel*), who are the *Merkavah*. Throughout their entire lives, they never ceased, even for a single hour, from connecting their consciousness and their souls to the Ribono shel Olam. From this, it is understood that this corresponds to the aspect of "food of faith," as opposed to the order of "I am Hashem **your Healer**."

Although, even within the order of "I am Hashem your Healer," there are, in particular, both aspects—including the aspect of "I will not place [any of these diseases] upon you" from the outset.

And according to what is written in various places, it may be suggested that this is also the matter of the distinction in the Supernal Will, in the language of Kabbalah, *Arich*—which is the acronym for "For I am Hashem your Healer" (*Ki Ani Hashem Rofecha*)—and the *Pnimiyus* of the Will, where "there is no left side in this *Atik*, it is all right side," and this is well understood.

With blessings for good tidings, in general and in particular.

## 8225

8225

By the Grace of Hashem, Lag B’Omer, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

- The 150th year since the passing and Hilula of the Alter Rebbe -
To all the chapters of Agudas N’shei U’Bnos Chabad everywhere, and
to the participants in the Eighth Annual Convention in particular,
May Hashem grant them life.

Peace and Blessing!

The current year’s convention of N’shei U’Bnos Chabad will, like all Chabad endeavors this year, surely stand under the impression of the 150th Yahrtzeit-Hilula of the Alter Rebbe, Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, the founder of the Chabad *shita*, way of life, and movement. Especially so, when taking into account the important place that the Jewish woman in general, and the Chabad woman in particular, occupies in Jewish life.

In connection with this, as well as the fact that the convention is taking place during the days of Sefirah, I wish to briefly share the well-known story regarding one of the Alter Rebbe’s first Chassidim, R’ Gavriel Nosson-Chen and his wife, Maras Chana Rivka.

* * *

R’ Gavriel was one of the most respected householders in Vitebsk, yet twenty-five years had passed since their wedding and they had no children. Then, due to certain persecutions he suffered, he lost his fortune. He therefore felt much distress when an appeal for *pidyon shvuyim* (redeeming captives) arose by the Alter Rebbe, and he, R’ Gavriel, could not participate with the sum that had been assessed for him. When his wife learned of all this, she sold her pearls and jewelry for which she received the necessary sum; she polished the coins until they shone, and with a prayer that their *mazal* should also shine, she packed the coins and gave them to her husband to take to the Alter Rebbe.

Upon entering the Rebbe’s room in Liozna, R’ Gavriel placed the package on the table and, at the Rebbe’s instruction, unpacked it. The coins shone with an extraordinary brightness.

The Alter Rebbe became lost in thought and said: Of all the gold, silver, and copper that the Jews gave for the *Mishkan*, nothing shone except for the *Kiyor* and its base (the washbasin and its stand) (which were made from the copper mirrors that the Jewish women had donated to the *Mishkan* with *mesiras nefesh* and joy).

"Tell me, where did you get these coins?" R’ Gavriel had to recount his situation and how his wife, Chana Rivka bas Baila, had obtained the money.

The Alter Rebbe leaned on his hands for a long time in *dveikus*, then raised his head and blessed him (and his wife) with children, long life, wealth, and extraordinary *nesi’us chen* (grace); he instructed R’ Gavriel to close his business in Vitebsk and begin trading in precious stones and diamonds. The Rebbe’s blessing was fully fulfilled. R’ Gavriel Nosson-Chen became a wealthy man, sons and daughters were born to them, and so on. He passed away at the age of 110, and his wife outlived him by two years.

While telling this story, the Rebbe Rayatz brought the Alter Rebbe’s teaching on it: that which is stated regarding *Sefiras HaOmer* (which is the preparation for Shavuos—to receive the Torah), **"U’sfartem lachem"**—"You shall count for yourselves," also means "You shall make the *lachem*—yourselves—**shine**" (from the word *sapir*, a precious stone).

* * *

The lesson of this story, among the other deep concepts within it, is: although the coins for *tzedakah* are the same in number and value, when one gives them with *mesiras nefesh* and joy, those same coins acquire a different value and a different brightness. It illuminates one's life even in this world, and—certainly—in the world of light.

Likewise, it is understood, this applies also to *tzedakah* in spiritual matters. Every effort and activity to spread Torah and *mitzvos*, when it is illuminated with the light and warmth of Chassidus—so that one performs it with *mesiras nefesh* and joy—in addition to the fact that the activity itself meets with greater success, it has a manifold effect and brings a very special merit.

May the Almighty grant that every one of you, within the entirety of *Klal Yisroel*, should fulfill the **"U’sfartem lachem"** as the Alter Rebbe explained it: that one should illuminate oneself, one’s home, and one’s surroundings with the light of Torah, *mitzvos*, and Chassidic conduct, even in daily life. Then it will be bright in all respects, both materially and spiritually.

With a blessing for success in all that is written above.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 826

826

B"H, Lag B'Omer, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

— The 150th year since the histalkus and hillula of Rabbeinu HaZaken, the Baal HaTanya —

To the participants of the Tanya study group at the Shaarei Tefillah Synagogue, in the city of Toronto,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received the news that in the coming days you will be completing the first part of the holy Tanya.

And surely, in accordance with the well-known custom to "connect the beginning to the completion," you will immediately begin the second part, which is Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah (and its introduction).

Regarding the content of the conclusion of the first part: "For Hashem your G-d is a consuming fire," as is explained in other maamarim—

—and perhaps it can be said that the intent here is to the maamar beginning "Ki Vayom Hazeh Yichaper" (Likutei Torah, beginning of Parshas Acharei)—

—the analogy of a consuming fire is that just as fire cannot be grasped or called by the name "light and fire" at all, and does not illuminate below except by catching onto a physical object and also "consuming" and destroying it—so too is it regarding Hashem (who becomes) "your G-d" (your strength and your vitality), who illuminates and is revealed below specifically through the 613 mitzvos, as is explained briefly also at the conclusion of Chapter 53, which is the conclusion of the first part.

And this is also the content of the matter of Sefiras HaOmer: the omer of barley, the food of an animal, which is the animal soul discussed at the conclusion of the first part, which through the sefirah (the purpose of which is "so that the souls of Your people Israel may be purified," meaning) the transformation of the animal soul until it reaches the level of "Adam" (Man)—"You are called Adam," after the likeness of the Supernal, which is the divine soul, a literal part of G-d from above.

And just as it was during this sefirah the first time, when Bnei Yisrael left Egypt, when He brought our souls out of the sitra achra, Heaven forbid, and brought us close and attached us to His Name literally, and He and His Name are One (see the beginning of Part II of Tanya).

This is why, at the completion of the avodah of the sefirah of the barley omer, we offer a "new meal-offering" specifically of wheat, the food of man (as the matter is explained in many places).

May it be the will that the aforementioned study also leads to action, that we may walk in the straight path that He has taught us from His ways, and we shall walk in His paths, forever.

This is the avodah of Hashem in spiritual matters; and in worldly matters, may there be found an abundance of Hashem's blessing, and "whoever is closest is prioritized for the blessing."

With respect and blessing.

## 8267

8267

B”H, 25 Iyar, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished individual, who possesses fine character traits and is involved in communal affairs, a branch of a noble family, etc.,
Rabbi Shazar, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

Your telegram was received on the bright day of Lag B’Omer. If you intended for it to arrive then, that is good; if it was orchestrated from Above, that is even better.

May it be the will of the Ribono shel Olam that the entire matter proceeds in the best possible way, with the emphasis of Chassidus that it should be "good" in a way that is visible and revealed, even to physical eyes. At the same time, its foundation must be in the truth that "there is no good other than Torah"—and in the Chabad sense, this means not only the revealed aspects of Torah, but also the inner dimensions of Torah.

As is the custom and nature of Yisrael to connect every matter to the day on which it occurs—especially according to the teachings of Hashgacha Pratis as emphasized by the Baal Shem Tov—one should note the greatness of Rashbi (whose Hillula is on Lag B’Omer) compared to the great Tannaim of his generation and even those before him. When there was a need to pray for physical requirements—the symbol and primary example of which is the request for rain (and herein lies the excellence of Eretz Yisrael, which "drinks water from the rain of the heavens")—the procedure, even among the great Tannaim, was to pray, and if they were not answered immediately, they would decree a public fast, etc. However, the procedure of Rashbi was that when people came to tell him there was a need for rain in the literal sense, he would reveal secrets of the Torah, and rains of blessing would begin to fall, as recounted in the Zohar, Vol. III, 59b and onwards. It is emphasized there specifically that the subject upon which he expounded and revealed these secrets of the Torah was the verse, "How good and how pleasant it is for brothers to dwell together," which is the concept of Ahavas Yisrael, so emphasized in the teachings of our master the Baal Shem Tov and the Alter Rebbe.

"By the way," and in continuation of the above: the meaning of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe’s name, Shneur Zalman, is well known. In the standard version, it means "two lights"—the light of Chassidus and the light of the revealed Torah. However, Chassidim also interpret "two lights" as referring to spirituality and physicality. This is similar to the saying of the Berditchever: *Zalman* is composed of the same letters as *l’zman* (for a time), meaning that he draws down all these matters into a specific time and place.

With respect, blessing, and anticipation of good news regarding all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

Although you are busy, I hope that the matter of the collection in connection with the 150th anniversary of the Alter Rebbe’s Hillula is progressing. I will share some good and happy news: for several years I have been searching for the first edition of the Alter Rebbe’s *Hilchos Talmud Torah*, and just recently I learned that it is in the British Museum.

## 8228

8228

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5723

...Regarding the completion celebration of Seder Moed and Maseches Yevamos, which is to take place on Sunday, the 3rd of Sivan, the upcoming days of Hagbalah.

Certainly, in the well-known style, one should attach the beginning (of the next Seder and Maseches) to the completion.

May your strength be fortified for the sake of Torah, for the matter of Talmud Torah is great in general, and all the more so Talmud Torah in public, and specifically the study of Gemara.

Especially when the study is mingled with words of inspiration and Yiras Hashem, as per the directive of Chazal: "If Yiras Hashem is his treasure, then [he has everything], etc."

According to the explanation of Rabbeinu HaZaken, the Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch — this year being the 150th anniversary of his histalkus and hillula — these are the matters of Pnimiyus HaTorah.

For as the words of Moshe Rabbeinu, the Ra'aya Mehemna, state: "There, there is no difficulty, etc., and no dispute, etc." On the contrary, through this (as in the completion of a Maseches), one increases peace in the world, and especially among Talmidei Chachamim.

Based on this, we can explain why the fire of Gehinom has no power over Talmidei Chachamim. For the fire of Gehinom could be created, and was only created, on the second day—the day on which dispute was created. This is not the case with peace, and the increase of peace.

Furthermore, according to the conclusion of the words of the Ra'aya Mehemna there: "Through this (the study of the Tree of Life), Yisrael will emerge from galus with mercy." This is the fulfillment of the destiny that "the maiden of Yisrael will be wed to the Kudsha Brich Hu," for this world is merely the betrothal, but in the days of Moshiach, it will be the marriage.

This is also the theme of these days—Hagbalah and preparation for the "day of His wedding," which is Matan Torah. The completion and ultimate perfection of this will be in the days of Moshiach, through the Torah of Moshiach, for then Hashem will reveal Himself to them once more to explain to them the secrets of its reasons and the hidden depths of its mysteries.

May it be the will of Hashem that the benches of the Beis Medrash be filled with the study of both the Nigleh and the Pnimiyus together, for the merit of the many depends upon it, and the merit of the many assists him...

## 8229

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, Torah-scholar, man of character, engaged in communal needs, scion of a noble lineage, etc.,
R' Schneur Zalman, shlita,

Peace and blessing!

The election results have been received, and I send you my heartfelt wishes that it should be with *siyata d'shmaya*, with success in all details, in matters of both the physical and the spiritual alike—especially since, for the Jewish people, even the physical is spiritual.

This is in continuation of my letter from the beginning of the week, which I am certain was received in due time.

It is customary in such instances to also say "Mazal Tov," even though, on the face of it, this entails a great increase in responsibility, as well as new responsibilities. But *minhag Yisrael Torah hi*—the custom of Israel is Torah—which means that it is truth. And it is understood that, certainly and surely, from the outset, all the strengths and possibilities are provided for the fulfillment of the responsibility in its entirety, and furthermore, assistance and help are provided as well.

May it be the will that all the aforementioned be with proper health, and with joy and goodness of heart, with all the interpretations of this matter in the teachings of Chassidus, beginning with the Baal Shem Tov, and with greater explanation and innovation from the Alter Rebbe, as this year is the one hundred and fiftieth year since his *histalkus-hilula*.

With respect, appreciation, and abundant blessing in all the aforementioned, and in anticipation of the upcoming holiday of Shavuos—in the well-known phrasing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe—that we may receive the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

**Menachem Schneerson**

Although it is contrary to the custom of Israel to "speak" about those who are in the World of Truth, nevertheless, I felt it my duty not to conceal what I have thought several times, in connection with what was repeated in his speeches and statements even before the elections—regarding following in the footsteps of so-and-so (may he live a long and good life)—that my hope, and may it be the will that it be fulfilled in practice, is that he will not only utilize all the possibilities in his new roles that exist even now, but that he will further develop and expand them—in pleasant ways, yet with the necessary firmness. For surely the actions will be in the spirit of the Israel of old, the tradition of our forefathers which they accepted upon themselves and their descendants at the standing at Mount Sinai. And what happened and occurred to his predecessors (may they live long and good lives)—**will make no impression whatsoever**—in the style of the Sages—"wants to but cannot, and can but does not want to"—rather, if he wants and wants, and as mentioned earlier in my letter—the ability will be given.

There is room to say that what is written here does not conform to protocol, and therefore it comes after the signature; and if there is room and need—I ask for his forgiveness.

With respect and with blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 8332

8332

B"H, 4 Sivan, 5723

Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Sivan:

At an auspicious time, I will mention you and all those you write about at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter.

Regarding the outline of the events of your life that you have experienced, as described in your letter, I have a strong hope that you will fulfill your good resolution to study our Torah—the Torah of life, both the revealed and the inner dimensions—with consistency and diligence. After all, study leads to action—the fulfillment of mitzvos in an orderly fashion and with *hiddur* (beautification). We have been promised that "one who comes to purify himself is assisted", and may it be His will that you also influence your friends and surroundings in this direction.

Regarding your writing that you have changed your *davening* to the Chabad *nusach* (which is the *nusach* of the Arizal), and you ask whether you should do the same regarding the tying of *tefillin*:

You do not specify what your doubt is in this matter. You have been privileged to succeed and are studying in a Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, founded and directed by our Rebbes, the leaders of Chabad. May it be His will that you act and increase in all the aforementioned matters with joy.

Regarding your writing about your lack of understanding of the Yiddish language, etc.: It is not the language that is the essence, but the content. See also the *sefer Torah Or* by the Alter Rebbe—as this year is the 150th anniversary of his passing, his *hillula*—on the verse, "And they saw... like the work of a sapphire brick."

Surely you are aware of the three daily *shiurim*—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—and at the very least, you should maintain them from this point forward.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned, and for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 8733

B”H, Erev Shavuos, Zman Matan Toraseinu, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

- The 150th year since the histalkus of the Alter Rebbe -

To all participants in the celebration of the groundbreaking for the new building of the central Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim in Brooklyn, and to our brethren, the children of Israel, who guard Torah and mitzvos, in general,
May Hashem keep them alive.

Peace and Blessing!

On the occasion of this great simcha shel mitzvah — the first step in the far-reaching undertaking to create a new building for the central Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in Brooklyn — I send my heartfelt greeting and blessing to all who are participating in this great simcha and great mitzvah.

I hope that every single person, to whom Torah and chinuch al taharas hakodesh are dear and precious, will utilize every possibility to ensure that not only will the beginning be with the fullest measure of success, but also that they will continue to help realize the construction of the new building as soon as possible. This requires a threefold self-sacrifice in money, effort, and spirit (**M**amon, **G**uf, **N**eshamah):

**B’mamono** — means, simply, with the greatest monetary contributions; not according to one’s own concepts, but *k’yad Hashem hatovah alav*.

**B’gufo** — to personally dedicate oneself, with time and effort, to create new friends, supporters, and participants for the new building.

**B’nishmaso** — with actual mesiras nefesh: even when it seems to him that he could have added to his own Torah study, etc.; for to strengthen and spread Torah and mitzvos to the masses justifies bringing a sacrifice from one’s own soul-life.

In truth, however, even in tzedakah in spirituality, as in tzedakah in physicality, there is the promise of **aser te’aser** — that setting aside a tenth of oneself for others is the source of wealth, both in physicality and in spirituality. And beyond the mitzvah of tzedakah, in which "Zevulun" supports "Yissachar’s" learning, Zevulun also has a share in Yissachar’s Torah.

In these days, which are connected with Matan Torah — days when, in essence, a Jew should remember the standing at Har Sinai every day — everyone will surely remember that it was in the merit of our children that we received the Torah, and will recognize the obligation to support the mosdos of chinuch al taharas hakodesh, especially since the central Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch has been known for many decades as one of the greatest fortresses of Torah in our time.

The merit of supporting and spreading Torah to the masses will surely assist every single person to be blessed in everything they need, both in physicality and in spirituality together.

With blessings for outstanding success and for receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness,

**Menachem Schneerson**
