## 6735

[Isru Chag, 5723]

Two fundamental points of Matan Torah are specifically connected to the Jewish woman and mother:

First, when Hashem gave the Torah, He commanded Moshe Rabbeinu to speak about it first to the women, and only afterward to the men, as our Sages of blessed memory explain the verse: "Thus shall you say to the **Beis Yaakov**"—this refers to the women—"(and then) tell the Bnei Yisrael"—the men.

Second, the Torah was given only when the Jews took upon themselves the responsibility that the children would be the guarantee that the Torah and mitzvos would, Heaven forbid, never be forgotten.

From this, it is understood that to a very great extent, the continuity of Torah and mitzvos is connected to the Jewish woman and mother: The woman can and must encourage her husband to study Torah; she can and must conduct the home on the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, with kedushah and taharah; and as a mother, who also has more time to devote to the children, she is to a great extent responsible for the proper Jewish upbringing of the children.

Furthermore, through organized activity to support the mosdos chinuch al taharas hakodesh and, in general, to strengthen Yiddishkeit in the surrounding environment, her influence and contribution are also highly significant outside of her own home...

Brooklyn, N.Y.
The 150th year since the passing of our Alter Rebbe

To the participants in the annual luncheon of the N.Y. Committee for the Seminary for Teachers and Vocational School for girls in Kfar Chabad in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established,

Coming from the Yom Tov of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah, each of the participants will surely remember the great zechus of the Jewish women, whose consent was required even before the consent of the men in order to receive the Torah at Mount Sinai.

This zechus, naturally, places a special responsibility upon Jewish women to do everything that depends on them to strengthen and spread Torah and mitzvos, not only within their own homes, but also outside the home; and first and foremost—to strengthen chinuch al taharas hakodesh, which is the foundation for the existence of Torah and mitzvos in daily life.

The work of your committee is directly connected to the aforementioned responsibility and zechus. I hope that you will dedicate yourselves to this work with increasing commitment, both personally and by involving new friends and supporters, and that this will be done with simcha and enthusiasm.

May Hashem Yisbarach grant you success in this holy work, which is also a channel and vessel to receive the blessings of the Ribono shel Olam in everything one needs, both in gashmius and in ruchnius alike.

With blessings for success and for good tidings.

## 6737

B"H, 10 Sivan, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Rabbi, Chassid, G-d-fearing, and diligent in communal affairs,
R' Ephraim Eliezer Hakohen, shluchah,

Shalom u'Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Erev Shabbos, and I will address the points you raised in order:

1) Regarding *Nesias Kapayim*, which involves two aspects: one mitzvah and three mitzvos.

It is worth noting the *Shulchan Aruch HaRav*, Siman 128, Seif 6 and Seif 57; the language there requires some study to reconcile.

See also *Emek She'eilah*, end of She'ilta 125.

2) Whether there is also an *aseh* (positive commandment) for Yisrael in this.

The discussion on this is noted in many places—in the book *Yesodei Yeshurun* by Rabbi Feder, shluchah, Part 2, at the beginning, which includes sources from the Rishonim as well, such as the *Rashba* to *Sukkah* 31b.

3) Regarding the omission by the *Rambam* concerning the days of Moshiach and the matter of mitzvos, which you noted in *Hilchos Teshuvah*, Chapter 9, Halacha 2, and which you wish to resolve.

As I recall, in our conversation I also mentioned the *Rambam’s Hilchos Teshuvah*. On the contrary, from there the difficulty you mentioned only grows, as he discusses the matter of mitzvos specifically in the context of the days preceding the days of Moshiach—in his words, "kingdoms that do not allow them to engage in Torah and mitzvos properly"—yet he omits this when writing about the engagement of Yisrael during the days of Moshiach.

4) Regarding your precision on what the *Rambam* wrote (in *Hilchos Melachim* at the end) concerning "Torah and its wisdom":

In my opinion, there is no room at all to interpret "Torah" here as referring to the engagement in mitzvos*, especially since he immediately clarifies "and its wisdom" (of the Torah). In my opinion, he is referring to the two aspects within Torah, as understood from the words of our Sages: "If one tells you there is wisdom among the nations, believe it; if one tells you there is Torah among the nations, do not believe it" (*Eicha Rabbah* 2:13). The distinction is simple: "Wisdom" is general, while "Torah" comes from the word *hora'ah* (instruction)—implying a conclusion and a **commandment**. This has no place among the nations, since their intellect is based on premises that have no foundation other than will and acceptance, **not** on intellect. And this is not the place to elaborate.

Furthermore, there is proof from the fact that in *Hilchos Melachim* he explains and writes, "and the entire world will be occupied only with knowing Hashem."

Incidentally, this also provides an answer to what you wished to explain: that "they did not yearn" (referring to *ta'avah*) applies only to Torah, but their engagement would still include mitzvos. *Kal v'chomer*.

With respect and blessing.

## 8440

8440

By the Grace of G-d
Sunday, Parshas Korach, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

The 150th year since the Histalkus-Hilula of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe
To the students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch
For the Siyum celebration,
Montreal,
May they live, G-d willing.

Greetings and blessings!

In honor of the Siyum celebration on 4 Tammuz — the month of redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe — I send my blessing to the students who are completing their studies and to their parents, to the Roshei Yeshiva and the administration, and to all the participants in this Simchas Torah, may they live.

It is superfluous to emphasize that the inner intent of a "Siyum" in matters of Torah and mitzvos is that it should serve as a preparation for a new beginning and a transition to a higher level in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of mitzvos in daily life.

At the beginning of this week’s parsha, we are told of the dispute of Korach against Moshe Rabbeinu. In the Midrash, our Sages, of blessed memory, tell us various details regarding this, for every detail in Torah is also Torah — "Torah" comes from the word *hora'ah* (instruction) — a lesson and guidance. One of these details is that Korach asked Moshe Rabbeinu whether a house filled with sefarim requires a mezuzah on the door. Korach argued that a house filled with holy books contains much more than the two parshiyos of the mezuzah, and therefore a mezuzah is redundant. However, Moshe Rabbeinu replied that even such a house must have a mezuzah on the door.

The lesson from this, which is especially important for students who are completing their studies, is:

When a student of an educational institution *al taharas hakodesh* reaches the level of a "Siyum," he might perhaps think that he is already like "a house filled with holy books" and is therefore exempt from a "mezuzah." To this, he is told that even when one is at such a level, he must first have the protection and safeguard of a "mezuzah" on the "doors" of his mind and his heart.

The content of a mezuzah is the two parshiyos, **Shema** and **Vehaya im shamoa**, which demonstrate that a Jew, whether sitting at home or going out into the street, must always remember that he and everything he possesses belong to the Almighty — **Hashem Elokeinu Hashem Echad**. From this comes the immediate conclusion — **Vehaya im shamoa tishme'u** — to fulfill the commandments of the Almighty and to conduct oneself according to the will of the Almighty in all the details of daily life.

And this is what a student who is a "mesayeim" must remember: although *Talmud Torah k'neged kulam* (the study of Torah is equivalent to all [other mitzvos]), and he has, thank G-d, succeeded in his Torah studies, this is not enough if the knowledge is merely in his head like books on a shelf. The essential thing is that the Torah should penetrate and permeate the mind and the heart, the thoughts and the feelings, until it descends and reflects itself in all the details of daily life, in the fulfillment of mitzvos with *hiddur* and with joy.

May the Almighty grant that every one of the students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch should be at the level of a "house filled with holiness," and specifically with a kosher "mezuzah" on the "doors" of the mind and heart, so that wherever he finds himself and wherever he goes, **Hashem Elokeinu Hashem Echad** should be evident, permeated with *ahavas Hashem*, *ahavas haTorah*, and *ahavas Yisrael* that are all one. Then, surely, the promise will be fulfilled: "And I will provide rain for your land in its time..." — all the Divine blessings enumerated in the parsha, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With blessings for outstanding success and good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8443

B"H, 10 Tammuz, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the honorable Rabbi, the Gaon, the G-d-fearing, the distinguished, the scholar and son of scholars, a man of vitality and many accomplishments, a master of good deeds, our teacher Rabbi Raphael Baruch, may he live, the spokesman of the holy community of the city of Meknes, whose influence is spread throughout the entire country.

May you have abundant peace and much blessing!

After a very long interval, your esteemed letter reached me, and from it I learned that you are currently in England.

With a request for your forgiveness, I must express my sorrow that your honor has moved away from the flock of your congregation in your city of Meknes and the country. Even though, as I have heard, due to your age—may Hashem lengthen your days and years in goodness and pleasantness—you may not hold an official position, surely there are many ways to strengthen Torah and mitzvos even without an official post. Given the situation in your city and country—and who knows the situation better than you?—the influence of your honor there is needed more than ever.

It is understood and simple that I do not intend to complain about the past, contrary to the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory, but perhaps there is a possibility to return to your city and country in a suitable and positive manner, and to influence the other Sephardic rabbis in Morocco to stand guard, to look after the welfare of their brethren, and to shepherd the flock of their congregation—tens of thousands, may they increase—who dwell in those lands and are in need of a guard, and a guard for the holy guard, to lead them beside still waters, the living waters of the Torah of life and its mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "And he shall live by them."

In these days, the days of redemption of 12-13 Tammuz, in which my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi of Israel, was redeemed from his imprisonment for having risked his life in the campaigns of Hashem and His hosts—as is known to your honor, the story of these days is "remembered and observed"—may it be the will of Hashem that each and every one of us utilize all the strengths and possibilities granted from Above for the dissemination of Torah and tradition, down to our daily lives, in a manner of "increasing and adding light," and the merit of the many will assist him.

With respect and blessing for much success and for good tidings.

***

**Rabbi Raphael Baruch:** Toledano. Additional letters to him appear above in Vol. 16, 5812, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

**Statement of our Sages:** See Berachos 54a.

## 8444

B"H, 10 Tammuz, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs with noble character, scion of noble ancestors, etc., R' Sh. Z. Shlita,

Shalom u’Bracha!

As we approach the auspicious days of 12-13 Tammuz, may it be the will of Hashem that these days—which are "remembered and observed"—awaken within each of us, and within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, the inner depth and strength of will to utilize, to the fullest possible extent, all the possibilities and powers granted from Above, following the example of the Baal HaGeulah, may his merit protect us and all of Israel.

For this very awakening itself reveals additional powers and possibilities.

And if there are difficulties—even realistic ones—the lesson of these days is that one must not be deterred by any difficulty or obstacle. Go and learn: if one man, though he was exalted above the people, stood at his full stature against a tyrannical and hostile government and emerged victorious in all the areas for which he fought—to the point where, in many details, they not only answered "Amen" against their will, but even assisted him—then how much more so for us, who have merited to operate under incomparably favorable conditions. Especially since the path is already paved before us, for when the Gedolei Yisrael open a path and a channel, it becomes possible for many to do as they did and to succeed.

Despite the changes, preoccupations, etc., that have occurred since last year, I am certain that you are interested in knowing what is transpiring regarding the various projects in the field of "Chabad Research," printing, etc.

Enclosed are copies from this year, in which, naturally, the primary matters are those connected to Rabbeinu HaZaken and his affairs, as this year is the 150th anniversary of his histalkus-hillula, and it is a year of segulah.

I would like to note that Project 2 of the Center for Chabad Research is based on your initiative and proposal.

Regarding the major project concerning the "Seven Generations of Chabad," I am confident that the merit of Rabbeinu HaZaken will stand by us in this as well, so that there will be good prospects, leading to actual implementation.

With appreciation, honor, and with blessings for a Chag HaGeulah and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8436

B"H, Days of Redemption 12-13 Tammuz, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.
- The year 150 since the passing of Rabbeinu HaZaken -

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters.

Regarding the matters of these days: Preceding this redemption was the prayer and request of the Baal HaGeulah, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael: "May Hashem our G-d be with us, as He was with our fathers; may He not forsake us and may He not abandon us" — and as he interpreted and explained it, this is a language of prayer and request, and its content.

And "prayer does" (*tefillah osah*) — and according to the second interpretation of the verse (which my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, said at that time), it is a language of promise, for all the nations of the earth saw that the verse "Hashem is for me among those who help me..." was fulfilled in him, and He bestowed all good upon him.

And every single year during this period, it is an *eis ratzon* for each and every one, and an awakening to make good resolutions to walk in the ways of our fathers, the *baalei mesiras nefesh* for Torah and *mitzvos*, and especially in the matters for which the Baal HaGeulah sacrificed himself. Through this, "Hashem his G-d is with him," and there is no *aven* or *amal* (iniquity or toil), but rather he will go "from strength to strength." And until where? Until he "appears before G-d in Tzion," in the true and complete general redemption.

With blessings for good tidings in a revealed and manifest way,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8747

B"H, 13 Tammuz, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, man of action, man of character, etc., Rabbi Pinchas Mordechai, shlita,

Shalom u’vracha!

In response to your letters in which you invite me to participate in a collection of articles dedicated to the subject of teshuvah:

Generally, this is not the custom of the Beis HaRav of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and we hold to the tradition of our ancestors.

Nevertheless, due to the great importance of the matter and out of respect for you, I will take this opportunity to express, at least briefly, the sentiments of my heart—which I have already expressed verbally on several occasions, including at public gatherings. To begin with the core of the matter of teshuvah: according to the style of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch—this year being the 150th anniversary of his passing—the concept of teshuvah is not specifically about sins. After all, our Sages of blessed memory said that one should be in a state of teshuvah all his days. Rather, it is a matter of the "return of the soul." Since the neshamah is a part of Hashem and descended from a high peak to a deep pit to be clothed in a body, the concept of teshuvah is that the spirit should return to the Elokim who gave it, through mesiras nefesh, the surrender of one's will, and so on.

Every era has its own unique focus. In our time, and especially in these very recent years, we see a spiritual awakening—a phenomenon of "he prophesied, though he did not know what he prophesied"—which people have called "a return to the sources." In truth and in its inner essence, this is nothing other than what was mentioned above: the matter of "the spirit returning to the Elokim." We see this awakening primarily among the youth. For them, this matter is even more significant because it is more internal and more powerful, and also because they do not fear a change in their lifestyle, provided they feel that they are being given the truth without compromises, without window-dressing, and without pretense.

In this country especially, the nature of the youth is not like the nature of the youth in other countries. In those places, double the work was required: first, to uproot the false ideologies that were entrenched in many circles, including among the youth, and only afterward was it possible to plant the straight and correct view within them. This is not the case in this country, where the youth are like virgin soil, provided that one gives them the matter as it is.

We see clearly that those who are not afraid and who "present" the truth without compromises have found a true echo among the youth.

Although I do not wish to criticize, G-d forbid, I must emphasize that, to our great regret, this awakening has not been utilized (as it ought to be) at all—especially by those who should be the shepherds of the people, their teachers, and their spiritual guides. And the wise will understand.

And according to the instruction of our Sages of blessed memory that "the deed is the essential thing," it is understood that in all that I have written above, my intention is not for a sermon, etc. Rather, it is my hope that through your efforts, and through similar endeavors, a broad and highly energetic campaign will be launched to strengthen this awakening, and primarily—to bring it into action and into the daily life of all those whom your voice and words can reach. In a matter of pikuach nefashos, even in a case of doubt—and certainly in a case of a double doubt—one must act. May it be the will of Hashem that this campaign and activity will reveal and awaken the inner point of the soul within every single Jewish man and woman, which has always been faithful to Him, to Hashem our G-d, leading to the actual fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos. As is known from the words of the great teacher, the Rambam, every single Jewish man and woman desires to perform all the mitzvos and distance themselves from sins (Rambam, Hilchos Geirushin, end of chapter 2). When each person does everything that depends on them, and does so with a strong confidence that they are acting as an emissary of the Makom—who rules and governs in every place—and with words that come from the heart, which then enter the heart and achieve their effect, they are guaranteed success.

With respect and a blessing for success, awaiting good tidings.

## 8748

15 Tammuz, 5723

To the Annual Convention of the Rabbinical Council of America,
May they live,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your notification regarding the annual convention to be held on the upcoming [dates]...

It is my hope that the convention will place on its agenda matters of practical action related to utilizing the opportune moment created by the spiritual awakening pulsating through broad circles of our people, and especially within the youth.

Anyone whose heart is sensitive to what is occurring among the youth knows that our current era, which is full of events, has brought about a spiritual revolution in broad circles, following the adventures and disillusionment with various strange ideologies and movements, as well as several other factors that this is not the place to elaborate upon.

However, for many, this awakening is still in the category of "he prophesied and did not know what he prophesied," while for others, the awakening is more tangible and clear, to the point that they have called it a "return to the sources." The common denominator between them is that this awakening has created an opportune moment to set broad circles of our people upon the line of truth and the straight path—the path of Torah and mitzvos. But the tragedy is that this opportune moment is not being utilized as it should be, and many are still groping in the dark for lack of proper influence and guidance to show the people of Hashem the way they should walk, and primarily—the deeds they should do.

This is especially important regarding the youth, whose nature is such that any awakening is experienced with greater inwardness and intensity, and they are not deterred by a change in their lifestyle if they only have the feeling and inner recognition that they are being given the truth without compromise, without artifice or pretense. Any positive influence is multiplied among them many times over, and "a good hour is better sooner."

Moving from one topic to a related one—regarding the status and situation of the younger sons and daughters of Israel, concerning whom it is specifically stated, "And you shall teach them to your children" in the first paragraph of the Shema, immediately upon the acceptance of the yoke of Heaven, and it is repeated in the second paragraph, due to the great necessity for a full education in purity and holiness, and "the study of Torah is equal to them all."

Even in the time of the Gemara, there were those who would fulfill the mitzvah of Torah study with one verse in the morning and one verse in the evening, and others who would toil in Torah day and night. How much more so in these days, when one must strive with all one's might so that every child of Israel learns holy subjects all day long, and at the very least, that they study in educational institutions known in this country as *yeshiva ketana*. But at the same time, one must not despair or abandon, Heaven forbid, those who study in public schools. The call of the hour is to strive with all one's might to guard this ember so it does not go out, Heaven forbid, and at the very least, through a **kosher prayer** every day, so that the name of Heaven becomes habitual in the mouths of the little ones. It is understood that this is not the final goal, for the necessity is, as mentioned, holy studies all day long, but do not consider this a small matter, especially since we are promised that "one mitzvah leads to another."

Unfortunately, one of the afflictions of the time is that there are those who fight against the mention of the name of Heaven in public schools, and they cause a *chillul Hashem* so alarming that its like has not been heard until this day. It is superfluous to emphasize again and again that we are speaking of a kosher prayer, meaning one that is non-denominational. And for this to be achieved as desired and in practice, one must reject the reading of the Bible in schools, since that could provide an opening for them to demand that it be read, and *lehavdil*, etc.

Based on the instruction of our Sages, *maaseh rav* (an action is the greatest teaching), and in order to refute the opinion of those who are mistaken or those who wish to cloak their opposition to the mention of the name of Heaven in schools in the guise of the *Shulchan Aruch*, it is known that one of the "holy labors" of the Baal Shem Tov was that he would strive to ensure that the name of Heaven was habitual in the mouths of all, including simple men, women, and children, by asking them and inquiring after their welfare in such a way that they would answer "Baruch Hashem" and the like. And as my father-in-law, the Rebbe, **emphasized**—this was not only in the synagogue and at home, but also in the street, in shops, and in places of labor and work, at all times and in all places (see at length *Sefer HaMaamarim*, Yiddish, 5701-5705, by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the *maamar* beginning *Ve'atah Kadosh Yoshev Tehillos Yisrael*, p. 138 and onwards).

Also in the same vein as mentioned above is the matter of federal aid to religious schools, *parochial schools*, regarding which I have already spoken several times about the great necessity for this. There is no basis to oppose it; on the contrary, it is a holy duty for each and every one to demand this aid with a full mouth, etc.

May it be the will that the members of the Rabbinical Council, *shlita*, the spiritual leaders and shepherds of Israel in many holy communities—may they increase—and the annual convention in particular, will take a vigorous and clear position on all the aforementioned matters, with a practical program of actual deeds. The merit of the many will assist them so that they succeed in this, as well as in other matters for the improvement of the state of Torah and mitzvos in daily life, each among the members of his congregation. There is always room for preference in matters of holiness and good, for their source is in the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He. May the Almighty grant that they do so with the appropriate energy and with joy and inner recognition that they are emissaries of the Omnipresent, and from them, many will learn to do likewise. The fulfillment of this mission is also the channel and vessel for receiving the blessing of the Almighty, each according to their needs and those of their families, may they live, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With respect and blessing for much success.

## 8489

B"H, 23 Tammuz, 5723
Brooklyn.

Yitzchak Elazar, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter in which you ask regarding the rulings of the Alter Rebbe in a case where there is a difference between his Shulchan Aruch and his Siddur, how we should act.

It is known that the Siddur is *basra'i* (the later work), and we follow the rulings of the Siddur. See regarding this the sefer *Shaar HaKollel* on the Siddur (by Rabbi Lavut), and with more explanation in *Piskei HaSiddur* by Rabbi Naeh, in which the legal rulings where there is a difference between the Shulchan Aruch and the Siddur have been collected.

And since everything is by *hashgacha pratis*, it is my duty and privilege to urge you regarding the necessity of setting times for the study of *pnimiyus haTorah*, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus—a set time every day, with an increase on the day of Shabbos, which is holy to Hashem.

I am sure you are aware of the three *shiurim* of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, and at the very least, you should maintain them from here on in.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

#### ***8489***

**Yitzchak Elazar:** Mashkowitz, Mt. Kisco.

## 8550

B"H, 24 Tammuz, 5723
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., Moreinu HaRav Yaakov Moshe,
May he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from the night of the second day, in which you ask my opinion regarding replacing the Machzor used until now with a new Machzor, etc.,

Since the determination of whether the new Machzor possesses advantages over the one used until now depends upon an examination of the new Machzor **in all necessary detail**, I am not in a position to offer an opinion on your question.

And since the burden of proof lies upon the one who wishes to change, it is understood that, as mentioned above, the review must be from beginning to end and in all its details; and in a case of doubt, it is better to refrain and not act.

The hope is strong that, in accordance with the name of the shul, there is a fixed time for Torah study—not only in the revealed aspects of Torah, but also in the teachings of the Arizal, which in our generation have been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. This is surely a significant matter, one that obligates and grants merit, and for one such as you, further elaboration is surely unnecessary.

With respect and blessing for good tidings in all the above.

#### ***8550***

**Moreinu HaRav Yaakov Moshe:** Geniuyish, St. Louis.

**To replace the Machzor:** In his letter: "When the shul was on Blackstone Street, the Rebbe of Lubavitch permitted the use of the *Avodas Yisrael* Machzor, Nusach Sefard, with English translation, and we have always used this... because a Machzor with Nusach HaAri z"l with an English translation was not available. However, we have now found a new Machzor, Nusach Sefard, with a superior translation and clear, elevated English. The name of this Machzor is *Machzor Rosh Hashanah Yom Kippur* with the commentary of Birnbaum, printed by the Hebrew Publishing Company... Therefore, I have come to ask regarding this matter if it is appropriate for us to purchase these Birnbaum Machzorim, Nusach Sefard, in place of *Avodas Yisrael*."

## 851

[24 Tammuz 5723]

...Following up on what we discussed during your stay here regarding the place of study for your son, may he live, I refrained from writing to you or to your son, may he live, in the middle of the school year for several reasons. Among them is the obvious fact that it is impossible to write anything contrary to the ruling of the Shulchan Aruch that a son should study specifically in the place his heart desires—and furthermore, it is significant that this instruction is placed not in the laws of Torah study, but in the laws of honoring one’s parents! On the other hand, I did not want to exacerbate the situation at home, hoping that the matter would resolve itself, and I justified my silence by the fact that it was the middle of the school year.

Now, as the time for registration for the upcoming school year approaches, I will permit myself to express my strong hope that both you and your wife, may she live, will allow your son, may he live, to study in the place that his heart has desired and yearned for for some time now. It is certainly best that this be done with your full consent. Furthermore, I must point out that your son’s desire in this matter is very strong and is by no means temporary or fleeting (as you have surely observed over the many months that have passed). That is to say, forcing him to do otherwise will affect him day by day, with consequences such as nervous tension, damage to your relationship, a lack of diligence in his studies, a hostile attitude toward the institution where he would be forced to study, **and much more**. These are phenomena that parents in general—and especially those whom Hashem has blessed with G-d-fearing, talented, and sensitive children—must surely do everything in their power to prevent, and to do so with joy, for the well-being of your son, may he live, is at stake, both physically and spiritually.

Due to the urgency of the matter, I am sending this letter as express and urgent, and I thank you in advance if you will inform me of good news regarding all of this as soon as possible.

#### ***851***

Published in Likutei Sichos, Vol. 21, p. 355.

## 8753

8753

B”H, Rosh Chodesh Menachem-Av, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

As we have entered the month of Menachem-Av, may it be the will of our Father, the Father of Mercy, to comfort His people Israel with a double consolation, as explained in the words of our Sages regarding this.

Just as it was with the matter that caused the exile—the breaking of the Tablets—where the consolation was "double for wisdom,"

It can be said that in these final generations, when, as the Arizal states, it is a mitzvah to reveal this wisdom—and especially since the publication of the Iggeres HaKodesh of the Baal Shem Tov, where it became known to all that the coming of Malka Meshicha depends on spreading the wellsprings outward—

And surely, this dissemination is by Divine Providence, and all the more so, *kal v'chomer*, from the matter of individual Divine Providence that exists in every detail of the world, as explained well in the teachings of Chassidus—

The double consolation will come and be hastened through the doubling and multiplication of the study of the revealed Torah and Chassidus, in accordance with the ruling of our Rebbe, the author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, and as hinted in his name—*Shnei Ohr* (Two Lights), and there is no "light" other than Torah.

This year being the one hundred and fiftieth year since his passing.

With blessings that these days will soon be transformed into gladness and joy,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8,454

B"H, 4 Menachem Av, 5723
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and pious individual, engaged in communal needs, Rabbi Pinchas Aharon, may he live:

Shalom and blessing!

...Regarding the matter of the telephone that you wrote about — it is not at all comparable to the issue of a microphone: 1) The speaker is not aware of it at all. 2) It is not agreeable to him (and on the contrary, it is against his will) that people in another room should hear. 3) It is not a *pesik reisha* **at all**, since only speaking in a loud voice and in close proximity to the telephone activates the telephone. And there are other reasons as well. And you will understand.

With blessing.

#### ***8,454***

**Rabbi Pinchas Aharon, may he live:** Weberman, Miami. Additional letters to him — see above, 8,191, and the references in the footnotes there.

**Regarding the telephone:** In his letter: In *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 2, p. 506, it is recounted that the Rebbe Rayatz, of blessed memory, would place a piece of wood on Erev Shabbos and Yom Tov to prop up the telephone in the room of his father, the Rebbe Rashab, of blessed memory, so that he could hear the *davening* from the other room. Perhaps we could derive a permit for a microphone, or a "tape recorder," if the speaker himself does not intend to speak into it.

## 8550

B"H, 7 Menachem Av, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Avreich, Raphael, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 4 Menachem Av, in which you write regarding how to influence a bochur, etc.

In general, it is understood that this depends on his knowledge, his character traits, and so on. Therefore, one must consult with those who know him; as it is already said, "In the multitude of counselors there is safety." It is certainly superfluous to emphasize what our Sages of blessed memory say: "Words that come from the heart enter the heart." Therefore, when one speaks with heartfelt words, there is a great possibility of succeeding. One of the primary things is to be a living example through one's daily conduct, which is more effective than words. May it be His will that you succeed in all that was mentioned above.

And since everything is by Divine Providence, it is my duty (and privilege) to arouse you regarding the necessity of having a set time every day for the study of *Piniyus HaTorah*, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus, with an addition on the day of Shabbos, which is holy to Hashem. The importance of this is explained in many *sefarim*, especially in *Kuntres Eitz Chayim* by the Rebbe Rashab, and in *Kuntres Limud HaChassidus* by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 8740

B"H, 21 Menachem Av, 5723
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent in communal affairs, etc., R' Nissan, shlita,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your two letters. I truly wished to fulfill your request regarding a letter in connection with the publication of your sefer, *Taharas HaMayim*. However, the difficulty is that I am surrounded by many preoccupations, and I do not know when I will have the free time to review it again, even cursorily. Therefore, if it is already prepared for print, it is questionable whether it is worthwhile to wait for the aforementioned, especially since the author has already proven himself, and his sefer has already proven its worth.

On this occasion, I must express my great distress regarding the absolute silence of [the rabbinical organizations] concerning prayer in public schools. Only a few days remain until the start of the school year in these schools. As the saying goes, "A mistake that has become established is difficult to correct" (*shavsta keivan d'al al*); how much more so regarding a matter that is entirely contrary to holiness, where there will be a **tremendous** loss—hundreds of thousands of our Jewish brethren will, G-d forbid, be deprived of even a single mention of the Name of Heaven once a day, and even more so, and this is the main point, prayer on those days. It requires great study (or rather, it requires no study at all): are there any matters more important for which the Rabbis bear responsibility to act? Especially as I have said many times, the silence of Jewish organizations is tantamount to an admission to those who oppose holiness, for their audacity is great, and they speak in the name of *Klal Yisrael*, yet no one opens their mouth to protest. It is difficult to elaborate on such an alarming matter.

Regarding the content of your first letter concerning the well-known *mikveh*: what is **not understood at all** is what the prohibition is against checking a *mikveh* that, apparently, for **decades** it has not occurred to anyone to check what is being done at the **foundation** of its *kashrus*. After all, even a spring is susceptible to changes, and especially since, as is the way in all cities in the United States, there have certainly been various excavations, etc., etc., which are liable to affect the aforementioned. The matter itself is a matter of *d'oraisa*, etc., etc., and surely for one such as yourself, there is no need for elaboration or explanation on this.

I was pleased to learn that you are in "green pastures" (*ne'os deshe*). May it be the will of Hashem that you utilize this time to its fullest, especially since the verse explicitly states, "He makes me lie down in green pastures; He leads me beside still waters," etc., etc. See also the *reshimos* of the *Admur HaTzemach Tzedek* on this verse.

With respect and blessing for a healthy and happy summer and always.

## 8557

B"H, 23 Menachem Av, 5723
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Following a pause, I received your letter from the 18th of Menachem Av.

It is understandable that I was alarmed by its opening, regarding your thought to discontinue your study of our holy Torah in the yeshiva, or even within a framework that is less than a yeshiva setting.

Based on my previous letters, a lengthy response is surely unnecessary, as this is not at all desirable. Especially at your age, we are commanded to study Torah in both its revealed aspects and Chassidus. Hashem does not deal tyrannically with His creations ; therefore, the ability has certainly been granted, and the matter depends only on will and choice—the choice as it is written: "See, I have set before you... **and you shall choose life**."

I hope that you are keeping up with the three known daily study portions of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you and all that you write regarding them at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

**Hashem does not deal tyrannically:** Avodah Zarah 3a.

## 8758

B"H, 25 Menachem Av, 5723
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, engaged in communal needs,
R' Yehoshua Mordechai and his wife, Mrs. Gita
Reizel, may they live.

Shalom u’Bracha!

I have read your letter, which was included with the letter from your son, may he live, and surely by now you have received my response to him.

On this occasion, I wish to express my hope that each of you is doing everything possible in the dissemination of Yiddishkeit in general, and the wellsprings [of Chassidus] in particular, as the necessity for this is explained in many places. This is especially true for the residents of the Holy City of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established, and for those who have merited and succeeded in being related to our Rebbes, the Nesi’im of Chabad.

We have been promised that "one who comes to purify himself is assisted," and the precision of the Alter Rebbe—in this year, the 150th anniversary of his histalkus and hillula—is well known: that one is also assisted in purifying others.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

## 6761

B"H, 28 Menachem Av, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs with noble character, a scion of a noble lineage, etc., R' Shazar, shlita,

Peace and blessing!

My secretary, Mr. Nissan Mindel, has just returned from his trip and conveyed to me the details of his meeting and conversation with you. I thank you from the bottom of my heart for your friendly regards and sentiments, and I also thank you for receiving my secretary with such openness and joy, despite your many preoccupations.

On this occasion, I wish to express to you the deep impression made upon me by the news of your participation with the community in Kfar Chabad on the occasion of Tisha B'Av—may it be transformed into joy and gladness. You surely intended by this to express a sense of unity with the fate of our brethren, the Children of Israel, shlita, in our former country, a shared heart with the residents of the village who came from there, and, to a certain extent, a participation in the spirit of mesiras nefesh and the tradition of the forefathers that permeates Kfar Chabad and its residents. My prayer is that the residents of the village, who are the first to break through the barrier, will open the conduit for a mass exodus from there in the near future. May the gates of mercy above, which have never been locked, open the gates below for the departure of our brethren from the straits into the expanse. May it be His will that this happens very soon, and may we merit to connect redemption to redemption and to witness the consolation of Tzion and Yerushalayim, speedily and in our time.

In accordance with the aforementioned aspiration, I am certain that you will continue to take an increasing interest in expanding the borders of the village and its capacity for absorption, especially since Divine Providence has granted you, at this time, the ability and opportunity to act on behalf of the village to an even greater extent. My hope is strong that you will utilize this opportunity to its fullest; and one only urges those who are already diligent.

I acknowledge with many thanks the receipt of your previous letter, and I shall return to it as is appropriate. I have written this primarily to express the aforementioned sentiments as promptly as possible.

With appreciation, respect, and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 6862

1 Elul, 5723
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi Shlomo, may he live and be well, who is engaged in the work of the Tzeirei Agudas Chabad:

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Sunday.

Many thanks for the good news regarding the activities to establish and disseminate Yiddishkeit in the city of Minneapolis and its surroundings, within the framework of the branch of the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch directed by your brother-in-law, the esteemed Rabbi Moshe, may he live and be well, who is full of energy, etc. It was certainly a pleasure for me to read at the end of your letter that your wife, may she live, also assisted in the aforementioned, exerted effort in this, and was successful.

This is especially true since, in the field of education, the ability of the daughters of Israel—each of whom is called a daughter of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah—to accomplish more than the men is something that can be seen tangibly.

May it be the will of Hashem that your aforementioned success awakens in you additional strengths to act in the times ahead in the same direction. Do not be satisfied only with those who are already within the "four amos" of Torah and mitzvos, but strive also to "bring forth the precious from the vile," as is well known from the words of Chazal regarding this (Bava Metzia 85a).

Although the time is not at all conducive to elaborating on the second half of your letter—especially since these matters are well-known in many places, including in print—nevertheless, as an expression of gratitude for the satisfaction you caused with the first half of your letter, I will not suffice with a mere remark, but will provide a few points, etc.

Regarding the matter of growing a beard: it is simple to **all** opinions that there is **a matter to this**. All the differences of opinion are only whether it is permissible to be lenient when one is, so to speak, forced by the aforementioned circumstances, and whether this is a prohibition of the Rabbis or of the Torah. However, as mentioned, it is simple in the revealed Torah, and especially and with greater intensity in the inner dimension of the Torah, that in the *tikunei dikna* (as they are called in the Zohar and in the books of Kabbalah, which are accepted with full authority of the Torah Shebe'al Peh by **everyone** among Bnei Yisrael), there is an extremely lofty holiness. And the attribute of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is "measure for measure": the attribute of the (lower) man’s (tikunei dikna) will draw down this attribute from above, as it were.

And it is certainly a matter that everyone agrees is called "the image of G-d."

According to the opinion of the Admur the Tzemach Tzedek and many other poskim before and after him, it is a clear prohibition from the Torah, as explained in his responsa, and in addition to them—in his *Piskei Dinim*. See also *Darchei Teshuvah* on Yoreh Deah, and *Responsa Minchas Elazar*, Vol. 2, Siman 40. Many opinions on this are collected, at length, both according to the revealed Torah and the inner dimension of the Torah, in the book *Amudei Arazim* by Rabbi Margalit, may he live and be well, of the Holy City of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established. He copied wonderful and even startling things regarding the growing of a beard and the opposite. There, one also finds a letter from the Gaon the Rogatchover (Rabbi Y. Rosen) that it is an absolute prohibition.

The reasons for the negative position that you wrote, in order:

a) The concern that by growing a beard, it will enter his mind that this exempts him from other matters of Torah and mitzvos.

The fallacy of this argument is understood: if so, there is no end to the matter, and one would have to abolish every *hidur mitzvah* (beautification of a mitzvah), and certainly matters of *mehadrin min hamehadrin*, and if you will say so—even the decrees of the Rabbis, etc. On the contrary, according to the announcement and promise of Chazal that "one mitzvah leads to another," every addition (even) in the beautification of a mitzvah eventually leads to adding in the mitzvos themselves, and this is well understood.

Perhaps your intention in the aforementioned is the matter of *michzei k'yuhara* (appearing as arrogance). But, thank G-d, in recent times it does not appear as arrogance at all. Not only that, but there are many other customs—such as the tzitzis being worn on the outside—which have become widespread even in Lithuanian yeshivos. And it is simple that even according to those who are lenient in the current case, this is not comparable to the matter of wearing tzitzis on the outside.

b) Your writing that one who is learned in the depths of halacha has the "weaponry" to fight against the world, as has been the case until now.

Your entire statement is a great wonder, for in close proximity to the Giving of the Torah, there was the opposite matter of "I am" and "You shall have no other," and among them—even those who saw the *Maaseh Merkavah* (and did not only study this matter, as is told in the Midrash). And from the first Golden Calf to what happened in close proximity to the building of the First Temple, as is brought regarding the wonder of their wisdom in matters of Torah, that all Torah scholars appear to them as... (Sanhedrin 102a). And similarly in the Second Temple, Tzadok and Baitos, and up to our own days—even in this very city, those who stand at the head of various movements that are against traditional Judaism studied beforehand and were learned in the depths of halacha, etc.

c) Your writing that it is possible that the logic for growing a beard is not for the sake of Heaven, but for ulterior motives, etc.

It is a *psak din*: a person should always engage in Torah and mitzvos even if it is not for its own sake, for from "not for its own sake" one comes to "for its own sake."

d) Regarding... your wife, may she live:

Having known some of her family, my hope is strong that, in the end, not only will there be no opposition on her part, but on the contrary, she will assist. Furthermore, your words—regarding fear of Heaven and Torah and mitzvos—will be elevated in her eyes and will be accepted more in the future. For it is close to saying that now, when she hears a demand from you in this, an idea is awakened in her mind (in the style of Chazal) that "the one who moistens in order to moisten" must himself be much more than that which he is moistening.

It is understood and simple that it has not escaped me that in several countries, and in this country, G-d-fearing people in truth have permitted the aforementioned, with various explanations, etc. Consequently, in the generation that followed, there were also G-d-fearing and pious people who practiced this themselves. But it certainly has not escaped you either that the change that occurred in the meantime—that then, in certain countries and at certain times, it seemed to those who permitted it that this was the only way to save many of Bnei Yisrael from the other extreme, and they labored and toiled to find a permit, etc. And a word to the wise is sufficient. And indeed, even regarding clear and major prohibitions of the Torah, such matters are found. And not only that, but even in the Written Torah—the whole matter of the "beautiful woman" (*yefas toar*), for which a clear permit was given by the Torah. And Chazal also explained the reason. And "do not judge your fellow until..." and perhaps in those countries and in those days, who knows, etc.

But as mentioned, thank G-d, this is not the situation at all in our time. And anyone who truly wants to—has the ability (and would that he would utilize it to its fullest)—to disseminate Judaism without compromises wherever his hand can reach; and in this, the current case is included.

In my conversation with someone who visited me with similar arguments to the aforementioned, and wanted to show sharpness and expertise to permit it, I asked him (with the preface of a request that he answer naturally without intent): What is the reason that when they depict the face of Moshe Rabbeinu or Aharon HaKohen—both by Bnei Yisrael and, to distinguish, by the nations of the world—they depict them specifically with a large beard? And if regarding Aharon they rely on the verse in Tehillim that "the beard of Aharon descends upon his garments," why is it so depicted regarding Moshe Rabbeinu? And he received the Torah from Sinai, and everything that a veteran student is destined to innovate was given to Moshe at Sinai, and "the power of leniency is greater."

And being an honest man, he answered me that even in his own mind, when he pictures for himself—not only Moshe Rabbeinu, but even someone in the generations after him who observes Torah and mitzvos—it is simple to him that he had a beard descending upon his garments without having touched it at all.

And to conclude with a matter of the day, that we are beginning the month of Elul: it is brought in the books of Kabbalah, and these things are brought in the book *Likutei Torah* (part Devarim 32b) by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe—this year being the 150th year since his passing and *hillula*—that the thirteen attributes of mercy, the *tikunei dikna* from above, shine. And would that he does not touch the vessel of their reception: the thirteen *tikunei dikna* of the lower man.

With blessings for good news and to be inscribed and sealed for good.

**M. Schneerson**

## 6663

B"H, 2 Elul, 5723
Brooklyn.

To the avreich Ezra Binyamin, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Elul, in which you write various reasonings regarding the continuation of your studies in the near future and ask for my opinion on the matter.

As it appears to me, it is appropriate that you study in one of the yeshivos in Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt and established speedily by Moshiach Tzidkeinu. As for which yeshiva, you should decide after you arrive there, visit the yeshivos, and consult with your friends in that place; for "in the multitude of counselors there is salvation."

And if these days are generally days of preparation for the coming year, how much more so when the plan for the year also includes ascending to the Holy Land, the palace of the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He. Certainly, along with the increased demands placed upon a person, he is also given additional strengths to fulfill this new demand, and with even greater intensity and vigor.

The manner of this preparation is explained in many places, and in every case, it must be with strong bitachon in Hashem, who oversees each and every one with Hashgacha Pratis [as is explained at length in the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov regarding this matter of Hashgacha Pratis], and with simcha (of a mitzvah, see Rambam, end of Hilchos Lulav) and a glad heart.

Especially since one sees tangibly that through this, one’s success in preparation is increased, and this is simple to understand.

I trust you are keeping up with the three daily shiurim—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—as is well known, in addition to your diligent and persistent study of Nigleh and Chassidus.

May it be Hashem’s will that you bring good news regarding all that has been mentioned, especially since we have entered the month of Elul, which, according to the words of Rabbeinu HaZaken—this year being the 150th year since his histalkus and hillula—is according to the parable of the King in the field, who receives everyone with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to all, etc. (Likutei Torah, Devarim 32:2).

With blessings for a kesivah v'chasimah tovah,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

S. M. Simpson
Secretary

2 Elul, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Shalom Levin

Greetings and blessings,

Following the long interval since our meeting, you will surely be surprised to receive a letter from me. However, I hope that just as our meeting and the content of our conversation remained in my memory, they have remained in yours as well—especially since our discussion touched upon matters of public concern, which deserve to be continued.

The immediate reason that has led me to write to you now is the news published in the press that you have been elected Chairman of the International Federation of Teachers’ Associations (IFTA). I wish to express my heartfelt wishes that you utilize to their fullest the new opportunities that have fallen to your lot for a true purpose: the establishment of proper education in all the countries of the world, and in our Holy Land in particular. For when a person accepts a new position, he receives additional responsibility, and Divine Providence surely grants the ability to carry it out.

In continuation of our aforementioned conversation, allow me to express an idea. Although, on the face of it, it may not seem appropriate for this occasion due to the somewhat somber nature of the subject, the verse already states, "In all sorrow there is profit," and the profit is the moral lesson contained within the matter. This is what I intend, and the matter is as follows:

When one observes elementary schools everywhere, it is understood that their purpose is to guide students through foundational stages toward specific achievements. Generally, these fall into two main areas: a) imparting a body of knowledge to the student, and b) educating the student and preparing him for appropriate conduct in his life once he grows up. Each of these two areas is, of course, divided into several categories. Regarding the area of education in particular, it includes the sphere of interpersonal relationships and the sphere of the student’s "private" development—how a person relates to his own desires and cravings.

One who observes the results of elementary schools in the United States and several European countries—and according to my information, the situation is similar in Eretz Yisrael—comes to the conclusion that in the sphere of education, elementary schools have achieved significant success in the part concerning interpersonal relationships, in reducing the barriers between person and person and bringing them closer together, and in general, in matters now called "democratic" (this is in addition to the achievements in the area of imparting knowledge). It is understood that, as in every matter, there are exceptions here as well, where intentionally or unintentionally, schools have been utilized in the opposite direction, but we are speaking of the majority and the general state of affairs.

And from here to the somber point: the aforementioned observation also leads to the recognition that elementary schools have **not** succeeded in the sphere of the "private" development of the students. That is to say, in the sphere of restraining desires. Only thanks to the influence of the home and religious education have they not completely cast off the yoke of culture and turned the world into a dense forest—a "jungle," in the vernacular.

Therefore, we see that in those countries where the influence of parents has weakened for various reasons, juvenile delinquency has grown out of all proportion compared to other countries, even though the standard of the schools is more or less equal in all of them.

I do not have the statistics to prove the above conclusion with numbers, but as you are an expert in this field, this is not necessary.

Indeed, there is no wonder in what is stated above. Regarding the expansion of a student’s knowledge, there are many ways to encourage him and awaken his desire for progress and achievement through explanation and means that affect him immediately or in the near future. Similarly, regarding the development of a "democratic" sense and the relationship between person and person, the very "mechanical" situation of the student being in the company of several boys and girls already does much to develop this sense. This is not the case, however, regarding the restraint of desires. This is not something that comes about by itself. As the well-known example goes, a person cannot lift himself up by grabbing his own hair and pulling upward; rather, a point outside of himself is required to lean upon. In our generation, we have witnessed, to our great sorrow, what can be expected from relying on the student to "lean" on the sense of justice and integrity that the teacher teaches him, or on the influence of his older brother, or even on the fear of the policeman. From year to year, the youth find new stratagems to free themselves from the fear of the policeman and the judge, and the plague of delinquency continues to spread. And to the extent that human culture in general is a broken reed to lean upon, we have seen in the country of Germany, whose superiority in philosophical systems and even "morality" was well known, but which in practice raised generations of beasts of prey in human form.

It is clear that there is no other way to plant decent and tangible discipline in the hearts of children and youth than through fear or love of a power higher than man himself. Only in this way is it truly possible to guide and educate them to restrain their desires and will. This is not a matter that can be delayed until the child is eighteen, or even thirteen, and only then begin to give them this education, while until then they walk in the stubbornness of their hearts, in the hope that the fear of flesh and blood will guide them in the path of good and uprightness.

As stated, there seems to be no other way than to root in the hearts of children, from the dawn of their childhood, a strong faith in the Creator of the world, who is also its active Guide even now—in the style of our Sages, of blessed memory, that there is an Eye that sees and an Ear that hears, and all your deeds are written in a book; a book that cannot be forged, and an Eye and Ear that cannot be bribed or led astray by all sorts of cunning and sophistry.

And in this point of faith in the Creator of the world and its Guide, every single one of the members of the nations of the world is also obligated according to our Torah, the Torah of life, and furthermore [and essentially in certain circles], this faith is also required by common sense.

Therefore, any school whose curriculum includes the matter of education—moral education, and not just democratic—must have as one of its foundations the aforementioned matter of faith. And not as an abstract study, but as a matter that touches upon daily life, and not only on Shabbos and Yom Tov. On the contrary, the essence of faith must be expressed in the weekdays and in mundane matters, to permeate them with holiness, or at the very least, the acceptance of the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven.

The conclusions correspond, as stated above, to what I have seen in various countries in Europe and in the U.S., and according to my information, also in Eretz Yisrael. And surely you have the possibilities to influence in the desired direction, not only in the land upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year, but also abroad. And although there are schools called simply "state schools," without the addition of the word "religious," according to what has been said, it is simple that the difference should only be regarding the quantity of hours dedicated to religious studies. But if, G-d forbid, the school is devoid of religiosity entirely, then it is inherently lacking a matter which, in this generation, is one of the primary tasks of the school: to educate the student to be a person worthy of the name, in contrast to the life of a beast. For first and foremost, the superiority of man over the beast is that man is not enslaved to instincts, desires, and natural tendencies, but rather, at the very least, strives to restrain them and rule over them.

I remember what you said to me in our conversation, that you are only a secretary in the Teachers’ Federation and many matters are not within your purview, etc. But I believe that even then I responded to this, that the intention is not to demand this of you in an official capacity, but an appeal to one who has been given the possibilities and strengths to find ways to rectify the existing situation, which, to our great sorrow, is not improving but, on the contrary, is going from bad to worse.

In any case, we are now speaking of the Chairman of a world federation.

Seemingly, it is strange that I am directing this appeal to a member of a party that is not counted among the religious parties, and on the contrary, a socialist party, etc., etc. But it is superfluous to elaborate that the situation now is not at all the same as it was at the time of the rise of the socialist system, and especially since, even from the outset, the assumption that socialism requires a war against religion was not justified, and all the more so now.

May it be the will that even if, after the first reading of this letter, this appeal seems a bit strange to you, considering the great value of the matter, you will reflect upon what has been said once more, without prejudice, calmly and uprightly. Then you will surely find several ways and means to act in the aforementioned direction, and the merit of the many will assist you.

With respect and blessing—and in accordance with the custom of Yisrael, which is Torah—with the blessing of *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah*.

On this occasion, I will express my thanks once again for continuing to send me the publications of the Teachers’ Federation, and my hope is that you will do so in the future as well. Thank you in advance.

## 6766

B"H, 19 Elul, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Noam Leon,

Shalom u’Bracha!

It was with pleasure that I learned of your assistance, both in the past and in the present, to the Yeshiva "Achie Temimim" in your city.

It is my firm hope that you will surely continue in this, and with an increase, in accordance with the requirement of our Sages that we must always ascend in matters of holiness. This is especially true given that the institution has progressed in its development and brings benefit and honor to the city and the district; certainly, as the mayor, you have the capacity to act, and the merit of the many will assist you.

As we stand in the month of Elul, the month of mercy—and especially as we come from Chai Elul, the birthday of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, this year being the one hundred and fiftieth anniversary of his passing—it is timely to mention what is explained regarding this month by way of a parable: of a king who, before entering his city, is met by the townspeople who go out to greet him in the field. At that time, anyone who wishes to go out to greet him is permitted to do so, and he receives them all with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to everyone, etc. (Likutei Torah, Re'eh, 32a). In this, there is a special empowerment to perform every good deed and to succeed.

With respect and with blessings for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

## 6767

B"H, 19 Elul, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

District Officer, Rehovot

May it be the will that each of us utilizes this opportunity to its fullest.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8678

B"H, 19 Elul, 5723
Brooklyn.

To the G-d-fearing, honorable, and distinguished, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Yaakov, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 15 Elul, in which you inquire regarding the *nusach* of *davening*.

Based on what we have heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *Nasi Yisrael*, one should not pressure students in the Reshet schools or similar institutions regarding changing the *nusach* of *davening* to which they are accustomed.

On the other hand, those students who wish to change, it is understood that they may do so.

Furthermore, since it is possible to change from *Nusach Ashkenaz* to *Nusach Sefard*, and from *Nusach Sefard* to *Nusach Ari*, but not the reverse, those who wish to change must resolve that they will indeed *daven* [in the new *nusach*] from this point forward.

It is my hope that they have begun the school year with the *hisorerus* and vitality as is required and commanded of us in our Torah, the Torah of life, and especially according to what is explained in the teachings of Chassidus.

And indeed, this year is the one hundred and fiftieth year since the *histalkus* and *hillula* of the Alter Rebbe.

With blessings for success in his holy work and for a *ksiva v'chasima tova*.

## 8,159

B"H, 19 Elul, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Year of the 150th anniversary of the passing of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch,

Chief Rabbi,
Constantinople, may it be protected.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive regards from you through the honorable Rabbi, Chassid, G-d-fearing man, involved in communal needs, etc., Rabbi Moshe Yitzchok Hecht, shlita, upon his return from his travels and his visit to our camp. He also told me of the gracious reception you extended to him, and I offer you my sincere thanks.

I am certain that you are utilizing your high position and all available opportunities to strengthen the Torah—the Torah of life—and its mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "and live by them," as the hand of Hashem is upon you. If it has always been the duty and privilege of every individual to bring our brothers, the Children of Israel, closer to their Father in Heaven and to establish them on the path of Torah and mitzvos in their daily lives, then this is all the more true in our times, and especially regarding a Rabbi and shepherd in Israel. May it be His will that you do so with joy and a glad heart, and in a manner that is "ever-increasing," in accordance with the directive of our Sages of blessed memory: "We increase in matters of holiness."

Since we are proceeding from the auspicious day of Chai Elul, the birthday of the two great luminaries, our Rebbe the Baal Shem Tov and our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, it is timely to mention the teaching of the Alter Rebbe—which is the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov—regarding the theme of this month, the month of mercy and favor. It is analogous to a king before he enters his city and his palace, when he is found in the field and all the people of the city go out to greet him; at that time, everyone can approach him, and the king shows a smiling countenance to everyone and receives their requests with favor.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I send my blessing to you and to all who are yours: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With respect and appreciation, and with blessings for good tidings.

## 8767

B"H, 28 Elul, 5723

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter... in which you write regarding the two theories concerning the rotation of the earth and the sun and the scientific perspective on this, etc. It is surprising that you write this, for surely you know that one of the foundations of the theory of relativity, which has been accepted by **all** scientists in recent decades, is:

That regarding a "system" of two bodies in relative motion to one another, **it is impossible** to determine which is in a state of rest and which is in motion. This is not due to a deficiency in our current knowledge, but rather because of the very "nature" of the matter—meaning that regarding the aforementioned question and the like, science has no position. On the contrary, it **denies** that there is a clear answer to be found. Furthermore, if one finds difficulties with one theory, there are similar ones regarding the other, as is explained at length in the theory of relativity.

From what has been said, it is understood that if someone were to come and say that for whatever reason they choose to establish that a certain body is stationary and the other revolves around it, **it is impossible**—from the standpoint of **science**—to find **any contradiction** to this.

By the way, even before the emergence of the aforementioned theory, there was no **absolute** refutation of the Ptolemaic system (that the earth is always stationary and the sun revolves around it), but rather a declaration and conclusion that the number of difficulties with this theory was greater than those regarding the Copernican system. However, there were also several "difficulties" and misunderstandings raised against the Copernican system as well. And this is not the place to elaborate.

... Of course, the time is not currently conducive for letters—but the great value of matters of education and study (in purity and holiness) is the deciding factor.

## 8778

[Elul 5723]

In response to your letter of the 2nd of Elul, in which you write about starting out on your own in matters of *parnassah*, and the first steps you have taken in this regard.

May it be Hashem’s will that this beginning be at a *sha'ah tovah u'mutzlachas* (a good and successful time), and that the initial period—which they say is difficult—may pass quickly, and that expansion may begin, both in *ruchniyus* and in *gashmiyus*, which for a *Yid* go hand in hand.

And may you and your wife, *tichyeh*, raise all your children, *shichyu*, in an atmosphere of peace of mind and body, to Torah, *chuppah*, and *ma'asim tovim*.

Especially now that we have entered the month of Elul, regarding which our *Rabbeinu HaZaken*—this year being the 150th anniversary of his *histalkus* and *hillula*—says that it is analogous to a king whose subjects greet him in the field, etc., and he receives everyone with *seiver panim yafos* (a pleasant countenance) and shows a smiling face to all (*Likutei Torah, Parshas Re'eh 32b*).

With blessings for good tidings and to be inscribed and sealed for good.
