## 879

B"H, Days of Selichos, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.

— The 150th year since the Histalkus-Hilula of Rabbeinu HaZaken —

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life,

Greetings and Blessings!

The days of Rosh Hashanah — the **Yamim Nora'im** with which the new year, which is coming upon us and upon all of Israel for good and for blessing, begins — fill every Jewish heart with a holy feeling.

This feeling of the "Days of Awe" is far deeper than **yiras ha'onesh** (fear of punishment, Heaven forbid), and the like. The yirah that awakens during the Yamim Nora'im is **yiras haromemus**, the feeling of awe that comes from the awareness that one is present at, and personally participating in, the **hachtarah** ("coronation") of the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He; which is the essence of Rosh Hashanah.

The **hachtarah** of the Creator of the world as *Melech al kol ha'aretz* (King of the world), which Jews pray for and bring about on Rosh Hashanah, renews the **personal** bond of **every** Jew with the Almighty; the direct and *pnimiyusdike* (internal) bond of every individual as an individual, and not merely as a part of the *tzibur* (community) and *klal* (collective). This **hachtarah** is carried out through the personal request of each and every one of us that the Almighty accept this coronation, and through this, the bond of "We are Your people and You are our King" is created.

The concept and feeling of this **hachtarah** finds special expression in the prayer: "Our G-d and G-d of our fathers, reign over the entire world in Your glory... and let every created being know that You created it... and let all who have a soul in their nostrils say, 'Hashem, G-d of Israel, is King, and His kingdom rules over all'" — the entire creation, and especially man with a *neshamah*, recognizes and submits to the royal dominion of the Almighty.

This prayer emphasizes the feeling of **yiras haromemus**, and simultaneously, the unavoidable consequence of it — the readiness and desire to fulfill the commandments of the King.

And therefore, despite the fact that Rosh Hashanah is the introduction to the *Aseres Yemei Teshuvah* and is the beginning of these days, *Tachanun* and *Viduy* for sins are not recited during the days of Rosh Hashanah. For the feeling of unity with the Almighty through the *hachtarah* so permeates a person that, however great the pain over the deeds of the past may be, it becomes *batel* (nullified) in the dominant feeling of **yiras haromemus**.

In truth, **teshuvah** — in its deeper concept, that of "returning (to the Source)" — is also in full harmony with the inner content of Rosh Hashanah, which is connected to the idea of **hachtarah**.

Only **after** Rosh Hashanah do the subsequent matters of *teshuvah* begin—regret for the past and resolution for the future, with *viduyim* and *selichos*, etc.—as the necessary outcome of the *hachtarah* of Rosh Hashanah: the awareness of the renewed and strengthened bond and unification with the King must awaken the desire and resolve to be worthy of it, and this obligates the person to remove everything that hinders this bond: the *pesha'im*, *avonot*, and even *chata'im* (unintentional sins).

* * *

Regrettably, it must be said that due to various reasons, there have been years and places where the spiritual elevation of Rosh Hashanah and the *Aseres Yemei Teshuvah* was not utilized to the proper extent. The *Yamim Nora'im* passed, and in some communities and among some individuals, the inspiration evaporated, and no change or improvement was noticed in the personal, daily life that one would have expected from every Jewish man or woman.

Consequently, there was also a lack of improvement in social life.

One of the main reasons for this is that the elevation and inspiration of the *Yamim Nora'im* are not utilized in a way that touches the **self**, but rather on matters that concern **others**. Not infrequently, these days are utilized for general slogans and world problems; "messages" that obligate no one in general, and certainly no one within their own *daled amos* (four cubits). This "satisfies" everyone, and one also has the "justification" for it, for Rosh Hashanah surely encompasses the entire creation, and there is no shortage in the world of general "great" matters that demand improvement or change.

And the talking, the getting worked up, and the making of firm resolutions regarding such lofty world problems (which, in most cases, the resolvers cannot do anything about anyway) — is a convenient and "nice" excuse for not giving the necessary and life-essential full attention to one's personal *cheshbon hanefesh* (soul-accounting) and to one's daily life (where, precisely, one's resolution has its full effect).

The safeguard against this is also emphasized in the mitzvah of **tekias shofar** — the unique and special mitzvah that is the *chovas hayom* (obligation of the day) of Rosh Hashanah. The mitzvah of *tekias shofar* is not an assembly of many musical instruments, but specifically **one** instrument, and that, too — not a complicated musical instrument meant to produce extraordinary musical compositions. The *shofar* is specifically a simple horn of an animal, and "all sounds are valid in the *shofar*." The *shofar* emphasizes that the orientation must be, first and foremost, on the individual, on the self, and that the emphasis must be placed on bringing *kedushah* into even the simple and mundane matters of the daily life of the individual, and **afterwards** into the social life of the individual as part of the *tzibur*, and so on.

* * *

May it be the will of the Almighty that every Jew, man or woman, and especially the spiritual leaders, should utilize the holy moments and the inner *neshamah* awakening of the *Yamim Nora'im* not for general world or national problems (which, however important these problems may be, are not the *inyan* of Rosh Hashanah and *Aseres Yemei Teshuvah*, neither for the individual nor for the community), but for the urgent call of these days — the call to ***tamlichuni aleichem*** — to accept the Almighty as King, as one's personal King — and the consequence of this — the call to **teshuvah, tefillah, tzedakah**, all of which must begin within oneself and from oneself, and afterwards around oneself, in the community and beyond.

And may the spiritual awakening and revitalization of these days illuminate and permeate all the days of the year. And may they lead to a deeper bond of every Jew with the Almighty, a bond that will express itself in daily life in accordance and in harmony with the G-dly Torah and G-dly *mitzvos*. And the change for the good in spiritual life will surely bring a change for the good in material life, so that it may be a blessed year in all respects.

With the blessing of *Kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year in revealed and manifest goodness,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 8780

B”H, Days of Selichos, 5723
Brooklyn, N.Y.
- The 150th year of the histalkus hilula of Rabbeinu HaZaken -

Greetings and blessings!

Your pidyon nefesh has been received.

As we approach the new year, which is coming upon us and upon all of Yisrael for good and for blessing, I hereby wish to express my blessing to you: a blessing of *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for success in Torah with yiras shamayim,

**M. Schneerson**

**P.S.** Regarding your inquiry concerning a *seder* and *tikkun*, etc.: Regarding fasts, it is understood from what Rabbeinu HaZaken writes in Iggeres HaTeshuvah—in this year, the 150th year of his histalkus hilula—that this is not applicable to our generations, and especially at your age. You should focus on learning *nigleh* and Chassidus with *hasmadah* and *shekidah*. We see tangibly that fasting the body disrupts the concentration of thought, *v’kal l’meivin*. One can instead substitute these with fasting from foods that are pleasurable to the body, and the like.

Regarding your question concerning the study of Chassidus in general: the matter is explained in Kuntres Eitz HaChayim. In any event, there must be study of this before morning davening. This is a settled ruling in Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim, siman 98, in the Rema, for this study is the *hisbonenus* in the greatness of Hashem—though this is the study of Chassidus for the purpose of davening. It is obvious that there must also be study of this *lishmah*, for the sake of the study itself. Its time each day is as explained in Kuntres Eitz HaChayim, with an addition on the day of Shabbos, which is holy to Hashem, as explained there.

Regarding the quantity of the aforementioned study, as well as regarding the *shiurim* in the study of *nigleh*, the *halachos* that are necessary, etc.—you should consult with your friends in your location who know you. It is best not to set a practice for several months, but rather for a few weeks, and according to the changes you find in the interim, you will be able to make adjustments.
